# CARE — Collaborative Agent Reasoning Ecosystem · Implementation TODO

CARE is the autonomous TUI front-end of the ecosystem. It accepts a user query
("I'd like a weather report", "Develop a helper for a financier"), drives MAGE
to synthesise CARL chains, optionally evolves them via GigaEvo Platform, runs
them via CARL's executor, and persists every artifact (steps, chains, agents,
AgentSkills, MCPs, memory cards) to GigaEvo Memory.

The current `/Users/glazkov/Development/care` is a Textual scaffold with two
panes (task input + heuristic pipeline preview). Everything below replaces or
extends that scaffold.

Priorities: **[P0]** blocker for first usable demo · **[P1]** required for v0.1 ·
**[P2]** required for the full ecosystem story · **[P3]** quality / polish ·
**[P4]** future / research.

---

## 0. Architecture target

```
┌─────────────────────────────────── CARE TUI (Textual) ──────────────────────────────────┐
│                                                                                         │
│   Query screen  ─►  Generation screen  ─►  Inspection screen  ─►  Evolution screen      │
│       ▲                  │                       │                       │              │
│       │                  ▼                       ▼                       ▼              │
│       │           ┌─────────────┐         ┌─────────────┐         ┌─────────────┐       │
│       │           │ MAGE async  │         │ CARL runner │         │ GigaEvo     │       │
│       └────────── │ pipeline    │         │ (execute    │         │ Platform    │       │
│                   │ + progress  │         │ chain)      │         │ evolution   │       │
│                   └─────────────┘         └─────────────┘         └─────────────┘       │
│                          │                       │                       │              │
│                          ▼                       ▼                       ▼              │
│                  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐           │
│                  │  GigaEvoClient (rebadged gigaevo-memory + platform SDKs) │           │
│                  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘           │
│                          │                                       │                      │
│                          ▼                                       ▼                      │
│                  GigaEvo Memory                          GigaEvo Platform               │
│                  (steps/chains/agents/                   (runner pool, evolution        │
│                   agent_skills/memory_cards)              experiments, SSE progress)    │
│                                                                                         │
│   AgentSkill sandbox  ◄─── triggered from CARL AgentSkillStep                           │
│   (Docker / e2b / firejail)                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

---

## 1. TUI core (P0–P1)

### 1.1 Screens & navigation

- **[DONE] Replace the single demo screen with a multi-screen workflow.**

  *Fully complete:* every §1.1 P0 sub-task (P0.1 – P0.37)
  has landed. The CARE TUI now ships the canonical screen
  stack — `WelcomeScreen` (splash + Recents sidebar +
  Resume-on-startup prompt) routes to `LibraryScreen` for
  returning users / `SettingsScreen` for first-run; from
  there the screen graph covers `QueryScreen` →
  `GenerationScreen` → `SaveAgentModal` →
  `InspectionScreen` (Chain + Run-history tabs), plus
  per-row actions (open / run / edit / evolve / show
  lineage / duplicate / delete), bulk-select (`Space` /
  `F` / `T` / `Del`), per-row context menu (`Ctrl+M` /
  right-click), and the supporting modal family
  (ConfirmModal, ContextMenu, CommandPaletteModal,
  LineageModal, DiffModal, TagEditorModal, ExportModal,
  ImportModal, RunContextModal, EditAgentScreen,
  ExecutionScreen, EvolutionScreen, HumanInputModal,
  ResumeModal). Polish layer: ToastHost mounted at the
  app level (`app.push_toast(...)`), TaskListDrawer via
  `Ctrl+B`, theme picker reading `list_themes()`,
  `Esc`-cancel on every long-running screen wired to
  `workers.cancel_group(..., "generate" / "execute" /
  "evolution")`. Every shipped data layer is now consumed
  by exactly one screen / modal — the §1.3 / §3 bullets
  that were `[DONE — data layer]` have been flipped to
  fully `[DONE]` as each P0.N sub-task landed.
  - `WelcomeScreen` — boots straight into `LibraryScreen` (the user's home)
    with an always-visible "+ New agent" affordance that opens `QueryScreen`.
    A `Recents` sidebar lists the last 5 generated/run agents for one-click
    return.
  - `LibraryScreen` — **the user's agent library** (see §1.3 below). This is
    where steps 4-5 of the canonical user flow live: browse generated
    agents, sort/filter/favourite, run / edit / duplicate / delete.
  - `QueryScreen` — current `TaskSetup` widget (task description + context file
    picker), plus optional fields: domain hint, allowed step types, target
    runtime (local / docker / e2b), max chain steps. `Ctrl+G` triggers
    generation. `Ctrl+L` returns to library without saving.
  - `GenerationScreen` — split layout:
    - left: live MAGE stage log (`memory_research → web_research → ... → self_refine`)
      with per-stage status badges (pending / running / done / failed) and
      elapsed time.
    - right: streamed DAG preview that fills in as `StepDescriber` emits each
      step (use Textual `Tree` or `RichLog`).
    - on completion, opens a `SaveAgentModal` (see §3 below) before
      proceeding to InspectionScreen.
  - `InspectionScreen` — read-only chain view: step list (selectable), step
    detail pane (prompt template, deps, config), DAG view (ASCII or
    Rich-rendered), memory-key footer linking to GigaEvo Memory.
    Action bar: `Run` / `Edit` / `Evolve` / `Duplicate` / `Back to library`.
  - `EditAgentScreen` — mutate a saved agent's name/description/tags, edit
    individual step prompts/configs, reorder dependencies. Save creates a
    new version in Memory (channel `latest`) keeping the prior version
    accessible for rollback.
  - `ExecutionScreen` — runs the chain locally via `ReasoningChain.execute()`,
    streams `on_step_start`/`on_step_complete`/`on_llm_chunk` callbacks, shows
    per-step memory and history. Reachable from LibraryScreen via `Run`,
    from InspectionScreen, or from a completed GenerationScreen.
  - `EvolutionScreen` — submit the chain to the platform, poll/stream progress,
    show best individuals, accept the winner back to memory.

  **Implementation roadmap.** Every "[DONE — data layer]" item
  above already ships the projection / async driver / persistence
  the corresponding Textual widget consumes — the work below is
  the thin renderer + key handler that flips both items
  (this P0 sub-task AND the unlocked data-layer item) to fully
  DONE. Pick ONE sub-task per iteration; ship the widget, write
  Pilot tests with `App.run_test()`, flip both bullets. Order
  reflects dependency: foundation → global affordances → home
  screen → canonical user flow → modals → polish.

  **A. Foundation (no upstream deps; cheap to test)**

  - [DONE — P0.1] **App shell + screen stack.** Refactored
    `care/app.py` from the single `DemoScreen` mount into a
    `CareApp` that owns:
    - Screen-stack navigation primitives inherited from
      Textual `App` (`push_screen` / `pop_screen` /
      `switch_screen`) — proven via a Pilot test that
      pushes + pops a dummy screen.
    - A `mode` reactive (`first_run` vs `returning`) set
      from `DEFAULT_CONFIG_PATH.exists()`. Explicit `mode=`
      constructor kwarg wins for test overrides.
    - Lazy facade slots — `config` (auto-loaded via
      `CareConfig.load()`), `memory` / `platform` (default
      `None` — populated by the first-run wizard /
      SettingsScreen), `task_registry`, `token_counter`
      (both `is None`-checked, not `or`-defaulted, so the
      caller's empty instance survives the constructor),
      `theme_pref` (loaded via
      `load_theme_preference()` with fallback to the default
      `ThemePreference(theme_name="auto")`).
    - Lazy `DemoScreen` import in `_build_boot_screen()` so
      the CLI-only `care --help` path doesn't pull Textual.
      When the WelcomeScreen (P0.2) and SettingsScreen
      (P0.32) land, only `_build_boot_screen` changes.
    - **Files:** rewrote `care/app.py`.
    - **Tests:** `tests/test_app_shell.py` (15 cases):
      construction (8 — defaults, returning-when-config-
      exists, explicit mode override, explicit config wins,
      explicit facades retained, memory/platform default
      None + explicit, theme_pref fallback);
      Pilot mount (4 — boot screen pushed, mode reactive
      set, returning mode pilot, screen stack push/pop);
      metadata (2); run entry point (1).

    Full CARE suite (1903 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  - [DONE — P0.2] **WelcomeScreen routing.** Shipped
    `care/screens/welcome.py`:
    - `WelcomeScreen(Screen)` with a centred splash
      (`#welcome-splash` Vertical container, `#welcome-title`
      + `#welcome-subtitle` Static rows).
    - Default 200ms `splash_seconds`; tests override to `0.0`
      via constructor kwarg + the `WelcomeScreen.DEFAULT_SPLASH_SECONDS`
      class attribute. Zero/negative splash routes via
      `self.call_later(self._route)` (Textual's `set_timer`
      divides by interval internally and crashes on 0).
    - `next_screen_factory: Callable[[str], Screen] | None`
      kwarg + module-level `default_next_screen(mode)` factory.
      Factory reads `app.mode` (or defaults to `"returning"`
      if the host doesn't expose one — defensive for
      bare-host test apps). Until P0.7 (LibraryScreen) and
      P0.32 (SettingsScreen) ship, both modes route to the
      existing `DemoScreen` — only `default_next_screen`
      changes when those screens land.
    - Re-entry guard (`_routed` flag) so a duplicate timer
      fire doesn't push two screens. `routed_to_mode`
      attribute records the routed mode for tests + future
      telemetry.
    - `care/screens/__init__.py` re-exports `WelcomeScreen`
      and `default_next_screen`.
    - `care/app.py::_build_boot_screen()` now returns
      `WelcomeScreen()` instead of `DemoScreen()`. When the
      routing targets land, this method stays untouched.
    - **Tests:** `tests/test_screen_welcome.py` (14 cases):
      construction (5 — default + explicit + zero splash,
      factory default None, routed flags start unset);
      routing (4 — returning + first_run + custom mode pass
      through, missing app.mode defaults to returning);
      re-entry guard (1 — double `_route()` calls
      idempotent); composition (1 — title + subtitle
      Statics queryable mid-splash);
      `default_next_screen` factory (2 — both modes return a
      Screen instance); CareApp integration (1 — full boot
      from `CareApp()` lands on the routed target via
      WelcomeScreen).

    Full CARE suite (1917 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **B. Global affordances (consume the shipped registries)**

  - [DONE — P0.3] **Header widget.** Shipped
    `care/widgets/header.py`:
    - `CareHeader(Horizontal)` — 1-row strip with three
      Statics by id (`#header-title` left, `#header-breadcrumb`
      centre/`1fr` width, `#header-version` right with dim
      style). DEFAULT_CSS handled inline so the widget drops
      into any host without extra TCSS plumbing.
    - Constructor accepts an optional `HeaderModel` snapshot;
      defaults to empty model (title `"CARE"`, no breadcrumb).
    - `set_model(model)` swaps the snapshot + repaints the
      three Statics. Mount-aware (`is_mounted` guard) so
      pre-mount snapshot changes don't trigger
      `query_one()` failures.
    - `refresh_from_app(*, active_screen, breadcrumb,
      version, title)` builds a fresh model via the shipped
      `build_header(...)` factory + applies it. Version
      defaults to a defensive lookup: `app.version` →
      `app.config.version` → `""`. The future
      `CareApp.watch_current_screen` hook calls this on
      every screen transition.
    - `model` property exposes the current snapshot for
      tests / telemetry.
    - Re-exported from `care.widgets` alongside
      `PipelinePreview` and `TaskSetup`.
    - **Tests:** `tests/test_widget_header.py` (16 cases):
      construction (2 — default + explicit model);
      mount + compose (3 — three Statics queryable,
      default empty breadcrumb, separator format `"A › B
      › C"`); set_model (2 — repaint preserves DOM, pre-mount
      no-crash); refresh_from_app (2 — builds via
      build_header, filters empty breadcrumb entries);
      version detection (4 — app.version,
      app.config.version, explicit override, missing falls
      back to empty); integration (2 — round-trips
      `build_header` output, multi-transition refresh);
      re-exports (1).

    **Unlocks header half of §1.1 P0 Header/footer + global
    key bindings.** Footer + key handler land in P0.4 +
    P0.5; once those flip DONE, the full data-layer
    `[DONE — data layer]` Header/footer item promotes to
    fully DONE.

    Full CARE suite (1933 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  - [DONE — P0.4] **Footer widget.** Shipped
    `care/widgets/footer.py`:
    - `CareFooter(Horizontal)` — 1-row hint strip with a
      leading `1fr` spacer `Static` (right-aligns the
      hints) followed by one `Static` per `FooterHint`.
      Each hint Static carries class `.footer-hint`
      (queryable in bulk via `query(".footer-hint")`) and
      stable id `#footer-hint-<action_id>` (queryable per
      action).
    - Inline DEFAULT_CSS: 1-row height, `$panel` background,
      muted foreground, hint statics `width: auto` with 1-col
      padding.
    - Constructor accepts an optional `FooterModel`
      snapshot; defaults to empty model so the host can mount
      pre-data.
    - `set_model(model)` — swaps the snapshot and triggers
      `recompose()` (scheduled via `app.call_later` because
      `recompose` returns a coroutine; lets the caller stay
      sync). The trivial diff-then-rebuild strategy collides
      on hint IDs because Textual's `Widget.remove()` is
      async-deferred — `recompose()` swaps the child set
      atomically.
    - Mount-aware (`is_mounted` guard) so pre-mount
      snapshot changes don't trigger Textual queries.
    - `refresh_from_app(*, active_screen, scope, registry)`
      builds a fresh model via the shipped
      `build_footer(...)` factory + applies it. Scope
      defaults to `"screen"`; modals pass `"modal"` and the
      registry's screen-only hints (Save / Re-run) drop
      automatically. Custom `registry` kwarg lets plugin
      authors wire their own bindings.
    - `model` property exposes the current snapshot for
      tests/telemetry.
    - Hint rendering helper `_format_hint(key, label)`
      produces the canonical `"[Key] Label"` string.
    - Re-exported from `care.widgets`.
    - **Tests:** `tests/test_widget_footer.py` (17 cases):
      construction (2 — default empty + explicit model);
      mount + compose (4 — spacer always present, hint
      per binding, namespaced IDs, modal scope drops
      screen-only hints); set_model (3 — rebuilds hints
      via recompose, screen→modal drops hints, pre-mount
      no-crash); refresh_from_app (4 — builds via
      `build_footer`, modal scope filters, custom registry,
      multi-transition refresh); hint formatting (3); re-
      exports (1).

    **Together with P0.3 (header) and P0.5 (key handler —
    pending), flips §1.1 P0 Header/footer + global key
    bindings closer to fully DONE.**

    Full CARE suite (1950 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  - [DONE — P0.5] **Global key handler.** Wired
    `CareApp.BINDINGS` to the shipped registry:
    - `_build_textual_bindings()` projects every
      `default_global_bindings()` entry into a Textual
      `Binding(b.textual_key, f"global_{b.action_id}",
      b.label, show=False)`. `show=False` keeps Textual's
      built-in footer from rendering its own hints — the
      `CareFooter` widget (P0.4) owns the visible hint
      strip.
    - `CareApp.ENABLE_COMMAND_PALETTE = False` disables
      Textual's built-in Ctrl+P palette so our binding
      wins. CARE's own `CommandPaletteModal` (P0.25) owns
      the gesture; the shipped §1 P3 data layer already
      lives in `care.runtime.command_palette`.
    - Five nested `Message` classes — `SaveRequested`,
      `RerunRequested`, `CommandPaletteRequested`,
      `BackRequested`. Active-screen handlers subscribe
      via `on_care_app_<name>` (Textual auto-resolves the
      handler name from the nested class qualname).
    - Five `action_global_*` methods:
      - `action_global_open_command_palette` — Ctrl+P →
        posts `CommandPaletteRequested` on the active
        screen.
      - `action_global_quit` — Ctrl+Q → `self.exit()`.
      - `action_global_save_artifact` — Ctrl+S → posts
        `SaveRequested`.
      - `action_global_rerun_artifact` — Ctrl+R → posts
        `RerunRequested`.
      - `action_global_back` — Esc → `pop_screen()` when
        the stack has more than one entry; otherwise posts
        `BackRequested` so top-level screens can implement
        their own back behaviour.
    - `_post_to_screen(message)` helper — posts on the
      active screen (Textual messages bubble UP, so posting
      on the screen lets the screen's handler run first
      before the message reaches the app). Falls back to
      `self.post_message` when the screen stack is empty.
    - `global_action_log: list[str]` telemetry attribute —
      every action method appends its action_id. Tests
      pin behaviour against this log; future TaskList
      drawer reads it for "recent actions" debugging.
    - **Tests:** `tests/test_app_global_keys.py` (14
      cases): bindings construction (4 — one-per-default,
      action names namespaced, textual_key normalised,
      `CareApp.BINDINGS` length matches);
      action dispatch (5 — Ctrl+P / S / R / Q each fire
      the right action method, Esc pops screen when stack
      deep); messages (3 — SaveRequested + RerunRequested +
      CommandPaletteRequested all reach the screen handler
      via `on_care_app_*`); action log (2 — initialised
      empty, records every fire).

    Together with P0.3 (header) + P0.4 (footer), flips
    §1.1 P0 Header/footer + global key bindings to fully
    DONE. The original `[DONE — data layer]` Header/footer
    bullet above promotes to fully DONE now that all three
    consumer parts (Header widget, Footer widget, key
    handler) have landed.

    Full CARE suite (1964 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  - [DONE — P0.6] **Theme application + reactive system
    appearance.** Wired CARE theming into `CareApp`:
    - `_care_theme_to_textual(theme)` projects a
      :class:`care.runtime.Theme` into Textual's native
      `textual.theme.Theme` shape (named colour args:
      primary / secondary / background / surface / panel /
      etc.; CARE extras `foreground-muted` + `border` ride
      along via the `variables` kwarg).
    - `CareApp._register_care_themes()` walks every
      concrete (non-auto) CARE theme and calls
      `App.register_theme(...)`. Skips themes already in
      `available_themes` so re-mounts don't crash. Built-in
      `dark` + `light` plus any plugin-registered customs
      become Textual-switchable.
    - `CareApp._apply_active_theme()` resolves the active
      `ThemePreference` via the shipped
      `resolve_active_theme(...)`, stamps the result on
      `app.active_theme`, and sets Textual's `app.theme =
      <name>` when the resolved theme is registered.
    - `CareApp.system_appearance: reactive[SystemAppearance
      | None]` — CARE's stand-in for the host's
      `prefers-color-scheme` signal. Textual doesn't expose
      one natively in our pinned version (`App.dark` is
      gone in 5.x); apps / tests / future OS-integration
      code flip this reactive to emulate appearance changes.
    - `watch_system_appearance(appearance)` re-resolves
      auto-preference themes on every flip. Concrete
      preferences (explicit `dark` / `light`) are NOT
      re-resolved — explicit user choice wins over the
      host signal.
    - `CareApp.apply_care_theme(name, *, persist=True)`
      public API. The SettingsScreen toggle (P0.32) calls
      this; `persist=False` lets the live-preview pane swap
      themes without writing to disk. Persistence failure
      (read-only config dir) degrades silently — the visual
      change still happens.
    - `on_mount()` now: sets `mode` reactive → registers
      CARE themes → applies the persisted theme → pushes the
      boot screen. Order matters: theme application before
      `push_screen` so the first paint uses the right
      palette.
    - **Tests:** `tests/test_app_theme.py` (15 cases):
      `_care_theme_to_textual` projection (3 — concrete
      translates, light-theme `dark=False`, extras ride
      along via `variables`); mount application (4 —
      concrete themes registered, auto resolves to concrete,
      explicit dark + light apply); apply_care_theme (4 —
      runtime swap, persist=True writes, persist=False
      skips, auto resolves to concrete); watch_system_appearance
      (2 — auto re-applies on flip both ways, explicit
      ignores flip); idempotent registration (1 —
      re-construction doesn't crash); theme list unchanged
      by app construction (1).

    **Unlocks §1 P2 Theming + dark/light toggle** —
    promoted to fully DONE. The SettingsScreen toggle UI
    (P0.32) still owes the form widget that calls
    `apply_care_theme`, but the wiring is in place.

    Full CARE suite (1979 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **C. Library home (the user's first real screen)**

  - [DONE — P0.7] **LibraryScreen scaffold + DataTable.**
    Shipped `care/screens/library.py`:
    - `LibraryScreen(Screen)` composes `CareHeader` (P0.3) +
      `Horizontal#library-main` (containing the sidebar
      placeholder `Vertical#library-sidebar` + a
      `DataTable#library-table`) + `CareFooter` (P0.4).
      Inline DEFAULT_CSS pins the sidebar at 24 cols and the
      table at `1fr`, matching the spec.
    - Eight columns rendered in canonical order via
      `LibraryScreen.COLUMNS`: `★ / Name / Domain / Steps /
      Last Run / Runs / Fitness / Tags`. The leading
      favourite indicator is a single-char column so it
      stays narrow; `cursor_type="row"` and
      `zebra_stripes=True` give the user a clear focus
      indicator.
    - Constructor accepts optional `sort` + `filters`
      kwargs (defaults to `LibrarySort()` + `LibraryFilters()`).
      `view` + `last_error` attributes track the most recent
      fetch outcome; future P0.9 (empty-state widget) reads
      both to pick the right empty template.
    - `on_mount()` populates header/footer via
      `refresh_from_app(active_screen="LibraryScreen",
      breadcrumb=("Library",))`, adds DataTable columns,
      then kicks the `_refresh()` worker (group=`"library"`,
      `exclusive=True` so a fresh refresh cancels in-flight
      work).
    - `_refresh()` async worker calls the shipped
      `fetch_library_view(memory, filters=, sort=)`,
      populates the table via `_populate_table(view)`, and
      records errors on `last_error` (caught — never
      crashes the worker). Missing `app.memory` (None
      facade) leaves the table empty rather than raising —
      the P0.9 empty-state widget will render the
      "no_library" template against `view=None`.
    - `_row_cells(row)` classmethod projects a `LibraryRow`
      into the 8-tuple of strings the DataTable expects:
      `"★"` / `""` for favourite, em-dashes for None
      step_count / last_run_at / fitness, 3-decimal fitness
      format, `"YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM"` datetime format,
      `", "` tag join. Exposed at class scope so tests pin
      formatting without driving the full widget.
    - `refresh_library()` public hook re-runs the worker;
      future P0.8 / P0.10 / P0.13 / P0.14 sub-tasks call
      this after mutating `filters` / `sort`.
    - `care/screens/__init__.py` re-exports `LibraryScreen`.
    - `care/screens/welcome.py::default_next_screen` now
      routes `mode="returning"` → `LibraryScreen()` (was
      `DemoScreen`); `mode="first_run"` still falls through
      to `DemoScreen` until P0.32 (SettingsScreen) ships.
    - **Tests:** `tests/test_screen_library.py` (25 cases):
      construction (2 — default state, columns constant);
      mount (4 — header/table/footer present, sidebar,
      column count = 8, header breadcrumb set);
      DataTable population (5 — rows from fetch,
      view attribute, favourites-first sort, no-memory
      empty, fetch-error → last_error); cell projection
      (10 — favourite indicator, label fallback, every
      None → em-dash, fitness 3 decimals, datetime
      format, tag join); refresh_library hook (1);
      re-exports (1); welcome routing (2 — returning →
      LibraryScreen, first_run still → DemoScreen).

    **Unlocks LibraryScreen layout (table half) of §1.3
    P0.** Sidebar + filter chips (P0.8), sort persistence
    (P0.10), per-row actions (P0.11), context menu (P0.12),
    bulk-select (P0.13), collections sidebar (P0.14), and
    empty-state widget (P0.9) all land on this scaffold
    next; the §1.3 P0 LibraryScreen layout bullet promotes
    to fully DONE once the sidebar (P0.8) lands.

    Full CARE suite (2004 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  - [DONE — P0.8] **LibraryScreen sidebar — filter chips +
    search.** Shipped `care/widgets/library_sidebar.py`:
    - `LibrarySidebar(Vertical)` — filter sidebar bound to
      a `LibraryFilters`. Hosts:
      - `Input#library-sidebar-search` — search box bound
        to `with_search`. Updates fire on every keystroke
        via `on_input_changed`.
      - `RadioSet#library-sidebar-status` with four radios
        (`All` / `Draft` / `Runnable` / `Evolved`) bound to
        `with_status`. Module-level `_STATUS_BY_BUTTON_ID`
        / `_BUTTON_ID_BY_STATUS` lookup tables keep the
        mapping in one place.
      - `Checkbox#library-sidebar-favourites` bound to
        `with_favourites_only`.
    - `LibrarySidebar.FiltersChanged(Message)` posted on
      every mutation carrying the new `LibraryFilters` —
      hosts subscribe via
      `on_library_sidebar_filters_changed`.
    - `set_filters(filters)` public hook for host-driven
      sync (e.g. when collections P0.14 picks a tag) —
      uses a `_suppress_count` counter pattern to absorb
      the 1–3 async events that Textual's `value=` setters
      schedule, so external sync doesn't loop back into
      another `FiltersChanged` post. The counter approach
      is essential because Textual's value-setter events
      fire AFTER the synchronous `set_filters` call
      returns (a simple boolean reset doesn't span the
      gap).
    - `focus_search()` method — wired to Ctrl+F on the
      host screen.
    - Re-exported from `care.widgets`.

    Updated `care/screens/library.py`:

    Shipped: `care/screens/evolution.py::EvolutionScreen`
    composes a 3-pane Horizontal split — `#evolution-status`

    `elapsed`, optional `error` / `accepted` suffixes),

    `evolution_run` worker that calls
    `platform.start_evolution(base_chain_id=...,
    **spec)` and drains
    `platform.stream_events(evolution_id)` via
    `_drain_events` (steps through the sync iterator via
    `asyncio.to_thread(next, iterator, sentinel)` so a
    blocking Platform call can't freeze the event loop).
    `_handle_event` dispatches `generation_started` /
    `individual_evaluated` / `best_updated` / `completed` /
    `accepted` / `failed` / `cancelled` payloads into the
    `EvolutionRunState`. Pareto-front sort is by descending
    fitness; `_upsert_individual` replaces existing entries
    by `individual_id`. Action bar: `Accept winner` (key
    `A`) calls `platform.accept_individual` against the
    currently-selected row (or the top-fitness fallback)

    `Back` pops; `Escape` cancels the worker group +
    flips `status="cancelled"`. No-platform / submit-failure /
    accept-failure paths land on `run.last_error` and refresh
    the status pane. 12 Pilot tests across dataclass helpers,
    `start_evolution` happy path, no-platform / submit-fail

    `model_copy(update=)` so the source instance stays
    untouched. `Validate` (Ctrl+V) runs
    `run_all_probes(current_config())` on the worker pool,

    `save_theme_preference(name)` and posts

    posts `SettingsScreen.Cancelled` and pops. 8 Pilot tests

    exports. Full CARE suite (2295 passed + 8 skipped); ruff
    clean.

    **Follow-up: disk persistence.** First-run users filling
    out SettingsScreen and clicking Save saw the snapshot
    envelope fire but nothing landed on disk — next launch
    re-prompted with empty fields. `CareConfig.save_to_disk
    (path=None) -> Path` now writes the form's snapshot to
    `~/.config/care/config.toml` (or the supplied path)
    using a hand-rolled `_format_toml` serializer (avoids a
    `tomli-w` dependency). `SettingsScreen.action_save_config`
    invokes the writer before posting `Saved` and renders
    `✓ saved to {path}` / `⚠ save failed: {exc}` inline.
    Memory + Platform API-key inputs were removed from the
    form (env-driven via `CARE_MEMORY__API_KEY` /
    `CARE_PLATFORM__API_KEY`); `current_config()` preserves
    the source instance's `api_key` values so a Save round-
    trip doesn't wipe credentials sourced from env or
    `care.toml`. An env-var hint Static (`#settings-keys-hint`)
    renders at the top of the form. 5 `TestSaveToDisk` round-
    trip tests in `tests/test_config.py` (default round trip,
    secrets round trip, parent-dir creation, special-char
    escaping, overwrite) plus 3 new SettingsScreen pilot
    tests (`test_memory_platform_api_keys_preserved_on_save`,
    `test_memory_and_platform_key_inputs_absent`,
    `test_keys_hint_renders`, `test_save_writes_to_disk`).
    Full CARE suite (2673 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

    `Cancel` (button + Escape) calls

  - [DONE — P0.35] **Toast / notification host.** Mounted at the
    app level. Every screen calls `app.push_toast(message,
    severity)`; widget displays then auto-dismisses after
    3s. Used by every shipped data layer's failure paths
    (`LibraryViewError`, `LineageError`, `RunHistoryError`,
    `AgentDiffError`, `LibraryBundleError`, etc.).

    Shipped: `care/widgets/toast.py::ToastHost` is a docked
    bottom widget with a `VerticalScroll` of `Static.toast`
    rows. `push(message, *, severity=, ttl=)` appends a row
    with the right badge (`· / ✓ / ⚠ / ✗`) + severity class
    (`severity-info` / `severity-success` /
    `severity-warning` / `severity-error`) and schedules
    auto-dismiss via `set_timer(ttl, ...)`; `ttl=0` keeps
    the toast sticky until manually removed. `history`
    captures every pushed `Toast` (bounded to the last 32
    entries) for tests + future telemetry. `CareApp.on_mount`
    now mounts a single :class:`ToastHost` before pushing
    the boot screen, and `CareApp.push_toast(message,
    severity=, ttl=)` routes through to it — every screen
    can call `self.app.push_toast(...)` without threading
    the host through manually. 10 Pilot tests across
    push + row mount, severity classes, history capture +
    32-entry bound, TTL auto-dismiss vs. `ttl=0` sticky,
    pure row formatter (with + without message), CareApp
    integration via `app.push_toast`, and re-exports. Full
    CARE suite (2320 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  - [DONE — P0.36] **Background TaskList drawer.** `Ctrl+B` opens a

    `last_cancelled_id`; `Switch to` posts
    `TaskListDrawer.SwitchRequested(record)` so the host
    routes (e.g. ExecutionScreen for in-flight chain runs) +

  - [DONE — P0.37] **Resume-prompt on startup.** `WelcomeScreen.on_mount`
    calls `RunStateStore().load()`; non-None → push
    `ResumeModal` offering "Resume" (re-prime from the
    stored payload) / "Discard" (clear via `store.clear()`).

    Shipped: `care/screens/resume.py::ResumeModal` is a
    `ModalScreen[ResumeResult]` constructed with
    `(state, store=...)`. The two-button form renders the
    stored job's `kind` / `label` / `started_at` / 12-char
    `run_id` prefix. `Resume` (focused primary button + Enter)
    dismisses with `ResumeResult(action="resume", state=...)`
    so the host re-primes from the payload; `Discard` calls
    `store.clear()` first then dismisses with
    `ResumeResult(action="discard", state=None)`; `Escape`
    dismisses with `action="cancel"` *without* clearing the
    store so the next launch offers the same prompt.
    `WelcomeScreen` accepts a `run_state_store` kwarg
    (defaults to `RunStateStore()`); `on_mount` calls
    `store.load()` and pushes `ResumeModal` when a snapshot
    is present, then posts
    `WelcomeScreen.ResumeRequested(state)` on resume so the
    host app routes to the right runtime (executor /
    generator). 8 Pilot tests across the standalone modal
    (`Resume` / `Discard` clears / `Escape` keeps) and the
    WelcomeScreen integration (no-snapshot no-op, snapshot
    pushes modal, resume posts message, discard clears +
    records action). Full CARE suite (2337 passed + 8
    skipped); ruff clean.

  Each sub-task above is intended to land in a single
  iteration: a focused screen / widget module, a Pilot test
  file, ruff clean, then update both this bullet AND the
  unlocked `[DONE — data layer]` bullet to fully DONE in the
  same PR.
- **[DONE] Header/footer + global key bindings:**
  `Ctrl+P` open command palette, `Ctrl+Q` quit, `Ctrl+S` save
  current artifact to memory, `Ctrl+R` re-run, `Esc` back.
  *Fully complete:* data layer shipped via §1.1
  `global_bindings.py`; the Textual widgets + key handler
  landed in P0.3 (header), P0.4 (footer), and P0.5 (key
  handler) on top.

  The Textual header / footer widgets + key handler are gated
  on §1 P0 multi-screen workflow, but the binding registry +
  dispatch + Header/Footer projection ship now.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/global_bindings.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `GlobalActionId` literal pinning the 5 canonical actions
      (`open_command_palette`, `quit`, `save_artifact`,
      `rerun_artifact`, `back`).
    - `BindingScope` literal (`always`, `screen`, `modal`)
      so the registry can express "save only applies on
      full-screen views, not in-modal".
    - `GlobalBinding` — frozen binding descriptor
      (`action_id`, `key`, `label`, `scope`, `description`)
      with `textual_key` (lowercased + Esc→escape) and
      `applies_to(scope)` accessors.
    - `HeaderModel` — frozen header projection (`title`,
      `breadcrumb` tuple, `version`, `active_screen`).
      `breadcrumb_text` derived accessor renders the
      `"Library › v3"` separator.
    - `FooterHint` — frozen per-row footer entry.
    - `FooterModel` — frozen aggregate (`hints` +
      `active_screen`).
    - `default_global_bindings()` — canonical 5-binding
      tuple matching the TODO spec EXACTLY (key labels
      preserved verbatim).
    - `find_binding_by_key(key, *, scope)` — case-insensitive
      + whitespace-tolerant key dispatch. Honours scope
      filter (Ctrl+S on a modal returns None because
      `save_artifact` is screen-scoped). Esc/escape both
      resolve to the `back` action.
    - `find_binding_by_action(action_id)` — canonical-name
      lookup for header/footer rendering.
    - `bindings_for_scope(scope)` — filter registry by
      scope. Used by `build_footer` internally.
    - `validate_registry(registry)` — duplicate-key
      detector. Raises `GlobalBindingError` on the first
      duplicate so a typo in a custom registry surfaces
      with a clear message before the Textual layer crashes.
    - `build_header(*, active_screen, breadcrumb, version,
      title)` — pure projection. Empty-string breadcrumb
      entries are filtered out so callers don't have to
      guard.
    - `build_footer(*, active_screen, scope, registry)` —
      pure projection. Filters by scope so the footer hides
      `Save` / `Re-run` on modals automatically.
    - `GlobalBindingError` — caller-mistake error class.

  **Scope semantics pinned by tests:**
  - `always` — every screen + every modal.
  - `screen` — full-screen views only (e.g. `save_artifact`,
    `rerun_artifact`).
  - `modal` — modal screens only (currently nothing uses
    this; reserved for future modal-specific affordances).
  - The default `back` (Esc) and `open_command_palette`
    (Ctrl+P) + `quit` (Ctrl+Q) are `always`-scoped so they
    work uniformly.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_global_bindings.py`, 35 cases):
  - **Registry (5):** all 5 spec'd action_ids present,
    canonical keys match spec verbatim, binding is frozen,
    defaults pass validation, duplicate-key detector flags
    bad registry.
  - **Textual key normalisation (3):** Ctrl+P → ctrl+p,
    Esc → escape, whitespace stripped.
  - **Scope semantics (3):** always applies to all,
    screen-only excludes modal, modal-only excludes screen.
  - **Lookups (10):** find by canonical key, case-
    insensitive, whitespace-tolerant, escape resolves to
    back, unknown returns None, scope filter on
    screen-only binding, always-scoped matches modal,
    find_by_action known + unknown.
  - **bindings_for_scope (3):** screen view shows all,
    modal hides Save + Re-run, custom registry respected.
  - **Header (4):** defaults, full build, breadcrumb
    filters empty entries, frozen.
  - **Footer (6):** screen has all 5, modal drops Save +
    Re-run, active_screen stamped, iter + len shortcuts,
    frozen, canonical keys preserved in hints, custom
    registry override.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1846 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future screen wiring:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      default_global_bindings, find_binding_by_key,
      build_header, build_footer, GlobalActionId,
  )

  class CareApp(App):
      BINDINGS = [
          Binding(b.textual_key, f"global_{b.action_id}", b.label)
          for b in default_global_bindings()
      ]

      def action_global_quit(self) -> None:
          self.exit()

      def action_global_open_command_palette(self) -> None:
          self.push_screen(CommandPaletteModal())

      def watch_current_screen(self, screen) -> None:
          # Header + footer reactive to screen change.
          self.header.update(build_header(
              active_screen=type(screen).__name__,
              breadcrumb=screen.breadcrumb_segments,
              version=self.version,
          ))
          scope = "modal" if isinstance(screen, ModalScreen) else "screen"
          self.footer.update(build_footer(
              active_screen=type(screen).__name__,
              scope=scope,
          ))
  ```

  The Textual `Binding` declaration consumes `textual_key`
  directly; the footer reads canonical `b.key` for human-
  readable hints. Same registry, two consumption surfaces.
- **[DONE] Status bar widget** at the bottom of every
  screen showing: Memory API health, Platform API health, current
  LLM model, total LLM tokens used in session, current run-id.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/status_bar.py`) +
  Textual widget (P1.1 – P1.5). `care/widgets/status_bar.py::StatusBar`
  docks at the bottom of `CareApp`, runs `aggregate_status_bar`
  on mount and a 5s interval, refreshes off-cycle on
  `TaskRegistry.on_change`, folds per-stage / chain LLM usage
  into the session counter via wired `MagePoster` +
  `CarlStreamer` `token_counter` kwargs, and renders the
  loading / probe-failure / aggregator-failure states inline.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/status_bar.py` exposes the full snapshot
    surface, re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `SessionTokenCounter` — thread-safe accumulator the
      `MagePoster` `StageCompleted` and `CarlStreamer`
      `ChainCompleted` adapters fold per-call usage dicts into.
      Accepts the standard CARL shape `{"prompt", "completion",
      "total"}`; missing `total` is derived from the split;
      non-int values are coerced via `int()` so a stringy
      provider doesn't crash; unparseable values count as 0
      but still bump `calls` so the avg-tokens computation
      reflects the missing data point.
    - `SessionTokenTotals` — frozen snapshot
      (`prompt`/`completion`/`total`/`calls`) the widget
      formats in fixed columns.
    - `HealthSnapshot` — per-service row mirroring
      `first_run.ProbeResult` but with a `checked_at`
      timestamp + `age_seconds(now=)` helper so the bar can
      render "memory ✓ (3s ago)". `HealthStatus` literal
      covers `ok | skipped | failed | unknown` — `unknown` is
      the bootstrap state before the first refresh tick.
    - `StatusBarSnapshot` — full payload (two `HealthSnapshot`
      rows + model + provider + `SessionTokenTotals` +
      `active_run_id` + `active_run_label` + `captured_at`),
      with a `format_text(now=)` rendering that pins the
      formatting contract (badge + age + model `provider/model`
      + thousands/millions tokens shortening + 8-char run-id
      prefix).
    - `probe_health(service, facade, timeout)` — runs the
      sync `facade.health_check()` in a thread with a
      deadline; timeout flips the snapshot to `failed` with
      `"timed out after Ns"` rather than blocking the bar.
    - `aggregate_status_bar(*, config, memory, platform,
      token_counter, active_task, timeout)` — fans the two
      probes out via `asyncio.gather` so the wall-clock floor
      is one timeout, not two. `memory=None` and
      `platform=None` produce `skipped` rows (e.g. before the
      first-run wizard ran).
    - `derive_from_task_registry(registry)` — pure projection
      picking the "current run" out of a `TaskRegistry`:
      prefers the most-recently-started running task; falls
      back to the most-recently-registered pending one;
      returns `None` when nothing's active. The aggregator's
      `active_task=` slot accepts the returned `TaskRecord`
      directly.

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** the aggregator accepts any
  `CareMemory`-like / `CarePlatform`-like facade exposing
  `health_check()`, any object exposing `id` + `label`
  attributes (or a dict with those keys) as `active_task`,
  and any object exposing `list_tasks(status=)` as the
  registry. Tests use lightweight stubs — no SDK / HTTP /
  real service touched.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_status_bar.py`, 36 cases):
  - **SessionTokenCounter (10):** starts-at-zero, basic add,
    accumulation, `None`/`{}` no-op, missing-total derived
    from split, non-int coerced, unparseable still bumps
    `calls`, reset, snapshot is frozen, 8-thread concurrent
    add no loss (800 calls).
  - **HealthSnapshot (2):** age_seconds None when never
    probed, age clamped to 0 on clock skew.
  - **probe_health (5):** skipped when facade is None, ok
    carries latency + detail, non-dict response wrapped as
    `{"raw": ...}`, exception wrapped as failed with
    typename, timeout flips to failed.
  - **aggregate_status_bar (5):** full snapshot fields, both
    facades skipped, dict `active_task`, partial failure (one
    ok one failed), concurrent execution proven via wall-clock
    floor.
  - **format_text (7):** happy path, failed service shows
    error, active run shortened to 8 chars + label, k/M
    formatting, zero tokens omitted, non-ok rows don't carry
    age suffix.
  - **derive_from_task_registry (6):** None registry, no
    active, running preferred over pending, most-recently-
    started wins, pending fallback, registry without
    `list_tasks` returns None.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  **What this enables for the future StatusBar widget:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      SessionTokenCounter, aggregate_status_bar,
      derive_from_task_registry,
  )

  class StatusBar(Static):
      def on_mount(self) -> None:
          self.counter = SessionTokenCounter()
          self.set_interval(5.0, self._refresh)

      async def _refresh(self) -> None:
          active = derive_from_task_registry(self.app.task_registry)
          snap = await aggregate_status_bar(
              config=self.app.config,
              memory=self.app.memory,
              platform=self.app.platform,
              token_counter=self.counter,
              active_task=active,
          )
          self.update(snap.format_text())
  ```

  The `MagePoster.handle_stage_completed` / `CarlStreamer.on_chain_complete`
  callbacks call `counter.add(usage)` when usage arrives, so
  the bar updates organically as the session runs.

- **[DONE] Theming + dark/light toggle** via TCSS
  variables.
  *Fully complete:* data layer shipped via §1 P2
  `care.runtime.theme` (registry + resolver + persistence);
  the Textual application (P0.6) registers every CARE theme
  with Textual's theme registry, sets the active theme on
  mount via `app.theme = <name>`, and re-resolves auto
  themes when `app.system_appearance` flips. The settings
  picker UI lands with P0.32.

  The Textual toggle widget is gated on §1 P0 multi-screen
  workflow, but the registry + resolver + persistence land now
  so the widget is a thin selector + reactive renderer.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/theme.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `ThemeKind` literal pinning the three modes (`light`,
      `dark`, `auto`).
    - `SystemAppearance` literal (`light` / `dark`) for the
      host's `prefers-color-scheme` signal.
    - `Theme` — frozen theme descriptor with `name`, `kind`,
      `variables` (TCSS variable dict, no leading `$`),
      `description`, and optional `light_pair` / `dark_pair`
      names for `auto`-kind themes that ship paired
      light/dark variants. `is_auto` predicate.
    - `ThemePreference` — frozen on-disk preference shape
      (`theme_name` + schema_version).
    - `ThemePreferenceStore` — atomic JSON store mirroring
      :class:`care.runtime.RunStateStore`: default
      `~/.config/care/theme.json`, atomic writes via
      tempfile + `os.replace`, tolerant `load()` returning
      `None` on every failure mode (missing / malformed /
      non-dict / schema-mismatch / empty theme_name).
      Thread-safe via internal lock.
    - Module-level `save_theme_preference` /
      `load_theme_preference` convenience wrappers.
    - `DEFAULT_THEMES` — canonical `(auto, light, dark)`
      tuple. Light / dark each ship 12 TCSS variables
      (`background`, `surface`, `panel`, `primary`,
      `secondary`, `accent`, `warning`, `error`, `success`,
      `foreground`, `foreground-muted`, `border`).
    - `register_theme(theme)` / `unregister_theme(name)` /
      `list_themes()` / `get_theme(name)` — module-level
      registry. Built-ins are immutable (register / unregister
      raise `ThemeError`); custom themes can be added and
      removed at runtime. `list_themes()` returns built-ins
      first in canonical order (`auto`, `light`, `dark`),
      custom themes appended alphabetically.
    - `resolve_active_theme(preferred_name, *,
      system_appearance, fallback)` — picks the concrete
      theme the app should render. Unknown names fall
      through `auto`; auto-kind themes route to their
      `light_pair` / `dark_pair` based on system appearance;
      missing partner themes fall back to the built-in
      light/dark. Returns a non-auto theme always so callers
      can safely call `theme_to_tcss_vars` on the result.
    - `theme_to_tcss_vars(theme)` — pure projection that
      maps `{key: value}` → `{$key: value}` for Textual's
      stylesheet variable layer. Auto themes return an
      empty dict (defensive — caller should have resolved
      first).
    - `ThemeError` — single error class for invalid theme
      operations.

  **Resolution semantics** (pinned by 8 resolver tests):
  - Explicit `light` / `dark` → returned directly.
  - `auto` + `system_appearance="light"` → `light` theme.
  - `auto` + `system_appearance="dark"` → `dark` theme.
  - `auto` + no appearance → `fallback` (default `dark` —
    matches CARE's terminal-first use case).
  - Unknown name → falls through `auto` → fallback rules.
  - Missing partner theme → built-in light/dark fallback.
  - Resolver NEVER returns an auto-kind theme (the consumer
    would get empty TCSS vars).

  **Tests** (`tests/test_theme.py`, 42 cases):
  - **Defaults (9):** built-in inventory, theme frozen,
    auto-first ordering, get_theme known / unknown,
    default path constant, light + dark have required
    variables, auto is kind=auto.
  - **Registry (8):** register custom, empty name raises,
    duplicate raises, built-in override raises,
    unregister custom + idempotent, unregister built-in
    raises, list_themes built-in order first + custom
    alphabetical.
  - **Resolver (9):** direct light/dark, auto+light_appearance,
    auto+dark_appearance, auto+no-appearance uses fallback,
    auto+custom-fallback, unknown name → auto → appearance,
    missing partner → built-in fallback, resolver always
    returns concrete (non-auto) theme.
  - **TCSS projection (3):** dark projection has $-prefixed
    keys, auto projection empty (defensive), values
    preserved.
  - **Persistence (12):** preference frozen + default auto,
    roundtrip, missing/malformed/non-dict/schema-mismatch/
    missing-name/empty-name all → None, atomic write no
    leftovers, save creates parent dirs, clear idempotent,
    8-thread concurrent save no corruption.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1888 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future toggle widget:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      resolve_active_theme, theme_to_tcss_vars, list_themes,
      load_theme_preference, save_theme_preference,
      ThemePreference,
  )

  class CareApp(App):
      def on_mount(self) -> None:
          pref = load_theme_preference() or ThemePreference()
          self._apply_theme(pref.theme_name)

      def _apply_theme(self, name: str) -> None:
          # Textual reports OS appearance via self.dark; we
          # mirror that into the resolver.
          appearance = "dark" if self.dark else "light"
          theme = resolve_active_theme(name, system_appearance=appearance)
          for var, value in theme_to_tcss_vars(theme).items():
              self.stylesheet.set_variable(var, value)
          # Persist the user's choice (not the resolved one —
          # we want "auto" to stay "auto" across restarts).
          save_theme_preference(ThemePreference(theme_name=name))

      def action_toggle_theme(self) -> None:
          # Cycles auto → light → dark → auto.
          current = load_theme_preference().theme_name
          next_ = {"auto": "light", "light": "dark", "dark": "auto"}[current]
          self._apply_theme(next_)
  ```

  The settings screen's theme picker reads `list_themes()`
  to render a dropdown that auto-includes plugin-registered
  custom themes.

  `entry.entry_id`.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/command_palette.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `PaletteEntryKind` literal pinning what the palette
      indexes (`chain`, `agent_skill`, `command`). Step +
      memory_card kinds excluded by design — palette is a
      navigation primitive over user-facing entities.
    - `CommandActionId` literal pinning the 7 built-in
      commands (`create_new_agent`, `show_library`,
      `open_settings`, `import_bundle`, `export_library`,
      `show_help`, `quit`).
    - `Command` — frozen built-in command descriptor with
      label / description / `shortcut_hint` (e.g.
      `"Ctrl+N"`) / keywords for haystack expansion.
    - `PaletteEntry` — frozen indexed row carrying
      `entry_id`, `kind`, `label`, `description`, `tags`,
      optional `command_action` (for `command` rows), and
      `score`. `is_command` predicate + `search_haystack`
      derived property (concatenated lowercase haystack).
    - `PaletteIndex` — frozen aggregate. `__len__` /
      `__iter__` / `is_empty` shortcuts; `filter_kinds()`
      pure projection for prefix-shortcut navigation (e.g.
      `@` restricts to chains).
    - `default_commands()` — canonical 7-command tuple.
    - `commands_to_entries(commands)` — pure projection
      (entry_id namespaced as `command:<action_id>`).
    - `fuzzy_score(query, candidate)` — fzf-style scorer:
      subsequence match (missing → 0.0); +0.5 prefix bonus;
      +0.3 substring bonus; +0.1 word-start bonus (post
      space / dot / slash / hyphen / underscore); +0.05
      consecutive-character bonus; divided by candidate
      length so shorter matches score higher. Case-
      insensitive.
    - `search_palette(index, query, *, top_k, kinds)` —
      pure ranker. Empty query → commands first + entities
      in insertion order. Non-empty → scores every entry,
      filters non-matches (score=0), sorts by `(-score,
      label.casefold())` for stable ranking. `kinds=` filter
      lets the modal narrow to a single kind without
      rebuilding the index.
    - `fetch_palette_index(memory, *, namespace, channel,
      limit, commands, timeout)` — async aggregator that
      fans `list_chains` + `list_agent_skills` out via
      `asyncio.gather` (one wall-clock timeout, not two).
      Missing SDK methods + per-call exceptions degrade
      silently (that kind's entries just don't appear)
      rather than crater the whole load. Built-in commands
      always present (the empty-query case stays useful
      even when Memory is unreachable).
    - `PaletteError` — single error class for caller-mistake
      / unrecoverable cases.

  **Scoring rules pinned by tests:**
  - Empty query → 0.0 (caller treats as "no input").
  - Non-subsequence → 0.0 (must match in order).
  - Prefix > substring > scattered subsequence.
  - Case-insensitive.
  - Word-start beats mid-word.
  - Consecutive run beats scattered (additive).
  - Shorter candidate slightly higher (length penalty).

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** aggregator accepts any
  `CareMemory`-like facade exposing `.client.list_chains(...)`
  and/or `.client.list_agent_skills(...)`. Projection accepts
  dict rows OR SDK model objects (attribute reads). Tests use
  lightweight stubs.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_command_palette.py`, 43 cases):
  - **fuzzy_score (10):** empty query / candidate, non-
    subsequence, subsequence positive, prefix > substring,
    substring > loose subsequence, case-insensitive, word-
    start bonus, consecutive bonus, shorter candidate
    higher.
  - **default_commands (4):** spec'd action_ids present,
    Command frozen, shortcut hints pinned, projection
    helper works.
  - **PaletteIndex (5):** len + iter, is_empty, kind
    filter, index frozen, entry frozen.
  - **search_palette (10):** empty query → commands first,
    empty respects top_k, query ranks by score, kind
    filter, non-match → empty, top_k caps, score populated
    on results, score=0 on empty query, command searched
    by keywords (matches "new" via the create_new_agent
    keywords), ties broken by label ascending.
  - **fetch_palette_index (12):** happy path, concurrent
    fetch (wall-clock proof under 0.09s for two 0.05s
    fetches), chain exception skipped, skill exception
    skipped, missing client raises, missing list methods →
    commands only, timeout wraps, custom commands,
    namespace + channel forwarded, limit clamped [1, 200],
    `_client` accessor works, rows-without-id skipped,
    attribute-access SDK rows.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1811 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future modal:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      fetch_palette_index, search_palette, PaletteError,
      PaletteEntry, CommandActionId,
  )

  class CommandPaletteModal(ModalScreen):
      async def on_mount(self) -> None:
          try:
              self.index = await fetch_palette_index(
                  self.app.memory,
                  namespace=self.app.config.namespace,
              )
          except PaletteError as exc:
              self.app.push_toast(str(exc))
              self.dismiss()
              return
          self._render_results(search_palette(self.index, ""))

      def on_input_changed(self, value: str) -> None:
          self._render_results(search_palette(self.index, value))

      def on_entry_selected(self, entry: PaletteEntry) -> None:
          if entry.is_command:
              self.app.dispatch_command(entry.command_action)
          elif entry.kind == "chain":
              self.app.push_screen(InspectionScreen(entry.entry_id))
          elif entry.kind == "agent_skill":
              self.app.push_screen(SkillDetailScreen(entry.entry_id))
          self.dismiss()
  ```

  The `@` / `#` prefix-shortcut affordances call
  `search_palette(self.index, rest, kinds=["chain"])` /
  `kinds=["agent_skill"]` for kind-narrowed mode.

### 1.2 Async wiring

- **[DONE]** Replace synchronous heuristic
  `_synthesize_pipeline()` with a proper `asyncio.Task` driven
  by `Worker(thread=False)`. Today the TUI blocks on
  `show_pipeline()`.

  **Shipped:**
  - **Async iterator extraction** in
    `care/widgets/pipeline_preview.py` — new
    `PipelinePreview._iter_pipeline(task, files)` async
    generator wraps the existing synchronous
    `_synthesize_pipeline` and yields one `PipelineStep` per
    iteration with an `await asyncio.sleep(0)` between each.
    The heuristic itself stays a pure sync function (still
    trivially testable); the iterator is the seam future
    MAGE-driven generation plugs into without changing the
    widget surface.
  - **Incremental rendering** in `show_pipeline`: now
    `async for step in self._iter_pipeline(...)`, mounting
    each card + arrow as the step lands. Cancellable mid-
    render: when the enclosing worker is cancelled the
    `CancelledError` propagates here, the partially-rendered
    pane stays intact (no torn DOM), and the next worker run
    starts from `remove_children()` cleanly.
  - **Textual worker wiring** in
    `care/screens/demo.py`:
    - New `_render_pipeline_worker(task, files)` helper that
      calls `self.run_worker(...)` with
      `name="pipeline_synthesis"`, `group="generate"`,
      `exclusive=True`, `exit_on_error=False`. The
      imperative `run_worker(...)` is used instead of the
      `@work` decorator so the screen stays
      Textual-version-agnostic (older Textual versions had
      different decorator semantics; the imperative API
      is stable).
    - `exclusive=True` on the `generate` group → a fresh
      `Ctrl+G` while a previous worker is still running
      cancels the old one before launching the new one.
      Same UX every future MAGE-driven screen will use
      (GenerationScreen / ExecutionScreen / EvolutionScreen
      will bind their workers to the same group convention).
    - `on_task_setup_generate_requested` now returns
      immediately after calling `_render_pipeline_worker` —
      the event loop never blocks on synthesis.
  - **`Esc` binding** wired to `action_cancel_generate`,
    which calls `self.workers.cancel_group(self,
    "generate")`. Sets the precedent for the future
    GenerationScreen / ExecutionScreen / EvolutionScreen Esc
    handlers (they all bind to the same `generate` group
    name so the same Esc behaviour ports straight across).

  **Tests (`tests/test_screens_demo_pilot.py`, 5 new + 6
  existing = 11 cases total):**
  - Existing Pilot tests (mount + actions + message routing)
    still pass.
  - `test_generate_method_directly_renders_pipeline`:
    drives `show_pipeline` directly (skipping the worker
    layer) and verifies cards mount — pins the
    async-iterator path the worker drives.
  - `test_escape_binding_cancels_group`: Esc invokes
    `action_cancel_generate` without raising even when no
    worker is in-flight (no-op safe).
  - `test_worker_spawned_on_generate`: monkey-patches
    `_render_pipeline_worker` to spy on calls; verifies
    `Ctrl+G` → button press → `GenerateRequested` message →
    `_render_pipeline_worker(task, files)` invocation chain
    is intact + receives the typed task string.
  - `test_pipeline_iterator_yields_same_set_as_sync`:
    regression guard that the async iterator emits the
    same step names in the same order as the sync
    heuristic — no steps dropped in the async path.
  - `test_pipeline_iterator_yields_to_loop`: pins that
    `_iter_pipeline` is in fact an async generator (using
    `inspect.isasyncgen`) so future contributors can't
    silently swap it for a sync generator + lose
    cancellation.

  **What this completes for §1 P0:** the worker pattern
  every future workflow screen uses is now in place against
  the existing demo. When `GenerationScreen` /
  `ExecutionScreen` / `EvolutionScreen` land in §1 P0 work,
  they copy this exact shape — `run_worker(..., group=
  "generate", exclusive=True)` + Esc binding to
  `workers.cancel_group(self, "generate")` — without
  introducing a new pattern. The wider §1 P0 multi-screen
  workflow remains the open piece.
- **[DONE] `MAGEProgressCallback` adapter** — implement
