- **[DONE]** Cancellation: each long-running Task must respect a
  `cancellation_token`; surfaced as `Esc` on the generation/execution screens.
  *Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/runtime/cancellation.py` ships the pure-Python
  primitive that every long-running CARE task (MAGE generation, CARL
  execution, Platform polling) shares. `CancellationToken` carries an
  atomic flag + an optional reason; `cancel()` is idempotent (returns
  `True` on the winning call, `False` on no-ops). Two consumption
  patterns: sync polling via `is_cancelled` / `raise_if_cancelled()`
  between work items, or async via `await wait_cancelled()`. The
  internal `asyncio.Event` is lazily bound to the running loop on
  first `wait_cancelled` so tokens can be constructed before the
  loop spins up. `on_cancel(callback)` registers fire-once listeners;
  late registration (after cancel) fires the callback immediately;
  listener exceptions are swallowed so one bad listener can't block
  the others. `CancelledByUserError(reason="...")` subclasses
  `asyncio.CancelledError` so existing `try/except` blocks catch it
  transparently while screens can still detect user-initiated cancel
  to show "Cancelled" instead of a traceback. `CancellationGroup`
  builds a parent/child tree — cancel-parent propagates to every
  child via `on_cancel` hooks, but cancel-child does NOT propagate
  upward (screen might want to abort one stage without killing the
  others); children created after the parent is already cancelled
  start out cancelled. `join_tokens(*tokens)`fan-in helper builds
a derived token that fires on first input cancel (useful for
deadline-OR-user-cancel patterns); fan-in is one-way — cancelling
the derived token does NOT propagate back to inputs. Thread-safe:
a`threading.Lock`guards the flip + the asyncio.Event notification,
and the test suite races 8 threads through`cancel()`to verify
exactly one transition + exactly one callback fire. 32 tests in`tests/test_cancellation.py`across 7 areas: basic token surface
(6 — defaults, custom reason, flip, idempotency, cancelled_at
stability);`raise_if_cancelled`sync + async (4); exception class
(3 — subclass of asyncio CancelledError, reason field, default);
async wait_cancelled (3 — immediate when already cancelled, blocks
until cancel, multiple waiters); on_cancel callbacks (4 —
registration order, late-registration fires immediately, listener
exceptions swallowed, fires only once); CancellationGroup (7 —
not cancelled, cancel_all, parent→child propagation, post-cancel
child cancelled, one-child does not propagate up, children
snapshot is copy, custom child reason); join_tokens (4 — empty
raises, single token, fires on first cancel, already-cancelled
fires immediately, cancel-derived no-back-propagate); concurrency
(1 — 8-thread race produces exactly one transition + one callback
fire). All pure Python; no upstream deps; ruff clean. Consumers:
the existing executor's`\_check_cancel`pattern can swap to`token.raise_if_cancelled()`; MAGE-side cancel via
`MAGEGenerator(progress=poster, cancel=token)` is the next
  integration step.\*
- **[DONE]** Background task registry — `TaskList` widget that lists all active
  generations, executions, evolutions, and lets the user switch focus or kill.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/runtime/task_registry.py` ships the
  **state model** behind the future TaskList widget. `TaskRegistry` is
  a thread-safe in-memory store of `TaskRecord(id, kind, label, status,
started_at, finished_at, error_message, metadata, token)` rows;
  frozen records (UI can snapshot safely) with `token` excluded from
  `__eq__` so two snapshots of the same task compare equal regardless
  of which cancellation token instance they carry. `TaskKind` literal
  pins the canonical set (`mage_generation | carl_execution |
platform_evolution | memory_sync | other`) for grouping; `TaskStatus`
  pins the state machine (`pending → running → completed | failed |
cancelled` — terminal stays terminal). State mutators
  (`mark_running`, `mark_completed`, `mark_failed`, `cancel`) validate
  source state and raise `TaskRegistryError("cannot transition")` on
  illegal moves so screens fail loudly instead of silently resurrecting
  a done task. `register(_, kind, label, token=None, metadata=None,
  task*id=None)`issues a fresh UUID hex id when none supplied,
attaches a default`CancellationToken`when caller doesn't pass one,
rejects duplicate ids.`cancel(task_id, *, reason=None)`is
idempotent on already-terminal tasks (user can smash Esc twice
without 500), flips the bound token AND transitions the record,
records the cancel reason in`metadata`. `clear(task*id)`only
touches terminal tasks (refuses to drop a running task — call cancel
first);`clear_finished()`bulk-cleans the terminal slice and
returns the count.`list_tasks(*, kind, status, active_only)`snapshot view with three orthogonal filters; sorted pending-first
then by`started_at`ascending so the TaskList renders in arrival
order. **Listener API**:`on_change(callback)`registers`(kind, record) → None`callbacks that fire on every`registered`/`updated`/`removed`event; returns an unsubscribe
closure for screen`on_unmount`. Listener exceptions are swallowed
so one bad subscriber can't break the rest — the same pattern as
`CancellationToken.on_cancel`. **Thread safety**: a single
`threading.Lock`guards every read + write; listener callbacks fire
outside the lock so a slow listener can't deadlock mutators; the
test suite races 8 threads through`register()` to verify zero loss
  - races 4 threads through `cancel()` to verify exactly one
    transition. 40 tests in `tests/test_task_registry.py` across 9
    areas: `TaskRecord` shape (4 — frozen + is_terminal + duration
    lifecycle + token-excluded-from-equality); registration (5 —
    fresh id, default token, caller token + caller id, duplicate
    raises); state machine (7 — pending→running, running→completed
    with metadata merge, running→failed with error message, completed
    directly from pending, terminal can't resurrect, unknown id raises,
    metadata merged not replaced); cancellation (4 — flips token +
    transitions + reason metadata, idempotent on terminal, unknown
    raises, cancel running); clear (4 — terminal removed, unknown
    returns None, non-terminal refused, clear_finished bulk); list_tasks
    (5 — empty, ordering pending-first, kind filter, status filter,
    active_only); listeners (5 — fires on register+updates, exception
    swallowed, unsubscribe works, double-unsubscribe safe, remove
    fires on clear); lookup (3 — **contains**, **len**, get raises);
    concurrency (2 — 8-thread register no loss, 4-thread cancel with
    bad+good listeners no crash). All pure Python; no upstream deps;
    ruff clean.\*
- **[DONE]** Resumable runs: persist `run_state.json` so a crash
  restores the last in-flight job from disk.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.runtime.run_state` with `RunState` frozen dataclass +
    `RunStateStore` atomic JSON store, re-exported from
    `care.runtime`. The in-memory `TaskRegistry` (§1.2 P1)
    already handles session-local multi-task tracking; this
    layer adds the cross-process resume contract on top.
  - **Single-slot by design.** Only one in-flight job is
    persisted at a time — background work like memory syncs
    doesn't write here, only user-initiated runs that the user
    might want to resume. Keeps the schema + the resume prompt
    simple.
  - `RunState(run_id, kind, label, started_at, payload,
schema_version)` with JSON-friendly `to_dict` / `from_dict`
    round-trip. `kind` is a free-form `str` (NOT a `Literal`)
    so adding new job kinds doesn't force a schema bump;
    `payload: dict[str, Any]` is per-kind so CARL-resume reads
    `payload["chain_entity_id"]` while MAGE-resume reads
    `payload["query"]`. Each kind owns its own contract;
    the store stays job-agnostic.
  - `DEFAULT_RUN_STATE_PATH =
~/.local/state/care/run_state.json` — XDG-style location
    keeps state separate from config (`~/.config/care`) and
    caches (`~/.cache`). Pinned as a module constant so
    docs / migration scripts can reference it without
    importing internals.
  - **Atomic writes.** Every `save()` goes through
    `tempfile.mkstemp` in the same directory + `os.replace`
    (matches `care.sandbox.trust.SkillTrustStore` and
    `care.runtime.draft.DraftSession`), so a crash mid-write
    leaves the prior snapshot intact. Parent directories are
    auto-created. Tempfile cleanup is best-effort if `replace`
    fails so a partial write doesn't leave `.run_state-*.tmp`
    files lying around.
  - **Tolerant `load()`.** Returns `None` for FIVE distinct
    failure modes, all meaning "nothing to resume": file
    missing, file unreadable (OSError), JSON malformed, JSON
    not a dict, schema_version mismatch, missing required
    field on `from_dict`. CARE's resume flow only ever needs
    a binary "do I have something to offer the user?" — broken
    state shouldn't block startup. Matches CARE's "loud config
    errors, quiet state errors" stance.
  - **Schema versioning.** `SCHEMA_VERSION = 1`. Older
    snapshots are dropped on load (not migrated) so a CARE
    upgrade doesn't choke on a snapshot from the prior
    version. The dropped file is left on disk so a user
    inspecting `~/.local/state/care/` can see what happened.
  - `clear()` returns `bool` (True if a file was removed,
    False if there was nothing to remove) and is idempotent.
    Called on graceful run completion so a successful run
    doesn't leave a stale "resume?" prompt for next startup.
    `FileNotFoundError` is swallowed; other OSError (e.g.
    read-only FS) propagates — the caller wants to know.
  - **Thread-safe.** Internal `threading.Lock` guards every
    public method so TUI + worker threads can both touch the
    store without races. 16-thread concurrent-save stress
    test verifies the file ends up well-formed (not a torn
    mix) and matches one of the writes.
  - Tilde expansion on the path arg — `RunStateStore("~/state.json")`
    works in configs.

  **Tests (`tests/test_run_state.py`, 26 cases):**
  - RunState shape: `to_dict` includes all fields including
    `schema_version`; `from_dict` is the inverse; default
    `payload={}` is independent across instances (regression
    guard for shared-mutable-default); default `started_at`
    via factory yields a sensible float; frozen-dataclass
    assertion; `from_dict` raises KeyError on missing
    `run_id`; coerces stringy/None values (started_at="12345.0",
    payload=None → 0.0 + {}).
  - Save + load: round-trip with full state object; nested
    parent dirs created; emitted file is valid JSON with
    sorted keys + schema_version stamp; second save
    overwrites cleanly (loaded state is the new one); no
    leftover tempfiles after multiple saves; default path
    constant pinned; tilde expansion via $HOME.
  - load() tolerance: missing file → None; malformed JSON →
    None; payload that's a list (not dict) → None;
    schema_version mismatch → None; missing required field
    → None.
  - clear(): returns True after save then removes file;
    returns False when file missing; idempotent (True then
    False); load() returns None after clear().
  - Concurrency: 16-thread concurrent-save stress yields a
    well-formed file matching one writer's payload; 4-thread
    save→clear→save cycle x20 doesn't corrupt or crash.
  - Re-export check: `care.runtime` exports `RunState`,
    `RunStateStore`, `DEFAULT_RUN_STATE_PATH` (so callers
    can `from care.runtime import RunStateStore` without
    knowing the submodule path).

### 1.3 Agent library (P0–P1)

The canonical user flow is: generate Agent A → save → generate B, C → return
to A and re-run. The library is the home of that flow.

- **[DONE] `LibraryScreen` layout** — full-screen
  DataTable of saved agents with columns: ⭐ favourite, name,
  domain, #steps, last_run_at, run_count, fitness (if evolved),
  tags. Sidebar with filters: domain, tag chips, status
  (`draft | runnable | evolved`), "only favourites" toggle.
  *Fully complete:* data layer shipped via §1.3
  `care.runtime.library_view`; the Textual screen (P0.7
  table half + P0.8 sidebar half) consumes
  `fetch_library_view`, renders the 8-column DataTable,
  and re-fetches on every filter change posted by the
  `LibrarySidebar` widget. Domain + tag-chip multi-select
  (P0.14 collections) and sort persistence (P0.10) layer
  on top.
  Search bar (`Ctrl+F`) does fuzzy match on name + description;
  `/` focuses it.

  The Textual DataTable + sidebar are gated on §1 P0 multi-
  screen workflow, but the row projection + filter / sort state
  model + concurrent Memory fetch driver + sort-preference
  persistence land now.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/library_view.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `LibraryRow` — frozen per-row carrying every column the
      DataTable renders: `entity_id`, `entity_type`,
      `display_name`, `name`, `description`, `domain`,
      `favourite`, `tags`, `run_count`, `last_run_at`,
      `step_count`, `fitness`, `is_draft`, `is_evolved`,
      `channel`. Derived `status` ∈ {`draft`, `runnable`,
      `evolved`} drives the sidebar group; `label` falls back
      from display_name → name → first 12 of entity_id.
    - `LibraryFilters` — frozen sidebar state with
      `domain` / `tags` / `status` / `favourites_only` /
      `search` / `namespace` / `channel`. Predicates
      `is_filtering` (drives "Clear filters" visibility) +
      `tag_set` for O(1) membership.
    - `LibrarySort` — frozen sort spec (`field` ∈
      {`last_run_at`, `run_count`, `display_name`,
      `created_at`}, `direction` ∈ {`asc`, `desc`},
      `favourites_first` toggle). Constructor validates the
      field + direction up-front so an invalid sort can't reach
      the wire.
    - `LibraryView` — frozen aggregate (`rows`, applied
      `filters` / `sort`, `total_returned`, `has_more`,
      `next_cursor`) with `__len__` / `__iter__` / `is_empty`
      shortcuts the table footer uses.
    - `parse_library_row(entity)` — pure projection from a
      `gigaevo_client.EntityResponse` (or plain dict).
      Mines `domain` from CARE metadata first, falls back to
      the `domain:{value}` tag; reads fitness from either
      `evolution_meta.fitness_score` or the CARE metadata
      `fitness_score` / `fitness` block; degrades cleanly
      when every optional field is missing.
    - `fetch_library_view(memory, *, filters, sort, limit,
      offset, timeout)` — async driver that calls
      `memory.client.list_chains(...)` with the filter knobs
      (domain auto-prepended to tags as `domain:{value}`,
      status narrows the channel for `draft` / `evolved`),
      projects every row, and applies the client-side
      favourites-first sort (server doesn't expose
      `favourite DESC` as a primary key). Limit clamped
      `[1, 200]`; `has_more` flag based on the page size.
      Per-call timeout via `asyncio.wait_for` so the table
      doesn't freeze on a hung server. Any error wraps as
      `LibraryViewError` so the screen's toast handler stays
      single-branch.
    - Filter mutators: `with_domain`, `with_tags` (strips
      whitespace, drops empties), `with_status` (validates
      against `{draft, runnable, evolved}`),
      `with_favourites_only`, `with_search`, `clear_filters`
      (preserves operator-level `namespace` + `channel`
      while resetting the user-facing knobs).
    - `LibraryViewState` — frozen persistence shape carrying
      `sort` + `filters` (schema-versioned at `1`).
    - `LibraryViewStateStore` — atomic JSON store mirroring
      `RunStateStore`'s contract: default
      `~/.local/state/care/library_view.json`, atomic writes
      via tempfile + `os.replace`, tolerant `load()`
      returning `None` for every failure mode (missing /
      malformed / non-dict / schema-mismatch / invalid
      field), idempotent `clear()`, thread-safe via
      `threading.Lock`. Module-level `save_view_state` /
      `load_view_state` convenience wrappers.

  **Sort behaviour:** the LibraryScreen's default view is
  `last_run_at desc` with `favourites_first=True` — recently
  run agents float up, ⭐ rows pin to the top within their
  partition. The constant `DEFAULT_VIEW_STATE_PATH` is
  re-exported so docs / first-run wizards can reference it
  without importing internals.

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** the fetcher accepts any
  `CareMemory`-like facade exposing
  `.client.list_chains(...)` (or `.​_client.​list_chains`); the
  projection accepts dicts OR `EntityResponse` model objects
  via attribute-or-dict reads. Tests use lightweight stubs —
  no SDK / HTTP / real Memory touched.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_library_view.py`, 52 cases):
  - **parse_library_row (13):** happy path, domain from tag,
    domain from CARE block wins over tag, draft status,
    draft via channel, evolved from fitness, evolved from
    `evolution_meta` column, label fallback chain (display →
    name → entity_id prefix), None entity raises, missing
    optional fields tolerated, ISO datetime with Z parsed,
    invalid datetime → None, attribute-access objects work.
  - **Model shape (5):** row + filters frozen, sort validates
    field + direction, filter predicates, view iter + len +
    is_empty.
  - **Filter mutators (8):** with_domain set + clear,
    with_tags strips whitespace, with_status known + unknown
    raises, with_favourites_only, with_search, clear_filters
    preserves operator settings.
  - **fetch_library_view (13):** happy path with default
    sort, favourites_first disabled passes server order,
    every filter knob forwarded (incl. tags merged with
    auto-domain), status=draft narrows channel + adds tag,
    status=evolved narrows channel, limit clamped [1, 200],
    has_more when page full, no_more below limit, missing
    client raises, SDK exception wraps, timeout wraps,
    unexpected type wraps, `_client` accessor works.
  - **Persistence (10):** roundtrip preserves every field,
    missing/malformed/non-dict/schema-mismatch all → None,
    invalid status collapses to None within state (load
    returns state), clear idempotent, save creates parent
    dirs, atomic save leaves no `.library_view-*` leftovers,
    8-thread concurrent save no corruption, default path
    constant pinned at `~/.local/state/care/library_view.json`.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1583 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future LibraryScreen:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      fetch_library_view, LibraryFilters, LibrarySort,
      LibraryViewError, load_view_state, save_view_state,
      LibraryViewState, with_search, with_status,
  )

  class LibraryScreen(Screen):
      def on_mount(self) -> None:
          # Restore the user's last sort / filter preferences.
          state = load_view_state()
          self.filters = state.filters if state else LibraryFilters()
          self.sort = state.sort if state else LibrarySort()
          self.run_worker(self._refresh, exclusive=True, group="library")

      async def _refresh(self) -> None:
          try:
              view = await fetch_library_view(
                  self.app.memory,
                  filters=self.filters,
                  sort=self.sort,
              )
          except LibraryViewError as exc:
              self.app.push_toast(str(exc))
              return
          self._populate_table(view)
          # Persist any change to the user's preferences.
          save_view_state(LibraryViewState(
              sort=self.sort, filters=self.filters,
          ))
  ```

  The future SidebarChips widget calls `with_status(...)` /
  `with_tags(...)` etc. on each toggle and re-runs the worker;
  the Search input pipes through `with_search()`.

  `Enter` opens, `R` runs, `E` edits, `F` favourites, `Del`

  *Fully complete:* data layer

  `LibraryScreen` (P0.11). The screen ships `BINDINGS` for
  `R` / `E` / `D` / `V` / `L` / `F` / `Delete` plus `Enter`

  status gating and routes to the shipped mutators
  (`toggle_favourite_row` / `delete_row` / `duplicate_chain`)
  on a worker. Destructive `delete` pushes a new

  `push_screen_wait` and aborts on cancel. Navigation-only
  kinds (`run` / `open` / `edit` / `evolve` / `show_lineage`)

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/row_actions.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `RowActionKind` literal pinning the eight canonical
      action names (`run`, `open`, `edit`, `duplicate`,
      `evolve`, `show_lineage`, `toggle_favourite`, `delete`).
    - `RowAction` — frozen descriptor (`kind`, `label`,
      `key_binding`, `requires_confirm`, `description`,
      `enabled_for_status` frozenset). Derived
      `is_destructive` predicate drives the confirm prompt
      gate.
    - `RowMutationOutcome` — frozen mutation result
      (`entity_id`, `success`, `error`, `detail` dict).

      TODO's order, key bindings matching the spec exactly
      (R, Enter, E, D, V, L, F, Delete). `evolve` +
      `show_lineage` gated on `enabled_for_status =
      {runnable, evolved}` so draft chains hide them.
    - `actions_for_row(row, *, registry)` — pure projection
      filtering by `LibraryRow.status`. Preserves declaration
      order.
    - `find_action_by_key(key)` — case-insensitive dispatch
      lookup for the Textual key handler.
    - `find_action_by_kind(kind)` — canonical-name lookup.
    - `is_destructive(action)` — accepts either `RowAction`
      or a bare kind string.

      — async helper that flips (or sets) the favourite
      column via `client._mark_favourite`. Routes via the
      row's typed `entity_type`. Returns the previous +
      current state on the outcome's `detail` dict.
    - `delete_row(memory, row, *, timeout)` — async helper
      that soft-deletes via `client._delete_entity`. The
      modal's confirmation prompt is the user-facing
      safeguard; this layer just fires the call.
    - `duplicate_chain(memory, row, *, new_name, timeout)`
      — async helper that round-trips
      `get_chain_dict(entity_id)` → `save_chain(...,
      entity_id=None)` (forces create). Default name
      synthesises `"{original} (copy)"`. Carries tags over.
      Unwraps either raw-content OR EntityResponse-shaped
      payloads so the save_chain call always sees a plain
      chain dict.
    - `RowActionError` for caller-mistake cases (missing
      `.client` attribute on the facade).

  **Action → existing data layer mapping** (no duplication
  with previously-shipped helpers):

  | Action            | Calls                                          |
  | ----------------- | ---------------------------------------------- |
  | Run               | `load_run_plan` + `execute_library_run`        |
  | Open              | (pure UI — push InspectionScreen)              |
  | Edit              | (pure UI — push EditAgentScreen)               |
  | Duplicate         | `duplicate_chain` (new helper, this module)    |
  | Evolve            | `start_evolution` on `CarePlatform`            |
  | Show lineage      | `fetch_chain_lineage`                          |
  | Toggle favourite  | `toggle_favourite_row` (new, this module)      |
  | Delete            | `delete_row` (new, this module)                |

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** mutators accept any
  `CareMemory`-like facade exposing `.client` (or `._client`)
  with the typed-router methods. Per-call HTTP failures land
  on `outcome.error` rather than raising — matches the
  bulk-ops contract.

  **What this enables for the future LibraryScreen:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      actions_for_row, find_action_by_key, is_destructive,
      toggle_favourite_row, delete_row, duplicate_chain,
      load_run_plan, fetch_chain_lineage,
  )

  class LibraryScreen(Screen):
      BINDINGS = [
          Binding(a.key_binding.lower(), f"row_{a.kind}", a.label)
          for a in default_actions()
      ]

      def context_menu_for(self, row) -> list[MenuItem]:
          return [
              MenuItem(a.label, action=a.kind)
              for a in actions_for_row(row)
          ]

      async def action_row_toggle_favourite(self) -> None:
          row = self.current_row
          outcome = await toggle_favourite_row(self.app.memory, row)
          if not outcome.success:
              self.app.push_toast(outcome.error)
              return
          self.refresh_row(row.entity_id)

      async def action_row_delete(self) -> None:
          row = self.current_row
          confirmed = await self.app.confirm("Delete?", row.label)
          if not confirmed:
              return
          outcome = await delete_row(self.app.memory, row)
          # …
  ```

  The `default_actions()` ordering is also what the
  right-click `ContextMenu` widget renders — single source of
  truth for both keyboard and pointer affordances.
- **[DONE] Sorting** — column headers clickable;
  default sort is `last_run_at DESC` with favourites pinned to
  top. Persist last sort to `~/.local/state/care/library_view.json`.
  *Fully complete:* data layer (`LibrarySort` +
  `LibraryViewState` + atomic JSON persistence at
  `DEFAULT_VIEW_STATE_PATH`); the Textual `LibraryScreen`
  consumes it via P0.10 — `COLUMN_SORT_FIELDS` maps the Name
  / Last Run / Runs columns to sort fields,

  repeat-click and resets to `desc` on field switch,
  `_save_view_state()` persists every change (swallowing
  `OSError` so a read-only FS can't crash the worker), and
  `restore_state=True` in the constructor restores both sort
  + filters from `load_view_state()` on mount. Favourites
  pinning is honoured client-side by
  `_apply_favourites_first()` in `fetch_library_view`

- **[DONE] Empty state** — when memory has zero
  saved agents, show a centered "Create your first agent" CTA
  that opens QueryScreen.
  *Fully complete:* data layer shipped via §1.3
  `care.runtime.empty_state` (classifier + templates); the
  Textual `EmptyStateView` widget (P0.9) consumes the
  classification on the LibraryScreen and renders the
  template, with CTA wiring for `clear_filters` (resets
  filters + syncs sidebar), `retry` (re-runs fetch), and
  `create_first_agent` (logs the click until QueryScreen
  P0.15 lands).

  The Textual empty-state widget is gated on §1 P0 multi-screen
  workflow, but the classifier + canonical message templates
  land now so the widget is a thin renderer.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/empty_state.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `EmptyStateKind` literal pinning the four classifications
      — `no_library` (Memory has zero rows; first-run state),
      `no_results` (namespace has rows but active filters
      hide them all), `loading` (fetch in flight, no prior
      paint), `error` (fetch failed).
    - `EmptyStateAction` literal pinning the four CTA hooks
      the screen wires up — `create_first_agent`,
      `clear_filters`, `retry`, `noop`. The noop sentinel
      lets the loading state render a label without a
      clickable affordance.
    - `EmptyState` — frozen rendering payload (kind, title,
      message, primary_action_kind + label, hint,
      error_detail). `has_action` predicate gates the CTA
      render.
    - `EMPTY_STATE_TEMPLATES` — canonical tuple exposing
      every template so storybook / preview modes can iterate
      them.
    - `classify_empty_state(view, *, filters, is_loading,
      error)` — pure projection picking the right state.
      Precedence: error → loading-before-first-paint →
      no_results (filters active) → no_library (truly
      empty). Returns `None` when the view has rows so the
      screen renders the table normally. Loading state
      ignored when a view already exists (refresh in flight
      shouldn't blank the table mid-render).

  **Classifier precedence rules** (pinned by 13 tests):
  1. `error` (truthy) → error state, regardless of `view` /
     `is_loading`. The user sees the failure rather than a
     stale "loading" or "no results" placeholder.
  2. `is_loading=True` AND `view is None` → loading state
     (first-paint).
  3. `view.is_empty` AND filters active (either caller-
     supplied or carried by the view) → no_results.
  4. `view.is_empty` AND no filters → no_library
     (first-run state).
  5. Rows present → `None` (table renders).

  **User-facing copy pinned by tests** so the screen + tests
  stay in lockstep:

  - **no_library**: title `"Your library is empty"`, CTA
    label `"Create your first agent"`, hint about Ctrl+N.
  - **no_results**: title `"No agents match your filters"`,
    CTA label `"Clear filters"`.
  - **loading**: title `"Loading…"`, no CTA.
  - **error**: title `"Couldn't load your library"`, CTA
    label `"Retry"`, diagnostic detail stamped onto
    `error_detail`.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_empty_state.py`, 23 cases):
  - **Classifier (13):** returns None on rows present,
    no_library on zero+no_filters, no_results with caller
    filters, no_results via view filters, loading first-
    paint, loading doesn't blank existing view, loading
    ignored when view present + empty, error wins over
    loading, error wins over rows (mid-refresh failure),
    empty error string doesn't trigger error state, None
    view falls to no_library, caller filters precedence,
    view filters used when caller missing, caller-empty
    filters fall through to view filters.
  - **Shape (4):** frozen, has_action predicate, templates
    tuple covers all 4 kinds, templates have non-empty
    labels where appropriate.
  - **Message templates (4):** pinned title/CTA text per
    spec; loading has noop+empty label; error stamps detail.
  - **Re-exports (2):** symbols + literals accessible via
    `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1768 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future widget:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      classify_empty_state, EmptyStateAction,
      with_search, with_status, clear_filters,
  )

  class LibraryScreen(Screen):
      async def _refresh(self) -> None:
          self.is_loading = True
          try:
              view = await fetch_library_view(
                  self.app.memory,
                  filters=self.filters,
                  sort=self.sort,
              )
          except LibraryViewError as exc:
              self._render_empty(
                  classify_empty_state(None, error=str(exc))
              )
              return
          finally:
              self.is_loading = False
          state = classify_empty_state(view, filters=self.filters)
          if state is None:
              self._render_table(view)
          else:
              self._render_empty(state)

      def on_empty_action(self, kind: EmptyStateAction) -> None:
          if kind == "create_first_agent":
              self.app.push_screen(QueryScreen())
          elif kind == "clear_filters":
              self.filters = clear_filters(self.filters)
              self.run_worker(self._refresh)
          elif kind == "retry":
              self.run_worker(self._refresh)
  ```
- **[DONE] Bulk operations** — multi-select with
  `Space`, then `T` to tag, `F` to favourite, `Del` to delete.
  Tag editor is a modal with the existing tag set as chips +
  free-form input.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/bulk_ops.py`) +
  Textual key handler on `LibraryScreen` (P0.13). The screen
  carries `bulk_selection: BulkSelection`, binds `Space` to
  toggle the focused row in/out of the selection, `Escape` to
  clear, and routes `F` / `Delete` through
  `apply_favourite` / `apply_delete` when
  `is_bulk_active` is true (per-row dispatch otherwise).
  Bulk-delete pushes the shipped `ConfirmModal` ahead of the
  call. Favourite intent: promote-all when any row is
  unfavourited, unfavourite-all when every selected row is
  already starred. `T` logs `tag_edit` against every
  selected target — the TagEditorModal lands in P0.22 and
  the wiring is already in place. `last_bulk_result` carries
  the :class:`BulkOperationResult` aggregate so the future
  toast renderer can render `"3/5 ok, 2 failed"` without
  reaching back into the worker.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/bulk_ops.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `BulkTarget` — frozen row snapshot (`entity_id` +
      `entity_type` ∈ `chain`/`agent`/`agent_skill` +
      `current_tags` + optional `display_name`). The
      `current_tags` slot is pre-loaded from the LibraryScreen's
      DataTable so the tag-edit helper doesn't re-fetch every
      row.
    - `BulkSelection` — frozen ordered set with `add` /
      `remove` / `toggle` / `clear` / `find` returning new
      instances; `is_empty` / `entity_ids` / `__contains__`
      predicates; iteration in insertion order.
    - `BulkOperationOutcome` — frozen per-target result
      (`target` + `success` + `error` + `duration_ms`) with
      `entity_id` shortcut.
    - `BulkOperationResult` — frozen aggregate with
      `total` / `succeeded` / `failed` / `all_succeeded` /
      `any_failed` / `failures` accessors plus
      `format_summary()` rendering ("favourite: 3/5 ok, 2
      failed") the modal pipes into a toast.
    - `merge_tags(current, *, add, remove)` — pure
      `(current ∪ add) \ remove` with stable order, dedup,
      whitespace-strip, and "remove wins over add" rule for
      the same tag in both lists. Case-sensitive matching.
    - `apply_favourite(memory, selection, *, favourite,
      concurrency, timeout)` — bulk `_mark_favourite` fan-out.
    - `apply_tag_edits(memory, selection, *, add_tags,
      remove_tags, concurrency, timeout)` — composes the new
      tag set per target (via `merge_tags`), falls back to a
      per-target `_get_entity` GET when the target's
      `current_tags` is empty AND `remove_tags` is non-empty
      so the remove pass doesn't silently no-op. Then PATCHes
      via `_update_metadata`. No-op when both add + remove
      lists are empty.
    - `apply_delete(memory, selection, *, concurrency,
      timeout)` — bulk `_delete_entity` fan-out.
    - `BulkOperationError` — raised for caller-mistake cases
      (missing client / missing SDK method). Per-target HTTP
      failures NEVER raise; they land on
      `BulkOperationOutcome.error` so one bad row can't
      crater the whole batch.

  **Concurrency model:** every driver fans out via
  `asyncio.gather` with a bounded `asyncio.Semaphore` (default
  5 in-flight). Per-target `asyncio.wait_for(...)` with the
  caller's `timeout` (default 10s). Output order matches input
  order so the modal can render outcomes next to the table rows.

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** the drivers reach into
  `memory.client` for the SDK's base typed-router methods
  (`_mark_favourite` / `_update_metadata` / `_delete_entity` /
  `_get_entity` — the existing helpers every per-type mixin
  delegates to). Works against either `memory.client` or
  `memory._client` accessors. Tests inject lightweight stubs.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_bulk_ops.py`, 45 cases):
  - **BulkSelection (9):** empty predicates, add appends +
    dedupes, remove drops + no-op, toggle round-trip, clear
    resets, find by id, iter ordering, contains rejects
    non-strings, target frozen.
  - **merge_tags (9):** pure add, pure remove, add+remove,
    dedup existing, add overlapping no-op, remove wins over
    re-add, whitespace stripped, empty strings skipped,
    case-sensitive.
  - **apply_favourite (7):** empty selection, all-succeed
    with typed routing, partial failure carries 503 error,
    unfavourite passes `value=False`, missing client raises,
    missing method raises, output order preserved.
  - **apply_tag_edits (8):** no-op when no tags, no-op on
    whitespace-only, add merged with existing, remove with
    known current_tags + no GET, remove fetches when
    current empty, add-only never fetches, partial failure,
    operation name ("+1 tag, -1 tag").
  - **apply_delete (3):** typed routing, empty no-op,
    partial failure.
  - **Timeout (1):** slow target times out without blocking
    others.
  - **Concurrency (2):** bounded semaphore caps in-flight at
    2 (wall-clock proves), concurrency=1 runs serially.
  - **Result shape (5):** format_summary all-ok / partial /
    empty, iter, outcome frozen.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1423 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future modal:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      BulkSelection, BulkTarget,
      apply_favourite, apply_tag_edits, apply_delete,
  )

  # State carried on LibraryScreen:
  selection = BulkSelection()

  def on_space(self, row) -> None:
      target = BulkTarget(
          entity_id=row.entity_id,
          entity_type=row.entity_type,
          current_tags=tuple(row.tags),
          display_name=row.display_name,
      )
      self.selection = self.selection.toggle(target)

  async def on_press_f(self) -> None:
      result = await apply_favourite(self.app.memory, self.selection)
      self.app.push_toast(result.format_summary())
      self.selection = self.selection.clear()
  ```
- **[DONE] Lineage view** — opens a modal showing the
  evolution tree (ancestors / descendants) of the selected agent
  via Memory's `/v1/chains/{id}/lineage` endpoint (Memory TODO §5).

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/lineage.py`) +
  Textual modal (P0.26).
  `care/screens/lineage.py::LineageModal` is a
  `ModalScreen[LineageResult]` that calls
  `fetch_chain_lineage(memory, entity_id)` on mount and
  renders the DAG via `graph.layers()` (ASCII tree + 5-column
  DataTable). Dismiss envelope carries the selected
  `version_id` so the host calls
  `prime_from_saved_chain(..., version_id=...)` for the
  "Re-run from here" gesture.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/lineage.py` exposes the full projection
    surface, re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `LineageNode` — frozen per-version row enriched with the
      CARE-rendered facts: `version_id` / `version_number` /
      `parents` (tuple) / `depth` / `created_at` / `change_summary`
      / `author` / `fitness` / `generation` / `mutation_kind` /
      `objectives` / raw `evolution_meta`. Derived `is_root` +
      `is_crossover` flags drive the tree-drawing in the modal.
    - `LineageGraph` — frozen aggregate over BFS-ordered nodes
      (`entity_id` / `root_version_id` / `nodes` /
      `max_depth_reached`). Navigation helpers:
      `find(version_id)` for O(N) lookup, `children_of(version_id)`
      for inverse-direction edge rendering, `layers()` for
      depth-grouped iteration, `root` / `best()` for highlights,
      and `fitness_delta(version_id)` that computes the "did
      this node win" delta against the best parent (handles
      crossovers — multi-parent nodes pick max-parent fitness
      as the baseline).
    - `build_lineage_graph(response)` — pure projection from a
      `gigaevo_client.models.LineageResponse` (or any duck-typed
      object exposing the same fields) into the CARE-side view.
      Tolerant: missing optional fields default, unknown extras
      pass through into `LineageNode.evolution_meta`, placeholder
      rows without `version_id` are skipped (rather than raising)
      so a mid-write Memory state doesn't crash the modal.
      Memory typically returns BFS-ordered rows but the projection
      re-sorts by `(depth, version_number)` so the contract
      stays crisp across server changes.
    - `fetch_chain_lineage(memory, entity_id, *, channel,
      version_id, max_depth, timeout)` — wraps the sync SDK
      call in `asyncio.to_thread` with a per-call deadline so
      the modal doesn't freeze on a hung server. Any error —
      timeout, HTTP failure, malformed response — surfaces as
      a single `LineageError` so the modal's toast handler
      stays single-branch. Accepts both `memory.client` (the
      public `CareMemory` accessor) and `memory._client` (the
      legacy underscored alias) so the helper works against
      any facade.
    - `LineageError` — single error class for the modal to
      catch.

  **Fitness extraction precedence** mirrors Memory's server-side
  rules from `docs/EVOLUTION_META.md` §5 P1: `fitness_score` (the
  standardised key) wins over the legacy `fitness` key; non-
  numeric values collapse to `None` so a flaky response doesn't
  crash the projection.

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** the fetch helper accepts any
  `CareMemory`-like facade exposing `.client.get_chain_lineage`;
  the projection accepts dicts OR SDK model objects (same field
  names either way via attribute-or-dict reads). Tests use
  lightweight stubs — no SDK / HTTP / real Memory touched.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_lineage.py`, 34 cases):
  - **build_lineage_graph (13):** minimal root-only,
    evolution_meta field extraction, legacy `fitness` fallback,
    `fitness_score` wins over legacy, non-numeric fitness →
    None, ISO datetime parsed, missing `entity_id` raises,
    missing `root_version_id` raises, empty versions list
    succeeds, unknown fields pass through, malformed rows
    skipped, BFS sort by depth + version_number, crossover
    detection.
  - **LineageGraph (12):** find existing/unknown, children_of
    single + multi-parent, layers grouped by depth, empty graph
    layers, root, best picks highest fitness, best is None
    without scores, fitness_delta single-parent, fitness_delta
    crossover picks best parent, no-parent-fitness → None,
    iteration yields nodes.
  - **fetch_chain_lineage (7):** happy path, all kwargs forwarded,
    underscored `_client` attr works, missing client raises,
    SDK exception wraps as `LineageError`, timeout → `LineageError`,
    malformed response → `LineageError`.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.
  - **SDK-shape integration (1):** projection against
    attribute-access SDK-style objects.

  Full CARE suite (1308 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future LineageModal:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import fetch_chain_lineage, LineageError

  class LineageModal(ModalScreen):
      async def on_mount(self) -> None:
          try:
              self.graph = await fetch_chain_lineage(
                  self.app.memory,
                  self.entity_id,
                  max_depth=20,
              )
          except LineageError as exc:
              self.app.push_screen(Toast(str(exc)))
              return
          self._render_layers(self.graph.layers())
          if (best := self.graph.best()) is not None:
              self._highlight(best.version_id)
  ```

  The `fitness_delta()` helper drives the "+0.13" deltas the
  modal shows next to each non-root node; `is_crossover` drives
  the merge marker on multi-parent nodes.
- **[DONE] Re-run with new context** — when the user
  picks `Run` on Agent A, show a `RunContextModal` letting them:
  (a) reuse the original task + files captured at generation time,
  (b) edit the task description, (c) swap context files, (d)
  override LLM model. Submitting goes to ExecutionScreen.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/run_context_draft.py`)
  + Textual modal (P0.21). `care/screens/run_context.py::RunContextModal`
  seeds the form via `extract_run_context_draft(chain)`,
  routes every field edit through the data-layer mutators,
  validates on each change (with `check_files=False`), and
  dismisses with `RunContextResult(submitted, draft)` so the
  host hands the draft to `apply_overrides(config, draft)` +
  `build_extra_kwargs(draft)` before the `execute_library_run`
  call.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/run_context_draft.py` ships the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `ContextFile` — frozen per-row file ref carrying
      `path` / `sha256` / `size_bytes` / `mime_type` plus a
      `status` field (`"saved"` / `"added"` / `"replaced"` /
      `"dropped"` / `"missing"`) so the modal can colour-code
      rows + offer undo on dropped saved files. Derived
      `is_active` predicate excludes `dropped` rows from the
      active run set; `is_user_edit` flags rows the user
      touched.
    - `RunContextDraft` — frozen form state with
      `source_entity_id` / `source_name` / `original_task` /
      `task_description` / `files` / `model_override` /
      `provider_override` / `streaming_enabled` /
      `extra_files` / `metadata`. Predicates `task_edited` /
      `has_overrides` / `has_file_edits` / `has_edits` drive
      the modal's "Run" vs. "Run (modified)" button label;
      `active_files` returns the rows the upcoming run sees
      (drops excluded).
    - `RunContextIssue` — frozen validation finding the modal
      renders inline (`severity` + `field` + `message` +
      optional `detail`).
    - `extract_run_context_draft(chain, *, source_name)` —
      pure projection from a saved chain (CARL
      `ReasoningChain`, dict, or any object with
      `get_care_metadata()`) into the initial draft state.
      Reads `task_description` + `context_files` +
      `display_name` from the CARE metadata block; tolerates
      missing fields and SDK model objects (via `model_dump`)
      OR plain dicts.
    - Mutator helpers — `set_task`, `add_file`, `drop_file`
      (saved files kept in tuple for undo; user-added rows
      vanish outright), `restore_file` (undo a drop on a
      saved file; no-op otherwise), `replace_file` (swap
      sha256/size/mime, flip status to `"replaced"`),
      `set_model_override` (set OR clear via `None`). Every
      mutator returns a new frozen draft so undo is a trivial
      list of past instances.
    - `validate_run_context_draft(draft, *, check_files)` —
      surfaces issues for empty task, missing files
      (statted on disk, only for active rows), and blank-but-
      non-None overrides. `check_files=False` skips disk I/O.
    - `apply_overrides(config, draft)` — projects the draft's
      per-run model/provider overrides onto a `model_copy`
      of the `CareConfig` so the session-wide config stays
      untouched. Returns the original when no overrides
      are set (zero-copy fast path).
    - `build_extra_kwargs(draft)` — bundles the modal's
      edits into kwargs for the pre-shipped
      `prime_from_saved_chain()`: edited task lands on
      `outer_context=`, edited files land on `files=` (a dict
      keyed by path) with `load_files_from_metadata=False` so
      the modal has full control. Missing files collapse to
      empty strings rather than raising — CARE's executor
      surfaces step-level errors for that.

  **Single call site for the modal:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      extract_run_context_draft, validate_run_context_draft,
      apply_overrides, build_extra_kwargs,
      prime_from_saved_chain, execute_chain_async,
  )

  draft = extract_run_context_draft(chain, source_name=name)
  # User edits → modal calls set_task / add_file / drop_file
  # / replace_file / set_model_override returning new drafts.

  issues = validate_run_context_draft(draft)
  if any(i.severity == "error" for i in issues):
      self._render_issues(issues)
      return

  config = apply_overrides(self.app.config, draft)
  api = build_llm_client(config.mage)
  context = prime_from_saved_chain(
      chain, api=api, **build_extra_kwargs(draft),
  )
  result = await execute_chain_async(chain, context)
  ```

  **Tests** (`tests/test_run_context_draft.py`, 38 cases):
  - **extract_run_context_draft (6):** pulls task + files
    from metadata, empty when no metadata, dict chain
    accepted, source_name param wins over display_name,
    Pydantic `model_dump` accepted, missing optional fields
    tolerated.
  - **Predicates (5):** no edits initially, edited task,
    whitespace-only task isn't an edit, overrides set
    flag, dropped file marks file_edit + excluded from
    active_files.
  - **Mutators (8):** add appends with `"added"` status,
    drop user-added removes outright, restore-dropped saved
    file, restore non-dropped no-op, replace flips to
    `"replaced"`, replace unknown path no-op, set_model_override
    clear both, draft is frozen.
  - **Validation (7):** clean draft yields zero issues,
    empty task error, missing file warning, dropped file
    not validated, blank model_override rejected, blank
    provider_override rejected, RunContextIssue is frozen.
  - **apply_overrides (5):** no-overrides → same config,
    model-only applied (original untouched), provider-only,
    both, non-`model_copy` object passed through unchanged.
  - **build_extra_kwargs (5):** no edits → empty dict, task
    edit → outer_context, dropped file → load_files_from_metadata=False
    + dropped excluded, added file in payload with content,
    missing file collapses to empty string.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1346 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.
- **[DONE] Side-by-side comparison** — multi-select
  two agents, press `D` → diff modal showing prompt/step
  differences (Memory's `diff_versions` works here too once
  both agents share an ancestor).

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/agent_diff.py`) +
  Textual modal (P0.27). `care/screens/diff.py::DiffModal`
  is a `ModalScreen[DiffResult]` that calls
  `fetch_agent_diff(memory, left, right)` on mount and
  renders title / metadata diff / per-step rows
  (`+ / − / ~ / ·` badges + indented field diffs) + footer
  showing `diff.format_summary()`. The Memory SDK's
  `client.diff_versions(entity_id, from, to)` handles the
  same-entity / lineage-walk case server-side; this modal
  consumes the "two arbitrary library entries" client-side
  projection.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/agent_diff.py` exposes the full projection
    surface, re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `FieldDiff` — frozen leaf-value row carrying `field`
      (dotted path inside the step content),
      `left_value` / `right_value`, `left_present` /
      `right_present` (key-absent vs. value-falsy distinction
      the modal colour-codes).
    - `StepDiff` — frozen per-step diff entry: `number`
      (canonical pairing key), `kind` ∈ {`added`, `removed`,
      `modified`, `unchanged`}, `title_*` + `step_type_*`
      surfaced for header rendering, `fields` tuple carrying
      the field-level breakdown. `is_change` predicate +
      `label` accessor (right wins on modified, falls back to
      left for removed, then `"Step N"`).
    - `MetadataDiff` — frozen chain-level diff
      (`display_name`, `description`, `task_description` as
      `FieldDiff`s; tag set-diff exposed as `added_tags` /
      `removed_tags` sorted tuples). `has_changes` predicate.
    - `AgentDiff` — frozen aggregate (sides + steps +
      metadata) with `added_steps` / `removed_steps` /
      `modified_steps` / `unchanged_steps` counters,
      `has_changes` predicate, `format_summary()` footer
      rendering ("+1 · -1 · ~1 of 4 steps").
    - `diff_chains(left, right, *, left_entity_id,
      right_entity_id, left_label, right_label)` — pure
      comparison. Accepts:
        * CARL `ReasoningChain` (via `to_dict()`).
        * Plain dicts in the SDK's `get_chain_dict()` shape
          (`{steps, content: {metadata: {care: {...}}}}`).
        * Flatter dicts (`{steps, display_name, ...}`).
        * Any duck-typed object via `model_dump()` or a final
          attribute-fallback.
      Steps are paired by `number`. Re-numbered steps surface
      as one removal + one addition (fuzzy pairing is a future
      enhancement).
    - `fetch_agent_diff(memory, left_entity_id, right_entity_id,
      *, left_label, right_label, channel, timeout)` — async
      helper. Two fetches run concurrently via
      `asyncio.gather` so the wall-clock floor is one timeout,
      not two. Per-call deadline via `asyncio.wait_for`. Any
      error — empty entity id, missing SDK method, timeout,
      HTTP failure, chain "not found" — wraps as
      `AgentDiffError` so the modal's catch clause stays
      single-branch.
    - `AgentDiffError` / `DiffKind` literal exposed.

  **Field-level walk rules:** the projection walks both step
  dicts recursively, emitting one `FieldDiff` per leaf
  mismatch with the dotted path (`config.prompt_template`).
  Dicts compare keyword-by-keyword (added / removed keys
  surface with `left_present=False` or `right_present=False`).
  Lists compare by-element recursively. The walk drops
  transient/runtime-only fields (`sub_chain`, `agents`,
  `base_step`, `metrics`, `cache`) so re-running the same chain
  doesn't churn the diff with caches and metrics — matches the
  documented CARL rebuild contract (PREPARE.md §5.8).

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** projection accepts dicts OR CARL
  chain objects OR any duck-typed shape; async fetch accepts
  any `CareMemory`-like facade exposing
  `.client.get_chain_dict(entity_id, channel)`. Tests use
  lightweight stubs — no SDK / HTTP / real Memory touched.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_agent_diff.py`, 42 cases):
  - **diff_chains step diffs (11):** identical chains all
    unchanged, added on right, removed on left, modified
    records nested field diff, title change surfaces, added
    field present-only-on-right, removed field present-only-
    on-left, steps sorted by number, transient fields dropped
    (metrics churn → unchanged), step_type carried through,
    label preference rule, list-field equality.
  - **diff_chains metadata (4):** display_name change,
    tags added + removed sets, identical metadata no
    changes, task_description change.
  - **Aggregate accessors (5):** format_summary no-diff,
    counts each kind ("+1 · -1 · ~1"), labels from metadata,
    label overrides, entity_ids stamped.
  - **Frozen models (4):** FieldDiff / StepDiff / MetadataDiff
    / AgentDiff are frozen.
  - **Coercion (4):** to_dict objects, model_dump objects,
    flat chain dict, None treated as empty.
  - **Async fetch (12):** happy path, concurrent fetch
    (wall-clock proof under 0.09s for two 0.05s fetches),
    empty left/right id raises, missing client raises,
    left/right not-found raises, SDK exception wraps,
    timeout wraps, labels propagate, `_client` accessor
    works, custom channel forwarded.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1625 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future modal:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      fetch_agent_diff, AgentDiffError,
  )

  class DiffModal(ModalScreen):
      async def on_mount(self) -> None:
          try:
              self.diff = await fetch_agent_diff(
                  self.app.memory,
                  self.left_row.entity_id,
                  self.right_row.entity_id,
                  left_label=self.left_row.label,
                  right_label=self.right_row.label,
              )
          except AgentDiffError as exc:
              self.app.push_screen(Toast(str(exc)))
              return
          if not self.diff.has_changes:
              self._render_no_changes()
              return
          self._render_metadata_diff(self.diff.metadata)
          for step in self.diff.steps:
              if step.is_change:
                  self._render_step_diff(step)
          self.footer.update(self.diff.format_summary())
  ```

  The same-entity lineage case (two versions of the same agent)
  can switch the fetcher to `memory.client.diff_versions(...)`
  and project that JSON-patch response — that's a small
  follow-up; today the client-side `diff_chains(left, right)`
  also works on a `get_chain` of two `version_id`s of the same
  entity, just slightly more expensive than the patch-based
  path.
- **[DONE] Sections / collections** — let the user
  group agents into named collections (just a reserved tag
  prefix `collection:`). Sidebar surfaces collections above tags.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/collections.py`)
  + Textual sidebar wiring (P0.14). `LibrarySidebar` mounts a
  "Collections" `OptionList` (synthetic "All collections" +
  one row per collection with `name (count)` label);
  `LibraryScreen._refresh_collections` runs after every
  fetch, calls `list_collections()`, and feeds
  `sidebar.set_collections(...)`. Click on a node →
  `LibrarySidebar.CollectionSelected(name | None)` →
  `filter_by_collection(filters, name)` (existing tag chips
  preserved so "Marketing ∩ #urgent" works) → persist +
  refresh. The shipped `apply_rename_collection` /
  `apply_delete_collection` workers are wire-ready for the
  P0.22-era rename / delete affordances; the sidebar
  pre-declares a `CollectionActionRequested` message hook
  for that future surface.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/collections.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `COLLECTION_PREFIX = "collection:"` — canonical tag
      prefix. Pinned as a module constant so callers don't
      hard-code the string.
    - `Collection` — frozen sidebar node (`name`,
      `member_count`, `sample_entity_ids` tuple) with
      `tag` accessor (`"collection:<name>"`) + `is_empty`
      predicate.
    - `collection_tag_for(name)` — pure name → tag. Refuses
      empty / whitespace-only names; refuses already-prefixed
      input rather than silently normalising (callers
      double-prefix sometimes; surfacing it loudly is the
      safer default).
    - `collection_name_from_tag(tag)` — inverse helper.
      Returns `None` for non-collection tags + for
      `"collection:"` alone (no bare name).
    - `is_collection_tag(tag)` — single-call predicate.
    - `extract_collections_from_tags(tags)` — pure tag list →
      collection names tuple. Dedupe + insertion order
      preserved.
    - `list_collections(memory, *, namespace, channel,
      sample_cap, fetch_limit, timeout)` — async aggregator
      that asks Memory for every chain in the namespace, mines
      the `collection:` tags, returns sorted `Collection`
      rows (alphabetical, stable). `sample_cap=5` default
      keeps the projection bounded; supports
      `sample_cap=0` for a count-only sidebar render.
      Channel + namespace + limit forwarded to the SDK.
      Wraps timeout / SDK / type errors as `CollectionError`.
    - `filter_by_collection(filters, name)` — pure projection
      from a LibraryFilters into a new one pinned to the
      collection. Strips any existing `collection:` tag from
      the filter (so switching from Marketing → Sales doesn't
      AND both); passing `name=None` strips collection tags
      entirely (the "Show all" sidebar action). Free-form
      tags survive (Marketing ∩ #urgent stays valid).
    - `active_collection_name(filters)` — walks the filter's
      tag list looking for the canonical prefix; returns the
      bare name or `None`. Drives the sidebar's "current
      selection" highlight.
    - `apply_add_to_collection` / `apply_remove_from_collection`
      / `apply_rename_collection` / `apply_delete_collection`
      — thin wrappers over the shipped
      `apply_tag_edits(memory, selection, add_tags=,
      remove_tags=)` so the bulk-mutation surface is uniform.
      Rename refuses no-op (`old==new` after strip) to surface
      caller misuse; `apply_delete_collection` is an explicit
      alias of remove for self-documenting call sites.
    - `CollectionError` — single error class.

  **Why tag-prefix instead of new entity type:** Memory's tag
  column is JSONB string array — zero schema changes. The
  prefix sorts alphabetically near other namespaced tags
  (`domain:`, `status:`) keeping the sidebar tidy. Server-side
  filtering already works via the existing `tags=` AND-filter
  on `list_chains`. No new endpoints needed.

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** aggregator accepts any
  `CareMemory`-like facade exposing `client.list_chains(...)`;
  mutators reuse the existing bulk-ops contract. Tests use
  lightweight stubs.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_collections.py`, 40 cases):
  - **Pure helpers (9):** tag_for happy path + strips
    whitespace + empty raises + double-prefix raises,
    name_from_tag handles non-collection / empty / None /
    `collection:` alone, is_collection_tag,
    extract_collections_from_tags (dedupe + order), empty
    iterable, COLLECTION_PREFIX constant.
  - **Collection model (3):** frozen, tag accessor,
    is_empty.
  - **Filter integration (5):** adds collection tag,
    replaces existing collection tag, `None` strips
    collection tags, active_collection_name on empty +
    pinned, first-wins on malformed input.
  - **list_collections (11):** empty library, aggregates
    counts + samples, sample capped, zero sample cap,
    namespace + channel forwarded, fetch_limit clamped
    [1, 200], missing client raises, SDK exception wraps,
    timeout wraps, unexpected type wraps, `_client`
    accessor works, attribute-access SDK rows, malformed
    meta skipped.
  - **Bulk mutators (8):** add merges with existing tags,
    remove strips collection tag preserving others, rename
    swaps old+new in one PATCH, rename same-name raises
    (incl. after whitespace strip), delete is alias of
    remove, add invalid name raises, empty selection no-op.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1665 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future sidebar:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      list_collections, filter_by_collection, active_collection_name,
      apply_add_to_collection, apply_remove_from_collection,
      apply_rename_collection, apply_delete_collection,
      CollectionError, BulkSelection, BulkTarget,
  )

  class CollectionsSidebar(Vertical):
      async def on_mount(self) -> None:
          try:
              self.collections = await list_collections(self.app.memory)
          except CollectionError as exc:
              self.app.push_toast(str(exc))
              return
          self._render(self.collections)
          self._highlight(active_collection_name(self.app.filters))

      def on_node_clicked(self, name: str) -> None:
          self.app.filters = filter_by_collection(self.app.filters, name)
          self.app.refresh_library()

      async def on_drop_into_collection(
          self, name: str, rows: list,
      ) -> None:
          sel = BulkSelection()
          for r in rows:
              sel = sel.add(BulkTarget(
                  entity_id=r.entity_id, entity_type=r.entity_type,
                  current_tags=tuple(r.tags),
              ))
          result = await apply_add_to_collection(
              self.app.memory, sel, name,
          )
          self.app.push_toast(result.format_summary())
  ```

  Right-click affordances (Rename / Delete) hook into
  `apply_rename_collection` and `apply_delete_collection` with
  the same `BulkSelection` shape — the sidebar pulls members
  from a fresh `list_collections().sample_entity_ids` (for the
  small case) or a dedicated `list_chains(tags=[collection:X])`
  fetch (for large collections).
- **[DONE] Export / import** — `LibraryScreen` action
  exports selected agents as `.tar.gz` of JSON chain dumps +
  skill SHA pins, suitable for sharing.

  *Fully complete:* data layer
  (`care/runtime/library_bundle.py`) + Export modal (P0.30) +
  Import modal (P0.31). `care/screens/export.py::ExportModal`
  consumes `export_library_bundle`;
  `care/screens/import_bundle.py::ImportModal` previews via
  `read_bundle_manifest` and submits through
  `import_library_bundle(memory, path, on_collision=,
  namespace=, dry_run=)`. The LibraryScreen-side menu wiring
  that pushes either modal lives alongside the CommandPalette
  entry shipped in P0.25.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/library_bundle.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - On-disk layout: top-level `manifest.json` + `chains/<id>.json`
      + `agent_skills/<id>.json`. Manifest schema-versioned at 1.
    - `BundleManifest` — frozen manifest projection (`schema_version`,
      `created_at`, `source_namespace`, tuples of
      `BundleEntry`). `total_entries` predicate.
    - `BundleEntry` — frozen per-row (entity_id + file path +
      display_name for chains, name + sha256 for skills).
    - `BundleExportResult` / `BundleImportResult` — frozen
      outcome rows with `success` predicate. Export carries
      `skipped_chains` / `skipped_skills` (per-row fetch
      failures don't crater the whole batch). Import carries
      `imported_count` / `skipped_count` / `failed_count` +
      `failures` tuple + parsed `manifest`.
    - `CollisionPolicy = Literal["skip", "overwrite", "raise"]`
      — `skip` strips entity_id (forces create), `overwrite`
      retains it (forces version-bump), `raise` documented
      for future server-side pre-flight.
    - `LibraryBundleError` — single error class.
    - `export_library_bundle(memory, entity_ids, output_path,
      *, skill_entity_ids, source_namespace, channel,
      timeout)` — async. Fetches each entity via the SDK's
      typed accessors (`get_chain_dict` + `get_agent_skill_dict`
      with `get_agent_skill` fallback), serialises to JSON via
      `model_dump(mode="json")` (datetime-safe), writes a
      tarball atomically (tempfile + `os.replace`, no
      `.bundle-*` leftovers on partial writes), auto-creates
      parent dirs. Per-entity failures land on
      `skipped_*` rather than raising. Required SDK methods
      checked up-front before any I/O.
    - `import_library_bundle(memory, tarball_path, *,
      on_collision, namespace, dry_run, timeout)` — async.
      Reads the manifest, extracts each `EntityResponse`
      payload, projects to `bulk_save` items (drops runtime-
      only fields like `etag`, `version_id`), stamps the
      target namespace, then calls
      `client.bulk_save(items)`. `dry_run=True` returns the
      counts as if it succeeded without touching the server.
      Empty bundles return a successful no-op.
    - `read_bundle_manifest(path)` — pure helper that reads
      JUST the manifest (no full unpack) so the import modal
      can preview "5 chains + 2 skills" before the user
      commits. Validates schema_version + JSON shape; raises
      `LibraryBundleError` with a friendly message on every
      drift.

  **Atomic write semantics:** export writes through
  `tempfile.mkstemp(dir=output.parent)` + `os.replace`. A
  crash mid-write leaves the previous bundle intact rather
  than a partial / corrupted file. Tempfile cleanup is best-
  effort on failure to avoid `.bundle-*` leftover paths.

  **Schema versioning:** `_BUNDLE_SCHEMA_VERSION = 1`. Newer
  bundles surface a friendly "upgrade CARE" error rather than
  silently misreading. Older bundles compatible with future
  versions land via the existing `_manifest_from_dict`
  projection (additive fields tolerated; required fields
  checked).

  **Tests** (`tests/test_library_bundle.py`, 35 cases):
  - **Model shape (7):** all four dataclasses are frozen,
    success/total predicates, total_entries predicate.
  - **Export (10):** writes tarball with manifest + chains,
    manifest readable post-export, skills included with
    sha256 + name, missing-chain skipped not aborted,
    chain exception treated as skip, empty entity_ids
    writes empty manifest, missing-client raises, missing-
    method raises (chain), skill-method missing raises ONLY
    when skills requested, atomic write leaves no leftovers,
    creates parent dirs.
  - **read_bundle_manifest (5):** missing file raises,
    manifest-missing-inside raises, malformed JSON raises,
    unsupported schema_version raises, missing
    schema_version raises.
  - **Import (12):** round-trip export → import preserves
    items + types, dry_run skips bulk_save, namespace
    stamping, skip-collision strips entity_id,
    overwrite keeps entity_id, failed items surface on
    `failures`, missing bulk_save returns error,
    missing bundle file returns error, bulk_save
    exception wraps, timeout wraps, empty bundle is a
    successful no-op.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1700 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future modals:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      export_library_bundle, import_library_bundle,
      read_bundle_manifest, LibraryBundleError,
  )

  class ExportModal(ModalScreen):
      async def on_confirm(self, output_path: Path) -> None:
          ids = [r.entity_id for r in self.selected_rows]
          skill_ids = sorted({
              s for r in self.selected_rows for s in r.allowed_skills
          })
          result = await export_library_bundle(
              self.app.memory, ids, output_path,
              skill_entity_ids=skill_ids,
              source_namespace=self.app.config.namespace,
          )
          if not result.success:
              self.app.push_toast(f"Export failed: {result.error}")
              return
          self.app.push_toast(
              f"Wrote {result.chain_count} chains + "
              f"{result.skill_count} skills to {result.path}"
          )

  class ImportModal(ModalScreen):
      async def on_mount(self) -> None:
          try:
              self.manifest = read_bundle_manifest(self.path)
          except LibraryBundleError as exc:
              self.app.push_toast(str(exc))
              self.dismiss()
              return
          self._render_preview(self.manifest)

      async def on_confirm(self) -> None:
          result = await import_library_bundle(
              self.app.memory, self.path,
              namespace=self.app.config.namespace,
              on_collision=self.collision_policy.value,
          )
          if not result.success:
              self.app.push_toast(f"Import failed: {result.error}")
              return
          self.app.push_toast(
              f"Imported {result.imported_count} entities "
              f"({result.failed_count} failed)"
          )
  ```

## 2. Configuration & secrets (P0–P1)

- **[DONE]** `care/config.py` — Pydantic `CareConfig` loaded from
  `~/.config/care/config.toml` and `$CARE_*` env vars. Fields:
  - `mage` → full `MAGEConfig` block (mode, provider, api_key, base_url,
    enable_memory_research, enable_web_research, web_search_api_key, …).
  - `memory.base_url`, `memory.api_key`.
  - `platform.base_url`, `platform.api_key`.
  - `sandbox.kind` (`local | docker | e2b | firejail`), `sandbox.cpu_limit`,
    `sandbox.mem_limit`, `sandbox.network_policy`, `sandbox.image`,
    `sandbox.pids_limit`.
  - `defaults.language` (`en | ru`), `defaults.max_history_entries`.
    \_Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/config.py` with 5 nested Pydantic models
    (`MageConfig` extra=allow for forward-compat with new MAGE knobs,
    `MemoryConfig`, `PlatformConfig`, `SandboxConfig`, `DefaultsConfig`)
    plus top-level `CareConfig(extra="forbid")` so typo-section names
    (`[platfrom]`) fail loudly. Loader merges TOML + `CARE\__` env vars
    with double-underscore nesting (`CARE_MAGE\_\_MODE=fast`); env wins
    over TOML, TOML wins over defaults. `SandboxConfig.mem_limit` field
    validator accepts Docker-style suffixes (`512m`, `1g`, `4096k`),
    rejects bare ints / unknown suffixes. Added `pydantic>=2.0`runtime
    dep;`pytest`+`ruff`moved to`[project.optional-dependencies].dev`.
    19 tests in `tests/test_config.py` across 6 classes: defaults
    (3 — load with no file + empty env, individual model defaults,
    default-path location); TOML loading (3 — values override defaults,
    unknown top-level section rejected, extra mage keys allowed);
    env overrides (4 — env beats TOML, double-underscore nesting,
    non-prefixed env ignored, boolean coercion); sandbox validation
    (6 — mem_limit suffix + case + bare-int + unknown-suffix + kind
  * network_policy enums); defaults validation (2 — language + range);
    full-example round-trip (1 — README config + one env override).
    All 19 pass; ruff clean.\*
- **[DONE]** First-run wizard (TUI
  `SettingsScreen`) that writes the config if none exists and
  validates connectivity (`memory.health_check()`, MAGE LLM
  ping, Platform `/health`).

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/first_run.py`) +
  Textual `SettingsScreen` (P0.32).
  `care/screens/settings.py::SettingsScreen` mounts the
  three-section form (Memory / Platform / MAGE) + theme
  picker, runs `run_all_probes(current_config())` in
  `action_validate`, and posts
  `SettingsScreen.Saved(SettingsSnapshot)` so the host
  writes the TOML via the shipped writer.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/first_run.py` with the full probe + writer surface,
    re-exported from `care` top-level:
    - `ProbeResult` frozen dataclass: `service`, `status`
      (`"ok" | "skipped" | "failed"`), `latency_ms`, `error`,
      `detail` dict.
    - `FirstRunReport` aggregator with `memory` / `mage` /
      `platform` results + `all_ok` / `any_failed`
      predicates + `format_text()` rendering with status
      badges (`✓` / `·` / `✗`) and per-service latency /
      error.
    - `probe_memory(config, *, memory_factory=None)` —
      builds a :class:`CareMemory` (or uses the injected
      factory) + calls its `health_check()` in a thread so
      the Textual event loop doesn't block on network I/O.
    - `probe_mage(config, *, client_factory=None)` —
      validates MAGE-side connectivity by building an LLM
      client via `care.runtime.build_llm_client` (or the
      injected factory) and capturing its
      `base_url`/`provider`/`model` for the detail dict.
      Full LLM `/models` ping deferred behind the
      `client_factory` hook so callers can swap in a
      deeper probe without changing the surface.
    - `probe_platform(config, *, platform_factory=None)` —
      same shape as memory; hits CarePlatform's
      `/health` endpoint.
    - `run_all_probes(config, ...)` — fans out the three
      probes concurrently via `asyncio.gather` and returns
      the aggregated `FirstRunReport`.
    - `write_initial_config(path, config, *, overwrite=False)`
      — atomic TOML writer (tempfile + `os.replace`) with
      parent-dir auto-create, tilde expansion, and an
      overwrite guard (defaults to refusing to replace an
      existing file because the wizard is first-run-only).
      Returns the resolved absolute path.
  - **Per-service skip semantics.** Probes return
    `status="skipped"` (not `"failed"`) when the relevant
    field on the config is empty (`memory.base_url` /
    `mage.api_key` / `platform.base_url`) — distinguishes
    "user hasn't filled this in yet" from "I tried and the
    service is unreachable." `FirstRunReport.all_ok` treats
    skipped as not-ok so the screen warns about
    half-configured installs, but `any_failed` only counts
    explicit failures so retry-UI doesn't fire on a deliberate
    skip.
  - **Latency stamping** on every attempted probe (even
    failed ones — captures partial round-trip when the
    failure happened mid-request). Skipped probes leave
    `latency_ms=None`.
  - **Duck-typed factories** for testability — same pattern
    every other CARE projector uses. Tests inject
    `_StubMemory` / `_StubPlatform` and a sentinel
    `client_factory` so no SDK / HTTP / real service
    touches the suite.
  - **TOML writer:** hand-rolled emit since stdlib doesn't
    ship a TOML *writer* (only the reader). Sorts sections
    (`mage` → `memory` → `platform` → `sandbox` → `tools` →
    `telemetry` → `defaults`) matching `.env.example`
    layout. Skips `None` values so re-edit produces a
    minimal file. Atomic write via tempfile in the same
    directory followed by `os.replace`; cleanup on partial
    failure prevents `.care-config-*.tmp` leftovers.
  - **Round-trip verified** via `CareConfig.load` — anything
    `write_initial_config` writes loads back to a
    semantically-equal `CareConfig`.

  **Tests (`tests/test_first_run.py`, 27 cases):**
  - **Shape (5):** `ProbeResult` frozen; `FirstRunReport.all_ok`
    is `True` when all ok, `False` on any skipped, `False` on
    any failed; `any_failed` only counts failed (not skipped);
    `format_text()` includes status badges + latency + error.
  - **probe_memory (4):** happy path; skipped on empty
    `memory.base_url`; failure wraps `RuntimeError` into
    `ProbeResult.error` with `RuntimeError:` prefix; non-dict
    `health_check` return coerced into `{"raw": ...}` detail.
  - **probe_mage (4):** skipped on missing/empty api_key;
    happy path via stub client factory captures the
    client's base_url; downstream factory exception wraps.
  - **probe_platform (3):** happy path; skipped; failure
    wraps.
  - **run_all_probes (2):** all-three-ok aggregates to
    `all_ok=True`; partial failure aggregates correctly
    (`memory=failed`, `mage=ok`, `platform=ok` →
    `all_ok=False`, `any_failed=True`).
  - **write_initial_config (9):** writes a valid TOML file
    that round-trips through `tomllib.load`; every nested
    section emitted with defaults; creates parent dirs;
    refuses to overwrite by default; `overwrite=True`
    replaces; atomic write leaves no `.care-config-*.tmp`
    leftovers; tilde expansion via `$HOME`; string path
    accepted; `CareConfig.load(path=)` round-trip preserves
    every field.

  **What this enables for the future `SettingsScreen`:**

  ```python
  from care import (
      CareConfig, run_all_probes, write_initial_config,
      DEFAULT_CONFIG_PATH,
  )

  async def on_validate_pressed(form_values: dict) -> None:
      cfg = CareConfig(**form_values)
      report = await run_all_probes(cfg)
      self.update_status_panel(report.format_text())
      if report.all_ok:
          write_initial_config(DEFAULT_CONFIG_PATH, cfg)
          self.app.pop_screen()
      else:
          self.enable_retry_button()
  ```

  Steps the SettingsScreen still owns (gated on §1 P0): the
  TUI form rendering, the status-panel widget, the
  "Save & continue" button wiring, the post-write
  app-restart flow.

validate`, `care import`) with a one-line description
