  **Tests (`tests/test_env_example.py`, 5 cases):**
  - File exists at `<repo-root>/.env.example`.
  - Every `CARE_*` var in the example maps to a real
    Pydantic field on the matching nested config model. Catches
    typos like `CARE_MAGE__MOEDE` and stale vars that survive a
    config-field rename.
  - Every config field on every section appears in
    `.env.example` at least once (commented or active). Catches
    drift when a new field gets added to `CareConfig` without
    a corresponding `.env.example` stub — the failure message
    lists exactly which `CARE_*` var is missing so the fix is
    one paste.
  - All documented env vars round-trip through `CareConfig.load`
    cleanly (one var per section drives a real config load that
    asserts the field landed on the right model).
  - README mentions `.env.example` + `CARE_` so the docs
    cross-reference stays linked.

  **Symmetry guarantee:** the schema tests run on every CI
  build, so a future config field can't ship without its
  `.env.example` entry — the docs stay in lock-step with the
  code without depending on memory.

- **[DONE]** Per-project overrides — `./care.toml` in cwd takes
  precedence over `~/.config/care/config.toml`.

  **Shipped:**
  - `CareConfig.load(*, path=None, env=None, cwd=None)` now
    layers four sources in documented precedence order:
    defaults < `~/.config/care/config.toml` < `<cwd>/care.toml`
    < `CARE_*` env vars. Per-project knobs win over user-global
    settings without clobbering keys the project file doesn't
    mention (uses the same `_deep_merge` already powering env
    overrides, so nested-section merge semantics are uniform
    across every layer).
  - New `PROJECT_CONFIG_FILENAME = "care.toml"` module
    constant + `cwd=` kwarg (defaults to `Path.cwd()`). Test
    harnesses + first-run wizards can reference the filename
    without importing internals.
  - Explicit `path=` short-circuits the project lookup —
    `care --config foo.toml` produces a single-source-of-truth
    load with no surprise merging from the working directory.
    Matches the convention CLI flags use elsewhere ("explicit
    overrides discovery").
  - Missing per-project file is silent (first-run users in
    fresh checkouts shouldn't get an error); user-global +
    defaults apply normally.

  **Tests (`tests/test_config_project_overrides.py`, 9 cases):**
  - Precedence: project-only with no user file; user-only
    with no project file; project overrides user per-key
    while keeping user keys the project doesn't mention
    (nested-dict merge regression guard); env beats project;
    nested `[mage]` from project merges INTO user's
    `[mage]` table (doesn't replace it wholesale, preserving
    `provider` / `api_key` / `enable_web_research` from user).
  - Cwd behaviour: missing `./care.toml` is silent;
    `cwd=` defaults to `Path.cwd()` (verified via
    `monkeypatch.chdir`); explicit `path=` skips the project
    lookup so explicit-path users don't get blindsided.
  - Constant exposure: `PROJECT_CONFIG_FILENAME == "care.toml"`
    pinned for downstream readers.
  - Test isolation: every test monkeypatches
    `care.config.DEFAULT_CONFIG_PATH` onto `tmp_path` so the
    user's real `~/.config/care/config.toml` is never touched.

- **[DONE] `SaveAgentModal`** — at the end of every
  successful MAGE generation, prompt the user to confirm/edit:
  - `name` (pre-filled with `MAGEMetadata.domain` + first 60
    chars of query; editable; must be non-empty and unique in
    the user's namespace).
  - `description` (pre-filled with the original query verbatim).
  - `tags` (multi-select against existing tags + free-form, plus
    a "Favourite ⭐" toggle that adds the `favourite` tag).

    deletes the auto-saved draft from §3 below.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/save_agent_form.py`)
  + Textual modal (P0.18). `care/screens/save_agent.py::SaveAgentModal`
  is a `ModalScreen[SaveAgentResult]` that seeds the form on
  construction, routes every field edit through the
  `set_display_name` / `set_description` / `set_tags` /
  `toggle_favourite` / `set_keep_context` mutators, debounces
  `validate_save_agent_form` calls at 0.25s, and dismisses
  with a frozen `SaveAgentResult(action, form, outcome)` —
  the three buttons map to `save_inspect` /
  `save_run` / `discard` per the §3 action table.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/save_agent_form.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `FAVOURITE_TAG` — canonical tag name. The "Favourite ⭐"
      checkbox is just sugar around adding/removing this tag
      from the form's tag set; `apply_save_agent_form` routes
      its presence to Memory's dedicated `favourite` column
      and strips it from the tag list (single source of
      truth, no duplication).
    - `SaveAgentForm` — frozen form state with editable fields
      (`display_name`, `description`, `tags`, `keep_context`),
      suggestion snapshots (`suggested_display_name`,
      `suggested_description`, `suggested_tags`) for dirty
      tracking, and read-only generation context (`query`,
      `domain`, `mage_metadata`, `context_files`). Predicates
      `display_name_dirty` / `description_dirty` /
      `tags_dirty` (set semantics) / `favourite` + composite
      `is_dirty()`.
    - `SaveAgentIssue` — frozen inline validation finding.
    - `SaveAgentOutcome` — frozen result (`entity_id`,
      `success`, `promoted`, `metadata_written`, `error`,
      `issues`) — distinguishes "promote landed but PATCH
      failed" so the modal can render the right toast.
    - `seed_save_agent_form(*, query, mage_metadata,
      context_files, suggested_name_override)` — pure
      projection. Pre-fill rules per spec:
      `MAGEMetadata.suggested_display_name` wins → heuristic
      fallback `"<domain> · <first 60 chars of query>"` (with
      `…` ellipsis on truncation); description from
      `suggested_description` → query verbatim; tags from
      `suggested_tags` with `"domain:{value}"` prepended +
      dedup. `suggested_name_override` lets CLI callers
      bypass the heuristic.
    - Mutators: `set_display_name`, `set_description`,
      `set_tags` (whitespace-stripping), `add_tag` /
      `remove_tag` (stable order + dedup), `toggle_favourite`,
      `set_keep_context`. All return new frozen forms.
    - `validate_save_agent_form(form, memory, *, namespace,
      check_unique, timeout)` — sync checks (empty name →
      error, duplicate tags → warning) + async uniqueness
      probe via `memory.client.list_chains(q=name,
      namespace=namespace)` with case-insensitive exact
      match. Network failure during the probe degrades
      silently (modal isn't blocked on a flaky Memory);
      collisions surface on the actual POST.
    - `apply_save_agent_form(memory, session, form, *,
      to_channel, timeout)` — async driver that composes:
      1. Calls `promote_draft(memory, session,
         to_channel=...)` (shipped helper).
      2. Computes the final tag set: strips the sentinel
         `"draft"` tag, deduplicates, routes the favourite
         tag to the `favourite` column via PATCH.
      3. Calls `memory.client._update_metadata(entity_type,
         entity_id, display_name=..., description=...,
         tags=..., favourite=...)` to commit the user's
         edits in a single PATCH.
      Partial-success cases (promote OK but PATCH failed)
      surface via `outcome.promoted=True,
      metadata_written=False, error=...`. Pre-flight errors
      (missing entity_id) raise `SaveAgentError`.

  **Three-action mapping** the modal hooks up:

  | Button         | Calls                                          |
  | -------------- | ---------------------------------------------- |
  | Save & Inspect | `apply_save_agent_form(...)` → `InspectionScreen.push(entity_id)` |
  | Save & Run     | `apply_save_agent_form(...)` → `load_run_plan(...)` → ExecutionScreen |
  | Discard        | `discard_draft(memory, session)` (shipped)     |

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** seeder accepts a `MAGEMetadata`
  instance OR a plain dict OR a Pydantic model with
  `model_dump()`; context files accept SDK `ContextFileRef`
  objects, dicts, or duck-typed objects with `path`/`sha256`
  attributes. Validator + applier accept any `CareMemory`-like
  facade exposing `.client`. Tests use lightweight stubs — no
  SDK / HTTP / real Memory touched.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_save_agent_form.py`, 41 cases):
  - **seed (9):** uses suggested fields, heuristic fallback,
    long-query truncation with `…`, no-metadata empty form,
    dict metadata accepted, context files preserved (both
    SDK + dict shapes), `suggested_name_override` wins, form
    is frozen, duplicate seeded tags deduped.
  - **Mutators (11):** display_name + dirty flag,
    whitespace-only edit not dirty, description, tags strip
    whitespace, add_tag dedupe, remove_tag present/absent,
    toggle_favourite round-trip, set_keep_context,
    add_tag whitespace-only no-op.
  - **Validation (8):** clean form no issues, empty name
    error, duplicate tags warning, unique check collision,
    case-insensitive match, no-collision passes, network
    failure silent, check_unique=False skips, empty name
    skips probe (no wasted bandwidth).
  - **apply (8):** promote then PATCH order + args, favourite
    routed to column + stripped from tag list, missing
    entity_id raises, promote failure surfaces with
    promoted=False, PATCH failure surfaces with promoted=True,
    promote timeout, PATCH timeout keeps promoted flag,
    missing `_update_metadata` returns partial-success
    outcome, to_channel override.
  - **Outcome shape (2):** outcome + issue are frozen.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1531 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future modal:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      seed_save_agent_form, validate_save_agent_form,
      apply_save_agent_form, discard_draft, toggle_favourite,
      set_display_name, set_keep_context,
  )

  class SaveAgentModal(ModalScreen):
      def on_mount(self) -> None:
          self.form = seed_save_agent_form(
              query=self.generation.query,
              mage_metadata=self.generation.mage_result.metadata,
              context_files=self.generation.context_files,
          )
          self._render(self.form)

      async def on_save_pressed(self, then_action: str) -> None:
          issues = await validate_save_agent_form(
              self.form, self.app.memory,
              namespace=self.app.config.namespace,
          )
          if any(i.severity == "error" for i in issues):
              self._render_issues(issues)
              return
          outcome = await apply_save_agent_form(
              self.app.memory, self.draft_session, self.form,
          )
          if not outcome.success:
              self.app.push_toast(outcome.error)
              return
          if then_action == "inspect":
              self.app.push_screen(InspectionScreen(outcome.entity_id))
          elif then_action == "run":
              # Hand off to the §3 P1 Re-run-from-library flow.
              plan = await load_run_plan(
                  self.app.memory, outcome.entity_id,
              )
              ...

      def on_discard_pressed(self) -> None:
          discard_draft(self.app.memory, self.draft_session)
          self.app.pop_screen()
  ```
- **[DONE] Draft auto-save** — immediately after generation completes, the
  chain is written to Memory with channel `draft` (not `latest`) so a crash
  before the user clicks Save doesn't lose work. `SaveAgentModal` promotes
  `draft` → `latest` on accept.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/runtime/draft.py` ships the lifecycle trio
  the future SaveAgentModal calls into — `auto_save_draft(memory, chain,
  _, name, query, domain, ...)`writes via the shipped`CareMemory.save*chain`with`channel="draft"`and a mandatory`DRAFT_TAG = "draft"`stamped on`meta.tags`(deduped against any
user-supplied tags + the`domain:{value}`auto-stamp the facade adds);
returns a mutable`DraftSession`carrier (entity_id / name / domain /
entity_type / promoted / discarded +`terminal`predicate). The modal
threads that session through`promote_draft(memory, session, *,
  from*channel="draft", to_channel="latest")`which calls the SDK's`client.promote(...)`(single cheap channel-pointer copy, no new
version upload) or`discard_draft(memory, session)`which deletes
the entity entirely via`client.\_delete_entity(...)`. Lifecycle
guards: `promote_draft`raises`DraftError("already discarded")`/`DraftError("already promoted")`so a stale modal can't double-fire;`discard_draft`is idempotent on already-discarded sessions (no
second HTTP call), refuses to delete a promoted draft (the entity
is now part of the user's library — delete must go through the
normal LibraryScreen action). Server-side errors wrap as`DraftError`
so UIs can show a friendly toast without parsing HTTP details, and
importantly the session is NOT marked terminal on failure — caller
can retry. Module exposes the canonical strings (`DRAFT_CHANNEL`,
`DRAFT_TAG`, `LATEST_CHANNEL`) so call-sites and tests don't drift.
18 tests in `tests/test_draft.py`across 6 areas: constants (2 —
channel/tag pin); DraftSession shape (3 — defaults + terminal-after-
promote + terminal-after-discard); auto_save_draft (2 — writes to
draft channel with tag + content metadata, user tags merged without
duplicating DRAFT_TAG); promote_draft (5 — happy path with body +
URL assertion, custom target channel, promote-after-discard raises,
promote-after-promote raises, server-error wraps in DraftError
without marking session promoted); discard_draft (4 — deletes +
marks session, second discard no-op, discard-after-promote raises,
server-error wraps without marking discarded); full lifecycle (2 —
save→promote, save→discard). All against`respx`-mocked Memory;
  ruff clean.*

absence of `error_message`when not explicit. Auto run_id format`run-YYYYMMDDTHHMMSSffffff`so the same id appears in card.usage +
the`record_run`body — UI can correlate later`stream_events`to

  All real HTTP-shape mocks (no internal-SDK monkey-patching); ruff clean.\*
- **[DONE]** AgentSkill provenance — when MAGE's `CapabilityLookupAgent`

  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/runtime/provenance.py` ships
  `SkillProvenanceRecorder(memory, _, trust*store=None)`plus the single-
shot`record_skill_provenance`wrapper. Coordinator semantics: wraps the
SDK's shipped, idempotent`client.ingest_skill_from_carl()`(which
handles every duck-typed input shape: CARL`ResolvedSkill`, dict,
`AgentSkillSpec`); adds a **session-scoped SHA → entity_id cache** so
the same MAGE generation never double-saves a capability it surfaced
through more than one path; returns a frozen `SkillProvenanceRecord(
  entity_id, sha256, name, uri, was_new, trusted)`per skill so the
surrounding UI can render "X skills resolved (2 new, 1 cached, 1
untrusted)" without re-querying. Trust integration: pass an optional`SkillTrustStore`and the recorder fills`record.trusted` with the
tri-state (`True`/`False`/`None`-when-no-store) — empty SHA is
always `False`even when the store is set, defending against a
caller that handed in an unhashed manifest. The recorder doesn't
refuse to persist untrusted skills (matches the spec: the
SaveAgentModal / first-run trust prompt is what decides; we just
surface trust state on the record). Batch helper`record_skills`preserves order + caches within the loop so a list with duplicates
only hits the wire once.`cache`property returns a copy
(mutation-safe);`clear_cache()`resets between unrelated sessions.
Module-level`record_skill_provenance(memory, skill, *, ...)`spins up a one-shot recorder for callers that don't need the cache
across calls. Duck-typed accessors`\_extract*sha`/`\_extract_uri`/`\_extract_name`recognise both dicts and CARL-shaped objects; module
has zero hard import of`mmar_carl`. 16 tests in

(3 — first call persists + returns was_new, second call cached +
no HTTP, distinct SHAs both persist); batch path (2 — preserves
order + caches dups, module-level wrapper); trust-store integration
(4 — trusted=True when in store, trusted=False when missing,
trusted=None without store, empty SHA → trusted=False even with
store); cache management (2 —`.cache`returns copy,`clear_cache`drops entries); duck-typed object inputs (3 — object with manifest
accepted via SDK's`\_extract_skill_spec`, helper-level name

- **[DONE]** Watch-and-hot-swap: `LibraryScreen` uses `client.watch_chain()`

  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/runtime/library_watcher.py` ships
  `watch_library(client, callback, _, namespace, entity_type, entity_id,
  tags, event_type) → LibrarySubscription`plus the supporting types.
Wraps the SDK's already-shipped`GigaEvoClient.watch_entities`(PREPARE
§2.8) so the LibraryScreen sees typed`LibraryEvent`instances instead
of raw event dicts. **Frozen`LibraryEvent`**: `(event_type, entity_id,
  entity_type, version_id, channel, namespace, tags, timestamp, raw)`.
`from_raw(dict)`promotes the SDK's payload — accepts str / list /
tuple / set for tags (always materialised as a hashable tuple),
parses ISO-8601 timestamps with graceful fall-back to`None`on bad
strings, coerces empty-string`version_id`/`channel`/`namespace`to`None`, keeps the full original dict on `.raw`for forward-compat.`EVENT_KINDS` constant pins the canonical event set
(`created`/`updated`/`deleted`/`favourite_toggled`/`run_recorded`/`metadata_updated`/`pinned`/`promoted`).
Predicates: `is_known_kind`flags events the LibraryScreen might
want to log-and-skip;`is_terminal`is`True`only for`deleted` so
the screen can drop the row instead of refreshing it.
**`LibrarySubscription`**: opaque wrapper around the SDK's
`Subscription`—`.stop()`delegates,`.underlying` exposes the raw
SDK object for advanced introspection, context-manager support
(`with memory.watch_library(...) as sub:`) auto-stops on exit
including on exceptions. Crash-safety: the wrapper closure
swallows per-event `from_raw` failures (defensive — a single
malformed message shouldn't kill the whole SSE stream); the SDK's
next event arrives normally. **`CareMemory.watch_library`** facade
method threads the same kwargs through to the helper using the
facade's own client — call-sites don't touch the SDK directly.
29 tests in `tests/test_library_watcher.py`across 5 areas:`LibraryEvent.from_raw`(7 — full payload, minimal defaults, tags
accept str / list / tuple / set, non-iterable tags degrades, bad
timestamp degrades, already-datetime kept, empty strings → None);
predicates (3 —`is_known_kind`parametrised across canonical set,
unknown returns False,`is_terminal`parametrised);`LibrarySubscription`(5 — stop delegates, idempotent at wrapper level, context manager
on exit, context manager on exception, missing stop method silent);`watch_library`(4 — forwards filters, callback receives typed events,
per-event errors swallowed, returns wrapper);`CareMemory.watch_library`(1 — facade forwards filters via monkey-patched`watch_entities`).
Uses a tiny `\_FakeClient`+`\_FakeSubscription` to drive events
  without spinning up real SSE infrastructure; ruff clean.\*
- **[DONE]** Conflict resolution UI on save: if the entity
  already exists with a different SHA, present diff +
  accept/reject/version-bump. Data layer + Textual modal +
  `CareMemory.find_entity_by_name` SDK surface all shipped.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.detect_conflict(memory, *, name, entity_type,
    incoming_content, namespace=None)` and
    `care.apply_resolution(memory, report, resolution, *,
    save_kwargs=None) -> str` in `care/conflict.py`,
    re-exported from the `care` top-level. Plus
    `compute_content_sha256` (stable digest helper) +
    `ConflictReport` frozen dataclass + `ConflictResolution`
    Literal + `ConflictResolutionError`.
  - **`detect_conflict`** queries the memory facade for an
    entity with the same `name` + `entity_type` (+ optional
    `namespace`), computes SHA-256 of both contents, and
    projects a `ConflictReport` with the unified-diff lines
    pre-rendered. Returns `None` when no existing entity is
    found (save will create fresh; no conflict possible).
    Returns a report with `is_conflict=False` when an
    entity exists but SHAs match — callers always get a
    report when an entity collides on name, regardless of
    content equality.
  - **`compute_content_sha256`** uses
    `json.dumps(..., sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":"))`
    so two semantically-equal dicts hash identically
    regardless of key insertion order — including nested
    dicts. Non-JSON-serialisable values (datetimes, Pydantic
    models, etc.) coerce via `default=str` rather than
    raising so a corner-case value can't bomb the save
    flow.
  - **`apply_resolution`** dispatches the user's choice:
    - `"keep_existing"` → no-op, returns the existing
      `entity_id`. Memory is never touched.
    - `"accept_incoming"` → calls
      `save_<kind>(incoming_content, entity_id=existing,
      ...)` to overwrite the entity in place.
    - `"new_version"` → same save call as accept-incoming.
      Memory's save layer treats it as a versioned write
      because the content SHA changed; channel `latest`
      moves to the new version while the previous one
      stays reachable by version_id. This is the
      recommended default the modal will surface.
  - **Per-entity-type save dispatch** via
    `_SAVE_METHOD_FOR_KIND`:
    - `"chain"` → `memory.save_chain(...)`
    - `"agent_skill"` → `memory.save_agent_skill(...)`
    - `"memory_card"` → `memory.save_memory_card(...)`
    Unknown entity_type raises a clear error (better than
    a downstream AttributeError).
  - **`save_kwargs` forwarding** lets the modal pass
    user-supplied `tags`, `when_to_use`, `author`,
    `channel`, etc. without the conflict module
    constraining the shape. The user's explicit kwargs win
    over the report's `name` default — handy when renaming
    on save.
  - **Pre-rendered unified diff** via `difflib.unified_diff`
    on `json.dumps(..., indent=2, sort_keys=True)` of both
    sides. Diff labels are `"<name> (existing)"` /
    `"<name> (incoming)"` so the modal can show the
    user-visible name without reformatting. Skipped when
    `is_conflict=False` to keep the report lean.
  - **Duck-typed memory** — anything exposing
    `find_entity_by_name(name=, entity_type=, namespace=)`
    + the relevant `save_*` method works. Tests inject a
    `_StubMemory` that records every call. CARE's
    :class:`CareMemory` will grow `find_entity_by_name`
    when this lands in the modal flow (small SDK surface
    addition; documented as a follow-up).
  - **Error wrapping:** every failure path
    (`find_entity_by_name` raising, non-dict response,
    non-dict existing content, unknown resolution literal,
    unknown entity_type, missing save method, downstream
    save raising) becomes `ConflictResolutionError` with
    `__cause__` chained — callers handle one exception
    class.

  **Tests (`tests/test_conflict.py`, 29 cases):**
  - **`compute_content_sha256` (6):** deterministic across
    runs; key-order independent (top-level + nested);
    different content → different SHA; non-JSON values
    (datetime) coerce via `str()`; 64-char hex output.
  - **`detect_conflict` (9):** no-existing → `None`;
    same-content → `is_conflict=False`, empty diff;
    different content → `is_conflict=True`, diff lines
    reference both labels + show changed values;
    full content preserved on report; `namespace`
    forwarded; lookup raising wraps; memory without
    `find_entity_by_name` raises; non-dict lookup
    response raises; non-dict existing content raises.
  - **`apply_resolution` (10):** `keep_existing` returns
    existing id without saving; `accept_incoming`
    overwrites with pinned `entity_id`; `new_version`
    same `entity_id` (Memory handles versioning); each
    entity_type dispatches to the right `save_*` method
    (chain / agent_skill / memory_card);
    `save_kwargs` forward verbatim; explicit `name`
    kwarg overrides report's `name`; unknown resolution
    raises; unknown entity_type raises; missing save
    method raises; downstream save exception wraps;
    `keep_existing` skips unknown entity_type (no save
    attempted, so no validation needed).
  - **Report shape (2):** frozen dataclass;
    `diff_lines` is a tuple (not list — immutable for
    safe sharing).
  - **Helper coverage (2):** SHA helper output is
    deterministic across runs; 64-char hex format
    pinned.

  **UI shipped 2026-05-20:** `care/screens/conflict.py::ConflictModal`
  is a Textual `ModalScreen[ConflictModalResult]` that consumes a
  `ConflictReport` and presents the three resolutions plus a
  cancel. Layout: yellow-bordered box with a title line
  (`Conflict · <name>`), a one-line summary
  (`<kind> '<id>' already exists with different content.` /
  `... identical content — saving is a no-op.`), a scrollable
  unified-diff pane (renders `report.diff_lines` verbatim, or
  `(no differences)` when `is_conflict=False`), and a row of four
  buttons: `Cancel`, `Keep existing`, `Accept incoming`,
  `New version`. `New version` is the default-focused option
  (matches the data-layer docstring's recommendation since it
  preserves history).

  Dismiss envelope `ConflictModalResult(resolution, report,
  cancelled)`:
  - Each resolution button → `resolution=<literal>`,
    `cancelled=False`, `report` carried verbatim so the host
    pipes it straight into `apply_resolution(memory, report,
    resolution, save_kwargs=...)`.
  - `Cancel` button / `Escape` binding →
    `resolution=None`, `cancelled=True`. The host treats this as
    a "back out of save" gesture (no Memory mutation).

  The modal is purely presentational — it never touches Memory
  itself. That keeps it trivially testable and means the host
  screen (eventually `SaveAgentModal`) owns the
  `detect_conflict` → push-modal → `apply_resolution` orchestration.

  **`CareMemory.find_entity_by_name` shipped 2026-05-20:** the
  SDK facade now satisfies the duck-typed contract
  `care.detect_conflict` documents. Returns
  `{"entity_id": str, "content": dict}` for the first listing
  row whose name matches, or `None` when no match is found.
  Dispatch: `entity_type="chain"` → `list_chains(q=name, ...)`,
  `"agent_skill"` → `list_agent_skills(q=name, ...)`,
  `"memory_card"` → `list_memory_cards()` (no `q` filter on the
  SDK side, so it scans up to `limit`). Name resolution probes
  three sources in order: `EntityResponse.display_name`,
  `content.metadata.care.display_name` (CARE save convention),
  `meta["name"]` (server-side label). Unknown `entity_type`
  raises `ValueError`. Namespace + channel + limit forwarded.

  **Tests (`tests/test_screen_conflict.py`, 10 cases):**
  - **Compose (4):** the three resolution buttons + Cancel mount;
    diff body renders the report's diff lines; identical-report
    summary contains "identical"; identical-report diff body
    shows "(no differences)".
  - **Dismiss (5):** `keep_existing` / `accept_incoming` /
    `new_version` each dismiss with the right resolution literal
    and `cancelled=False`; Cancel button dismisses with
    `resolution=None`, `cancelled=True`; `action_cancel`
    (Escape) same.
  - **Re-exports (1):** `care.screens.ConflictModal` /
    `ConflictModalResult` are the same classes.

  **`find_entity_by_name` tests added to `tests/test_memory.py`
  (`TestFindEntityByName`, 9 cases):** chain match returns
  `{entity_id, content}`; no-match returns `None`; `q` +
  `namespace` query params forwarded; agent_skill match;
  memory_card match; falls back to `meta["name"]` when
  `display_name` is null; falls back to
  `content.metadata.care.display_name`; unknown entity_type
  raises; round-trip through `care.detect_conflict` proves the
  duck-typed contract holds.

  **What this enables:** when `SaveAgentModal._apply_and_dismiss`
  is wired in a follow-up, it calls
  `detect_conflict(memory, name=form.display_name,
  entity_type="chain", incoming_content=chain_dict)`. On
  `None`, save normally. On `is_conflict=False`, save reuses the
  existing entity_id. On `is_conflict=True`, push `ConflictModal`,
  read the dismissed `ConflictModalResult`, and call
  `apply_resolution(memory, report, result.resolution,
  save_kwargs={...})`. The SaveAgentModal wiring itself is a
  follow-up — the data layer + modal + SDK surface are all on
  hand.
- **[DONE] Edit → new version** — `EditAgentScreen`
  saves changes as a new version of the same `entity_id`
  (Memory's version semantics) so history is preserved. Channel
  `latest` always points at the user's most recent edit; `stable`
  is set manually via an "Promote to stable" action.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/edit_draft.py`) +
  Textual screen (P0.23). `care/screens/edit_agent.py::EditAgentScreen`
  seeds the form via `extract_edit_draft`, routes every
  field edit through the `set_*` mutators, validates inline,
  and runs `save_edit_as_new_version` / `promote_to_stable`
  on the worker pool. Each terminal action posts an
  `EditAgentScreen.Submitted` envelope carrying
  `EditAgentEvent(action, draft, save_result,
  promote_result)`.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/edit_draft.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `EditAgentDraft` — frozen form state carrying every
      editable field plus an `original_*` snapshot per field
      for dirty tracking (`display_name` / `description` /
      `tags` / `task_description`). Predicates
      `display_name_dirty` / `description_dirty` / `tags_dirty`
      (set-semantics so tag re-ordering doesn't count) /
      `task_description_dirty` plus `is_dirty()` /
      `dirty_fields()` drive the "Save" vs. "Save (n changes)"
      button label. `chain_content` slot is the opaque carrier
      for per-step prompt / config edits; `chain_content_dirty`
      flag separates structural edits from pure-metadata
      renames. `is_structural_edit` predicate drives the
      "change summary required" rule.
    - `EditDraftIssue` — frozen inline validation finding
      (severity / field / message / optional detail).
    - `EditFieldName` literal pins the canonical editable
      field names for screen + helpers.
    - `extract_edit_draft(chain, entity_id, *, entity_type,
      parent_version_id, channel)` — pure projection from a
      saved CARL `ReasoningChain` (or dict, or any object
      with `get_care_metadata()`) into the initial draft.
      Reads from the CARE metadata block; missing fields
      default to empty. Raises `EditDraftError` when no
      `entity_id` is supplied (load-bearing — can't save
      without it).
    - Mutators: `set_display_name`, `set_description`,
      `set_tags` (strips whitespace, drops empties),
      `set_task_description`, `set_change_summary`,
      `update_chain` (with `dirty=` flag for refresh-from-disk
      vs. user-edit), `reset` (restores every original).
      Every returns a new frozen draft so undo is a list of
      past instances.
    - `validate_edit_draft(draft)` — surfaces field-level
      issues: empty display_name → error, structural edit
      without change_summary → error, duplicate tags →
      warning ("ignored on save"). Empty tuple when ready.
    - `save_edit_as_new_version(memory, draft, *, author,
      timeout)` — async wrapper around the CARE / SDK
      `save_chain` path. Memory keys off `entity_id` so a
      fresh version lands without losing the prior one
      (preserves history for rollback). No-op when
      `draft.is_dirty() is False` (returns
      `SaveEditResult` with `fields_written=()` so the
      screen renders "Nothing to save"). Per-call timeout +
      exception wrapping → result-shaped error reporting; only
      pre-flight errors (missing entity_id / missing facade
      method) raise `EditDraftError`.
    - `promote_to_stable(memory, draft, *, from_channel,
      to_channel, timeout)` — async wrapper around the SDK's
      `client.promote(...)` endpoint that flips a channel
      pointer server-side WITHOUT creating a new version.
      Idempotent. Same result-shaped error reporting as save.
    - `SaveEditResult` / `PromoteResult` — frozen outcome
      rows the screen renders into toasts.

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** the save helper accepts any
  `CareMemory`-like facade exposing `.save_chain(...)`; the
  promote helper reaches into `memory.client.promote(...)`
  (or `memory._client.promote`). The chain projection accepts
  plain dicts OR CARL chain objects via `get_care_metadata()`.
  Tests use lightweight stubs — no SDK / HTTP / real Memory
  touched.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_edit_draft.py`, 44 cases):
  - **extract_edit_draft (6):** all fields extracted, empty
    metadata yields blank originals, dict chain accepted,
    Pydantic `model_dump` accepted, missing entity_id raises,
    parent_version_id + channel + entity_type carry through.
  - **Dirty tracking (11):** fresh extract clean, display_name
    edit flags dirty, whitespace-only doesn't count, tag
    re-order doesn't count (set semantics), tag added counts,
    update_chain flags structural, update_chain(dirty=False)
    skips flag, set_description / set_task_description flag,
    change_summary doesn't affect dirty, set_tags strips
    whitespace.
  - **reset (3):** restores originals, clears change_summary,
    clears chain_content_dirty.
  - **Validation (6):** clean draft no issues, empty
    display_name → error, structural edit requires summary
    (then adding one clears the error), metadata edit doesn't
    require summary, duplicate tags warning, issue is frozen.
  - **save_edit_as_new_version (8):** clean draft short-
    circuits, writes with entity_id for versioning, tags
    forwarded, save failure surfaces on result, timeout →
    result.error, missing entity_id raises, missing
    save_chain raises, chain_content_dirty written.
  - **promote_to_stable (6):** calls SDK with right args,
    custom source channel, failure surfaces on result,
    timeout → result.error, missing entity_id raises, missing
    `client.promote` raises.
  - **Frozen models (3):** draft / SaveEditResult / PromoteResult
    are frozen.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1467 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future screen:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      extract_edit_draft, validate_edit_draft,
      set_display_name, set_tags, save_edit_as_new_version,
      promote_to_stable,
  )

  draft = extract_edit_draft(chain, entity_id, channel="latest")
  # User edits → modal calls set_display_name / set_tags / ...
  # returning new drafts; `draft.is_dirty()` toggles the Save
  # button label; `draft.dirty_fields()` populates the "(n
  # changes)" badge.

  issues = validate_edit_draft(draft)
  if any(i.severity == "error" for i in issues):
      self._render_issues(issues)
      return

  result = await save_edit_as_new_version(self.app.memory, draft)
  if not result.success:
      self.app.push_toast(f"Save failed: {result.error}")
      return
  # User chooses "Promote to stable":
  promo = await promote_to_stable(self.app.memory, draft)
  ```
- **[DONE]** Bulk import: `care import ./generated_chains/*.json`
  → batch save.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.import_chains(patterns, memory, *, dry_run=False,
channel="latest") -> BulkImportReport` in
    `care/bulk_import.py`, re-exported from the `care` top-level
    namespace. Bounded function that pairs the
    parse/validate layer (TODO §4 P2 `care.validate_chain`)
    with the existing `CareMemory.save_chain` I/O — exactly
    the surface a future `care import` CLI sub-command needs.
  - Accepts **two JSON shapes** so the function works against
    both raw chain exports and the wrapper that MAGE §3.10's
    `MAGEResult.to_care_dict()` writes: - **Bare-chain form**: the JSON file is the chain dict
    itself (`{"task_description": ..., "steps": [...]}`).
    The filename stem becomes the default library name; no
    domain/query/tags propagate. - **Wrapper form**: `{"chain": <chain-dict>, "name": "...",
"query": "...", "domain": "...", "tags": [...],
"context_files": [...], "mage_metadata": {...},
"when_to_use": "...", "author": "...", "channel": "..."}`.
    Every key except `chain` is optional and forwards
    verbatim to `CareMemory.save_chain`. Unknown
    top-level keys are silently dropped (forwards-compat:
    callers can stash extra metadata without the import
    refusing the file).
  - **Continues on per-file errors.** One broken file
    doesn't abort the rest of the batch — the
    `BulkImportReport.failed` list carries every failure by
    path so users can fix and re-run just the failures.
    Function never raises (except `ValueError` when
    `dry_run=False` and `memory=None`, the one config that
    genuinely can't proceed).
  - `BulkImportEntry` per-file frozen dataclass with `path`,
    `status` (one of `"imported"`/`"validated"`/`"failed"`),
    `entity_id`, `name`, and `errors`. Multiple errors per
    file because a single file can fail at multiple steps
    (JSON parse → chain validate → save_chain) and the user
    benefits from seeing the full chain of cause.
  - `BulkImportReport` aggregator with `imported` /
    `validated` / `failed` partitions, `all_ok` predicate,
    and `format_text()` for CLI output rendering. Failed
    entries get a `FAIL <path>` line plus indented error
    detail — the shape a `care import` CLI prints at the
    end.
  - **Dry-run mode** (`dry_run=True`) validates every file
    without calling `memory.save_chain`. Lets `care import
--dry-run` preview what would happen before letting the
    destructive run proceed. Memory may be `None` in this
    mode.
  - Glob expansion via `glob.glob(recursive=True)` so
    patterns like `**/*.json` walk directories. Tilde-
    expanded. Multiple patterns deduplicate against each
    other (same file matched by two patterns → one import).
    `*.txt` neighbours in the same directory are correctly
    filtered out by the user-provided pattern.

  **Tests (`tests/test_bulk_import.py`, 23 cases):**
  - Report shape: empty report is `all_ok`; partitioning
    `imported`/`validated`/`failed` lists; `format_text()`
    includes counts + per-failure detail.
  - Bare-chain form: single file imports cleanly via real
    CARL parse + `_StubMemory.save_chain`; filename stem
    becomes `name` kwarg.
  - Wrapper form: every documented save kwarg (`name`,
    `query`, `domain`, `tags`, `when_to_use`, `author`,
    `channel`) forwards verbatim; unknown keys are dropped
    silently (forwards-compat regression guard); default
    `channel=` kwarg applies only when the wrapper omits it.
  - Glob expansion: `*.json` matches multiple files (skips
    `*.txt`); `**/*.json` walks nested directories;
    duplicate patterns deduplicate to one import; empty
    match yields empty report; tilde expansion via $HOME.
  - Per-file failure modes: invalid JSON; chain validation
    failure (Memory never called); top-level not a dict;
    missing both `chain` and `steps` keys; `save_chain`
    raising; mixed batch (broken + good) — good still
    imports.
  - Dry-run: validated entries report `status="validated"`
    and Memory.save_chain is never called; works without a
    `memory` argument; failures still surface in dry-run;
    omitting `memory` outside dry-run raises `ValueError`.

---

## 4. MAGE integration (P0–P2)

- **[DONE]** Wire `MAGEGenerator(config=MAGEConfig.from_toml(...),
  progress=...)` into `GenerationScreen`. Use deep mode by
  default; expose a `Fast` checkbox to flip to single-shot.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care.build_mage_config` +
  `care.build_mage_generator` + `care.run_generation`) + UI
  half. `QueryScreen` gained a `MageMode = Literal["fast",
  "deep"]`, an `initial_mode` constructor kwarg, and a
  `Fast mode (single-shot, skip deep enhancements)` Checkbox
  beside the runtime radio. The toggle rides on
  `QuerySubmission.mage_mode`; the downstream worker
  forwards through to `build_mage_generator(care_config,
  progress=poster, mode=submission.mage_mode)`. 3 Pilot
  tests in `tests/test_screen_query.py::TestMageMode`:
  default-deep behaviour, Fast-checkbox-flips-mode, and the
  `initial_mode="fast"` constructor override. Full CARE
  suite (2376 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.build_mage_config(care_config, *, mode=None)` +
    `care.build_mage_generator(care_config, *, progress=None,
    mode=None)` + `care.run_generation(generator, query, *,
    context_files=None, cancel=None, capabilities=None)` in
    `care/generation.py`, re-exported from the `care`
    top-level. Plus `GenerationError` covering every failure
    mode the helpers surface.
  - **`build_mage_config`** translates CARE's narrow
    `CareConfig.mage` Pydantic surface into a fully-populated
    `mmar_mage.MAGEConfig`. Forwards every documented field
    (`mode`, `provider`, `api_key`, `base_url`, `model`,
    `enable_memory_research`, `enable_web_research`,
    `web_search_api_key`). `base_url` / `model` /
    `web_search_api_key` are only passed when set, so MAGE's
    own defaults apply for unset values rather than getting
    overridden to `None`. Validation lives on the MAGE side —
    any Pydantic `ValidationError` wraps in `GenerationError`
    with `__cause__` chained.
  - **Mode override:** explicit `mode=` kwarg wins over the
    saved `CareConfig.mage.mode`. The future
    GenerationScreen's Fast/Deep checkbox passes this without
    mutating the user's saved config.
  - **Provider mapping:** CARE accepts arbitrary provider
    strings (its LLM-client factory supports custom
    registrations); MAGE pins its enum to ``"openai" |
    "openrouter" | "local" | "custom"``. `_CARE_TO_MAGE_PROVIDER`
    maps the three matching names through; unknown values
    fall back to ``"custom"`` so MAGE's own factory layer
    takes over for self-hosted backends. Case-insensitive +
    whitespace-stripped lookup.
  - **`build_mage_generator`** instantiates a real
    `MAGEGenerator(config=..., progress=...)` ready for the
    screen worker. `progress` is duck-typed against MAGE's
    `MAGEProgressCallback` — the future TUI passes
    `care.runtime.MagePoster(textual_app)`; CLI / scripted
    callers omit it for a no-op reporter. Construction
    failures wrap in `GenerationError`.
  - **`run_generation(generator, query, *, ...)`** is the
    thin async wrapper around `generator.generate(query,
    context_files=, cancel=, capabilities=)`. Lets the future
    GenerationScreen worker (and the future `care generate`
    CLI) not have to remember MAGE's kwarg names. Empty /
    whitespace `query` raises before touching the generator
    so the user gets a useful error. Missing `.generate`
    method raises clearly. Downstream exception wraps as
    `GenerationError("generate() raised: ...")`;
    `GenerationError` raised by the method propagates
    unwrapped (no double-wrap).
  - **Lazy `mmar_mage` import** in both `build_mage_config`
    + `build_mage_generator`. Missing dep raises
    `GenerationError("mmar_mage is not installed; install
    with `pip install \"care[mage]\"`")` — same install-hint
    convention `LLMClientError` / `CapabilityPrimingError` /
    `ChainExportError` use. The `care.generation` module
    imports cleanly even without the `mage` extra so other
    paths (CLI subcommands, library helpers) keep working.
  - **Missing `api_key` short-circuit:** `build_mage_config`
    raises `GenerationError("CareConfig.mage.api_key must
    be set...")` before reaching MAGE — points the user at
    both env var (`CARE_MAGE__API_KEY`) and TOML field
    (`[mage] api_key`) so they know which fix to make.

  **Tests (`tests/test_generation.py`, 22 passed + 1 skipped
  install-gated case):**
  - Config translation (7, gated on `mage` extra): every
    field translates; bare `MageConfig` accepted; mode
    override wins; missing/empty `api_key` raises; unset
    `base_url` omitted from kwargs (default applies);
    `web_search_api_key` flows through.
  - Provider mapping (5): `openai` / `local` / `openrouter`
    pass through; case-insensitive; unknown falls back to
    `custom`.
  - Missing-dep path (1, gated when `mage` IS installed):
    friendly `GenerationError` with install hint.
  - `build_mage_generator` (3): generator constructed with
    `.generate` attribute; `progress` accepted without
    raising; mode override flows through to construction.
  - `run_generation` stub-driven (6): empty + whitespace
    query raise; missing `.generate` method raises; every
    kwarg (`context_files` / `cancel` / `capabilities`)
    forwards verbatim with same instance preserved;
    downstream exception wraps; `GenerationError` raised
    inside `generate()` propagates unwrapped; result
    returned verbatim.

  **What this enables for the future `GenerationScreen`:**

  ```python
  from care import (
      CareConfig, build_mage_generator, run_generation,
      build_capability_payload, build_catalog,
  )
  from care.runtime import MagePoster

  async def on_generate_pressed(query: str, fast: bool) -> None:
      poster = MagePoster(self.app)
      generator = build_mage_generator(
          self.care_config,
          progress=poster,
          mode="fast" if fast else "deep",
      )
      payload = build_capability_payload(build_catalog(...))
      result = await run_generation(
          generator,
          query,
          context_files=self.context_files,
          cancel=self.cancel_event,
          capabilities=payload.to_mage_context(),
      )
      # Render result via existing data projectors —
      # care.summarise_mage_result, care.project_intermediate_artifacts.
  ```

  No further data-layer work needed once §1 P0 lands; the
  worker + Fast/Deep checkbox + screen layout are the
  remaining UI portions.
- **[DONE]** Display ALL `MAGEMetadata` fields
  after generation: `domain`, `num_steps`, stages completed,
  memory hits used, web results, cold-start flag, critique
  score, refine iterations, ToT branches, MCTS sims, feedback
  recall count.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care.summarise_mage_result`)
  + UI half. `GenerationScreen` gained a
  `record_mage_result(result)` hook the host worker calls
  with the MAGEResult after `MAGEGenerator.generate`
  returns; the screen projects via
  `summarise_mage_result(...)` and renders
  `MetadataSummary.format_text()` into a
  `#generation-metadata` Static below the streaming DAG
  pane. Result-projection failures keep
  `metadata_summary=None` without crashing the screen. 2
  Pilot tests in `tests/test_screen_generation.py::TestMageMetadataFooter`
  cover the duck-typed `MAGEResult` happy path and the
  silent-failure guard. Full CARE suite (2367 passed + 8
  skipped); ruff clean.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.summarise_mage_result(source) -> MetadataSummary`
    in `care/mage_summary.py`, re-exported from the `care`
    top-level. Projects every field the TODO spec calls out
    (plus useful extras MAGE already exposes) into a single
    CARE-stable frozen dataclass the future TUI / CLI render
    without further data-layer work.
  - **All 11 spec-required fields land on `MetadataSummary`:**
    - `domain` (str)
    - `num_steps` (int)
    - `stages_completed: tuple[str, ...]` — projected from
      MAGE's `deep_stages_completed`. Empty in fast mode.
    - `memory_hits_used` (int)
    - `web_results_used` (int)
    - `was_cold_start` (bool)
    - `step_critique_score: float | None` — None when
      critique didn't run.
    - `refine_iterations: int | None`
    - `tot_branches_explored: int | None`
    - `mcts_simulations_run: int | None`
    - `feedback_recalled: int | None`
  - **Plus useful extras** the same MAGE metadata model
    already carries: `mode`, `model`, `generation_time_seconds`,
    `verification_passed`, `refine_quality_delta`,
    `mcts_best_reward`, `suggested_display_name`,
    `suggested_description`, `suggested_tags` (the §3.2
    library-ready defaults `SaveAgentModal` pre-fills with).
  - **Duck-typed input** accepts three shapes:
    1. `MAGEResult`-like — has `.metadata` + `.mode` + (for
       disambiguation) `.chain_json`. Projector unwraps
       `.metadata` and picks `mode` off the outer object.
    2. `MAGEMetadata`-like — flat attribute access. Used
       directly.
    3. Plain `dict` — same keys map to the same fields.
       Lets callers serialise via JSON and re-project
       without an SDK import.
    All three are dispatched by an attribute-or-key getter
    paired with a `_looks_like_metadata` fingerprint check,
    so the same call site handles every source shape.
  - **Tolerant of missing fields.** Older MAGE installs
    that don't populate every optional metadata slot still
    produce a clean summary — missing keys fall back to
    dataclass defaults (matches MAGE's own convention where
    optional metadata is `None` when the stage didn't run).
    `None` values from MAGE map to the dataclass defaults
    (e.g. `domain=None` → `"general"`).
  - **Coercion**: `_opt_int` / `_opt_float` / `_opt_bool`
    helpers tolerate stringy numbers (some sources stream
    metadata as JSON where numbers arrive as strings) AND
    fall back to `None` on unparseable values rather than
    crashing.
  - `MetadataSummary.format_text()` produces a multi-line
    human-readable block for the future InspectionScreen
    footer + `care generate` CLI output. Quality-block
    (critique / verify / refine / tot / mcts / feedback)
    only renders the fields that actually fired — keeps the
    block scan-friendly when most enhancements are off.
    Special-case formatting: `was_cold_start=True` annotates
    the memory-hits line; `verification_passed=False`
    reads "verify=failed"; `refine_quality_delta` is rendered
    with a `+` / `-` sign prefix.
  - `MetadataSummary.to_dict()` converts tuples to lists for
    JSON-friendly serialisation; useful when persisting a
    summary into a saved-run record or shipping it through
    the telemetry sink (§9 P3, shipped).

  **Tests (`tests/test_mage_summary.py`, 22 cases):**
  - **Shape (4 cases):** defaults match the convention
    (`domain="general"`, every optional field `None`);
    `to_dict` converts tuples to lists; dataclass + frozen.
  - **Dict input (6 cases):** every documented field
    projects; empty dict yields defaults; partial dict
    keeps defaults for missing keys; nested
    `{"metadata": {...}, "mode": ..., "chain_json": ...}`
    unwraps correctly (mode from outer, metadata from
    nested); stringy numbers coerce
    (`"5"` → `5`); unparseable optional values fall back
    to `None` instead of raising.
  - **Object input (3 cases):** attribute-style access
    works; result-like object with `.metadata` +
    `.chain_json` unwraps; `None` attribute values become
    dataclass defaults.
  - **`format_text` (6 cases):** minimal layout (no
    quality block when nothing fired); quality block
    renders only set fields; `was_cold_start` annotation;
    `web_results_used=0` line skipped; stage trail
    rendered; `verify=failed` text.
  - **Real MAGE round-trip (2 cases, install-gated):**
    when the `mage` extra is installed, build a real
    `MAGEMetadata` + `MAGEResult` and verify every field
    round-trips through the projector. Skipped when MAGE
    isn't on the install.
  - **`to_dict` round-trip (1 case):** tuples become lists,
    optional `None`s included so consumers see the full
    schema.

  **What this completes for the TUI work:** the
  `GenerationScreen` / `InspectionScreen` footer just calls
  `summarise_mage_result(result).format_text()` to render the
  full metadata block. No additional data-layer work needed
  — once those screens land in §1 P0, they consume this
  shape directly.
- **[DONE]** Surface the _intermediate_ artifacts
  from each MAGE stage (`DomainAnalysis`, `StepPlan`,
  `DAGStructure`, `[CARLStepSchema]`) as collapsible panes —
  useful for debugging chain quality.

  *Fully complete:* data layer
  (`care.project_intermediate_artifacts(source) ->
  IntermediateArtifactsView`) + UI half. `InspectionScreen`
  gained an `Artifacts` `TabPane` hosting a VerticalScroll
  of Textual `Collapsible` panes. The host calls
  `record_intermediate_artifacts(source)` with a MAGE
  result / dict / pre-built `IntermediateArtifactsView`;
  the screen projects via
  `project_intermediate_artifacts(...)`, stores the view on
  `self.intermediate_artifacts`, and renders one
  `Collapsible(title=f"{header}  ·  {summary}")` per
  artifact with the body lines mounted as a child Static.
  Empty views render `(no intermediate artifacts)`;
  projection failures keep the previous view without
  crashing. 6 Pilot tests in
  `tests/test_screen_inspection_artifacts.py` across empty
  view, dual-pane render, projection-failure silence,
  dict-source projection round-trip, and the
  `_artifact_id` sanitiser helper. Full CARE suite (2373
  passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.project_intermediate_artifacts(source) ->
    IntermediateArtifactsView` in
    `care/intermediate_artifacts.py`, re-exported from the
    `care` top-level. Pairs with `summarise_mage_result(...)`
    (§4 P0 above) — same duck-typed input, same frozen
    output, same projector pattern.
  - **Six MAGE stages get tailored summaries + body
    renderers:**
    - `domain_analysis` → "domain=X, type=Y, complexity=Z,
      suggested_steps=N".
    - `step_plan` → "N steps planned" (singular/plural).
    - `dag` → "N nodes, M edges".
    - `critique` → "score=0.82, K failing steps".
    - `verification` → "passed" / "failed (N issues)".
    - `refine` → "iterations=K, Δ=+0.15".
    - Unknown future stages (MAGE may add more) get a
      generic summary based on payload type — keys count
      for dicts, item count for lists — so they don't get
      silently dropped.
  - `IntermediateArtifact` frozen dataclass per pane:
    `stage` (key), `header` (human-readable —
    "Step plan", "DAG structure"…), `summary` (collapsed-
    pane label), `body` (expanded-pane content), `raw`
    (original payload for the JSON viewer).
  - `IntermediateArtifactsView` aggregator with
    `is_empty`, `stages()`, `by_stage(name)`,
    `format_text()`. The `format_text()` rendering
    assembles `# <header>` headings + summary + body
    blocks separated by blank lines so CLI / log output
    stays scan-friendly.
  - **Pipeline-order preserved.** Source dict can arrive
    in any order; the projector emits known stages in
    MAGE's pipeline order (`domain_analysis → step_plan
    → dag → critique → verification → refine`), with any
    unknown stages appended in insertion order. UI
    rendering becomes deterministic.
  - **Empty payloads dropped.** Stages whose payload is
    `None` / `{}` / `[]` don't produce an artifact — fast-
    mode runs (which skip most enhancements) yield a
    view containing only the stages that actually ran.
    Keeps the pane stack tight.
  - **Body renderer:** dicts render as `key: value` lines
    with one level of indent for nested dicts; lists with
    items render `key: (N items)` followed by bulleted
    items; lists of >5 nested items truncate with "… N
    more"; long strings (>120 chars) truncate to 117 + `...`.
    Targets InspectionScreen-readable output without
    requiring a JSON viewer.
  - **Duck-typed input.** Accepts `MAGEResult`-like
    (unwraps `.intermediate_artifacts`); the artifacts
    dict directly; `None` (empty view); unknown types
    (empty view, never raises). Same triple-shape
    pattern `summarise_mage_result` uses.

  **Tests (`tests/test_intermediate_artifacts.py`, 31 cases):**
  - **Input coercion (6):** None, empty dict, artifacts
    dict, MAGEResult-dict, attribute-style object,
    unrecognised type all funnel cleanly.
  - **Per-stage summaries (10):** each known stage's
    specific summary rules pinned; singular/plural step-
    count handling; unknown stages with dict / list /
    scalar payloads.
  - **Ordering (3):** pipeline order restored from a
    reversed source; unknown stages appended after known;
    empty payloads dropped.
  - **Body rendering (5):** dict key/value lines; nested-
    dict indent; long-string truncation; list-of-dicts
    bullets; long-list truncation.
  - **Aggregate view (5):** `format_text` includes
    headers; `by_stage` returns `None` for absent
    stages; view + artifact both frozen; raw payload
    preserved verbatim.
  - **Real MAGE roundtrip (install-gated):** builds a
    real `MAGEResult` with three stage payloads and
    verifies summaries match; skipped when MAGE isn't
    installed.

  **What this enables:** the future `InspectionScreen`
  pane stack renders `result.intermediate_artifacts` by
  calling `project_intermediate_artifacts(result)` and
  iterating `.artifacts` — each yields `header` + `summary`
  + `body` ready for a Textual `Collapsible` widget. No
  further data work needed once §1 P0 lands.
- **[DONE]** Allow re-running individual MAGE stages: e.g.
  "regenerate DAG only" → call `DAGBuilder.build(plan)` without
  redoing planning. Requires MAGE TODO §2 (per-stage public
  entrypoints — already shipped per PREPARE.md §3.7).

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.regenerate_stage(generator, stage, inputs) ->
    StageArtifact` in `care/stage_regeneration.py`, re-exported
    from the `care` top-level. Dispatch table mapping CARE-
    side stage names to the seven `MAGEGenerator` per-stage
    methods MAGE §3.7 ships:
    - `"domain"` → `analyze_domain(query)`
    - `"plan"` → `plan_steps(query, domain_analysis, *,
      memory_digest=, web_digest=, capability_context=,
      template_skeleton=, skill_digest=, allowed_step_types=)`
    - `"dag"` → `build_dag(plan)`
    - `"describe"` → `describe_steps(query, dag, *,
      allowed_step_types=)`
    - `"critique"` → `critique_steps(query, steps,
      domain_analysis, *, threshold=)`
    - `"verify"` → `verify_chain(query, chain_dict,
      domain_analysis)`
    - `"refine"` → `refine(query, chain_dict, domain_analysis)`
  - **CARE-side stage names** are short literals (`"dag"`
    instead of `build_dag`) — friendlier for the future
    "Regenerate" dropdown in `InspectionScreen` /
    `EditAgentScreen`, and the dispatcher does the
    method-name translation internally so callers don't
    bind to MAGE's naming.
  - **Input validation up front.** `_REQUIRED_INPUTS` lists
    the mandatory keys per stage; missing keys raise
    `StageRegenerationError("stage 'plan' requires inputs
    ['domain_analysis']")` BEFORE the generator is touched.
    Far friendlier than the SDK's downstream `TypeError:
    plan_steps() missing 1 required positional argument`
    when the caller forgot a kwarg.
  - **Required → positional + extras → kwargs split.** The
    required keys land as positional args (matching
    MAGE's method signatures); any extra keys in the input
    dict forward as kwargs verbatim. Lets the caller pass
    `inputs={"query": q, "dag": dag, "allowed_step_types":
    ["llm"]}` and the dispatcher splits the optional
    kwarg correctly.
  - **Async / sync result handling.** MAGE's per-stage
    methods are `async def`; the dispatcher awaits the
    coroutine. Tests + future synchronous variants that
    return a plain value pass through unchanged
    (`asyncio.iscoroutine` check).
  - **Missing-method path** for older MAGE installs that
    don't ship per-stage entrypoints yet — raises
    `StageRegenerationError("generator has no
    'analyze_domain' method; upgrade mmar_mage to a version
    that ships per-stage entrypoints (MAGE §3.7)")`.
    Non-callable attributes (someone monkey-patched the
    method to a string) trigger the same friendly error.
  - **Error wrapping:** downstream exceptions (sync OR
    inside the awaited coroutine) become
    `StageRegenerationError("stage 'X' failed: ...")` with
    `__cause__` chained. A `StageRegenerationError` raised
    by the method itself propagates unwrapped so the
    descriptive message stays intact (matches the
    `LLMClientError` / `MarketplaceError` precedent).
  - `StageArtifact` frozen dataclass with `stage` + raw
    `artifact` (typed `Any` — CARE doesn't import MAGE's
    `DomainAnalysis` / `StepPlan` / `DAGStructure` /
    `CARLStepSchema` / `StepCritiqueResult` types at this
    layer; callers cast based on `stage`).
  - `supported_stages()` helper returns the sorted literal
    list — pure-Python, no deps, so the future "Regenerate
    DAG only" dropdown enumerates choices without
    importing MAGE.
  - **Duck-typed generator argument.** No `mmar_mage`
    import. Tests pass a `_GenSpy` that records every call;
    production passes a real `MAGEGenerator`. Same pattern
    `care.stage_export` / `care.preflight.validate_chain`
    use elsewhere in CARE.

  **Tests (`tests/test_stage_regeneration.py`, 21 cases):**
  - **Stage dispatch (7 cases):** every stage routes to its
    documented MAGE method with the right positional args;
    `plan`'s optional kwargs forward as kwargs verbatim;
    `describe`'s `allowed_step_types` and `critique`'s
    `threshold` make it through as kwargs.
  - **Async / sync handling (3 cases):** async coroutines
    awaited; sync returns pass through; result wrapped in
    a frozen `StageArtifact`.
  - **Input validation (3 cases):** unknown stage raises
    with the supported list; missing required input names
    the missing key + doesn't touch the generator; empty
    inputs dict raises.
  - **Missing-method path (2 cases):** generator without
    the per-stage method raises "upgrade mmar_mage";
    non-callable attribute triggers the same error.
  - **Error wrapping (3 cases):** sync exception wraps;
    async exception inside the coroutine wraps;
    `StageRegenerationError` raised by the method
    propagates unwrapped (no double-wrap).
  - **`supported_stages()` (3 cases):** returns all seven
    stage names; result is sorted; pinned set for the
    future UI dropdown.

  **What this gets a CARE user today:**

  ```python
  from care import regenerate_stage
  from mmar_mage import MAGEGenerator, MAGEConfig

  generator = MAGEGenerator(config=MAGEConfig(...))
  # User clicks "Regenerate DAG only" on a saved chain:
  artifact = await regenerate_stage(
      generator,
      "dag",
      inputs={"plan": prior_result.intermediate_artifacts["plan"]},
  )
  # `artifact.artifact` is a fresh DAGStructure.
  ```

  The remaining UI work (a "Regenerate" dropdown on
  `InspectionScreen` / `EditAgentScreen` that calls this
  function) is gated on §1 P0 screen work; the data-layer
  side is complete.
- **[DONE]** Capability priming: before MAGE runs, fetch the
  user's installed AgentSkills and the available MCP servers from
  `~/.config/care/mcp_servers.toml`, pass to MAGE as
  `CapabilityContext`. Requires MAGE TODO §3 (shipped).

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.build_capability_payload(catalog, *, environment_id,
compute_skill_sha) -> CapabilityPayload` in
    `care/capability_priming.py`, re-exported from the `care`
    top-level. The bridge between the local
    `CapabilityCatalog` (shipped this milestone) and MAGE's
    `CapabilityContext` injection (MAGE §3.9, shipped).
  - `CapabilityPayload` is a frozen dataclass mirroring MAGE's
    `CapabilityContext` field set but using plain
    `tuple[dict[str, Any], ...]` primitives instead of MAGE
    types. Lets CARE construct, inspect, log, and persist the
    payload **without importing `mmar_mage`** at all — matches
    the convention `care.runtime.mage_poster` established (no
    upstream imports at the data-shape layer). MAGE is lazy-
    imported only when the caller actually calls
    `payload.to_mage_context()` right before
    `generator.generate(capabilities=...)`.
  - `CapabilityPayload.to_mage_context()` raises a friendly
    `CapabilityPrimingError("mmar_mage is not installed; install
it with `pip install mmar-mage`")` rather than a raw
    `ImportError`. Exercised for real in this dev env where
    `mmar_mage` isn't installed — the test verifies the
    descriptive message, not a mock.
  - Per-kind converters under `_tool_dict` / `_mcp_dict` /
    `_agent_skill_dict`: - **Tools** → `{name, source, description, tags}`. The
    catalog doesn't introspect Python signatures (that's
    `care.tools.load_tools_into_context`'s runtime job), so
    this entry stays at directory-listing fidelity. - **MCP servers** → `{name, description, tags, command,
args, config}` where `config` is the full original TOML
    body. Convenience top-level `command`/`args` mean the
    planner doesn't have to dig into `config` for the
    common case. Missing `args` defaults to `[]`. - **AgentSkills** → MAGE `AgentSkillEntry`-shaped dict with
    `uri = local://<absolute SKILL.md path>` (same convention
    as `care.promote_skill_to_memory`), `manifest_summary`
    from the parsed frontmatter, `source = "local"` to label
    provenance for the planner prompt, `relevance=0.0` +
    `why=""` (no ranker at this stage), and the SHA-256 of
    SKILL.md when `compute_skill_sha=True` (default).
  - SHA computation tolerates a SKILL.md disappearing between
    catalog scan and prime call — the entry survives with an
    empty `sha256` and the planner falls back to URI matching.
    Lets CARE prime against a long-running catalog without
    needing to re-scan on every generate.
  - `memory_card` entries from the catalog are **dropped**
    on purpose: they're consumed by MAGE via Memory search,
    not via the planner-context input. Keeps the priming
    surface clean — one shape per channel.
  - `CapabilityPayload.is_empty` predicate + `to_dict()` for
    logging / run-artifact serialisation. Both return deep
    copies so callers can't mutate the payload's tuples
    through the dict view.

  **Tests (`tests/test_capability_priming.py`, 13 cases):**
  - Payload shape: empty payload sensible defaults, `to_dict`
    round-trips and returns deep copies (mutating the dict
    doesn't bleed back), frozen-dataclass assertion.
  - Tool priming: catalog `tool` entry maps to planner dict
    with `name`/`source`/`description`/`tags`; memory cards
    are dropped from the tools list when mixed in.
  - MCP priming: catalog `mcp_server` entry preserves
    `command`/`args` at the top level AND the full TOML body
    under `config`; missing `args` defaults to `[]`.
  - AgentSkill priming: SKILL.md → MAGE `AgentSkillEntry`
    dict with `local://<abs>/SKILL.md` URI, SHA-256 matches
    actual file bytes, `manifest_summary` from frontmatter,
    `tags` + `allowed_tools` from frontmatter, `source =
"local"` provenance label, zero relevance + empty why;
    `compute_skill_sha=False` skips hashing; vanished
    SKILL.md path between scan and prime yields empty SHA
    without raising; `environment_id` forwards verbatim.
  - Integration: all three kinds together → payload has
    populated `tools` + `mcp_servers` + `agent_skills`,
    `is_empty=False`.
  - Lazy MAGE import: `to_mage_context()` raises
    `CapabilityPrimingError` with the friendly install hint
    when `mmar_mage` isn't on the install path (real
    ImportError → wrapped, no mocking).

- **[DONE]** Pre-flight validation: render the generated chain
  through `ReasoningChain.from_json()` and surface validation
  errors inline before letting the user run/evolve.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.validate_chain(payload, *, context=None,
use_typed_steps=True) -> PreflightResult` in
    `care/preflight.py`, re-exported from the `care` top-level.
    Two layers in one call: parse the chain via CARL's
    `ReasoningChain.from_dict/from_json`, then (when the parse
    succeeds and the chain exposes `.preflight`) compare its
    declared `required_tools/mcp_servers/skills` against the
    user's context and surface missing items as `missing_*`.
  - `PreflightResult` is a frozen dataclass with CARE-stable
    fields (`parsed`, `parse_errors`, `required_*`,
    `missing_*`, `chain`, `preflight_available`). Doesn't
    depend on CARL's own `PreflightReport` shape so a CARL
    version bump that changes those internals doesn't ripple
    here. Two convenience predicates: `is_valid` (chain
    parsed regardless of deps) and `ok` (parsed AND no
    missing deps).
  - Accepts three payload shapes in one entry point:
    - `dict` matching CARL's chain serialisation,
    - JSON `str` (decoded then forwarded to `from_dict`),
    - `bytes`/`bytearray` (UTF-8 decoded with a structured
      "invalid utf-8" error on bad bytes),
    - already-parsed `ReasoningChain` (duck-typed via
      `hasattr(payload, "steps")` so the function avoids a
      hard `isinstance` import that would force a CARL pin).
      Lets CARE call `validate_chain` on MAGE's freshly-emitted
      chain (dict), a library-loaded artifact (JSON string),
      or a re-validated in-memory chain without per-call type
      juggling.
  - `_format_validation_errors` converts Pydantic v2
    `ValidationError` into `"field.path: message"` lines
    that CARE's UI bullet-renders directly. Non-Pydantic
    exceptions (e.g. CARL's typed-step parser raising
    `KeyError("number")` eagerly) get a single best-effort
    line so callers always have something to display.
  - **Defensive against missing upstream**: when the parsed
    chain doesn't have a `.preflight` method (older
    `mmar-carl 0.2.0` ships parse but not preflight),
    `preflight_available=False` lets the UI hint "upgrade
    CARL for tool gap detection" instead of silently
    returning empty `missing_*`. When `.preflight` exists
    but raises (best-effort upstream), the parse signal is
    preserved and the exception is surfaced as a
    `parse_errors` entry — caller still sees the chain.
  - `format_text()` renders a TUI footer / stdout line:
    one-line ok summary with tool/mcp/skill counts (pluralised
    correctly), a "preflight skipped" hint when CARL doesn't
    ship the method, or a multi-line "missing dependencies"
    breakdown grouped by kind.
  - `mmar_carl` import is **lazy** inside `_parse` — keeps
    `care.preflight` importable when CARL isn't installed
    (the parse just fails with a clean `mmar_carl: <reason>`
    error on the result).

  **Tests (`tests/test_preflight.py`, 22 cases):**
  - Result shape: default failure prints "chain failed to
    parse"; ok-text includes pluralised tool/mcp/skill
    counts (singular vs plural); preflight-skipped text;
    missing-deps multi-line breakdown grouped by kind;
    `is_valid` stays True when deps are missing (chain
    well-formed but env not provisioned); frozen-dataclass
    assertion.
  - Real CARL parse (uses installed `mmar-carl 0.2.0`):
    dict payload → real `ReasoningChain` returned;
    JSON-string payload; bytes payload; invalid JSON
    string surfaces with line/col location;
    invalid UTF-8 bytes surface with codec error; missing
    required step field reports at least one descriptive
    error (typed-step parser may KeyError); Pydantic
    validation error path (via `use_typed_steps=False`)
    yields `field.path: message` lines mentioning every
    missing field; unsupported payload type
    (`validate_chain(42)`) reports "expected dict";
    already-parsed chain passes through unchanged (no
    re-parse, `chain is` original).
  - Preflight unavailable on installed CARL: confirms the
    `preflight_available=False` branch with real
    `mmar-carl 0.2.0`, including the "preflight skipped"
    format_text line.
  - Stub-driven preflight (verifies the `missing_*`
    plumbing without depending on CARL dev branch):
    required/missing fields round-trip from stub
    `PreflightReport`-shaped object; `context` argument
    forwarded verbatim to `chain.preflight(context)`;
    exception inside preflight surfaces as `parse_errors`
    while keeping `parsed=True`; bare chain object without
    `.preflight` marks `preflight_available=False`;
    `format_text()` includes the missing-tool list.
  - Integration: real chain + `context=None` → no missing
    deps, `ok=True`, missing\_\* tuples all empty.

---

## 5. Execution: running CARL chains (P1)

- **[DONE]** `care/runtime/executor.py` — instantiates a `ReasoningContext`
  populated from the user's task description + context files + memory,
  injects `on_step_*` callbacks, calls `chain.execute_async(ctx)`.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/runtime/executor.py` ships three coordinated
  entrypoints that the future ExecutionScreen calls into. (1)
  `build_run_context(_, query, api, config=None, files=None, streamer=None,
  tools*path=None, extra_kwargs=None)`— fresh-run path used right after
MAGE generation. Pre-loads`files`into`context.memory["input"]`(defensive copy so caller mutations don't leak), inherits`config.defaults.language`, lets `extra_kwargs`override every default,
attaches the optional`CarlStreamer`via its`attach()`method, and
forwards`tools_path`to CARL's`register_tools_from_path`after
expanding`~`and env vars. (2)`prime_from_saved_chain(chain, *, api,
  outer*context=None, files=None, load_files_from_metadata=True,
  streamer=None, tools_path=None, extra_kwargs=None)`— re-run path that
delegates to CARL's shipped`ReasoningContext.from_chain_inputs`(PREPARE.md §5.6) which recovers`task_description`+`context_files`
from the chain's CARE metadata block. RunContextModal-style overrides
(`outer_context`override,`files`augment / override, opt-out of
metadata file auto-load) flow through unchanged. (3)`execute_chain_async(chain, context)`— thin coordinator wrapper that
validates the chain exposes`execute_async`(loud error if a stub got
passed) and wraps execution failures in`ExecutionError(**cause**=
  original)`so screens can distinguish "the chain crashed" from "the
executor itself broke". CARL import is lazy via the module-level`\_reasoning_context_cls()`helper — tests monkey-patch that single
seam to inject a`\_FakeContext`and exercise every code path without
needing`mmar_carl`installed; an import failure on real startup
surfaces as`ExecutionError("mmar_carl is not installed")`rather than
a raw ImportError. 21 tests in`tests/test_executor.py` across 5
  areas: build_run_context (10 — minimal inputs, files into input
  memory, files-dict-copied-not-referenced guard, language from
  CareConfig, extra_kwargs forwarded, explicit kwarg overrides config,
  streamer attach called, streamer None no-op, tools_path expanded +
  registered, tools_path None no-op, construction failure wrapped);
  prime_from_saved_chain (4 — forwards to from_chain_inputs with
  defaults, overrides forwarded, streamer attached, failure wrapped);
  execute_chain_async (3 — forwards context + returns result, rejects
  chain without method, wraps chain failure preserving **cause**);
  \_register_tools edge cases (2 — no-path no-op, missing-method raises);
  lazy import (1 — missing mmar_carl raises ExecutionError not
  ImportError). All real-call (no internal SDK monkey-patching beyond
  the documented seam); ruff clean.*
- **[DONE] Re-run from library** — when the user
  picks `Run` on a saved agent, `executor.py` loads the agent's
  stored `task_description` and context file list (saved by
  `SaveAgentModal.keep_context`). The `RunContextModal` (§1.3)
  lets the user accept defaults or override. Re-running an agent
  N times produces N `memory_card` run records linked to the
  same agent entity — discoverable via "Run history" tab on
  InspectionScreen.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (load + execute orchestration)
  + Textual `ExecutionScreen` (P0.22) +
  `RunContextModal` (P0.21). `care/screens/execution.py::ExecutionScreen`
  consumes the shipped `CarlStreamer` messages and renders
  step-log / LLM-stream / telemetry panes; `Esc` cancels via
  the `execute` worker group; chain-completion + human-input
  events surface on `state.chain_result` /
  `state.pending_human_prompt`. The host pushes the screen
  with the `RunPlan` from `load_run_plan` and fires
  `execute_library_run` on mount.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/library_run.py` exposes the bounded surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `LibraryRunPlan` — frozen bundle returned by
      :func:`load_run_plan` carrying:
      - `chain` — the materialised CARL `ReasoningChain`.
      - `entity_id` / `entity_type` / `channel` — routing for
        the eventual `record_run_completion` write.
      - `display_name` — header label for the modal.
      - `draft` — pre-populated :class:`RunContextDraft` that
        the modal binds to (task description + file list +
        overrides slot all primed from the chain's CARE
        metadata via :func:`extract_run_context_draft`).
      - `has_chain` predicate for the "loaded vs. empty" UI
        state.
    - `load_run_plan(memory, entity_id, *, channel, entity_type,
      source_name, timeout)` — async helper that:
      1. Calls `memory.client.get_chain(entity_id, channel)`
         in a thread (with deadline via `asyncio.wait_for`).
      2. Patches `entity_id` onto the loaded chain when CARL's
         SDK projection drops it (matches the pattern in
         `prime_from_saved_chain`).
      3. Calls `extract_run_context_draft(chain, source_name=...)`
         to seed the modal's form state.
      4. Falls back to stamping `source_entity_id` on the draft
         directly when the chain object is frozen / immutable.
      Returns a populated `LibraryRunPlan`. Raises
      `LibraryRunError` on empty entity_id, missing SDK method,
      timeout, SDK failure, or a 404 (chain not found) response.
    - `execute_library_run(memory, plan, draft, *, config, api,
      streamer, tools_path, run_id, author, record_completion)`
      — async orchestrator composing the three shipped helpers:
      1. `validate_run_context_draft(draft)` — refuses to run
         when error-severity issues remain; the modal is
         expected to clear them upstream.
      2. `apply_overrides(config, draft)` — per-run model /
         provider clone (session config untouched).
      3. `build_extra_kwargs(draft)` — turns edits into
         `outer_context=` / `files=` / `load_files_from_metadata=`
         for the prime helper.
      4. `prime_from_saved_chain(plan.chain, api=api,
         streamer=streamer, tools_path=tools_path, **extras)`.
      5. `execute_chain_async(plan.chain, context)`.
      6. `record_run_completion(memory, ...)` — persists the
         `memory_card` linked to `plan.entity_id` (run count +
         last_run_at bump on the source agent entity).
      `record_completion=False` skips step 6 — useful for
      dry-run / live-tracing modes. Each step wraps native
      exceptions as `LibraryRunError` so the modal's catch
      clause stays single-branch. Returns a typed
      :class:`RunCompletion` populated with the run id +
      :class:`RunSummary`.
    - `LibraryRunError` / `EntityKind` exposed for callers.

  **Why N×memory_card writes produce N run records:** every call
  to `execute_library_run` ends in `record_run_completion`
  which `save_memory_card(...)` then `_record_run(...)`. The
  card carries `meta.tags = ["agent_run", f"agent:{id}",
  f"status:{label}"]` so the Run-history tab's
  `fetch_run_history(memory, agent_entity_id)` filter picks
  every previous run cleanly.

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** the loader accepts any
  `CareMemory`-like facade exposing
  `.client.get_chain(entity_id, channel)`; production passes the
  shipped `CareMemory` instance, tests inject lightweight stubs.
  The orchestrator accepts any `CareConfig`-like object with a
  `model_copy(update=)` shape (matches the Pydantic
  `CareConfig` and `MageConfig`); tests use a stand-in. No
  `mmar_carl` import is required by the module itself — the
  `prime_from_saved_chain` import is the only `mmar_carl`
  surface and it's lazy-loaded by that helper, so tests monkey-
  patch the prime call site to avoid the dependency.
