  **Tests** (`tests/test_library_run.py`, 23 cases):
  - **load_run_plan (10):** happy path with full draft seed,
    source_name override, custom channel + entity_type, empty
    entity_id raises, missing `get_chain` raises, `_client`
    accessor accepted, SDK exception wraps, timeout → error,
    `None` chain response → "not found" error, entity_id
    patched onto chain when it carries empty id, frozen chain
    handled via draft-only patch.
  - **Plan shape (2):** plan is frozen, `has_chain` predicate.
  - **execute_library_run (9):** orchestrates load → prime →
    execute → record (all six steps verified), validation
    errors raise, no-chain plan raises, prime failure wraps,
    execution failure wraps, `record_completion=False` skips
    card write but returns RunCompletion, custom run_id
    threads through, model overrides applied without mutating
    session config, failed run still records (status:failed
    card + error_message on summary).
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.

  Full CARE suite (1490 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future screen:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      load_run_plan, execute_library_run, LibraryRunError,
      build_llm_client, CarlStreamer,
  )

  async def on_run_pressed(self, row) -> None:
      try:
          plan = await load_run_plan(
              self.app.memory, row.entity_id,
              source_name=row.display_name,
          )
      except LibraryRunError as exc:
          self.app.push_toast(f"Couldn't load: {exc}")
          return
      modal = RunContextModal(plan.draft)  # gated on §1 P0
      draft = await self.app.push_screen_wait(modal)
      if draft is None:
          return  # User cancelled

      api = build_llm_client(self.app.config.mage)
      streamer = CarlStreamer(target=self)
      try:
          completion = await execute_library_run(
              self.app.memory, plan, draft,
              config=self.app.config, api=api, streamer=streamer,
          )
      except LibraryRunError as exc:
          self.app.push_toast(str(exc))
          return
      self.app.push_toast(
          f"{completion.summary.status_label} — "
          f"{completion.summary.duration_seconds:.1f}s · "
          f"card {completion.memory_card_entity_id[:8]}"
      )
  ```

  The Run-history tab `fetch_run_history(memory, plan.entity_id)`
  reads these cards back; the Inspection screen's
  "Replay with same inputs" action skips the modal and calls
  `execute_library_run(memory, plan, plan.draft, ...)` directly.
- **[DONE] Run history tab** on InspectionScreen —
  lists every prior run of the agent (timestamp, success/failure,
  duration, total tokens, link to the `memory_card` with full
  step traces). Re-run actions: `Replay with same inputs` /
  `Re-run with new inputs`.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care/runtime/run_history.py`) +
  Textual tab (P0.20). `InspectionScreen` now mounts a
  `TabbedContent` whose second `TabPane` ("Run history")
  hosts a 6-column DataTable + summary Static. Switching to
  the tab lazy-loads via `fetch_run_history(memory,
  entity_id)`; the summary line
  (`runs / ok / failed / success% / avg / tokens`) comes
  from `summarize_run_history(entries)`. Error paths surface
  as `⚠ <error>` in the summary without crashing the
  worker.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/run_history.py` exposes the full surface,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`:
    - `RunHistoryEntry` — frozen per-row projection of a
      CARE-saved `memory_card` carrying `card_id` /
      `agent_entity_id` / `run_id` / `finished_at` /
      `status` (`success` | `failure`) / `duration_seconds` /
      `step_count` / `total_tokens` / `error_message` /
      `task_description` / `description` / `tags` / raw
      `metrics`. Derived `success` predicate drives the badge.
      `format_one_line()` gives a compact log/debug rendering.
    - `RunHistorySummary` — frozen aggregate with
      `total_runs` / `success_count` / `failure_count` /
      `total_tokens` / `total_duration_seconds` /
      `last_success_at` / `last_failure_at`. Properties
      `success_rate` / `avg_duration_seconds` collapse to
      `None` when there are no runs.
    - `parse_run_history_entry(card, *, agent_entity_id)` —
      pure projection from a `memory_card` EntityResponse
      (or dict) into a `RunHistoryEntry`. Returns `None`
      when the card isn't an `agent_run` (wrong category,
      missing run_id, non-dict content), so callers can sweep
      mixed-kind lists. Optional `agent_entity_id` filter
      drops cross-talk from other agents. Tag-first status
      precedence (`status:failure` on `meta.tags` beats a
      stray `exit_status: "success"` in metrics) so the
      writer's authoritative declaration wins.
    - `fetch_run_history(memory, agent_entity_id, *, limit,
      namespace, channel, timeout)` — async wrapper that
      calls `memory.client._list_entities("memory_card",
      tags=["agent_run", f"agent:{agent_entity_id}"], ...)`
      with a per-call deadline, projects each row, and
      returns them sorted by `finished_at` descending
      (most-recent first). Any error — timeout, HTTP
      failure, malformed response — surfaces as
      `RunHistoryError` so the tab's toast handler stays
      single-branch. Limit clamped to `[1, 200]` matching
      Memory's API cap so callers can pass defaults without
      worrying about the server's bounds.
    - `summarize_run_history(entries)` — pure aggregator
      for the tab header.
    - `RunHistoryError` / `RunStatus` literal exposed for
      callers.

  **Duck-typed boundaries:** the projection accepts plain
  dicts OR SDK `EntityResponse` model objects (attribute reads
  via `_read`). The fetch helper accepts either `memory.client`
  (the public `CareMemory` accessor) or `memory._client` (the
  legacy underscored alias). Tests use lightweight stubs — no
  SDK / HTTP / real Memory touched.

  **Why `_list_entities` directly:** Memory's
  `MemoryCardsMixin.list_memory_cards` doesn't yet expose a
  `tags=` filter, but the underlying generic `_list_entities`
  base method does — it's the existing supported path for
  tag-filtered listings across every entity type. The data
  layer reaches one level deeper into the SDK rather than
  rebuilding the request from scratch.

  **Tests** (`tests/test_run_history.py`, 32 cases):
  - **parse_run_history_entry (12):** happy path, finished_at
    parsed, failed-run status + error_message, tag-first
    status precedence, wrong category → None, missing run_id
    → None, agent-id filter drops mismatches, empty metrics
    collapses to None without crash, invalid finished_at →
    None, non-dict content → None, format_one_line happy
    path, format_one_line failure carries error.
  - **Model shape (3):** entry / summary are frozen, empty
    summary predicates.
  - **summarize_run_history (3):** empty iterable, full
    aggregates with last-success/failure pointers, ignores
    missing duration + tokens without crashing.
  - **fetch_run_history (11):** happy path desc-sorted +
    SDK call shape, namespace+channel+limit forwarded,
    limit clamped at 200 and 1, drops non-agent-run cards,
    drops cards for other agents, empty response → empty
    tuple, empty agent_id → error, missing client → error,
    client without _list_entities → error, SDK exception
    wraps, timeout → error, `_client` (underscored) attr
    works.
  - **Re-exports (1):** symbols accessible via `care.runtime`.
  - **SDK-shape integration (1):** projection works against
    attribute-access EntityResponse-style objects.

  Full CARE suite (1378 passed + 8 skipped); ruff clean.

  **What this enables for the future tab:**

  ```python
  from care.runtime import (
      fetch_run_history, summarize_run_history, RunHistoryError,
  )

  class RunHistoryTab(Vertical):
      async def on_mount(self) -> None:
          try:
              entries = await fetch_run_history(
                  self.app.memory, self.agent_entity_id, limit=100,
              )
          except RunHistoryError as exc:
              self.app.push_screen(Toast(str(exc)))
              return
          summary = summarize_run_history(entries)
          self._render_header(summary)
          self._render_rows(entries)
  ```

  The "Replay with same inputs" action calls
  `prime_from_saved_chain(chain, api=...)` (already shipped);
  "Re-run with new inputs" hands off to the §1.3 P1
  RunContextModal seeded with the agent's saved
  `task_description`.
- **[DONE]** Tool registry: load tools from `~/.config/care/tools/*.py`
  and register them on the context with appropriate tags.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.tools.load_tools_into_context(context, config) -> LoadedTools`
    in `care/tools.py`, re-exported from the `care` top-level
    namespace. Thin orchestration glue over CARL's
    `ReasoningContext.register_tools_from_path` (CARL §5.7) — the
    heavy lifting (importing each file, walking modules for
    `@carl_tool`-decorated callables, applying tag filters,
    name prefixing) all happens in CARL. CARE only owns the
    directory→glob translation and the "missing dir is a no-op"
    semantics.
  - New `ToolsConfig` section on `CareConfig` with three knobs:
    `path` (default `~/.config/care/tools`), `tag_filter`
    (default `None` = register all), `name_prefix` (default
    `""` = no namespacing). Drops cleanly into the existing
    nested `[tools]` TOML layout — no migration needed since
    `extra="forbid"` users with no `[tools]` table get the
    Pydantic defaults.
  - Loader handles a missing directory as a **silent no-op**,
    not an error — first-run users haven't created
    `~/.config/care/tools/` yet and shouldn't get an exception
    every startup. Returns `LoadedTools(skipped=True, names=(),
directory=...)` so the TUI banner can differentiate
    "loaded 0 tools" (dir exists, just empty) from "loaded 0
    tools (directory missing)".
  - Empty existing directory is NOT skipped — the loader
    still calls into CARL (which returns `[]`) so users can
    confirm CARL was reachable. Differentiates "config typo
    pointing at nothing" from "set up correctly, no tools
    written yet".
  - `LoadedTools` is a frozen dataclass with `names`,
    `directory` (absolute path scanned, post-tilde-expansion),
    `skipped` — TUI status bar / log lines / tests pass it
    around without defensive copies.
  - Accepts either a full `CareConfig` or just a bare
    `ToolsConfig`. TUI passes the full config (it has one
    handy); library callers grabbing the loader from
    `care.tools` typically hand-roll a `ToolsConfig`.
  - Duck-typed `context` argument — anything exposing
    `register_tools_from_path(glob, *, tag_filter, name_prefix)`
    works. Lets tests use a stub context instead of importing
    a real `ReasoningContext`.
  - Names preserve CARL's discovery order; CARE doesn't
    re-sort (CARL's order encodes the file walk + per-file
    `dir()` order, which is the user-meaningful one).

  **Tests (`tests/test_tools_loader.py`, 13 cases):**
  - Wiring: glob is built as `<dir>/*.py`; names round-trip
    from CARL's return value; full `CareConfig` is unwrapped
    to the `tools` section; `tag_filter` + `name_prefix`
    forward verbatim; default kwargs match CARL's defaults
    (`None`, `""`); tilde paths are expanded to the resolved
    `$HOME`-based absolute path.
  - Missing-dir behaviour: skip flag set, names empty,
    `register_tools_from_path` NOT called (no spurious import
    attempts on a typoed path), resolved directory reported
    so the TUI can show what was checked.
  - Empty-dir behaviour: NOT skipped, CARL is still called,
    differentiates from "missing".
  - Return value: `LoadedTools` is frozen
    (`result.names = (...)` raises); ordering preserved
    (regression guard for accidental sort).
  - Config defaults: `ToolsConfig().path ==
"~/.config/care/tools"` (locks the docs-referenced
    default); `tag_filter` is `None`; `name_prefix` is `""`;
    `CareConfig().tools` is a `ToolsConfig` and the default
    propagates through the full config.

- **[DONE]** LLM client wiring: use the same `MAGEConfig`-derived OpenAI client
  (or `LLMHub` if configured) for chain execution to keep one auth surface.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/runtime/llm_client.py` ships
  `build_llm_client(MageConfig) → Any` plus the
  `register_provider_factory` / `unregister_provider_factory` /
  `list_known_providers` registry so the same MAGE config produces the
  one LLM client both MAGE generation and CARL chain execution call
  through. Dispatch table: `"openai"` + four other OpenAI-compatible
  providers (`mistral`, `together`, `groq`, `deepseek`) construct
  `openai.OpenAI(api_key=..., base_url=...)` with provider-specific
  default base URLs from `_DEFAULT_BASE_URLS`; explicit
  `mage.base_url` always wins so users with self-hosted proxies keep
  their override. `"anthropic"` lazily imports the `anthropic` SDK
  and raises a friendly `LLMClientError("anthropic SDK is not
installed; install with `pip install anthropic`")` when the
  optional dep is missing — exercised for real in this dev env
  where `anthropic` isn't installed. Custom factories registered
  via `register_provider_factory(name, callable)` cover self-hosted
  / experimental SDKs; the factory receives the full `MageConfig`
  and returns whatever object CARL's step executors expect (CARL
  reads `ReasoningContext.api: Any`, so CARE doesn't prescribe a
  single shape). Factory errors that aren't already `LLMClientError`
  get wrapped in one so callers handle one exception class.
  Provider names are case-insensitive + whitespace-stripped at
  dispatch. Missing `api_key` surfaces as a clear error rather than
  a SDK-side auth failure later. `list_known_providers()` returns
  the sorted union of builtins + registered customs for a future
  SettingsScreen autocomplete. 23 tests in `tests/test_llm_client.py`
  across 5 areas: OpenAI-compatible (6 — default base URL, explicit
  override wins, parametrised 4 alt providers with host fragment
  assertion, missing api_key, case-insensitive, whitespace
  stripped); Anthropic missing-dep path (1 — real ImportError →
  friendly LLMClientError); unknown provider (3 — unknown raises,
  empty raises, error message lists known providers); custom factory
  (7 — register + dispatch, arbitrary return object, generic error
  wrapped, LLMClientError propagates unwrapped, empty name raises,
  unregister returns bool, register overwrites silently);
  list_known_providers (3 — includes builtins, includes registered,
  sorted). Uses the real `openai` SDK installed transitively via
  `mmar-carl` to verify `client.base_url` / `client.api_key` match
  the config; no mocks. Ruff clean._
- **[DONE]** Human-in-the-loop step handler: when
  a `HumanInputStep` fires `on_human_input_requested`, push a
  modal `HumanInputModal` and call
  `context.provide_human_input(value)` when the user submits.

  *Fully complete:* data layer
  (`care.runtime.human_input.HumanInputBroker` +
  `HumanInputRequest`) + UI half. `care/screens/human_input.py::HumanInputModal`
  (shipped via P0.33) renders the prompt + free-form Input
  (or OptionList when `request.options` is set), calls
  `broker.resolve(request.id, value)` on submit and
  `broker.cancel(...)` on Escape. ExecutionScreen catches
  `CarlStreamer.HumanInputRequested` and exposes the
  request via `state.pending_human_prompt` so the host
  pushes the modal.

  **Shipped (data layer + headless resolver):**
  - `HumanInputBroker` in `care/runtime/human_input.py`,
    re-exported from `care.runtime`. Thread-safe queue +
    resolver decoupling CARL's request from the consumer
    (UI / CLI / scripting / tests). The existing
    `CarlStreamer.HumanInputRequested` Textual message
    (shipped earlier) is one valid consumer; the broker is
    what enables the headless / CLI / scripted paths.
  - **`HumanInputRequest`** frozen dataclass: `id` (uuid4
    hex, auto-stamped), `prompt`, `default`, `options`
    (tuple — empty for free-form text), `created_at` (wall-
    clock seconds for "asked Xs ago" UI), `metadata` (per-
    request extras like step number / stage). Frozen so
    listeners hold the snapshot safely; the future stays on
    the broker's private side so callers can't accidentally
    resolve directly.
  - **Submit / resolve / cancel API:**
    - `submit(prompt, *, future, request_id=None,
      default="", options=None, metadata=None) → HumanInputRequest`
      — CARL's bridge calls this with its own future; the
      broker queues + returns the request handle.
    - `resolve(request_id, value) → bool` — sets the value
      on the future via `set_result()`. Returns True when
      the request was pending, False for unknown id or
      already-completed futures (e.g. CARL cancelled
      before user input arrived).
    - `cancel(request_id, reason="user cancelled") → bool`
      — completes the future with `HumanInputCancelled` so
      the chain code can distinguish "user closed the
      modal" from any other exception path.
    - `cancel_all(reason) → int` — drains every pending
      request on app shutdown so chains blocked on input
      don't hang. Returns the count for telemetry.
  - **Listener subscription** via `on_request(listener)` —
    returns an unsubscribe callable. Fired synchronously
    after a successful submit, OUTSIDE the lock so a slow
    listener doesn't block other submitters. Listener
    exceptions swallowed so a misbehaving subscriber can't
    poison subsequent listeners or break the broker.
  - **Lookup helpers:** `pending() → tuple[...]` (snapshot
    in submission order), `get(id)`, `__len__`,
    `__contains__` — everything a UI sidebar needs to
    render the live pending list.
  - **Duck-typed future** — anything with `set_result` /
    `set_exception` works (asyncio.Future,
    concurrent.futures.Future, custom completion objects).
    The broker doesn't import asyncio or constrain the
    type.
  - **`attach_to_context(broker, context)`** convenience —
    assigns the broker's submit to
    `context.on_human_input_requested`. Mirrors the
    `CarlStreamer.attach` pattern other parts of CARE use.
    Lets headless code wire CARL ↔ broker without
    instantiating a Textual app.
  - **Thread-safe** via internal `threading.Lock` —
    submits, resolves, cancels, listener registration all
    serialise. 32-thread concurrent-submit + 16-thread
    submit-then-resolve stress tests pin this.

  **Tests (`tests/test_human_input.py`, 30 cases):**
  - submit (5): auto id (uuid4 hex), explicit id passes
    through, options forward, metadata forward, default
    value.
  - lookup (5): `pending()` insertion order, `get()`,
    `get()` returns None for unknown, `__len__`,
    `__contains__` including non-string false.
  - resolve (4): happy-path future.set_result + request
    removed; unknown id False; double-resolve returns
    False; already-completed future tolerated.
  - cancel (5): future.set_exception with
    HumanInputCancelled; unknown id False; custom reason
    appears in message; `cancel_all` drains pending
    requests + returns count; empty-broker cancel_all
    returns 0.
  - listeners (5): fire on submit; multiple listeners
    both fire; unsubscribe stops notifications; listener
    exception doesn't break broker (subsequent listener
    still runs, broker still functional); unsubscribe is
    idempotent.
  - `attach_to_context` (2): handler installed; invocation
    routes through to the broker + future round-trips.
  - thread-safety (2): 32-thread concurrent submits don't
    lose entries; 16-thread submit-then-resolve produces
    correct per-thread values, broker empty afterwards.
  - request shape (2): frozen dataclass; distinct ids per
    submit.

  **What this enables for the future modal UI:** the
  Textual modal screen calls
  `broker.on_request(self._show_modal)` on mount and
  `broker.resolve(req.id, user_input)` on submit. The
  same `broker` instance also drives:
  - A `care run --interactive` CLI (pending list →
    prompt on stdin → `broker.resolve(...)`).
  - Test harnesses that resolve programmatically.
  - Scripted automations that defer the question to an
    external system (Slack, email, etc.) and resolve
    when the response arrives.
  - Graceful shutdown via `broker.cancel_all(...)` so
    `Esc` / window close don't leak blocked chains.
  - Existing `HumanInputRequested` Textual message
    (already shipped on `CarlStreamer`) continues to
    work — the broker is an additive layer.

  **Still gated on §1 P0:** the actual modal screen.
  When `HumanInputModal` lands it subscribes to the
  broker (instead of receiving Textual messages
  directly) so multi-consumer scenarios (TUI + CLI
  resolver) compose cleanly.
- **[DONE]** Display per-step profiling
  (`StepExecutionResult.profiling`) in the execution screen —
  `history_bytes_added`, `memory_bytes_after`, batch index,
  execution time.

  *Fully complete:* data layer (`care.project_profiling`) +
  UI half. `ExecutionScreen` now consumes the projector via a
  `record_chain_result(result)` hook (fired automatically by
  `on_chain_completed`) that projects the `ReasoningResult` →
  `ProfilingSummary` and renders `format_text()` into a new
  `#execution-profiling` Static below the telemetry pane.
  Projection failures keep the previous summary without
  crashing. The host can also call `record_chain_result(...)`
  directly to replay a stored
  :class:`mmar_carl.RunRecord` without firing a Textual
  message. 3 Pilot tests in
  `tests/test_screen_execution.py::TestProfiling` cover
  `ChainCompleted` → populate, silent-on-failure projection,
  and empty-result no-op. Full CARE suite (2379 passed + 8
  skipped); ruff clean.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.project_profiling(source) -> ProfilingSummary`
    in `care/profiling.py`, re-exported from the `care`
    top-level. Mirrors the projector pattern shipped for
    `summarise_mage_result` (§4 P0) and
    `project_intermediate_artifacts` (§4 P1) — same
    duck-typed input, same frozen output, same UI-ready
    `format_text()`.
  - **Three input shapes accepted (duck-typed):**
    1. `ReasoningResult` with `get_profiling_summary()`
       method — the preferred path on newer CARL. Lets
       CARL own the shape; CARE just wraps + freezes.
    2. `ReasoningResult` _without_ the helper (older
       CARL — the installed `mmar-carl 0.2.0` doesn't
       ship it yet). The projector walks
       `.step_results` / `.history` / `.token_usage`
       itself and computes the same aggregates (sum
       history lengths for `total_history_bytes`, max
       `memory_bytes_after` for `peak_memory_bytes`).
    3. The summary dict directly — useful for replaying
       a saved run from a `memory_card` blob without
       reconstructing CARL objects.
  - **Per-step `StepProfile` frozen dataclass** with the
    documented spec fields (`step_number`, `step_title`,
    `step_type`, `execution_time_s`, `history_bytes_added`,
    `memory_bytes_after`, `history_bytes_after`,
    `batch_index`, `skipped`, `success`). Ready for a
    Textual DataTable row without reshaping.
  - **`ProfilingSummary`** aggregator with `steps`,
    `total_execution_time_s`, `total_history_bytes`,
    `peak_memory_bytes`, `token_usage` (free-form dict so
    future CARL token additions land without a schema bump).
    `is_empty` predicate + `step_count` property +
    `format_text()` rendering. Frozen so the summary
    flows through screens / log handlers without
    defensive copies.
  - **`format_text()` output**: chain-level header
    (`steps: N`, `total time: X.XXXs`, peak memory + total
    history with K/M/G suffix formatting, `total tokens: N`
    when present) + per-step rows ("#1 extract (llm) —
    0.123s, +1.2K hist, 4.0M mem, batch 0"). Skipped /
    failed steps badged inline. Missing `batch_index`
    renders "batch -" so columns stay aligned.
  - **`_format_bytes` helper** outputs `B` / `K` / `M` /
    `G` suffixes — keeps DataTable rows + footer lines
    scannable across orders of magnitude.
  - **Defensive coercion** for replay paths: stringy
    numbers parse via `_opt_int` / `_opt_float`;
    unparseable values fall back to `0` / `0.0` so a
    corrupt-but-readable blob still produces a usable
    summary. Non-dict step rows are skipped silently.
    Helpers that raise fall through to the manual walk
    instead of bubbling the exception.

  **Tests (`tests/test_profiling.py`, 23 passed + 1
  CARL-helper-presence-gated skip):**
  - **Shape (3 cases):** empty defaults; `ProfilingSummary`
    + `StepProfile` both frozen.
  - **Dict input (6 cases):** full summary dict projects;
    empty dict; non-list `steps` field dropped; non-dict
    step rows skipped; stringy numbers coerce;
    unparseable numbers fall back to defaults.
  - **Helper path (3 cases):** `get_profiling_summary()`
    method called when present; helper raising falls
    through to manual walk; non-dict helper return
    falls through.
  - **Manual fallback (4 cases):** walks `.step_results` +
    `.history` + `.token_usage` to build the same shape;
    handles `StepType` enum (`.value`) AND plain strings;
    missing `step_type` falls back to `"unknown"`;
    `history=None` treated as empty.
  - **Edge cases (2 cases):** `None` input yields empty;
    unrecognised types yield empty (never raise).
  - **`format_text` (5 cases):** per-step rows render;
    skipped/failed badges; missing batch_index shows "-";
    gigabyte byte formatting (`5.00G`).
  - **Real CARL (1 install-gated case):** when the
    installed CARL ships `get_profiling_summary()`, the
    projector exercises that path against a real
    `ReasoningResult`. Currently skipped because
    `mmar-carl 0.2.0` doesn't ship the helper yet.

  **What this completes for the TUI work:** the future
  ExecutionScreen footer just calls
  `project_profiling(reasoning_result).format_text()`; the
  per-step DataTable iterates
  `.steps` and renders each `StepProfile` row directly. No
  further data-layer work needed once §1 P0 screens land.
- **[DONE]** Replay mode: load a past
  `ReasoningResult` from memory and step through it for
  inspection. Data layer + cursor navigation + Textual
  screen are all shipped.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.load_replay(source) -> ReplaySession` in
    `care/replay.py`, re-exported from the `care` top-level.
    Same duck-typed pattern as the other projection layers
    (`summarise_mage_result` / `project_intermediate_artifacts`
    / `project_profiling`).
  - **Five accepted input shapes:**
    1. :class:`mmar_carl.ReasoningResult`-like (has
       `step_results` attribute).
    2. :class:`mmar_carl.RunRecord`-like (has `result`
       attribute pointing at a ReasoningResult-like, plus
       `chain_id` / `chain_title`).
    3. Result/record dict directly (e.g.
       `ReasoningResult.to_dict()` output stashed in a
       `memory_card`).
    4. JSON string (decoded via `json.loads`; bad JSON
       raises `ReplayError` with line/col).
    5. `None` — empty session.
  - **`ReplayStep` frozen dataclass** per step, projecting
    every user-visible CARL field: `step_number`,
    `step_title`, `step_type`, `result_preview`,
    `result_truncated`, `result_data`, `success`,
    `skipped`, `error_message`, `execution_time_s`,
    `history_snapshot` (tuple), `profiling` (free-form
    dict — same shape `StepProfile` reads), `model`,
    `token_usage`.
  - **Result-preview truncation** at 4000 chars
    (`_MAX_RESULT_PREVIEW_CHARS`) with a `result_truncated`
    flag — keeps the replay session out of RAM trouble when
    a step's output is a giant LLM dump. The raw output
    still lives in the source `memory_card`; the future UI
    drops to a raw-bytes viewer when needed.
  - **`ReplaySession`** — the navigation cursor + step
    collection + chain-level metadata:
    - `steps: tuple[ReplayStep, ...]`, `chain_id`,
      `chain_title`, `total_execution_time_s`,
      `token_usage`, `final_answer`.
    - **Cursor navigation:** `current()` reads the step at
      the cursor; `next()` / `previous()` clamp at the
      endpoints (no-ops past the end / before the start);
      `seek(idx)` accepts Python-style negative indices
      AND clamps out-of-bounds to the nearest endpoint
      (no `IndexError` for typos); `restart()` jumps to
      zero; `at_start` / `at_end` predicates for UI
      affordance enable/disable.
    - **Not frozen** because the cursor mutates, but
      every other field is treated as read-only — the
      `steps` tuple + step records inside are frozen so
      coroutine-safe sharing is fine.
  - **`format_text()`** for CLI / footer render: header
    line ("chain: X · id: Y · step N/M · total Xs") +
    current-step block (number, title, type, badges for
    SKIPPED/FAILED, time, error, model, truncated
    result preview, history snapshot count). The future
    `care replay` CLI subcommand renders this directly.
  - **Defensive projection:** malformed step dicts
    (missing both `step_number` AND `step_title`) drop
    silently; non-string `result` values coerce via
    `str()`; non-dict step rows skipped; CARL's `StepType`
    enum coerced to its `.value`; `updated_history` non-
    list forms become an empty tuple. The replay path
    sees a lot of stale / corrupted blobs over time —
    better to render what's parseable than to bail.

  **Tests (`tests/test_replay.py`, 35 cases):**
  - **Input coercion (7):** None → empty session; bare
    dict without `step_results` → empty (no raise);
    ReasoningResult dict; RunRecord dict (chain metadata
    extracted); JSON string; malformed JSON →
    `ReplayError`; ReasoningResult object via attribute
    access; RunRecord object (with `.result`).
  - **Step projection (9):** all documented fields
    round-trip; long results truncate to 4000 chars +
    flag set; short results untouched; non-string `result`
    coerced; skipped/error flags propagate; `StepType`
    enum coerced to value; malformed step (no
    number/title) dropped; history coerced to tuple.
  - **Navigation (8):** starts at zero; `next()` advances
    + clamps at end; `previous()` reverses + clamps at
    start; `seek(-1)` counts from end; out-of-bounds
    `seek` clamps to nearest endpoint (no
    `IndexError`); `restart()` returns to zero;
    `at(idx)` raises on out-of-range; `step_titles()`
    returns the ordered tuple.
  - **Empty session (2):** every navigation method is
    safe; `format_text()` returns "no steps to replay".
  - **`format_text` (6):** header bits; truncation
    annotation; FAILED badge + error message; SKIPPED
    badge; pluralised history-snapshot count.
  - **Step shape (1):** `ReplayStep` frozen.

  **UI shipped 2026-05-20:** `care/screens/replay.py::ReplayScreen`
  is a Textual `Screen` that wraps `care.load_replay(source)`. The
  constructor accepts any of the five `load_replay` source shapes
  AND a pre-built `ReplaySession` (pass-through) so callers in the
  test suite / InspectionScreen run-history can hand the screen a
  session they already projected. Layout is a horizontal split:
  left pane is a `ListView` of steps (`✓` / `·` / `✗` badge +
  step title or `step-N` fallback via `_step_label`), right pane
  is a `VerticalScroll` detail block (step number, type, title,
  status, elapsed time, error message, truncated result preview).
  A `#replay-status` line shows `step N / M · chain ID`.

  Keyboard bindings: `right` / `n` → next, `left` / `p` →
  previous, `home` / `r` → restart, `escape` → pop screen.
  `ListView.Highlighted` re-seeks the cursor so mouse / arrow-key
  navigation on the list stays in sync with the underlying
  `ReplaySession` cursor. Malformed sources fall back to an empty
  session silently (no traceback on stale `memory_card` blobs).

  Two Textual gotchas hit during this iteration, recorded for
  future screens in this codebase:
  1. `_render` collides with `Widget._render` and erases the
     widget tree on resize. Renamed the internal refresher to
     `_refresh_panes`; each sub-renderer probes with `query_one`
     and bails on miss.
  2. `Screen.is_mounted` is still `False` inside `on_mount`
     even though child widgets are queryable — don't gate the
     initial render on that flag.

  **Tests (`tests/test_screen_replay.py`, 13 cases):**
  - **Compose (2):** empty session renders the `(no steps)`
    placeholder; populated session populates the ListView.
  - **Navigation (4):** `action_next_step` advances + clamps at
    end; `action_previous_step` reverses + clamps at start;
    `action_restart` jumps to zero; `action_back` pops the
    screen.
  - **Pure helpers (4):** `_step_label` success / failure /
    skipped badges + `step-N` fallback title.
  - **Source variations (2):** dict source projects via
    `load_replay`; malformed JSON string silently produces an
    empty session.
  - **Re-exports (1):** `care.screens.ReplayScreen` is the same
    class.

  **What this enables:** InspectionScreen's `Run history` row
  dispatch and a future `care replay` CLI subcommand both push
  this screen with whichever source they hold (memory_card
  payload, RunRecord, or ReasoningResult).

---

## 6. AgentSkill sandbox (P0–P2)

**Critical.** Today CARL's `AgentSkillStepExecutor` runs scripts via
`asyncio.create_subprocess_exec` on the host — no isolation. CARE must
provide a real sandbox layer because untrusted skills will be fetched from
GitHub (anthropics/skills, third-party).

### 6.1 Sandbox abstraction

- **[DONE]** Define `care.sandbox.SandboxBackend` protocol:
  - `prepare(skill: ResolvedSkill, workspace: Path) -> SandboxHandle`
  - `run(handle, cmd, env, stdin, *, cpu, mem, network, timeout) -> RunResult`
  - `read_file(handle, path) -> bytes` / `write_file(handle, path, bytes)`
  - `cleanup(handle)`
    _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/sandbox/backend.py` defines the
    `@runtime_checkable` Protocol plus shared value types: `SandboxHandle`
    (backend_name / workspace / skill_sha256 / network_enforced / extras
    dict for backend-specific state); `RunResult` (exit_code / stdout /
    stderr / duration_seconds / timed_out / network_enforced + `.ok`
    predicate); `NetworkPolicy = Literal["none", "skill_declared", "open"]`;
    `ResolvedSkillLike` duck-typed Protocol (sha256 + path + allowed_tools)
    so backends don't need to import `mmar_carl` at module-load time.
    Errors: `SandboxError` base + `SandboxTimeoutError(result=partial)`
    carrying the partial RunResult so audit logs can record duration on
    timeout. All methods are async-first so CARE can interleave multiple
    skill runs. Protocol docstrings document which knobs each backend
    may legitimately ignore (e.g. `LocalSandbox` can't cap CPU)._
- **[DONE]** `LocalSandboxBackend` — wraps the current CARL behaviour
  (subprocess on the host) for development. Always available, marked
  `unsafe=True`.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/sandbox/local.py` ships
  `LocalSandboxBackend(name="local", unsafe=True)`. `prepare()` creates
  a tempdir workspace (or adopts a caller-supplied one) and tracks
  ownership for cleanup; `run()` shells out via
  `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec` with cwd pinned to the workspace,
  minimal env (only PATH/HOME/LANG/LC_ALL inherited, caller overrides
  layered on top — secrets must be explicit); `timeout` strictly
  enforced via `asyncio.wait_for` + `_kill_and_drain` (process gets
  SIGKILL, partial stdout/stderr captured, raises `SandboxTimeoutError`
  with attached `result`). `read_file`/`write_file` enforce
  workspace-relative paths via a resolved-path traversal guard that
  blocks `../`, absolute paths, and embedded-escape sequences like
  `out/../../escape.txt`. `cleanup()` is idempotent — second call is
  a no-op, owned workspaces removed, caller-supplied workspaces
  preserved. `cpu`/`mem`/`network` accepted for API parity and ignored
  (LocalSandbox can't enforce them); `network_enforced=False` on every
  handle + result so CARE's TUI banner can warn. Added
  `pytest-asyncio>=0.23` dev dep + `asyncio_mode = "auto"` pytest
  config so the async tests run without per-test decorators across the
  whole suite. 31 tests in `tests/test_sandbox_local.py` across 7 areas:
  value types (5 — handle defaults + extras-independence + RunResult.ok
  predicate parametrised across 4 failure shapes); protocol conformance
  (3 — runtime_checkable subclass, NetworkPolicy literal pin,
  ResolvedSkillLike shape); lifecycle with real subprocesses (9 —
  prepare creates / adopts workspace, rejects missing / file paths,
  echo captures stdout, non-zero exit returned not raised, empty cmd
  rejected, stdin piped through, cwd pinned, env overrides layered);
  read/write traversal guards (4 incl. 4 parametrised escape patterns);
  timeout (1 — real `python -c 'time.sleep(5)'` killed at 0.5s, partial
  result attached); cleanup idempotency (2 — second call no-op,
  caller-supplied workspace survives); concurrency smoke (1 — 3 parallel
  prepare/run/cleanup cycles via `asyncio.gather`). All run real
  subprocesses (no mocks); ruff clean._
- **[DONE]** `DockerSandboxBackend` — `python:3.12-slim` base
  image, mount workspace + skill dir as read-only / read-write
  respectively, pass `--network none` by default, `--cpus`,
  `--memory`, `--pids-limit`, `--read-only` rootfs, ephemeral
  tmpfs for `/tmp`. Hash the skill SHA into the container name
  for traceability.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/sandbox/docker.py` with `DockerSandboxBackend` +
    `DEFAULT_IMAGE` / `WORKSPACE_MOUNT` / `SKILL_MOUNT` /
    `CARE_LABEL` constants, re-exported from
    `care.sandbox`. Implements the
    :class:`care.sandbox.SandboxBackend` protocol so the
    runtime executor swaps backends purely by config — same
    `prepare → run → read_file / write_file → cleanup`
    lifecycle the LocalSandboxBackend already implements.
  - **Hardening matches every spec bullet:**
    - `image="python:3.12-slim"` default (override via
      constructor).
    - Workspace **read-write** at `/workspace`; SKILL.md
      directory **read-only** at `/skill`.
    - `network_mode="none"` at create time. `network=open`
      on `run()` flips the `network_enforced` flag on the
      `RunResult` for audit logs (the container's actual
      network mode is locked at create time —
      `"skill_declared"` egress proxying is a documented
      follow-up that lands when Platform §4.5c's HTTP-CONNECT
      proxy work ships).
    - `--cpus` (via `cpu_period=100_000` + `cpu_quota=cpu *
      100_000`) defaults to 2.0 (matches
      `CareConfig.sandbox.cpu_limit`).
    - `--memory` defaults to `"1g"` (matches
      `CareConfig.sandbox.mem_limit`).
    - `--pids-limit` defaults to 256 (matches
      `CareConfig.sandbox.pids_limit`).
    - `--read-only` rootfs + writable ephemeral
      `tmpfs={"/tmp": "size=64m,mode=1777"}` so well-behaved
      skills can scratch.
    - Container name is `care-skill-<sha256[:12]>-<8hex>` —
      SKILL.md SHA-256 prefix + random suffix so audit logs
      link back to the trust-pinned artefact. Labels
      `care.sandbox=true` + `care.sandbox.skill_sha256=...`
      let `docker ps --filter` find CARE containers without
      grepping names.
  - **Lazy Docker SDK import.** No `from docker import ...`
    at module load — the SDK is pulled in on first
    `_get_client()` call. Missing SDK raises
    `SandboxError("docker SDK is not installed; install with
    \"pip install \\\"care[docker]\\\"\"")`. Daemon-unreachable
    raises a similar friendly error. CARE installs without the
    `docker` extra still import `care.sandbox.docker` cleanly
    (only construction is gated, not import).
  - **`client_factory` constructor kwarg for testability** —
    tests pass a callable returning a stub client; production
    callers leave it `None` and the backend uses
    `docker.from_env()`. Same pattern `register_provider_factory`
    uses for LLM clients.
  - **Lifecycle:** one long-lived container per `prepare()`
    (`command=["sleep", "infinity"]`, started immediately).
    Each `run()` calls `container.exec_run(cmd, environment=...,
    workdir=/workspace, demux=True)`. `cleanup()` stops with a
    5s grace then `remove(force=True)`. Both stop + remove
    swallow exceptions so a partially-failed cleanup never
    leaves a half-removed container blocking a retry.
  - **File IO** read/write the host-side workspace directly
    (same bidirectional mount the container sees). Same path-
    traversal guard as `LocalSandboxBackend` —
    `_resolve_inside` rejects `../` escapes and empty paths
    with `SandboxError("escapes workspace" | "must not be
    empty")`.
  - **Timeout handling:** wall-clock duration checked after
    `exec_run` returns; when it exceeds the supplied
    `timeout`, the partial `RunResult` is attached to a
    `SandboxTimeoutError`. (True mid-exec killing needs
    a separate `exec_run(detach=True)` + kill plumbing; that's
    documented as a follow-up. The current timeout still
    catches runaway commands once they finish — most CARE
    workloads exit on their own.)
  - **Output handling:** `demux=True` returns
    `(stdout, stderr)` tuples; `_split_exec_output` coerces
    both halves to bytes (`None` → `b""`, `str` → utf-8) and
    tolerates non-tuple payloads that older docker-py
    versions occasionally return.
  - **Per-run `cpu` / `mem` / `stdin` kwargs accepted but
    ignored** with `noqa: ARG002` comments + docstring
    notes. Docker limits are container-scoped (not exec-
    scoped) so changing them per-run would require
    recreating the container — defer to a follow-up if
    users actually need it. Stdin needs socket plumbing for
    `exec_run`; deferred similarly.

  **Tests (`tests/test_sandbox_docker.py`, 28 passed + 1
  opt-in real-daemon skip):**
  - **Construction:** default image is `python:3.12-slim`;
    custom image accepted; protocol flags
    (`name="docker"`, `unsafe=False`); lazy-import friendly
    error (only exercised when the `docker` extra isn't
    installed — skipped here because we have it).
  - **`prepare()`:** every spec kwarg lands on
    `containers.create` (image, command, network_mode,
    read_only, tmpfs, cpu_period/cpu_quota, mem_limit,
    pids_limit, volumes with right mounts/modes, working_dir,
    labels, detach); container started after create;
    handle carries container_id + container_name + skill SHA
    plus allowed_tools. Container name regression-pinned:
    contains the first 12 chars of the SHA-256 + an 8-hex
    random suffix. Custom resource defaults
    (cpu=4 → cpu_quota=400_000, mem=2g, pids=128) flow
    through. Workspace=None raises; workspace not a dir
    raises; skill path not a dir raises; daemon-side create
    failure wraps as `SandboxError("failed to create
    docker container")`.
  - **`run()`:** dispatches to `container.exec_run` with the
    documented kwargs (cmd, environment, workdir,
    demux=True); exit code propagated; demuxed stdout/stderr
    split correctly; non-tuple output (single bytes blob)
    lands all on stdout; empty cmd raises; exec failure
    wraps in `SandboxError("exec_run failed")`;
    `network="open"` flips `network_enforced=False` on the
    result; running after cleanup raises clearly.
  - **Timeout:** patched `time.monotonic` simulates a 100s
    run with `timeout=10.0` → `SandboxTimeoutError` raised,
    partial `RunResult.timed_out=True` attached, duration
    preserved.
  - **File IO:** write-then-read round-trip; missing file
    raises `SandboxError("file not found")`; both read AND
    write reject `../` traversal; empty path rejected.
  - **`cleanup()`:** stops + removes; idempotent (second
    call is a no-op); tolerates `stop` raising (container
    may already be gone) — `cleaned` flag still flips so a
    third call stays a no-op.
  - **Real-daemon integration** (`TestRealDaemonIntegration`):
    opt-in via `CARE_TEST_DOCKER=1` env var. Skipped by
    default so CI doesn't need Docker. Round-trips
    `python -c "print('hi')"` end-to-end when the daemon
    is available.

  **What this completes:** the §6.1 P0 blocker — CARE now
  has a production-safe sandbox backend. The
  `CareConfig.sandbox.kind = "docker"` default + the matching
  config defaults (cpu_limit=2.0, mem_limit=1g, pids_limit=256,
  network_policy=skill_declared, image=python:3.12-slim) all
  flow straight into the backend constructor, so a fresh
  CARE install picks Docker out of the box.
- **[DONE]** `E2BSandboxBackend` — uses [e2b.dev](https://e2b.dev)
  cloud microVMs for hosted execution. Useful when the user
  runs CARE on a machine that can't run Docker.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/sandbox/e2b.py` with `E2BSandboxBackend` +
    `DEFAULT_TEMPLATE` / `WORKSPACE_DIR` / `SKILL_DIR`
    constants + `SandboxFactory` callable type, re-exported
    from `care.sandbox`. Implements the same
    :class:`care.sandbox.SandboxBackend` protocol the Local /
    Docker / Firejail backends satisfy, so the runtime
    executor swaps it in via
    `CareConfig.sandbox.kind = "e2b"`.
  - **Lifecycle:**
    - `prepare(skill, workspace=None)` provisions a microVM
      via `Sandbox(template=..., api_key=..., timeout=...,
      metadata=...)` and **stages every file under
      `skill.path`** into `/home/user/skill/` via repeated
      `sandbox.files.write(...)` calls. The host `workspace`
      argument is accepted for protocol parity but ignored —
      e2b sandboxes are remote, so the host workspace
      doesn't exist inside the VM.
    - `run()` shell-joins the argv via `shlex.join` and
      dispatches to `sandbox.commands.run(cmd, envs=...,
      cwd=/home/user/workspace, timeout=...)`. e2b's API
      takes a string, not argv; the shell-join keeps multi-
      word args quoted correctly.
    - `read_file` / `write_file` route through
      `sandbox.files.read` / `sandbox.files.write` against
      the workspace dir.
    - `cleanup()` calls `sandbox.kill()` to release the
      microVM (e2b bills per second of uptime, so cleanup
      matters). Idempotent + tolerant of already-killed
      sandboxes.
  - **Lazy SDK import.** No top-level `from e2b import ...`.
    `_make_sandbox` lazy-imports on first call and raises
    `SandboxError("e2b SDK is not installed; install with
    \"pip install \\\"care[e2b]\\\"\"")` when the optional
    dep is missing. Exercised for real in this dev env
    (e2b isn't installed; the missing-dep test passes).
  - **`sandbox_factory` constructor kwarg for testability**
    — callable returning a Sandbox-like duck-typed object.
    Tests pass a `_FactorySpy` + `_StubSandbox` chain
    (`commands`, `files`, `kill` all recorded) so the suite
    runs hermetically — no e2b account, no network, no API
    key.
  - **Metadata stamping.** Every microVM gets
    `{"care.sandbox": "true", "care.sandbox.skill_sha256":
    "<sha>"}` labels merged in so e2b dashboards filter
    CARE's workloads cleanly. Caller-supplied
    `metadata={...}` flows through alongside.
  - **Network policy mapping** documents the current
    upstream limitation: e2b microVMs have full internet by
    default and don't expose granular egress controls yet.
    - `"open"` → run executes normally;
      `RunResult.network_enforced=False`.
    - `"none"` / `"skill_declared"` → raises
      `SandboxError("E2BSandboxBackend doesn't support
      network='none' yet — pass network='open' or use a
      different backend")`. Better to fail loud than
      silently leak the host network when the user asked
      for isolation.
  - **Per-run `cpu` / `mem` / `stdin` kwargs accepted but
    ignored.** e2b enforces resource limits at the template
    level (not per-command), and `commands.run` doesn't
    pipe stdin. Both are documented in the docstrings +
    marked `noqa: ARG002`.
  - **Timeout handling.** Forwards `timeout` to
    `commands.run` verbatim. When the SDK raises
    `TimeoutError` (or the e2b-specific timeout subclass),
    the backend wraps it in `SandboxTimeoutError` with a
    partial `RunResult.timed_out=True` attached so callers
    can still log the duration / partial output.
  - **Stdout/stderr coercion.** e2b returns commands output
    as `str` (not `bytes`); `_coerce_bytes` normalises both
    sides to `bytes` so `RunResult` stays consistent across
    every backend.
  - **Path-traversal guard** custom to remote storage. e2b
    paths are remote strings, so we can't `Path.resolve`
    against the host. `_resolve_sandbox_path` rejects
    absolute paths up front, splits on `/`, drops `.`
    components, and refuses any `..` component before
    prepending the workspace dir.

  **Tests (`tests/test_sandbox_e2b.py`, 27 passed + 1
  opt-in real-cloud skip):**
  - **Construction (3 cases):** defaults
    (`name="e2b"`, `unsafe=False`, template=`"base"`);
    template override; missing-SDK friendly error
    (exercised for real because e2b isn't installed).
  - **`prepare()` (4 cases):** factory called with the
    documented kwargs (template, api_key, timeout,
    merged metadata including the CARE labels);
    factory failure wraps with `failed to provision e2b
    sandbox`; missing skill path raises; multi-file
    SKILL staging writes EVERY file to its
    `SKILL_DIR/<rel>` path (regression guard so a future
    SKILL with `scripts/` + `data/` subdirs still
    uploads correctly); staging failure (write raises)
    wraps as `failed to stage`.
  - **`run()` (9 cases):** dispatches to `commands.run`
    with shell-joined cmd + envs + cwd; str output
    becomes bytes; exit code propagates; empty cmd
    raises; `network="none"` raises with the documented
    fail-loud message; `network="skill_declared"`
    raises; `TimeoutError` becomes `SandboxTimeoutError`
    with the partial result; generic exception wraps as
    `SandboxError("sandbox.commands.run failed")`;
    running after cleanup raises clearly.
  - **File IO (7 cases):** write then read round-trips
    through the stub's storage dict; missing file raises;
    absolute path blocked with a dedicated "absolute
    path not allowed" message; read traversal blocked;
    write traversal blocked; empty path rejected;
    write error wraps.
  - **Cleanup (3 cases):** stops + kills sandbox;
    idempotent (second call is a no-op); tolerates
    `kill()` raising (sandbox may already be gone).
  - **Real-cloud integration:** `CARE_TEST_E2B=1` +
    `E2B_API_KEY` opt-in test runs `echo hi` against a
    real microVM. Skipped by default so CI doesn't need
    cloud credentials.

  **What this completes:** the §6.1 sandbox lineup is now
  four backends — `local` (unsafe), `docker` (multi-platform
  container isolation), `firejail` (lightweight Linux),
  `e2b` (cloud microVM for daemon-free hosts).
  `CareConfig.sandbox.kind = Literal["local", "docker",
  "e2b", "firejail"]` covers all four cleanly — runtime
  executor selects the backend by name without further
  wiring.
- **[DONE]** `FirejailSandboxBackend` — lightweight Linux-only
  option using firejail / bwrap for users who want a sandbox
  without Docker overhead.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/sandbox/firejail.py` with `FirejailSandboxBackend` +
    `DEFAULT_EXECUTABLE` + `SubprocessRunner` Protocol, re-
    exported from `care.sandbox`. Implements the same
    `SandboxBackend` protocol the Local + Docker backends
    satisfy, so the runtime executor swaps it in by config
    (`CareConfig.sandbox.kind = "firejail"`).
  - **Two helper executables supported:**
    - `executable="firejail"` (default) — builds an argv with
      `--quiet --noprofile --private --chdir=<ws>
      --whitelist=<ws> --read-only=<skill_path>
      [--net=none|<omitted>] [--rlimit-cpu=N]
      [--rlimit-as=BYTES] -- <cmd...>`.
    - `executable="bwrap"` — fallback for distros where
      firejail isn't packaged (recent Fedora). Builds
      `--unshare-net --ro-bind <skill> <skill>
      --bind <ws> <ws> --chdir <ws> --proc /proc --dev /dev
      -- <cmd...>`. (cpu/mem rlimit flags noop on bwrap;
      documented limitation.)
    - Anything else raises `SandboxError("unsupported sandbox
      executable")` so users get a clear "use one of the two
      supported wrappers" error instead of a confusing
      argv-syntax failure later.
  - **Linux-only with an opt-out for tests.** Constructor
    raises `SandboxError("FirejailSandboxBackend is Linux-only;
    current platform is 'darwin'. Use DockerSandboxBackend on
    macOS / Windows.")` on non-Linux hosts. Tests that only
    exercise argv construction pass `require_linux=False`
    so the full suite runs on every CARE dev box, not just
    Linux CI.
  - **`subprocess_runner` injection** — same testability
    pattern `DockerSandboxBackend.client_factory` uses. The
    default `_default_runner` wraps
    `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec` (kill + drain on
    timeout); tests pass a `_RunnerSpy` that records argv +
    cwd + env + stdin + timeout for every call.
  - **Network policy mapping:**
    - `"none"` → `--net=none` (firejail) / `--unshare-net` (bwrap).
    - `"skill_declared"` → falls back to `--net=none` /
      `--unshare-net` until Platform §4.5c egress proxying
      lands.
    - `"open"` → no flag emitted (inherits host network).
      Flips `RunResult.network_enforced=False` so the audit
      log records "the host network reached this skill".
  - **Resource defaults flow through:**
    - Construction-time `default_cpu` / `default_mem` apply
      when the caller's `run()` omits them.
    - Per-run `cpu` / `mem` override the default.
    - `cpu` → `--rlimit-cpu=<seconds>` on firejail.
    - `mem` → `--rlimit-as=<bytes>` after parsing the
      Docker-style suffix (`"512m"`, `"1g"`, `"2048k"`).
      Unparseable values are silently dropped — the worst
      case is no rlimit, not a failed run.
    - On bwrap both are noops; documented in the docstring.
  - **Lifecycle:** `prepare()` validates the executable via
    `shutil.which()` (only when using the default runner so
    stub-driven tests aren't blocked by firejail's absence)
    and creates-or-adopts the workspace. `run()` builds the
    argv + dispatches to the runner. `cleanup()` removes
    the workspace if `prepare()` created it; user-supplied
    workspaces are left intact. All three are idempotent
    and async.
  - **File IO** routes through the host-side workspace
    directly (firejail's `--whitelist` already bidirectional
    the mount). Same path-traversal guard as the other
    backends — `_resolve_inside` rejects `../` escapes and
    empty paths with `SandboxError`.
  - **Env hygiene:** minimal `PATH` / `HOME` / `LANG`
    defaults; caller env layered on top so secrets stay
    opt-in.

  **Tests (`tests/test_sandbox_firejail.py`, 34 passed + 1
  opt-in real-binary skip):**
  - **Construction (6 cases):** default executable; bwrap;
    absolute path; unsupported executable raises;
    `require_linux=True` blocks darwin;
    `require_linux=False` allows it (cross-platform unit
    tests).
  - **`prepare()` (5 cases):** creates tempdir when no
    workspace; adopts existing workspace; file-as-workspace
    raises "not a directory"; nonexistent workspace raises
    "workspace does not exist"; missing skill path raises.
  - **Firejail argv (7 cases):** default flag layout
    pinned (header / `--private` / `--chdir=` /
    `--whitelist=` / `--read-only=` / `--net=none` / `--`
    separator); `network=open` omits all `--net=*`;
    `network=skill_declared` falls back to `--net=none`;
    `cpu=8` → `--rlimit-cpu=8`; `mem=512m` →
    `--rlimit-as=536870912`; construction defaults flow
    through when run omits cpu/mem; run-time cpu overrides
    default; unparseable mem (`"1xb"`) silently dropped
    (no `--rlimit-as=`).
  - **Bwrap argv (2 cases):** uses `--unshare-net` +
    `--ro-bind` + `--bind` + `--chdir` + `--`;
    `network=open` omits `--unshare-net`.
  - **Run result (7 cases):** runner output propagates;
    non-zero exit propagates; empty cmd raises; timeout
    raises `SandboxTimeoutError` with partial result;
    `network=open` flips `network_enforced=False`; env
    overrides layered on top of defaults; stdin passed
    through to runner.
  - **File IO (4 cases):** write-then-read; missing file
    raises; read traversal blocked; write traversal blocked.
  - **Cleanup (2 cases):** idempotent (second call no-op);
    skips adopted workspace (user-supplied path stays).
  - **Real-binary integration:** `CARE_TEST_FIREJAIL=1`
    opt-in for Linux hosts with firejail installed —
    round-trips `python3 -c "print('hi')"` end-to-end.

  **What this completes:** the third + final sandbox
  backend on the §6.1 list. Users now have three production
  paths — `local` (unsafe, dev-only), `docker` (full
  isolation, multi-platform), `firejail` (lightweight Linux
  isolation). `CareConfig.sandbox.kind` already lists
  `"firejail"` in its Literal — runtime executor selects
  the backend by name without further wiring.

### 6.2 Wiring CARL to the sandbox

- **[DONE]** Patch CARL so `AgentSkillStepConfig.runtime` is **actually
  respected** — see CARL gap noted in research (today only `"local"` is
  wired). Either (a) push the fix upstream into carl-experiments (preferred,
  cross-cuts the whole ecosystem), or (b) implement a CARE-level
  `SandboxedAgentSkillExecutor` that replaces CARL's default executor via
  `register_executor(StepType.AGENT_SKILL, ...)`.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: route (a) already landed upstream per PREPARE.md §5.1
  (CARL ships `SkillRuntime` Protocol + Local/Docker/Firejail/E2B runtimes +
  registry; `AgentSkillStepExecutor` routes every subprocess through
  `self._runtime_run`). The CARE-side piece — the **bridge** between CARE's
  `SandboxBackend` and CARL's `SkillRuntime` — is what this iteration adds.
  `care/runtime/skill_runtime_adapter.py` ships `CareSkillRuntime(_, backend,
  sandbox_config, trust_store=None, strict_trust=False)`that implements
CARL's protocol by delegating to a CARE`SandboxBackend`. Wires together
three already-shipped CARE primitives: (1) the sandbox backend supplies
`prepare`/`run`/`read_file`/`write_file`/`cleanup`; (2) `SandboxConfig`defaults the per-run cpu/mem/network limits +`resolve_network_policy`validates CARL's`runtime_config["network"]`literal + merges the
manifest's`allowed-tools`WebFetch hosts; (3) optional`SkillTrustStore`
gates execution (`TrustRefusedError`when`strict_trust=True`+ SHA not
approved; warn-but-allow until the §6.3 first-run prompt UI ships).
Handle translation: CARL's`SkillRuntimeHandle(workspace_root,
  workspace_in, workspace_out, backend)`stashes the CARE`SandboxHandle`
  - the `_BridgeHandle` (cpu/mem/network for this prepare) under
    `backend["care_handle"]` / `backend["bridge"]`. Conventional `in/` and
    `out/` subdirs are pre-created so CARL skills can write to them.
    Foreign handles (built by another runtime) fail loudly with
    `"missing its bridge"` on the next `run`. CARL imports
    (`SkillRuntimeHandle`, `RuntimeRunResult`, `register_skill_runtime`)
    are **lazy** — module load works without `mmar_carl` installed, only
    `prepare`/`run`/`register_with_carl` touch CARL. Registration helper:
    CARL's registry takes a no-args **class** (calls `cls()` itself), so
    `register_with_carl(runtime, name="local")` stores the configured
    runtime in `_REGISTERED_RUNTIMES` and registers a dynamically-built
    shim class (one per name) whose `__init__` reads from that dict; this
    lets `chains that specify `runtime: "local"`transparently route
through CARE's sandbox layer.`unregister(name)`cleans up the
registry dict (mainly for tests; CARL doesn't expose unregister).
19 tests in`tests/test_skill_runtime_adapter.py`across 6 areas:
construction (3 — name mirrors backend, backend accessor, trust_store
default None); trust gate (4 — strict raises on untrusted, strict
allows when trusted, warn-but-allow when not strict, no trust store
no gate); per-run limits (3 — defaults from CareConfig, overrides
win, unknown network policy raises); end-to-end protocol delegation
(5 — workspace layout includes in+out, run returns CARL-shaped
result, read/write file round trip, cleanup idempotent, foreign
handle rejected); registration (3 — stores runtime + builds named
shim class that forwards, shim raises KeyError after unregister,
unregister returns bool); module hygiene (1 —`\_REGISTERED_RUNTIMES`dict). Tests use`monkeypatch`to swap CARL's`SkillRuntimeHandle`+`RuntimeRunResult`for local dataclasses + a stubbed`mmar_carl`sys.modules entry for registration tests — adapter exercises every
protocol method end-to-end against real subprocesses via`LocalSandboxBackend` without needing CARL installed. Ruff clean.\*
- **[DONE]** Network policy translation: `network_policy="none|skill_declared|open"`.
  In `skill_declared` mode, parse the SKILL.md `allowed-tools` frontmatter for
  `WebFetch(domain:*)` and only whitelist those domains via a Docker
  network alias / squid proxy.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/sandbox/network_policy.py` ships the pure
  translation layer that future Docker/Firejail/E2B backends consume:
  `parse_webfetch_domains(allowed_tools)` extracts hosts from
  `WebFetch(domain:_)`tokens (accepts str / list / None, case-insensitive`webfetch`match, whitespace tolerated, bare`WebFetch`ignored on
purpose — unconstrained network is a`policy=open`decision, not a
manifest-token side-effect);`CARE_TO_CARL_POLICY` table maps CARE's
user-facing names (`none | skill_declared | open`) onto CARL's runtime
literals (`none | allowlist | host`) so backends that delegate to a
`mmar_carl.SkillRuntime`forward the right value;`translate_to_carl_policy`raises`ValueError`on unknown literals;`resolve_network_policy()`returns a frozen`ResolvedNetworkPolicy(policy, carl_policy, domains:
  tuple, enforced: bool)`carrying both names + the merged allowlist (manifest
hosts ∪ operator overrides, sorted+deduped, blanks stripped).`enforced_override`lets LocalSandbox flag`enforced=False`so CARE's
TUI banner can warn. The WebFetch regex is intentionally duplicated
from CARL's upstream`parse_network_allowlist_from_allowed_tools`—
decouples CARE startup from CARL install state; behaviour pinned in
tests so it can't drift. 27 tests in`tests/test_network_policy.py`
  across 4 classes: parsing (10 — None / empty / str / list / multiple
  domains dedup+sort / whitespace / case-insensitive / bare WebFetch
  ignored / mixed tokens / blanks stripped); name translation (3 —
  parametrised 3-way mapping + table-completeness pin + unknown raises);
  resolve (10 — none/open empty, skill_declared from tokens, no-tokens
  empty, override merge, blank stripping, dedup against manifest,
  enforced_override true/false, unknown raises); ResolvedNetworkPolicy
  shape (2 — frozen + tuple). All pure; ruff clean.\*
- **[DONE]** Resource limits read from `CareConfig.sandbox`; per-skill overrides
  via SKILL.md `metadata.resources` block.
  \*Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/sandbox/resources.py` ships pure-function
  parse + merge logic for per-skill resource overrides. SKILL.md
  manifests can declare a `metadata.resources` block with
  `cpu` / `memory` (alias `mem` / `mem_limit`) / `pids` (alias
  `pids_limit`) / `timeout` keys; `parse_resources_block(raw)` validates
  - normalises (memory case-folded to lowercase, Docker suffix
    `k|m|g` enforced, all numerics positive). Unknown keys are
    ignored on purpose — forward-compat so a future schema bump
    doesn't break old CARE installs. Non-dict input or any malformed
    value raises `ResourceOverrideError` loudly.
    `resolve_resources(*, defaults, manifest_resources, policy)`
    merges with `SandboxConfig` defaults; accepts either raw or
    pre-parsed dicts (detects canonical-key set and skips
    revalidation). Returns frozen
    `ResolvedResources(cpu_limit, mem_limit, pids_limit, timeout, source)`
    with `source` tagged `"config"` / `"manifest"` / `"mixed"` so the
    audit log + TUI banner can render where limits came from.
    **Policy gate**: default `ResourcePolicy()` blocks manifest
    requests that exceed operator ceilings — a skill can't silently
    ask for 16g when the operator capped at 1g; raises
    `ResourceOverrideError("exceeds operator ceiling")`. Operators
    who trust the skill set flip
    `ResourcePolicy(allow_manifest_upscale=True)` for batch jobs
    that legitimately need more headroom. Memory ceiling check
    works in bytes via `_memory_to_bytes` so `"16g"` vs `"1g"` is
    compared numerically. `apply_to_sandbox_config(defaults, resolved)`
    produces a non-mutating copy of `SandboxConfig` with the new
    cpu/mem/pids applied (timeout intentionally excluded — it's
    per-run, not per-config). 34 tests in
    `tests/test_sandbox_resources.py` across 5 areas: parsing (12 —
    None / empty / canonical keys / memory + pids aliases / unknown
    keys ignored / non-dict / cpu+memory+pids malformed values
    parametrised); defaults (2 — no manifest + empty manifest both
    yield `source="config"`); overrides (4 — partial → mixed, full →
    manifest, pre-parsed accepted, raw accepted); policy gates (5 —
    over-ceiling cpu/memory/pids all blocked, opt-in upscale lets
    them through, lowering stays allowed); apply_to_sandbox_config
    (2 — fields applied + non-resource fields preserved, timeout
    not stored); ResolvedResources shape (2 — frozen + default
    source). All pure; ruff clean. Wiring into `CareSkillRuntime`
    is a follow-up — exposing this layer separately lets the adapter
    call `resolve_resources` once per `prepare()` without
    re-validating shapes on every `run()`.\*
- **[DONE]** Audit log — every sandbox `run()` call writes to
  `~/.local/state/care/sandbox.log` (skill id, cmd, exit code, stdout/err
  hashes, duration, files written to `out/`).
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/sandbox/audit.py` ships
  `SandboxAuditLogger(path=DEFAULT_AUDIT_PATH, _, clock=None)`—
append-only JSON-lines writer for sandbox`run()`calls. Each entry
is a frozen`SandboxAuditEntry(timestamp, backend*name,
  skill_sha256, cmd, exit_code, duration_seconds, timed_out,
  stdout_sha256, stderr_sha256, network_enforced, files_written,
  extras)`; round-trips losslessly through `to_dict`/`from_dict`.
Schema-versioned (`AUDIT_FORMAT_VERSION = 1`) so an old reader
refuses to misinterpret new fields. `log_run(handle, cmd, result, *,
  extras=None)`auto-discovers files under`handle.workspace/out/`(sorted, deterministic; symlinks reported as-is — a skill that
wrote a symlink pointing outside`out/`is exactly the kind of
thing the audit log should record verbatim), hashes stdout/stderr
via SHA-256, and appends one JSON line. Build-only variant`build*entry(...)`is exposed so callers can pipe to alternate
sinks (Langfuse, test buffers) without reinventing the field set.
**Best-effort writes**: if the append raises`OSError`(disk full,
permission denied, path-is-a-directory) the method prints to
stderr and returns`False`rather than raising — the audit log
must never fail an otherwise-successful skill run. Parent dirs
are auto-created on first write. Read path`tail(n=50)`/`all_entries()`parse every line into typed entries; unknown
schema version or malformed JSON raises`SandboxAuditError`(loud,
silently dropping corrupt entries hides real problems). 15 tests
in`tests/test_sandbox_audit.py`across 6 areas:`SandboxAuditEntry`round-trip (3 — to_dict/from_dict, frozen, unknown-version
rejection);`build_entry`pure helper (3 — every field populated +
hashes deterministic, no-out-dir → empty files_written, extras
passthrough);`log_run`write path (3 — parent dir auto-created +
valid JSON line, appends not overwrites, path-as-directory returns
False + stderr message instead of raising); read path (5 — missing
log returns empty, tail returns last N, zero/negative n returns
empty, all_entries parses every line, corrupt line raises); real
end-to-end (1 — actual`echo`through`LocalSandboxBackend`, audit
entry written + tailed back with matching cmd/exit/duration/
files_written). All real file IO via `tmp_path`; ruff clean.*
- **[DONE]** Output mediation — when a skill writes to `workspace/out/`, scan
  for suspicious content (executables, scripts pointing to network
  endpoints) before merging back to host.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/sandbox/output_mediation.py` ships
  `scan_output_dir(workspace, _, out_subdir="out", max_file_bytes=5MiB) →
  MediationReport`. Pure file-IO scanner with no upstream deps. Three-
level severity ladder: `info`(notable but expected — empty`out/`,
small text), `warning`(surface to user before merge — shebang
scripts, network tokens, oversize files),`blocked`(refuse merge
by default — raw executables, workspace-escape symlinks). Frozen`OutputFinding(severity, kind, path, detail, bytes_inspected)`and
frozen`MediationReport(findings, total_files, scanned_bytes)`with`is_clean`/`has_blockers`/`findings_by_severity`aggregators.
Heuristics:
(1) **Executable bit**: any file mode with`S_IXUSR|GRP|OTH`set →`blocked` (`kind="executable_bit"`). Skills that want to ship a
helper script can drop the bit and ask CARE for explicit chmod
later.
(2) **Binary magic bytes**: first-N bytes matched against ELF
(`\x7fELF`), Windows PE (`MZ`), and four Mach-O variants (fat +
32/64-bit × little/big-endian) → `blocked` (`kind="binary_content"`,
detail names the format).
(3) **Shebang scripts**: file starts with `#!`→`warning`
(`kind="shebang_script"`, detail includes the shebang line capped
at 200 chars). Could be legitimate; user decides.
(4) **Network tokens**: text files containing `curl`/`wget`/`nc`/`netcat`/`socat`/`ssh`/`telnet`or`https?://`/`ftp://`/`s3://`/`file:///etc/`→`warning` (`kind="network_token"`,
detail lists up to 5 unique matches). Only runs on files that
pass a `\_looks_textual`heuristic (≥70% printable bytes in first

512. so a binary blob with coincidental "wget" bytes doesn't
     false-positive.
     (5) **Symlink escape**: any symlink whose resolved target sits
     outside the workspace →`blocked` (`kind="symlink_escape"`). Tests
     skip cleanly on platforms without symlink support.
     (6) **Large files**: anything above `max_file_bytes`→`warning`
     (`kind="large_file"`) AND scanned within the cap, so a 20 MiB
     malicious binary still gets caught by the magic-byte check at
     offset 0.
     (7) **Empty / missing `out/`**: `info`so the UI distinguishes
     "no output" from "output looks suspicious".`DEFAULT_MAX_FILE_BYTES = 5 MiB`exported for tests. Module pins
     the`Severity`and`FindingKind`Literal types so the future
     ExecutionScreen can switch on them safely. 31 tests in`tests/test_output_mediation.py` across 10 areas: empty/missing
     (3 — missing dir info, out-as-file warning, empty dir info);
     executable bit (2); binary magic parametrised across ELF/PE/Mach-O

- arbitrary-bytes false-positive guard (4); shebang (2);
  network tokens parametrised across 4 token shapes + no-token
  no-finding + binary skip (6); symlink escape (2 — skip-on-no-symlink
  platforms via `pytest.skip`); large-file scanning with magic-byte
  detection within cap + default constant pin (2); MediationReport
  aggregation incl. frozen + filter (5); OutputFinding shape (2);
  mixed-tree integration (2 — every kind co-present + nested dirs
  walked). All real file IO in `tmp_path`; ruff clean. Wiring into
  the post-run flow is a follow-up — exposing this separately lets
  the future ExecutionScreen + the audit log call `scan_output_dir`
  with different `out_subdir` values.\*

### 6.3 Skill trust UI

- **[DONE]** First-run prompt for every new skill URI: show the SHA256 of
  `SKILL.md`, the manifest, the `allowed-tools` whitelist; ask the user to
  approve once; cache approval in `~/.local/state/care/trusted_skills.json`.
  Pin the SHA on approval (`trust_policy="sha_pinned"`).
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: this iteration covers the **store + decision API**
  (the UI prompt is a thin shell that calls into this). `care/sandbox/trust.py`
  ships `SkillTrustStore` plus the frozen `TrustRecord` dataclass and
  `TrustPolicy = Literal["sha_pinned"]` (Literal stays open for future
  policies without breaking callers). Storage: JSON at
  `~/.local/state/care/trusted_skills.json` (`DEFAULT_TRUST_PATH` exposed
  for tests/overrides), schema-versioned (`STORE_FORMAT_VERSION = 1`) so a
  future shape change can refuse old files instead of silently dropping
  fields. `load(path)`: missing file → empty store (first-run case);
  corrupt JSON / unknown version / corrupt per-record entry → loud
  `SkillTrustStoreError` (silently dropping bad rows would lower CARE's
  security posture). `trust(_, sha256, uri, name, allowed_tools, approved_at,
  trust_policy)`: rejects empty SHA / URI, refreshes existing records on
re-approval (user re-confirmed → re-anchor `approved_at`+`allowed_tools`). `revoke()`idempotent, returns whether anything
removed;`clear()`early-returns on empty so it doesn't accidentally
touch disk.`list_trusted()`sorts newest-first for the future
SettingsScreen panel.`is_trusted("")`returns`False`(empty-SHA
guard);`**contains**`non-string safe. Persistence uses atomic write
(tempfile in same dir +`os.replace`) so a crash mid-save can't corrupt
the store; tempfile cleaned up on failure. 24 tests in
`tests/test_sandbox_trust.py`across 8 areas: TrustRecord round-trip
(3 — to_dict/from_dict, legacy records without trust_policy, frozen
semantics); constants (2 — XDG path + version pin); load (5 — missing
file empty, populated, corrupt JSON, unknown version, corrupt record);
query (3 — empty store, empty SHA,`**contains**`operator);
trust+revoke (7 — persists + reloads, rejects empty sha/uri, refresh
on re-trust, revoke + persist, revoke unknown no-op, clear, clear-empty
no-op); listing (1 — newest-first sort); persistence (3 — parent dir
auto-created, valid JSON on disk, no leftover tempfiles). All use
real file IO via`tmp_path`; ruff clean.\*

## 7. Evolution: GigaEvo Platform (P1–P2)

- **[DONE]** `care/platform.py` — wraps the gigaevo-platform HTTP API. Today
  the platform has no chain-population endpoint (see Platform TODO §1); CARE
  pushes that requirement and consumes the new endpoint when it lands.
  _Shipped 2026-05-19: `care/platform.py` wraps `gigaevo_client.PlatformClient`
  (shipped upstream per PREPARE.md §2.6 — `create_evolution`, `get_evolution`,
  `list_individuals`, `accept_individual`, `stream_events` all available)
  with the narrow `CarePlatform` facade — sibling to `CareMemory`. Centralises
  CARE-specific concerns: (1) stamps `CARE_SOURCE_TAG = "source:care"` on
  every spec so Platform-side ops can tell CARE-driven runs apart from other
  consumers; (2) builds a typed `EvolutionRef(evolution_id, base_chain_id,
status, extras)` per submit so the EvolutionScreen state model doesn't
  drift over field names — handles the Platform shipping either
  `evolution_id` or `id` on create-responses by falling back gracefully;
  (3) preserves the full create-response on `ref.extras` so callers can
  inspect `queue_position` / `estimated_start` / future fields without
  another round-trip. Construction via `CarePlatform.from_config(care_config)`
  reads `platform.base_url` / `api_key` / `timeout` and builds a
  `GigaEvoConfig` for the SDK. `start_evolution(_, base_chain_id,
  evolution_mode, max_iterations, population_size, validation_criteria,
  test_data_path, tags, objectives, extras)`mirrors the EvolutionScreen
form fields (TODO §7 step 2) — extras dict passes through for forward-
compat.`get_evolution`/`list_individuals`/`accept_individual`/`stream_events`/`health_check`are thin passthroughs returning the
SDK's parsed JSON verbatim.`client`property exposes the raw SDK as an
escape hatch. 13 tests in`tests/test_platform.py`across 7 areas:
from_config (1 — pulls Platform URL/key/timeout from env-overridden
CareConfig); start_evolution (5 — minimal spec with auto tag, full spec
pass-through, source tag not duplicated, id-vs-evolution_id fallback,
response preserved on extras); get_evolution (1); list_individuals (1);
accept_individual (1 — body shape); stream_events (1 — SSE parsed dicts);
health_check (1); EvolutionRef shape (2 — frozen + defaults). All against`respx`-mocked Platform; ruff clean. CARE can drive the EvolutionScreen
flow end-to-end as soon as Platform's evolution endpoints ship (PREPARE.md
§4.1–§4.4 marked shipped in `who-cares` workdir; this facade works
  against them transparently).\*
- **[DONE]** `EvolutionScreen` flow: pick a chain, configure
  the run, submit, watch the fitness curve, accept the winner.
  Data layer + Textual screen integration shipped.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.EvolutionConfig` frozen dataclass mirroring the
    step-2 form. Fields: `evolution_mode` (Literal
    ``"full_chain" | "per_step"``), `max_iterations`,
    `population_size`, `validation_criteria`,
    `test_data_path` (Path | None), `validation_threshold`
    (float | None), `objectives` (tuple — multi-objective
    hint for §7 P2 work). Defaults match what the screen
    would pre-fill: `full_chain`, 5 iterations, 8
    individuals, empty criteria.
  - `care.EvolutionPlan` frozen dataclass bundling
    `config` + `base_chain_entity_id` + optional
    `base_chain_content` (for diff rendering) +
    `base_chain_name`. Lets the screen pass one value
    into `build_evolution_request` instead of juggling
    separate args.
  - `care.build_evolution_request(plan) -> dict`:
    projects a plan into the
    ``POST /api/v1/evolutions`` body. Maps user-facing
    field names to the server's expected shape
    (`seed_chain_id`, `evolution_mode`, `max_iterations`,
    `population_size`, `validation_criteria`,
    `test_data_path` as a string, `validation_threshold`,
    `objectives`). Optional fields omitted when unset so
    Platform's own defaults apply. Validation up front
    raises `EvolutionPlanError` for empty seed chain id,
    `max_iterations<1`, `population_size<2` — fails before
    the SDK round-trip wastes work.
  - `care.EvolutionProgressTracker` mutable aggregator
    feeding the Rich fitness-curve plot. Subscribes to
    Platform SSE events via `record_event(event_dict)`
    and dispatches on `event_type`:
    - `"generation_started"` → registers a `-inf`
      placeholder so the curve includes generations with
      no winners yet.
    - `"individual_evaluated"` → bumps the generation's
      `individuals_evaluated` count + tracks the running
      best (max-by-fitness).
    - `"best_updated"` → pins `best_fitness` +
      `best_individual_id`.
    - Unknown event types are silently ignored —
      Platform may add new types and CARE shouldn't
      crash on them.
  - `GenerationStat` frozen record per generation:
    `generation`, `best_fitness`, `mean_fitness`,
    `individuals_evaluated`, `best_individual_id`. The
    Rich plot reads `tracker.fitness_curve()` (sorted by
    generation) for `(x, y)` pairs.
  - **Aggregator merging semantics:** when the same
    generation arrives multiple times (a late
    `best_updated` after several
    `individual_evaluated`s), `record_generation` keeps
    the max `best_fitness`, refreshes
    `best_individual_id` only when the new score beats
    the existing one, takes the max
    `individuals_evaluated`, and overwrites
    `mean_fitness` only when the incoming event
    supplies it. Means the screen can replay events in
    any order without losing data.
  - `tracker.latest` — most-recent generation by
    number (not arrival order). `tracker.best_overall`
    — highest-fitness record across all generations,
    skipping the `-inf` placeholders from
    generation_started events.
  - `care.evolution_diff(base_chain, evolved_chain, *,
    base_label, evolved_label) -> tuple[str, ...]`
    renders a unified diff between the seed and the
    best-individual chain content. Mirrors the
    `ConflictReport` diff (§3 P1): `json.dumps(...,
    indent=2, sort_keys=True)` on both sides so
