    semantically-equal dicts produce no diff regardless
    of key order. Empty/None inputs yield an empty
    tuple — the screen can show "no diff available"
    without a special branch.
  - **Duck-typed Platform integration.** The Platform
    SDK shape (`PlatformClient.create_evolution(body)`,
    `stream_events(evolution_id)`,
    `accept_individual(id, individual_id)`) is what the
    builder + tracker target, but no `gigaevo_client`
    import is needed at this layer. Tests drive the
    helpers directly with synthetic events.

  **Tests (`tests/test_evolution_session.py`, 28 cases):**
  - **EvolutionConfig (3):** defaults pinned; frozen;
    per-step mode literal accepted.
  - **build_evolution_request (6):** minimal body when
    defaults only; full config serialises every
    documented field; empty/whitespace
    `validation_criteria` omitted; missing seed chain
    id raises; `max_iterations=0` raises;
    `population_size=1` raises.
  - **EvolutionProgressTracker (12):** empty tracker
    predicates; record_generation insertion + merge
    (max best_fitness wins); per-event-type dispatch
    (`individual_evaluated` / `best_updated` /
    `generation_started`); `-inf` placeholder skipped in
    `best_overall`; fitness_curve sorted by generation;
    individuals_evaluated counter; unknown event types
    ignored; missing-generation event uses default 0;
    unparseable fitness coerces to 0; `latest` returns
    highest-generation record regardless of arrival
    order.
  - **evolution_diff (6):** identical chains → empty
    diff; different chains produce labelled unified
    diff; custom labels forward; None inputs (either
    side) yield empty tuple; empty dict inputs yield
    empty tuple; key-order independent.

  **UI integration shipped 2026-05-20:** the existing
  `care/screens/evolution.py::EvolutionScreen` (P0.24) now
  consumes the canonical data-layer surface end-to-end:

  - **`EvolutionConfig` + `EvolutionPlan` built up-front.** The
    constructor accepts the full form-field set
    (`evolution_mode`, `max_iterations`, `population_size`,
    `validation_criteria`, `test_data_path`,
    `validation_threshold`, `objectives`) plus
    `base_chain_content` + `base_chain_name` for the diff hook,
    folds them into a frozen `EvolutionConfig` (`self.config`)
    and a frozen `EvolutionPlan` (`self.plan`) so the screen
    holds the canonical typed shape rather than a raw `_spec`
    dict.
  - **`build_evolution_request(plan)` drives the submit body.**
    `_submit_and_stream` now projects the plan via the
    builder, swaps `seed_chain_id` → `base_chain_id` (the
    facade's kwarg name), and forwards the rest to
    `CarePlatform.start_evolution(**spec)`. Validation
    (empty seed id, `max_iterations<1`, `population_size<2`)
    runs in the builder, so the screen surfaces a typed
    `EvolutionPlanError` on `run.last_error` instead of a
    Platform 422 round-trip after the fact.
  - **`EvolutionProgressTracker` aggregates the SSE stream.**
    The screen owns a `self.tracker = EvolutionProgressTracker()`.
    `_handle_event` now calls `tracker.record_event(...)` for
    every SSE payload, flattening the wire shape
    `{"event": "...", "data": {...}}` into the
    `{"event_type": kind, **payload}` dict the data layer
    reads. Best-fitness / mean-fitness / individuals-evaluated
    merge semantics + `-inf` placeholder filtering are owned
    by the tracker.
  - **Fitness-curve text strip rendered into the status pane.**
    `format_fitness_curve(width=6)` formats the tail of
    `tracker.fitness_curve()` as
    `gen 0: 0.420   gen 1: 0.553   ...`, skipping the `-inf`
    placeholder records `generation_started` emits before any
    winners. `refresh_status` mounts this below the run summary
    so the user sees live progress without a Rich plot widget
    (the textual line is enough for the M2 UX; a richer plot
    widget is a §1 P3 follow-up).
  - **`evolved_diff_lines(evolved_content)` public helper.**
    Wraps `care.evolution_diff(...)` with sensible labels
    derived from `plan.base_chain_name` so the future
    "show diff" pane (gated on the inspection-fetch flow that
    pulls the winner chain's content) plugs straight in.
    Returns an empty tuple when either side is missing —
    callers render "no diff available" without a special branch.

  **New tests (`TestDataLayerIntegration`, 8 cases added to
  `tests/test_screen_evolution.py`, total 20):**
  - `config` + `plan` built from constructor kwargs (every
    documented field).
  - `_submit_and_stream` calls the platform with the
    builder's body (with `seed_chain_id` → `base_chain_id`
    swap, `objectives` list passed through,
    `validation_criteria` forwarded).
  - SSE events feed the tracker (`generation_started` +
    `individual_evaluated` + `best_updated` across two
    generations); `tracker.best_overall` returns the
    highest-fitness record.
  - `format_fitness_curve` skips `-inf` placeholder
    generations (no winners) so the strip stays informative.
  - `format_fitness_curve` returns the empty string when the
    tracker hasn't seen any events.
  - `evolved_diff_lines` returns labelled unified-diff lines
    when both base + evolved are present.
  - `evolved_diff_lines` returns an empty tuple when no
    base_chain_content was supplied (gated on optional kwarg).
  - `evolved_diff_lines` returns an empty tuple for identical
    chains (semantically equal, no diff).

  **Steps 1 + 5 (chain pick + accept-winner) already covered**
  by the existing `CarePlatform.start_evolution(...)` /
  `accept_individual(...)` facade methods + InspectionScreen's
  "Evolve" CTA path. Steps 2–4 (form, submit, fitness curve)
  are fully wired through the data layer + screen now.
- **[DONE]** Local micro-evolution fallback — if Platform is
  unreachable, run a tiny single-machine GA over chains using
  CARL's own executor as fitness evaluator. Useful for demos.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.MicroEvolution` driver + frozen value objects in
    `care/micro_evolution.py`, re-exported from the `care`
    top-level. The fallback the TODO calls out — a small
    sequential GA that runs in-process when GigaEvo Platform
    isn't reachable.
  - **Algorithm: tournament selection + elitism + caller-
    supplied mutator + caller-supplied evaluator.** Each
    generation: elites carry over verbatim (their cached
    scores are not re-evaluated); the rest are filled by
    mutating winners of random tournaments. Simple enough to
    debug step-by-step, expressive enough for the four-quarter
    demo loop.
  - **Sequential by design.** The Platform is the production
    evolution path; this fallback runs each evaluation in-line
    so the loop stays trivially debuggable. No threads, no
    asyncio.
  - **Frozen value objects:**
    - `Individual(chain, score, breakdown, generation)` —
      one member of the population. `breakdown` preserves the
      raw per-objective scores when the evaluator returned a
      dict.
    - `MicroEvolutionResult(best, history, population,
      evaluations)` — what `run()` returned. `history` has one
      entry per generation (the best at that gen), so callers
      can plot fitness curves.
  - **Config knobs** (`MicroEvolutionConfig`):
    `population_size` (default 5), `generations` (default 4),
    `elitism` (default 1), `tournament_size` (default 3),
    `seed` (RNG seed for reproducibility — None uses default
    entropy), `score_reducer` (collapses multi-objective dict
    output to a scalar — default `sum`, override for weighted
    or Pareto-style).
  - **Caller-provided mutator + evaluator** — the library
    doesn't prescribe chain-mutation strategies because CARL
    has eight step types with different semantics. Instead
    CARE ships safe defaults in `builtin_mutators()`:
    - `perturb_step_titles` — tacks a random suffix on one
      step's title (semantically safe, lets evaluators tell
      variants apart).
    - `drop_optional_step` — removes a non-first leaf step
      that nothing depends on (conservative: never produces a
      dangling-dependency chain).
    - `noop_mutator` — placeholder for tests + the GA
      configuration that wants to exercise selection without
      mutation.
    - `compose_mutators(*ms)` — pick one mutator uniformly
      at random per call.
  - **Multi-objective support.** Evaluators returning a dict
    (`{"accuracy": 0.8, "latency": -0.5, "cost": -0.1}`)
    keep the raw breakdown on `Individual.breakdown`; the
    scalar fitness is reduced via `config.score_reducer`
    (default sum). Pass a custom reducer for weighted or
    Pareto behaviour.
  - **Deterministic with a seed.** Same `MicroEvolutionConfig.seed`
    plus same evaluator → identical result. Tests rely on this for
    replay assertions.
  - **Config validation up front.** Invalid
    `population_size` / `generations` / `elitism` (out of
    `[0, population_size]`) / `tournament_size` raises
    `MicroEvolutionError` at construction — before the first
    evaluator call — so misconfiguration fails fast rather
    than after wasting LLM-evaluation budget.
  - **Evaluation budget formula** documented + tested:
    `population_size + (generations - 1) * (population_size -
    elitism)`. Elites are scored once and cached. CI test
    verifies a real run consumes exactly the expected number
    of evaluator calls.
  - **NOT a CARL-runtime integrator.** The bullet mentions
    "using CARL's own executor as fitness evaluator" — the
    interface here is shape-compatible (the evaluator is just
    `Callable[[chain_dict], float | dict[str, float]]`), so
    a caller can wrap `ReasoningChain.execute_async(...)` +
    custom scoring and plug it in. Wiring CARL execution is
    a separate task that depends on the §5 runtime work; this
    module gives that task somewhere to plug in.

  **Tests (`tests/test_micro_evolution.py`, 29 cases):**
  - Config validation: non-dict seed_chain, population_size
    < 1, generations < 1, elitism > population_size,
    negative elitism, tournament_size 0 — every misconfig
    raises with a clear message.
  - Determinism: two independent runs with the same seed +
    same evaluator yield identical best scores AND identical
    per-generation history.
  - Selection + elitism: best score monotonically non-
    decreasing across generations when elitism ≥ 1; total
    evaluator calls match the documented formula
    `population_size + (generations - 1) * (population_size - elitism)`;
    history length equals `generations`; final population is
    sorted descending by score.
  - Mutator drives evolution: noop_mutator + constant
    evaluator → all individuals score identically; real
    mutator + diversity-rewarding evaluator → best score
    beats the seed.
  - Multi-objective: dict evaluator → `Individual.breakdown`
    preserves the raw dict, `score` is the reduced scalar;
    custom `score_reducer` (e.g. `2*accuracy + cost`)
    applies; scalar evaluator keeps `breakdown == {}`.
  - Built-in mutators: `noop_mutator` returns input
    unchanged; `perturb_step_titles` modifies exactly one
    title; empty-steps list is safe; `drop_optional_step`
    removes a leaf step + always preserves the required
    early steps (10-trial random regression); single-step
    chain is left alone; `compose_mutators` picks exactly
    one of its arguments per call; empty `compose_mutators()`
    falls back to noop; `builtin_mutators()` smoke-runs.
  - Result shape: `MicroEvolutionResult` is frozen;
    `result.best == result.population[0]` (population
    sorted descending); `Individual.generation` reflects the
    birth generation (with `elitism=0`, every final-pop
    member is from the last generation); `Individual` is
    frozen.
- **[DONE]** Multi-objective: evolve for {accuracy, latency,
  token cost}; UI shows the Pareto front and lets the user
  pick a point.

  Shipped in two iterations: this bullet captures the data-
  layer half (`compute_pareto_front`, `ObjectiveDirection`,
  `MicroEvolutionResult.pareto_front`); the EvolutionScreen
  UI half landed in the follow-up bullet immediately below
  (`directions=` kwarg, `pareto_front_individuals()`
  projection, `★` badge column on `#evolution-pareto-table`).

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.compute_pareto_front(individuals, *, directions)`
    in `care/micro_evolution.py`, re-exported from the `care`
    top-level. Returns the non-dominated subset of any
    iterable of :class:`Individual`. Insertion order
    preserved on the result tuple (matches how Platform §4.2
    documents its Pareto endpoint).
  - `ObjectiveDirection = Literal["maximize", "minimize"]`
    plus a `directions: dict[str, ObjectiveDirection] | None`
    parameter. Latency/cost/token-spend objectives use
    `"minimize"` while accuracy/coverage use `"maximize"`.
    Missing direction keys default to `"maximize"` — matches
    the scalar :class:`Evaluator` contract ("higher is better").
    `directions=None` treats every objective as maximise so
    callers with aligned objectives don't need to spell out a
    dict.
  - **Domination rule:** `a` dominates `b` when `a` is at
    least as good as `b` on every objective AND strictly
    better on at least one — the textbook Pareto definition.
    Equal individuals both survive (neither strictly
    dominates the other).
  - **Missing-objective convention:** an individual whose
    `breakdown` doesn't include a referenced key is treated
    as the worst possible value for that direction
    (`-inf` for maximise / `+inf` for minimise). Matches
    Platform §4.2's "missing scores as worst" convention so
    CARE's local fallback and the production GA produce
    consistent fronts. An individual with a partial
    breakdown can still survive if it strictly beats every
    other on the keys it does have.
  - **Scalar fallback** when every individual has empty
    `breakdown`: the function falls back to a single-
    objective max-by-`score` comparison (ties all included).
    Lets micro-evolution runs with scalar evaluators still
    return a sensible "front" without callers having to
    branch on the evaluator's shape.
  - `MicroEvolutionResult.pareto_front(directions)` —
    convenience wrapper round-tripping against the standalone
    function. The future `EvolutionScreen` calls this on the
    result it just got back; library callers can keep using
    `compute_pareto_front(population, directions=...)`
    directly.
  - Implementation kept O(n²) intentionally — micro-evolution
    populations are tiny (5–20 individuals), and the
    naive double-loop is far easier to debug than the
    sort-based Kung-Luccio-Preparata algorithm. Document the
    bound so future scaling work knows where to look.

  **Tests (`tests/test_pareto.py`, 16 cases):**
  - **Edge inputs:** empty input → empty tuple; single
    individual → single-element front.
  - **Maximise + maximise (default):** dominated point
    removed; tradeoff set preserved; insertion order
    preserved on the result tuple; classic three-way
    tradeoff with three orthogonal axes.
  - **Mixed directions:** accuracy max + latency min
    correctly identifies the "fast + accurate" tradeoff
    set; all-minimise picks the lowest-cost-and-latency
    point; missing direction keys default to maximise.
  - **Equality:** two identical breakdowns both survive
    (neither strictly dominates the other — regression
    guard against a bug where equal points kill each
    other).
  - **Missing objectives:** worst-case substitution under
    both maximise and minimise; an individual with a
    partial breakdown can still be on the front when it
    strictly wins on the keys it does have.
  - **Scalar fallback:** all-scalar individuals collapse
    to max-by-score (ties included); mixed scalar +
    breakdown forces multi-objective mode, and the
    scalar-only point gets dominated when any objective
    key exists.
  - **`MicroEvolutionResult.pareto_front` helper:** delegates
    correctly to the standalone function (run a real GA,
    compare both call sites byte-for-byte); default
    directions = all maximise.

  **What this gets a CARE user today:** running a
  `MicroEvolution` with a multi-objective evaluator that
  returns `{"accuracy": ..., "latency_ms": ..., "tokens": ...}`,
  the caller can then ask for the tradeoff frontier:

  ```python
  result = MicroEvolution(...).run()
  front = result.pareto_front(directions={
      "accuracy": "maximize",
      "latency_ms": "minimize",
      "tokens": "minimize",
  })
  ```

  Each `Individual` on the front carries its `breakdown`
  dict for the UI to plot. The UI picker (the second half
  of the §7 P2 bullet) is the screen-side work — once
  `EvolutionScreen` lands it consumes this same shape
  without further data-layer work needed.

- **[DONE]** Multi-objective Pareto picker — UI half (closes
  the `[DONE — data half]` parent above).

  **Shipped 2026-05-20:**
  - **`directions` constructor kwarg** on `EvolutionScreen`
    (default `None` = all-maximise). Stored as
    `self.directions: dict[str, str]` and forwarded to
    `compute_pareto_front` per render.
  - **`pareto_front_individuals()`** method on the screen
    projects each `EvolutionIndividual` (SSE-fed row shape)
    into a `care.micro_evolution.Individual`
    (`chain=individual_id`, `score=fitness`,
    `breakdown=dict(objectives)`, `generation=generation`),
    calls the shipped `compute_pareto_front(adapters,
    directions=self.directions or None)`, then maps the
    returned adapters back to the original
    `EvolutionIndividual` rows via an `individual_id` →
    row dict. Returns the original-shape tuple so callers
    render the screen's rows directly — the projection is
    fully internal.
  - **`★` badge column** added as the leading column of
    `#evolution-pareto-table` (titles updated to
    `"★", "ID", "Gen", "Fitness", "Summary"`). The row's
    badge fills with `★` when its individual_id is in the
    computed front, blank otherwise. Recomputed on every
    `_render_pareto_table` call so the badge stays in
    sync as the SSE stream arrives.
  - **Selection wiring already existed:** the screen's
    `on_data_table_row_selected` slots the row key into
    `self.selected_individual`, which
    `action_accept_winner()` already consumes. Picking a
    starred row therefore drives Accept end-to-end without
    new code.
  - **`format_pareto_front()`** one-line summary for tests /
    logs (`"N on front: id1, id2, ..."` or
    `"no non-dominated individuals"` when empty).
  - Scalar fallback: when no individual carries any
    objectives, the data-layer falls through to scalar
    `fitness` comparison (highest wins, ties included). The
    screen exercises this path automatically via the same
    `compute_pareto_front` call.

  **Tests (`tests/test_screen_evolution.py::TestParetoPicker`,
  8 cases):** empty population → empty front + canonical
  placeholder text; scalar fallback picks top-fitness;
  multi-objective front correctly identifies non-dominated
  pair (`accuracy` max + `latency_ms` min); default
  all-maximise directions; render-table marks
  front rows with `★`; `format_pareto_front` summary;
  `directions` kwarg stored on the screen; end-to-end
  winner-from-front → `action_accept_winner` →
  `platform.accept_individual(evolution_id, winner_id)`.

  No new data-layer code needed — every change is in
  `care/screens/evolution.py` consuming the already-shipped
  `compute_pareto_front` surface.

---

## 8. Capability catalog (P1–P2)

- **[DONE]** Data model + discovery for the capability catalog
  (`care/catalog.py`, exported from `care` top-level). The CLI
  subcommand and `CatalogScreen` are downstream surfaces that
  consume `build_catalog(...)`; this iteration ships only the
  data layer that powers both.

  **Shipped:**
  - `CapabilityCatalogEntry` frozen dataclass with `kind`,
    `name`, `source`, `summary`, `tags`, `metadata`. `kind`
    is a `Literal["agent_skill", "mcp_server", "tool",
"memory_card"]` — adding a new kind bumps the Literal and
    every reader gets a type error for the missing branch.
  - `CapabilityCatalog` aggregator with `is_empty`,
    `by_kind(kind)`, `by_tag(tag)` accessors and a separate
    `errors` channel for non-fatal discovery diagnostics
    (a broken SKILL.md / a 503 from Memory shouldn't kill
    the whole catalog).
  - `build_catalog(*, skills_paths, mcp_config_path,
tools_path, memory, memory_card_tag="capability",
memory_top_k=50)` — the single entry-point the CLI/screen
    will both call. Every parameter is optional; passing
    `None` skips that source. Output is deterministically
    sorted (kind → name) so `--json` output is stable across
    runs.
  - Per-source scanners isolated and each returning
    `(entries, errors)` tuples: - `_scan_skill_dir` — walks `*/SKILL.md` files recursively
    (vendor/deep layouts work). Uses a tiny YAML-ish
    `_parse_skill_md` that handles scalars, single/double
    quoted values, and `key:` + indented `- item` lists (covers
    the SKILL.md shapes CARE writes today + the
    `allowed-tools` list anthropics/skills uses). Falls
    back to the directory name when no frontmatter is
    present. - `_scan_mcp_config` — `tomllib.load`s a
    `mcp_servers.toml` and turns each `[servers.<name>]`
    table into an `mcp_server` entry. The constructed
    `source` is `"command args..."` so the CLI can show
    what would be exec'd; full TOML block is preserved in
    `metadata`. Malformed TOML, `servers` not being a
    table, and individual server entries not being tables
    all degrade to entries on `errors` while keeping the
    rest of the file usable. - `_scan_tools_dir` — enumerates `*.py` files without
    importing them (that's `register_tools_from_path`'s
    job at runtime). Skips `_*.py` so `__init__.py` and
    private helpers don't clutter the catalog. Best-effort
    summary picks up a one-line docstring or
    `# Description:` comment in the first 30 lines. - `_fetch_memory_cards` — calls `memory.search(tag,
entity_type="memory_card", top_k=...)` and converts
    hits into `memory_card` entries. Wraps the whole call
    in a broad `except Exception` so an unreachable
    Memory server doesn't fail the catalog; the error
    lands on `CapabilityCatalog.errors`. Non-dict hits
    are skipped defensively.
  - User-supplied paths run through `_expand` (Path +
    `expanduser`) so `~/.agents/skills` works in configs.

  **Tests (`tests/test_catalog.py`, 31 cases):**
  - Frozen-dataclass assertion (`entry.name = ...` raises),
    independent default factories so `metadata={}` isn't
    shared across instances.
  - `is_empty`, `by_kind`, `by_tag` predicates on both empty
    and populated catalogs.
  - Skill discovery: frontmatter with scalars + list +
    quoted values, directory-name fallback when no
    frontmatter, single-quote handling, summary first-line
    truncation, recursive nested-skill walk, file-instead-of-dir
    error path, tilde expansion via $HOME, string-path
    acceptance.
  - MCP discovery: happy path with multiple servers
    (verifies deterministic name sort + composed `source`),
    malformed TOML → error, missing file = silent skip,
    `servers` not a table, individual server entry not a
    table (good entries still land), empty `[servers]`
    table.
  - Tools discovery: skips `__init__.py` / underscore-prefixed
    files / non-`.py` files; picks up docstring AND
    `# Description:` comment summaries; missing dir =
    silent skip; file-instead-of-dir = error; no-docstring
    case yields empty summary + `line_count` metadata.
  - Memory cards: happy path with `_StubMemory.search`
    spy (verifies query / entity_type / top_k); custom
    tag + top_k threading; `search` raising any
    `Exception` lands on `errors`; non-dict hits skipped;
    missing `entity_id` falls back to `memory://`;
    `memory=None` skips the whole source.
  - Combined integration: all four sources together
    produce the right `kind` → `name` ordering; one
    broken source per kind still lets the others
    contribute entries.

- **[DONE]** `care catalog` CLI subcommand + `CatalogScreen`
  TUI surface — both consume the same
  `CapabilityCatalog.entries`/`errors` data layer so the two
  surfaces render identical content.

  - **CLI half** (`care catalog`) shipped alongside the §9 P2
    CLI router (see the `care` CLI shipping note for full
    details).
  - **`CatalogScreen` TUI half shipped 2026-05-20**:
    `care/screens/catalog.py::CatalogScreen` consuming the
    same `build_catalog`/`CapabilityCatalog` surface.
    - **Construction:** accepts a pre-built
      `CapabilityCatalog` (preferred — tests + most hosts) or
      a lazy `catalog_factory` callable that builds one on
      mount. Best-effort: a factory that raises lands an
      empty catalog rather than crashing the screen.
    - **Kind-chip sidebar** (`#catalog-kind-list`): an `all`
      chip plus one chip per `EntryKind` that has at least
      one entry. Empty-kind chips are hidden so the sidebar
      stays lean on partial catalogs. Re-clicking the active
      chip clears the filter (matches the
      `MarketplaceScreen.tag` chip convention).
    - **Results DataTable** (`#catalog-table`): five columns
      (Kind, Name, Source, Tags, Summary). Source truncates
      to 50 chars from the head (`…/path/tail`) — paths
      matter more at the end than the beginning. Summary
      truncates to 60 chars + ellipsis.
    - **Promote action** (`P` binding or the explicit
      "Promote" button) posts a
      `CatalogScreen.PromoteRequested(entry)` message for
      `agent_skill` entries; non-skill entries get a
      friendly warning toast instead of a no-op so the
      user knows why nothing happened. The screen does NOT
      call `promote_skill_to_memory` itself — the host owns
      the confirmation flow (source_uri prompt, target
      namespace selection, etc.) so the screen stays
      pure-presentation.
    - **Warnings panel** (`#catalog-warnings`): collapsible
      footer rendering `CapabilityCatalog.errors` (broken
      SKILL.md / 503 from Memory / etc.). Hidden when
      `errors == ()`; otherwise shows up to 5 entries +
      `… N more` truncation marker.
    - **Status line** (`#catalog-status`): empty-catalog
      placeholder pointing at the CLI's `--skills` /
      `--tools` / `--mcp-config` flags so users know how to
      populate; otherwise `N entr{y|ies} [· filtered to
      #<kind>]`.

  **Tests (`tests/test_screen_catalog.py`, 15 cases):**
  - Compose (1): every pane mounts.
  - Catalog source (3): pre-built catalog renders entries
    + populates DataTable; `catalog_factory` runs on mount;
    factory failure renders an empty catalog without
    crashing.
  - Kind filter (3): chip per present kind (empty kinds
    hidden); selection narrows rows + toggles cleanly;
    only-one-kind catalog hides the other chips.
  - Promote (3): agent_skill entry posts the
    `PromoteRequested` message; no selection is a no-op;
    non-skill entry suppresses the message (and pushes a
    toast).
  - Warnings (3): renders one line per error (up to 5);
    empty errors panel is blank; > 5 errors truncate with
    `N more`.
  - Empty (1): empty-catalog status line points at the CLI
    flags.
  - Re-exports (1): `care.screens.CatalogScreen` is the
    same class.

  No new data-layer code shipped — every line of new code
  is in `care/screens/catalog.py` consuming the already-
  shipped `CapabilityCatalog` surface that `care catalog`
  + `tests/test_catalog.py` have exercised since the CLI
  half landed.

  **TUI dispatch wired 2026-05-20:**
  - `CareApp` gained a `Ctrl+K` global binding →
    `action_open_catalog()` that constructs a
    `CatalogScreen(catalog_factory=lambda: build_catalog(
    memory=self.memory))` so the same data layer the CLI's
    `care catalog` returns lands in the TUI.
  - The `Ctrl+K` binding is registered in the help registry
    as a global "Browse capability catalog" entry — shows up
    in `?` HelpScreen + `care help` automatically.
  - **Command-palette entry** `open_catalog` ("Browse
    capability catalog") added to `_DEFAULT_COMMANDS` and to
    the `CommandActionId` Literal so the palette router
    can dispatch it. Keywords:
    `catalog / capabilities / skills / mcp / tools / browse`.
  - **Companion marketplace dispatch shipped same iteration:**
    `action_open_marketplace()` constructs
    `MarketplaceScreen(memory=app.memory.client or
    app.memory)` and pushes it. No keyboard binding — opened
    via the new `open_marketplace` palette command
    ("Browse capability marketplace", keywords
    `marketplace / search / skills / install / share`).
  - **3 new dispatch tests** in
    `tests/test_screen_catalog.py::TestAppDispatch`:
    `CareApp.BINDINGS` contains `open_catalog`;
    `action_open_catalog` lands a `CatalogScreen` in the
    stack; `action_open_marketplace` lands a
    `MarketplaceScreen` in the stack. Plus the existing
    `tests/test_command_palette.py` default-commands test
    now pins `open_catalog` + `open_marketplace` in the
    expected set.

  Both new screens (`CatalogScreen`, `MarketplaceScreen`)
  are now reachable from inside the running TUI — no longer
  orphans only the CLI could exercise.

  **Palette → action dispatch shipped 2026-05-20:**
  - `Ctrl+P` (`action_global_open_command_palette`) now
    actually pushes `CommandPaletteModal(memory=self.memory)`
    onto the screen stack with `_dispatch_palette_action` as
    the `on_dismiss` callback. The legacy
    `CommandPaletteRequested` message is still posted so
    pre-existing subscribers (tests + screens that wire
    custom behaviour) keep working.
  - `_PALETTE_ACTION_DISPATCH` module-level table maps each
    `CommandActionId` literal to a single-line lambda
    invoking the matching `action_*` method:
    ```python
    {
        "open_catalog": lambda app: app.action_open_catalog(),
        "open_marketplace": lambda app: app.action_open_marketplace(),
        "show_help": lambda app: app.action_open_help(),
        "quit": lambda app: app.exit(),
    }
    ```
    New palette commands plug in by adding one row to the
    table — no if/elif chain to grow.
  - `_dispatch_palette_action(selection)` defends every
    failure mode (None selection, missing entry, unknown
    action, handler exception) and silently returns rather
    than crashing the screen stack on a stale palette entry.

  Closes the loop end-to-end:
  `Ctrl+P` → modal pushes → user types → `Enter` picks the
  `open_catalog` entry → modal dismisses with the selection
  → `_dispatch_palette_action` routes to
  `action_open_catalog` → `CatalogScreen` lands on the
  stack. Same chain for `open_marketplace` / `show_help` /
  `quit`.

  **Chain + agent_skill palette picks wired 2026-05-20:**
  `_dispatch_palette_action` now branches on
  `entry.kind` so chain / agent_skill rows route to their
  natural destination (no longer no-ops):
  - **`kind == "chain"`** → pushes
    `InspectionScreen(entry.entry_id)`. Picks a saved chain
    from the palette and lands on its detail view — the same
    screen the LibraryScreen's `Enter` action opens.
    Empty `entry_id` (defensive — shouldn't happen but a
    stale palette index could deliver one) silently no-ops.
  - **`kind == "agent_skill"`** → routes to
    `_open_catalog_focused(focus_entry_id=entity_id)` so the
    user lands on the catalog browser with the DataTable
    cursor already on the picked skill row. `Ctrl+K` opens
    the unfocused variant (top of the list).

  **`CatalogScreen.focus_entry_id=` kwarg shipped same
  iteration:** new constructor parameter that auto-focuses
  the table cursor on the entry whose `source` /
  `memory://<id>` URI / `name` matches the supplied id.
  Match strategy (in order): `source == entry_id` (file-
  backed entries — the most common path); `source ==
  f"memory://{entry_id}"` (memory_card palette picks);
  `name == entry_id` (fallback for agent_skill picks where
  the catalog source is the SKILL.md path but the palette
  delivers the Memory entity_id). Unresolved focus IDs
  silently no-op — the user can still scroll manually.

  `_open_catalog_focused(*, focus_entry_id)` helper on
  `CareApp` is the shared push site `action_open_catalog`
  (Ctrl+K, focus=None) and the palette dispatch
  (focus=picked_entity_id) both call through — keeps the
  build_catalog factory + memory wiring in one place.

  **`CareApp.on_catalog_screen_promote_requested` wired
  2026-05-20:** the CatalogScreen stays pure-presentation,
  posting `PromoteRequested(entry)`; the App's handler now
  drives the actual Memory upload by calling
  `care.promote_skill_to_memory(entry.source, app.memory,
  name=entry.name, tags=entry.tags)` on a worker. Forwarded
  kwargs let the catalog's already-parsed name + tags win
  over the SKILL.md frontmatter defaults — so user-overridden
  values via `--skills` lookup paths persist.

  Failure modes (each emits a toast, no exceptions cross the
  worker boundary):
  - `app.memory is None` → error toast pointing at
    `care.toml` / `CARE_MEMORY__*` env vars; no worker
    started.
  - `SkillPromotionError` raised by the data layer →
    `Promote failed: <reason>` error toast.
  - Unexpected exception → `Promote crashed: <Type>: <msg>`
    error toast.
  - Success → `Promoted <name> → <entity_id>` success toast.

  **`CareApp.on_marketplace_screen_installed`** added as a
  deliberate no-op anchor. The screen's own internal toast
  already handles user feedback; the app-level handler
  exists so Textual doesn't log "no handler" warnings and
  gives future iterations a single anchor point to wire
  telemetry / library-refresh side effects without
  modifying the screen.

  **`CareApp.on_evolution_screen_acceptance_complete`
  shipped 2026-05-20:** pushes a success toast
  (`Accepted <individual_id> from evolution <evolution_id>
  → promoted to stable`) so the user gets a final
  confirmation that survives popping the EvolutionScreen.
  Missing-attribute events default to `"?"` for both ids
  rather than raising (defensive — the screen always sets
  both, but a future stub-driven test or replay path might
  not).

  **`CareApp.on_edit_agent_screen_submitted` shipped 2026-05-20:**
  reads `event.payload` (the frozen `EditAgentEvent`) and
  branches on `payload.action`:
  - `back` → silent (matches every other cancel path).
  - `save` with `SaveEditResult.success=True` →
    `Saved → <entity_id>` success toast.
  - `save` with `error` (or `save_result is None`) →
    `Save failed: <error>` error toast.
  - `promote` with `PromoteResult.success=True` →
    `Promoted to stable` success toast.
  - `promote` with `error` (or `promote_result is None`) →
    `Promote failed: <error>` error toast.
  - Missing `payload` attribute → silent no-op (defensive
    guard for non-conformant event objects).

  **7 new `TestAppPostScreenHandlers` tests:** evolution
  acceptance handler runs with full event, runs with empty
  event (default `"?"` fallback); edit-agent back action is
  silent; save-success / save-failure / promote-success
  paths each fire their respective toast; missing-payload
  event safely no-ops.

  Both `EvolutionScreen.AcceptanceComplete` and
  `EditAgentScreen.Submitted` were previously orphan
  messages — posted by the screen but unhandled by the host.
  They now drive user-facing toasts that survive the screen
  pop.

  **Three more orphan-message handlers wired 2026-05-20:**

  **`on_inspection_screen_action_requested(event)`** routes
  the five-button action row (`run` / `edit` / `evolve` /
  `duplicate` / `back`):
  - `back` — silent (cancel convention).
  - `run` — info toast pointing at the
    `care run <id> --execute` CLI (TUI executor wiring
    pending; same gating that the §9 P2 CLI bullet
    documents).
  - `edit` — `_push_edit_agent_for(entity_id)` fetches
    the chain via `memory.get_chain(...)` and pushes
    `EditAgentScreen(chain=chain_dict, memory=...,
    entity_id=...)`. Missing memory → error toast.
  - `evolve` — `_push_evolution_for(entity_id)` pushes
    `EvolutionScreen(base_chain_id=entity_id)`. Missing
    platform → error toast pointing at
    `CARE_PLATFORM__BASE_URL`.
  - `duplicate` — info toast pointing at the
    `care memory show <id> --export ...` + `care import`
    round-trip (TUI duplicate wiring pending).
  - Unknown action → silent no-op.

  **`on_settings_screen_saved(event)`** reloads the in-
  memory `config` / `memory` / `platform` facades from disk
  via `CareConfig.load()` + `CareMemory.from_config()` +
  `CarePlatform.from_config()`. Each rebuild is wrapped in
  best-effort try/except so a single misconfigured facade
  doesn't bring down the others — the relevant facade
  attribute is set to `None` instead. Pushes a final
  toast: `Settings saved · Memory / Platform reloaded`
  (success) or `Settings saved but reload failed: <reason>`
  (warning).

  **`on_settings_screen_cancelled(event)`** — explicit no-op
  anchor (cancel paths never toast).

  **`on_welcome_screen_recent_selected(event)`** pulls
  `event.row.entity_id` off the `LibraryRow` payload and
  pushes `InspectionScreen(entity_id)` — the canonical
  "jump to last agent" gesture. Missing row / empty
  entity_id → silent no-op; push failure → error toast.

  **12 new tests across three new test classes** in
  `tests/test_screen_catalog.py`:
  - `TestInspectionActionDispatch` (8): back / run /
    edit-no-memory / edit-with-memory→push EditAgentScreen /
    evolve-no-platform / evolve-with-platform→push
    EvolutionScreen / duplicate / unknown-action.
  - `TestSettingsHandlers` (2): saved reloads config;
    cancelled is silent.
  - `TestWelcomeRecentSelected` (2): row pushes
    InspectionScreen; missing row no-ops.

  Before this iteration `InspectionScreen.ActionRequested`,
  `SettingsScreen.Saved/Cancelled`, and
  `WelcomeScreen.RecentSelected` were all orphan messages.
  Now the canonical user gestures they encode (open Edit /
  open Evolve / open Inspection for a recent / reload after
  settings save) all route through the App's handlers to
  the right destination screens with toast feedback.

  **Final five orphan-message handlers wired 2026-05-20:**
  every `Message` class defined on a CARE screen now has a
  matching `CareApp.on_<screen>_<message>` handler. The
  audit is closed.

  - **`on_query_screen_generate_requested(event)`** — pulls
    the `QuerySubmission` off the event, surfaces an info
    toast (`Generate (<mode>) queued: '<task preview>'`)
    pointing at the `care generate '<task>'` CLI fallback
    while the in-TUI MAGE worker is gated on a follow-up
    that threads `MAGEProgressCallback` into a
    GenerationScreen push. Empty task → silent no-op
    (matches the screen's own gate); missing submission →
    no-op.
  - **`on_query_screen_back_requested(event)`** — silent
    anchor (the screen already pops itself on `Ctrl+L`;
    the handler exists so Textual doesn't log
    "no handler" warnings and future cross-screen telemetry
    has a single hook).
  - **`on_task_list_drawer_switch_requested(event)`** —
    pulls `record.task_id` + `description` off the
    `TaskRecord` and pushes an info toast. Full
    focus-switch wiring (popping screens until the screen
    owning this task is on top) needs per-task screen
    attribution the registry doesn't track yet — flagged
    as a follow-up.
  - **`on_welcome_screen_resume_requested(event)`** —
    pulls `state.chain_id` off the `RunState` and pushes
    an info toast. Full resume push (rebuild
    ExecutionScreen from the snapshot via
    `ReasoningContext.restore(snapshot)`) is gated on the
    same runtime wiring `care run --execute` blocks on.
    Missing state → warning toast.
  - **`on_import_modal_preview_loaded(event)`** — explicit
    no-op anchor (the modal renders the preview itself;
    future iterations can hook telemetry / a
    library-refresh post here).

  **9 new tests** across four new test classes
  (`TestQueryHandlers`, `TestTaskListSwitch`,
  `TestResumeRequested`, `TestImportPreview`): each
  handler exercised with a full event, an empty/missing
  attribute event (defensive no-op path), and the
  positive-path toast queued without raising.

  **Orphan-message audit fully closed:** every `Message`
  class on every CARE screen now has a matching handler on
  the App. New screen messages plug in by adding one
  `on_<screen>_<message>` method following the same
  convention; the test harness pattern in
  `tests/test_screen_catalog.py` is the worked example.

  **4 new `TestAppPromoteHandler` tests** in
  `tests/test_screen_catalog.py`: `app.memory is None`
  short-circuits with an error path (no save attempted);
  successful upload calls
  `memory.save_agent_skill(name=, tags=, ...)` end-to-end
  with the catalog entry's values; missing skill path
  raises `SkillPromotionError` and the handler catches
  cleanly (no save attempted); the no-op marketplace
  handler accepts the canonical message shape without
  raising.
  - Unknown kinds + None selections stay no-op.

  **9 `TestPaletteDispatch` + 5 `TestFocusEntry` tests** in
  `tests/test_screen_catalog.py`:
  - **Command kind (3):** `open_catalog` selection pushes
    `CatalogScreen`; `open_marketplace` pushes
    `MarketplaceScreen`; `show_help` pushes `HelpScreen`.
  - **Chain kind (2):** chain pick pushes `InspectionScreen`
    seeded with the chain's `entry_id`; chain pick with
    empty `entry_id` is a no-op (defensive guard).
  - **Agent_skill kind (1):** skill pick pushes
    `CatalogScreen` with `_focus_entry_id` set to the
    picked entity_id (the new focus path).
  - **No-op paths (3):** `None` selection (user cancelled);
    unknown command action (stale palette entry); entry
    without `command_action` on a command-kind entry.
  - **Focus entry (5):** focus matches by exact `source`
    (file-backed entries); matches by `memory://<id>` URI
    (memory_card rows where `source` includes the URI
    prefix); matches by `name` fallback (agent_skill picks
    where source is the SKILL.md path); unresolved focus_id
    is a no-op (selected_entry stays None); empty string is
    normalised to None at construction time.
- **[DONE]** "Promote installed skill to Memory" action — uploads
  the manifest + SHA + source URI as an `agent_skill` entity.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.promote_skill_to_memory(skill_path, memory, *, source_uri,
name, description, tags, when_to_use, author, entity_id, channel)`
    in `care/skills.py`, re-exported from the `care` top-level
    namespace. The orchestration glue between
    `CapabilityCatalog` discovery (TODO §8 P1 data layer) and the
    existing `CareMemory.save_agent_skill` I/O method.
  - `_locate_skill_md` accepts either the `SKILL.md` file itself
    or the enclosing folder (`<skill-name>/SKILL.md` convention).
    Tilde-expands paths and raises `SkillPromotionError` with a
    clear message for the four bad-input cases: path missing,
    path is a non-SKILL.md file, path is a folder without
    SKILL.md, manifest has no `name` and no parent dir to fall
    back on.
  - Reuses `care.catalog._parse_skill_md` so the manifest shape
    the catalog screen renders and the manifest shape that lands
    in Memory stay in lock-step. Frontmatter `name` /
    `description` / `tags` / `allowed-tools` map to the
    corresponding `AgentSkillSpec` fields; explicit
    `name=` / `description=` / `tags=` kwargs always win.
  - Description falls back through three layers when missing:
    explicit override → frontmatter `description:` → first
    non-heading paragraph of the SKILL.md body → empty string.
    Stops authors who skipped frontmatter from getting blank
    Memory entries.
  - SHA-256 of the raw SKILL.md bytes is the trust-pinning key
    — same digest CARE's sandbox `SkillTrustStore` already
    checks against, so a sandboxed run can verify the on-disk
    skill matches what was promoted.
  - Default `source_uri = "local://<absolute-path>"`. Callers
    promoting a git-checkout skill pass
    `source_uri="github://acme/skills/foo@v1"` so other users
    can re-fetch the same revision.
  - `entity_id=` forwards through unchanged so the action is
    idempotent — re-promoting an updated skill against the same
    `entity_id` creates a new version of the existing entity
    instead of a duplicate row (matches the
    `ingest_skill_from_carl` convention).
  - All Memory-side kwargs (`when_to_use`, `author`, `channel`)
    forward verbatim to `CareMemory.save_agent_skill`.

  **Tests (`tests/test_skills_promotion.py`, 22 cases):**
  - Locator: accepts SKILL.md path; accepts folder; accepts
    string paths; tilde expansion via $HOME; missing path
    raises; non-SKILL.md filename raises; folder without
    SKILL.md raises.
  - Manifest extraction: name/description/tags/allowed-tools
    pulled from frontmatter into the `save_agent_skill` call;
    each explicit override (name/description/tags) wins;
    name falls back to folder name when frontmatter missing;
    description falls back to first body paragraph; description
    falls back to empty when body has only a heading;
    missing `allowed-tools` yields `[]` instead of `None`.
  - SHA pinning: digest matches `hashlib.sha256(bytes).hexdigest()`
    exactly and is 64 chars; mutating the body produces a
    different digest on the next promote (regression guard for
    accidental caching).
  - URI handling: default `local://<abs-path>` ending in
    `/SKILL.md`; explicit `source_uri` wins.
  - Memory passthrough: `when_to_use` / `author` / `entity_id`
    / `channel` forward verbatim; the returned `entity_id` is
    whatever Memory returned (not silently rewritten); the
    idempotent re-version flow keeps the same `entity_id`
    across two calls when the user updates the SKILL.md body.

- **[DONE]** Capability marketplace browser — search Memory
  across all users' shared `agent_skill` entities (depends on
  Memory multi-tenant work). Memory's cross-namespace query
  support is still upstream-pending — the function forwards a
  `namespace=None` to the SDK today (single-scope default);
  once Memory ships multi-tenant the same call automatically
  widens, no consumer-side change needed.

  Shipped in two iterations: this bullet captures the data-
  layer half (`search_marketplace` / `MarketplaceListing` /
  `MarketplaceResult` / `MarketplaceError`); the
  `MarketplaceScreen` UI half + `care marketplace <query>`
  CLI companion landed in the follow-up bullet immediately
  below.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.search_marketplace(memory, query, *, top_k,
    min_score, tags, namespace, deep) -> MarketplaceResult`
    in `care/marketplace.py`, re-exported from the `care`
    top-level. Thin wrapper around the SDK's
    `client.find_capability_matches(...)` that adds the
    CARE-side concerns the SDK doesn't own:
    - **Sort by score descending** so the future screen
      doesn't have to re-sort.
    - **CARE-side `tags` filter (all-of)** applied AFTER the
      backend's top-K — tag-tight queries don't crowd out
      high-relevance hits.
    - **`min_score` threshold** for callers who want a
      strict relevance floor.
    - **Empty-query short-circuit** — returns an empty
      result without hitting the backend (saves a round-trip
      on every keystroke when the future screen wires this
      to a search input).
  - `MarketplaceListing` frozen dataclass mirrors the SDK's
    `CapabilityHit` field set
    (`entity_id` / `name` / `description` / `score` /
    `tags` / `matched_via` / `snippet`) but uses plain
    primitives so CARE doesn't need the SDK installed to
    inspect or persist a result. `matched_via` is preserved
    so the UI can badge high-signal matches
    (`skill_description` is BM25-cleanest;
    `skill_instructions` runs against the full body).
  - `MarketplaceResult` aggregator with `listings`,
    `query` (normalised), `is_empty` predicate, and
    `by_tag(tag)` filter for the future screen's tag-chip
    sidebar.
  - **Duck-typed memory argument** — anything exposing
    `find_capability_matches(rough_aim, top_k=,
    namespace=, deep=)` works (the SDK's `GigaEvoClient`
    method matches exactly). Tests use a `_StubMemory`
    spy.
  - **Duck-typed hit shape** — the function projects both
    Pydantic `CapabilityHit` instances AND plain dicts via
    an attribute-or-key getter. Lets tests build hits
    without depending on the SDK's model imports.
  - **Backend errors are wrapped** in `MarketplaceError`
    with the original chained via `from`, so callers
    handle one exception class. A hit missing `entity_id`
    raises the same error rather than silently dropping
    the row.

  **Tests (`tests/test_marketplace.py`, 21 cases):**
  - Result shape: empty result `is_empty=True`; `by_tag`
    filter; `MarketplaceListing` frozen.
  - Empty-query short-circuit: empty string, whitespace
    only, and `None` all return an empty result WITHOUT
    calling the backend (verified via stub-call recorder).
  - Backend forwarding: query is normalised (leading/trailing
    whitespace stripped) before forwarding; default
    `top_k=10`; custom `top_k`; `namespace` and `deep`
    kwargs reach the backend unchanged.
  - Result projection: dict-style hit → listing with every
    field round-tripped; attr-style hit (Pydantic-ish) also
    works; missing `entity_id` raises
    `MarketplaceError("missing required")`; the normalised
    query is preserved on the result for UI breadcrumbs.
  - Sort + filter: listings sorted by score descending;
    `min_score` filter (inclusive `>=`); `tags` filter
    requires ALL listed tags (regression guard against
    accidental any-of semantics); empty `tags=[]` is a
    no-op (doesn't drop everything).
  - Error wrapping: backend exception becomes
    `MarketplaceError("search failed: ...")`; original
    exception chains via `__cause__`.

  **What this gets a CARE user today:**

  ```python
  from care import CareMemory, search_marketplace

  memory = CareMemory.from_config(...)
  result = search_marketplace(
      memory.client,
      "extract tables from a PDF",
      top_k=20,
      min_score=0.3,
      tags=["finance"],
      deep=True,
  )
  for li in result.listings:
      print(f"{li.score:.2f}  {li.name}  ({li.matched_via})")
  ```

  Once Memory ships cross-namespace search, the same call
  widens automatically. Once `MarketplaceScreen` ships, the
  screen renders `result.listings` as a sorted DataTable
  with `by_tag` filtering — no further data-layer changes
  needed.

- **[DONE]** Marketplace browser — UI half (closes the
  `[DONE — data half]` parent above).

  **Shipped 2026-05-20 (both the TUI screen and CLI companion):**

  **`care/screens/marketplace.py::MarketplaceScreen`** — Textual
  `Screen` consuming the already-shipped
  `care.search_marketplace(memory, query, ...) -> MarketplaceResult`:

  - **Top input bar** (`Input`) bound to `self.query_text`
    (named `query_text` not `query` to avoid shadowing the
    inherited `Screen.query(selector)` DOM-walker method —
    naming the reactive `query` silently breaks Textual's
    auto-focus path with a cryptic
    `TypeError: 'str' object is not callable`).
    `Enter` fires `action_submit_search` immediately; typed
    changes debounce via `set_timer(0.3, _run_search_worker)`
    so back-to-back keystrokes coalesce into one search
    call. An `on_input_changed` guard ignores spurious
    Changed events that fire when `Input(value=...)` first
    mounts (no-op when `event.value == self.query_text`).
  - **Results DataTable** (`#marketplace-table`) with five
    columns: ★ (high-signal-match badge for
    `matched_via == "skill_description"`), score, name,
    matched_via, tags. Listings render in score-descending
    order (already pre-sorted by the data layer).
  - **Tag-chip sidebar** (`#marketplace-tag-list`) collected
    via `collect_tags()` — distinct tags across the full
    result set in encounter order. Each chip is a `Button`
    with id `marketplace-tag-<tag>`; clicking calls
    `_select_tag(tag)` which toggles
    `self.selected_tag` (reactive) and re-renders.
    Re-clicking the active chip clears the filter
    (matches the data-layer's `by_tag` toggle convention).
    `visible_listings()` is what the table renders:
    `result.listings` when no tag is selected,
    `result.by_tag(selected_tag)` otherwise.
  - **Install action** (`I` binding or the explicit
    "Install" button) dispatches `_install(listing)` on a
    worker. Worker calls
    `memory.client.save_agent_skill(entity_id=...,
    name=...)` (idempotent SDK save path that's safe to
    re-run); on success pushes a `★ Installed <name>` toast
    via `self.app.push_toast(...)` and posts a
    `MarketplaceScreen.Installed(listing, saved_entity_id)`
    message for the host to react to (refresh library /
    bump counters / etc.). On failure records the error in
    `self.last_error` (rendered via the
    `#marketplace-status` line) and pushes an error toast.
    `_extract_saved_entity_id(response, listing)` probes
    `response.entity_id` / `response["entity_id"]` /
    `response.id` / falls back to `listing.entity_id` so
    SDK shape evolution doesn't break the install flow.
  - **Status line** (`#marketplace-status`) shows
    `(type to search)` when idle, `N listing(s) for '<q>'
    [· filtered by #<tag>]` after a successful search, the
    error message prefixed with `⚠` on failure, and the
    `no results for '<q>'` placeholder when the search ran
    but found nothing.
  - **Pre-seeded queries** via the `initial_query=`
    constructor kwarg — fires one search on mount so the
    caller can land the user directly on a result set
    (used by the future LibraryScreen "Find capability"
    CTA + the `care marketplace <q>` CLI when piped to the
    TUI).

  **Failure modes:**
  - `no memory facade configured` (when constructed without
    `memory=`) lands on `last_error`.
  - `MarketplaceError` from the data layer surfaces as the
    error text (full backend message).
  - Unknown backend exceptions caught + serialised as
    `<TypeName>: <message>`.
  - Install failure (`save_agent_skill` raises) surfaces as
    `install failed: <reason>` on `last_error` + an error
    toast. The except path uses inner try/except around
    `_render_status` + `_push_toast` so a downstream render
    crash doesn't clobber the `last_error` assignment.

  **`care marketplace <query>` CLI companion shipped same
  iteration:** wraps `search_marketplace(memory.client or
  memory, query, ...)` so terminal users get the same
  surface. Flags:
  - `--top-k N` (default 10), `--min-score F` (default 0.0),
    `--tag TAG` (repeatable, all-of), `--namespace NS`,
    `--deep` (match against skill_instructions too).
  - `--json` emits `{query, namespace, deep, listings[]}`.
  Text output: header `marketplace: N listing(s) for '<q>'`
  followed by one line per listing
  `★|space  <score>  <id-prefix>  <name>  [<tags>]`.

  **Tests (23 new cases total):**
  - `tests/test_screen_marketplace.py::TestCompose` (1):
    every pane mounts (input, table, tag-list, status).
  - `tests/test_screen_marketplace.py::TestSearch` (3):
    initial_query fires the worker + populates result;
    `Enter` submits immediately; empty query short-
    circuits without calling the backend.
  - `tests/test_screen_marketplace.py::TestTagFilter` (2):
    `collect_tags()` returns distinct tags in encounter
    order; `_select_tag` narrows + toggles cleanly.
  - `tests/test_screen_marketplace.py::TestInstall` (3):
    install calls `save_agent_skill` with the right
    kwargs + posts `Installed`; no selection is a no-op;
    install failure records `last_error` + skips the
    `Installed` post.
  - `tests/test_screen_marketplace.py::TestErrors` (2):
    search backend failure lands on `last_error`; no
    memory facade lands on `last_error` too.
  - `tests/test_screen_marketplace.py::TestRender` (2):
    `★` badge fills only for `skill_description` matches;
    tag-chip buttons render one per unique tag.
  - `tests/test_screen_marketplace.py::TestReExports` (1):
    `care.screens.MarketplaceScreen` re-exported.
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestMarketplaceCommand` (9):
    populated listings render with score / tag chips /
    ★ badge for skill_description matches; empty result
    placeholder; `--json` payload; every filter forwarded
    (`--top-k` / `--min-score` / `--tag` / `--namespace` /
    `--deep`); CARE-side `--tag` filter is all-of (drops
    listings missing any required tag); Memory-build
    failure surfaces; backend failure surfaces; `main()`
    router routes `marketplace --json`; parser surface
    pins `_cmd_marketplace` + defaults.

  **Two Textual gotchas surfaced + documented during this
  iteration:**
  1. **`query` is a reserved attribute name on `Screen`.**
     Naming a reactive `query` shadows
     `Screen.query(selector)`, which Textual's auto-focus
     path calls with `'*'` → cryptic
     `TypeError: 'str' object is not callable` on mount.
     Use `query_text` or similar.
  2. **`Input(value=initial)` emits an `Input.Changed`
     event on mount.** A naive `on_input_changed` handler
     fires the search worker twice (once from
     `initial_query`-driven explicit call, once from the
     mount event) and the second can clobber state set
     between them (e.g. `last_error` from an install
     failure). Guard with `if event.value == current:
     return`.

  No new data-layer code needed — every line of new code is
  in `care/screens/marketplace.py` + `care/cli.py` consuming
  the already-shipped `search_marketplace` contract.

---

## 9. Packaging & UX polish (P2–P3)

- **[DONE]** Replace the placeholder `pyproject.toml` deps.

  **Shipped:**
  - **Required runtime deps** (always installed, listed under
    `[project.dependencies]`): `textual>=8.2.6`,
    `pydantic>=2.11` (bumped from `>=2.0`), `httpx>=0.27` (new
    — explicit pin; was previously only transitive),
    `gigaevo-client>=0.3.0`. The required set covers every
    top-level CARE import; the catalog / validate / import
    CLI surfaces all work against this minimal install.
  - **Optional `[project.optional-dependencies]` extras** for
    every upstream that CARE imports **lazily** (inside
    functions). The lazy convention means the CARE package
    imports cleanly without these extras, and each lazy
    import surfaces a friendly `*Error("X is not installed;
install with ...")` when the user calls into a code path
    that needs them. - `mage` → `mmar-mage>=0.1` (for
    `MAGEGenerator.generate(...)` +
    `CapabilityPayload.to_mage_context()`). - `carl` → `mmar-carl>=0.2` (for runtime executor +
    preflight against a real `ReasoningChain`). - `openai` → `openai>=1.0` (one provider option for the
    LLM client factory). - `anthropic` → `anthropic>=0.20` (the other provider). - `docker` → `docker>=7.0` (for the future
    DockerSandboxBackend §6 P0). - `e2b` → `e2b>=0.17` (for the future E2BSandboxBackend
    §6 P1). - `full` → aggregate convenience; `pip install
"care[full]"` pulls every upstream + every backend in
    one go.
  - **Path-pinned uv source** for `mmar-mage`:
    `[tool.uv.sources]` now lists `mmar-mage = { path =
"../carl-mage", editable = true }` next to the existing
    `gigaevo-client` entry. `mmar-mage` isn't on PyPI yet so
    users installing the `mage`/`full` extras get the local
    checkout; once `mmar-mage` is published, the path source
    drops and the version constraint takes over without any
    consumer-side change.
  - **`care` CLI entry-point** already pointed at
    `care.cli:main` in the prior iteration; that's preserved
    here.
  - **Deferred from the original spec on purpose:**
    `tomli-w` (TOML writing) and `rich` (CLI styling) were
    listed in the TODO but CARE doesn't import them yet —
    pinning unused deps just bloats the supply-chain surface.
    They'll join the required list (or land under a `cli`
    extra) the day CARE actually uses them — the first-run
    wizard (§2 P0) is the natural trigger for `tomli-w`,
    and richer CLI output for `rich`.

  **Verification:**
  - `uv sync` (no extras) installs the slim 4-dep base; 667
    test suite passes against this install.
  - `uv sync --extra mage` installs `mmar-mage` from
    `../carl-mage`. The previously-skipped
    `test_to_mage_context_raises_when_mage_missing` flips to
    the success branch
    (`test_to_mage_context_returns_real_capability_context`)
    via a `_mage_installed()` helper and
    `pytest.mark.skipif`. Tests now pass on both install
    shapes — no MAGE (1 skip, the success test skipped) and
    with-MAGE (1 skip, the missing-dep test skipped). Result:
    667 passed, 1 skipped (whichever branch isn't exercised
    by the active install).
  - `uv run care --help` smoke-tested clean after the
    refresh.

- **[DONE]** `care` CLI (separate from TUI). The router shell +
  sixteen subcommands (`catalog` / `validate` / `import` /
  `memory ls` / `memory show` / `memory history` / `evolve` /
  `help` / `run` / `generate` / `replay` / `lineage` /
  `search` / `diff` / `favourite` / `marketplace`) are in
  place — including `care run --execute`'s live CARL invocation
  via `ReasoningContext.from_chain_inputs(...)` +
  `chain.execute_async(...)`.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/cli.py` with `main(argv=None) -> int` router.
    `pyproject.toml`'s `[project.scripts]` entry-point now
    points to `care.cli:main`. Running `care` with no
    subcommand still launches the TUI (preserves existing UX);
    `care <subcommand>` dispatches to a headless handler.
  - Argparse-based router with three subcommands so far: - **`care catalog`** — wraps `build_catalog(...)`. Flags:
    `--skills DIR` (repeatable), `--mcp-config PATH`,
    `--tools DIR`, `--kind agent_skill|mcp_server|tool|memory_card`,
    `--json`. Default text output groups entries by kind
    with `# <kind>` headings + `- <name> — <summary>` rows
    mirroring how the future CatalogScreen will render the
    same data. JSON output is `{"entries": [...], "errors":
[...]}` so CI scripts can `jq` it. Catalog warnings
    (broken SKILL.md, malformed `mcp_servers.toml`, etc.)
    go to stderr — text output keeps stdout clean for
    pipelines. Closes the second half of §8 P1. - **`care validate <file>`** — wraps `validate_chain(...)`.
    Reads the file, parses it as a CARL chain, prints the
    `PreflightResult.format_text()` line (or `--json` payload
    with every field for scripting). Exit codes encode the
    outcome: `0` parsed, `1` parse failed, `2` file unreadable. - **`care import <pattern>...`** — wraps `import_chains(...)`
    in **dry-run-by-default** mode. The destructive `--apply`
    flag inverts the module-level default so users opt in to
    writes (matches `rsync --dry-run` / `terraform plan`
    conventions). `--channel` configures the default channel
    for wrapper-form chains that don't carry one. `--apply`
    currently returns `2` with an explanatory stderr message
    that Memory wiring isn't shipped in the CLI yet — the
    structured error path is in place so adding the wiring
    later doesn't change exit-code semantics.
  - **Stream-injectable handlers.** Every subcommand is a
    `_cmd_*(args, stdout, stderr) -> int` function — the tests
    capture output via `io.StringIO` instead of monkey-patching
    `sys.stdout/sys.stderr`. Same pattern means new
    subcommands plug in without touching the entry-point.
  - **Lazy TUI import.** `care --help` / `care validate ...`
    don't pay the Textual import cost; only the no-subcommand
    branch imports `care.app`. CLI startup stays under the
    cost of the imports each subcommand actually needs.
  - Top-level `--help`, `-V/--version` flags reserved on the
    parser so users get familiar UX. Unknown subcommand
    returns argparse's standard exit code (non-zero) without
    crashing.

  **Tests (`tests/test_cli.py`, 19 cases):**
  - `care catalog`: empty text output prints "no entries";
    populated text output groups by kind + shows summary;
    JSON output round-trips the catalog shape;
    `--kind` filter restricts the listing; catalog warnings
    (file-as-skills-dir) route to stderr while exit code
    stays `0`.
  - `care validate`: valid chain exits `0` + prints ok-text;
    invalid chain exits `1` + prints "failed to parse";
    missing file exits `2` + writes "read failed" to stderr;
    `--json` emits the full PreflightResult payload (every
    field); JSON output is still emitted on failure with
    `parsed: false` + populated `parse_errors`.
  - `care import`: dry-run is the default; broken file in
    dry-run yields exit `1` + "1 failed" summary; `--apply`
    returns exit `2` with explicit "requires Memory wiring"
    message (the structured stub for future wiring); empty
    glob match succeeds with the "0 imported, 0 validated,
    0 failed" summary.
  - `main()` router: `--help` returns `0`; subcommand-via-`main`
    routes correctly to `validate` and `catalog` handlers
    using pytest's `capsys`; unknown subcommand returns
    non-zero; `import` dry-run produces "validated" output
    when called through the full router (not just the
    `_cmd_*` direct path).

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care --help`, `uv run care
catalog --help`, `uv run care validate <chain.json>`, and
  `uv run care memory ls --help` all work after editing
  `pyproject.toml`'s `[project.scripts]` and reinstalling.

  **`care memory ls` shipped 2026-05-20:** wraps
  `CareMemory.list_entities(...)` — the new SDK-listing surface
  on the facade. Builds the facade from
  `CareConfig.load()` via a private `_build_memory()` helper
  that wraps every failure mode (missing config, unreachable
  server, SDK import error) in `CliMemoryError` so the handler
  always emits a single-line stderr message and returns exit
  `2`. Flags:
  - `--entity-type {chain,agent,agent_skill,memory_card}`
    (default `chain`)
  - `--limit N` (default 20), `--channel CHANNEL` (default
    `latest`)
  - `--namespace NAMESPACE` (CARE namespace scope)
  - `--tag TAG` (repeatable, AND semantics — forwarded to the
    server's listing filter)
  - `--q SUBSTR` (case-insensitive name/description filter)
  - `--favourites-only` (restrict to favourited entities)
  - `--json` (emit `{"entities": [...]}` instead of the text
    table)

  Text output renders one row per entity:
  `<entity_id-prefix>  ★ / ' '  <display_name>  runs=N  [tag1, tag2]`.
  The favourite star is set from the `favourite` boolean;
  display name probes `display_name` → `meta.name` →
  `(unnamed)`. JSON output serializes via `default=str` so
  datetimes round-trip without crashing.

  Test-injection hook: `cli._BUILD_MEMORY_OVERRIDE` lets tests
  swap in a `_StubMemory` without touching `CareConfig`. The
  production path keeps the override at `None` and refuses to
  use it unless tests explicitly set it.

  **`CareMemory.list_entities(entity_type=, ...)`** shipped
  alongside the CLI: routes to `list_chains` / `list_agents` /
  `list_agent_skills` / `list_memory_cards` depending on the
  kind, forwards every documented SDK filter
  (`limit` / `offset` / `channel` / `namespace` / `tags` / `q` /
  `favourites_only` / `sort_by` / `sort_dir`), and returns
  plain dicts (not `EntityResponse` instances) so call sites
  don't depend on the SDK's response model. Memory cards
  silently ignore the namespace/tag/q kwargs (the SDK's
  `list_memory_cards` doesn't expose them).

  **Tests added this iteration:**
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestMemoryLsCommand` + `TestMemoryParserSurface`
    — 10 new cases covering text output, empty rows, JSON
    output, every filter flag forwarded, default entity type
    is `chain`, Memory build failure → exit 2 with stderr
    message, list-call failure → exit 2 with `lookup failed`,
    `main()` router routes `memory ls`, and the parser
    surface (no-subcommand leaves `_handler=None`).
  - `tests/test_memory.py::TestListEntities` — 5 respx-mocked
    cases covering chains / agent_skills / memory_cards
    routes, every filter param landing in the request URL,
    and unknown entity_type → `ValueError`.

  **`care evolve <chain_id>` shipped 2026-05-20:** wraps
  `care.build_evolution_request` + `CarePlatform.start_evolution`
  + `CarePlatform.stream_events` + `EvolutionProgressTracker` +
  `accept_individual` for a one-shot evolution submission from
  the terminal. Builds the facade via `_build_platform()`
  (mirrors the `memory ls` pattern — wraps every failure in
  `CliPlatformError` → single-line stderr → exit 2). Flags:
  - `--mode {full_chain,per_step}` (default `full_chain`)
  - `--iterations N` (default 5), `--population N` (default 8)
  - `--validation-criteria TEXT`
  - `--objective NAME` (repeatable, multi-objective fitness)
  - `--test-data-path PATH`, `--threshold FLOAT`
  - `--wait` — block on the SSE stream until
    `completed`/`failed`/`cancelled` arrives; render per-event
    lines (`[gen 0] started`, `[gen 0] evaluated <id>
    fitness=0.420`, `[gen 0] best now <id> fitness=0.550`,
    `[done] evolution completed`) via the
    `_format_evolution_event(kind, payload, tracker)` helper.
  - `--accept` — after a successful `--wait`, call
    `platform.accept_individual(evolution_id,
    tracker.best_overall.best_individual_id)`. Requires `--wait`
    (the handler rejects `--accept` without `--wait` with exit
    2 and a one-line stderr explanation, since promoting a
    winner without observing the run to completion is a
    contract violation).
  - `--json` — emit a one-shot summary
    `{"evolution_id", "status", "generation", "best_fitness",
    "best_individual_id", "accepted_individual_id"}` instead of
    per-event lines.

  Plan validation (`EvolutionPlanError` from
  `build_evolution_request`) surfaces as exit 2 with
  `"invalid plan: <reason>"` — empty seed id, `iterations<1`,
  `population<2` all fail before the HTTP round-trip.
  `seed_chain_id` ↔ `base_chain_id` swap (the body shape vs.
  the facade signature) happens once in the handler so the
  user never sees the dual-name confusion.

  Test-injection hook: `cli._BUILD_PLATFORM_OVERRIDE` lets
  tests swap in a `_StubPlatform` without touching CareConfig.
  Production callers leave it at `None`.

  **Tests added this iteration:**
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestEvolveCommand` — 12 new cases
    covering basic submit (without `--wait`), every flag
    forwarded to `start_evolution` (mode/iterations/population/
    objectives/threshold), `--wait` drains the SSE stream and
    prints labelled progress lines, `--accept` promotes the
    best individual after `--wait`, `--accept` without
    `--wait` rejected with exit 2, invalid plan (iterations=0
    or empty chain_id) rejected with exit 2, submit failure
    surfaces, accept failure surfaces, `--json` output round-
    trip (status + best fitness + accepted id), platform-
    build failure surfaces, and `main()` router routes
    `evolve` correctly.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care evolve --help` renders
  the documented flag set.

  **`care help` shipped 2026-05-20:** wraps the §9 P3 help-screen
  data layer (`care.build_registry()` +
  `HelpRegistry.format_text` / `format_markdown`) for a headless
  cheat-sheet that works without launching the TUI. Flags:
  - `--markdown` — switch from plain-text to Markdown output
    (README-friendly: `**bold**` step titles, `` `Ctrl+Q` ``
    backticks, `> Try:` blockquote hints,
    `*(ScreenName)*` italic suffixes).
  - `--category {global,library,generation,execution,evolution}` —
    filter the bindings listing to one category. Tutorial steps
    still render in full (the walkthrough isn't gated by
    category).
  - `--screen NAME` — filter the bindings listing to one screen
    (e.g. `LibraryScreen`). Same tutorial-untouched semantics.

  Plugin-registered tutorial steps + bindings show up
  automatically because the command goes through
  `build_registry()` (not `default_registry()`), so any
  `register_help_extension(...)` call inside a plugin's entry
  point lights up in the CLI same as the TUI HelpScreen.

  Filter implementation: build a fresh `HelpRegistry`, copy
  every step verbatim, copy only bindings whose
  `category` / `screen` match. Keeps the registry mutation
  internal — the user never sees a partial defaults registry
  leak through.

  **Tests added this iteration:**
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestHelpCommand` — 6 new cases covering
    plain-text output (tutorial + bindings + every category
    section + the canonical globals); markdown output (every
    documented structural element: `## Walkthrough`,
    `## Keys`, `**1. Welcome to CARE**`, `` `Ctrl+Q` ``,
    `> Try:` blockquote); `--category library` keeps the
    library section + drops the generation / execution
    sections; `--screen LibraryScreen` keeps the
    LibraryScreen-scoped bindings + drops global bindings
    (which have no screen attribute); `main()` router routes
    plain + markdown variants.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care help` and
  `uv run care help --markdown` both work end-to-end against
  the shipped registry.

  **`care run <chain_id>` shipped 2026-05-20:** fetches a
  saved chain from Memory and runs the shipped preflight path
  on it. Flags:
  - `--channel CHANNEL` (default `latest`) — which version
    channel to read.
  - `--export PATH` — also write the fetched chain to disk via
    `care.export_chain`. Format inferred from the destination's
    extension; `--export-format {json,python}` overrides.
  - `--json` — emit a JSON payload carrying `entity_id`,
    `channel`, and every `PreflightResult` field (`parsed`,
    `ok`, `preflight_available`, `parse_errors`,
    `required_*`, `missing_*`).
  - `--execute` — reserved for the future CARL-runtime wiring
    (LLM client + `ReasoningContext` bootstrap). Surfaces a
    friendly stderr message + exit 2 today, but still runs the
    preflight path first so the user gets a useful answer
    instead of a bare error. Pipelines get a stable exit-code
    contract for when live execution lands.

  Failure modes:
  - Memory build failure → `CliMemoryError` → exit 2 with
    stderr message.
  - Chain fetch failure (unknown id, network error) → exit 2
    with `failed to fetch chain <id>: <reason>`.
  - Export failure (unknown format, malformed dict, missing
    MAGE for `.py`) → exit 2 with `export failed: <reason>`.
  - Preflight parse failure (chain doesn't parse) → exit 1
    with the canonical "failed to parse" text.
  - Successful preflight + no `--execute` → exit 0.

  **`CareMemory.get_chain(entity_id, *, channel="latest")`**
  shipped alongside: thin wrapper over the SDK's
  `get_chain_dict` so call sites (CLI, future runtime) get a
  uniform facade entry-point. Tests are respx-mocked.

  **Tests added this iteration:**
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestRunCommand` — 10 new cases
    covering fetch + preflight (stub returns chain dict,
    `get_chain_calls` recorded), `--channel` forwarded to
    `memory.get_chain`, `--json` payload shape, `--export`
    writes a file with round-trippable content, export
    failure surfaces via `ChainExportError` → exit 2, fetch
    failure surfaces with `failed to fetch chain`,
    Memory-build failure surfaces, invalid-chain → exit 1,
    `--execute` returns exit 2 with the reserved-message
    stderr while still printing preflight to stdout, and
    `main()` router routes `run` correctly.
  - `tests/test_memory.py::TestGetChain` — 2 respx-mocked
    cases: returns the content dict; `channel` query param
    forwarded.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care run --help` renders
  the documented flag set.

  **`care generate "<task>"` shipped 2026-05-20:** wraps
  `MAGEGenerator.generate(query)` for one-shot CLI chain
  generation. Flags:
  - `--mode {fast,deep}` — forwarded to `MAGEConfig.mode`.
    Omitted defaults to `MAGEConfig`'s own default.
  - `--save NAME` — persist the generated chain to Memory via
    `CareMemory.save_chain(chain_dict, name=NAME, query=...)`.
    Emits a `saved: <entity_id>` line on success.
  - `--output PATH` — write the chain to disk via
    `care.export_chain`. Extension drives format
    (`.json` / `.py`); `--output-format` overrides.
  - `--json` — emit the chain dict as JSON instead of the
    one-line summary (`generated chain: N steps, mode=M`).

  Construction flow: `_build_mage_generator(mode)` —
  - Lazy-imports `mmar_mage.MAGEGenerator` + `MAGEConfig`;
    missing dep surfaces as
    `CliMageError: mmar_mage isn't installed: ... Install with
    'pip install care[mage]'`.
  - Reads `CareConfig.load()`. Forwards the user's `mage.*`
    knobs (`provider`, `model`, `api_key`, `base_url`) into
    `MAGEConfig(...)` so the CLI uses the same LLM credentials
    as the TUI. Caller-supplied `--mode` wins over the config
    default.
  - Test-injection hook: `cli._BUILD_MAGE_OVERRIDE` lets tests
    swap in a `_StubMageGenerator` without touching
    `CareConfig` or pulling `mmar_mage`.

  Result extraction: `_result_chain_dict(result)` probes
  `result.chain_dict` (MAGE's canonical shape), then
  `result.chain.to_dict()` (CARL `ReasoningChain` instances),
  then `result.chain` if it's already a dict — keeps the CLI
  resilient to future MAGE-result-shape evolution. Empty
  result → exit 2 with explicit "nothing to save / export"
  message rather than silently writing an empty chain.

  Failure modes (every one returns exit 2 with a single-line
  stderr message):
  - MAGE build failure → `CliMageError`.
  - `await generator.generate(...)` raising →
    `generation failed: <reason>`.
  - Empty chain dict from MAGE → "MAGEResult.chain_dict is
    empty — nothing to save / export."
  - `CareMemory` build failure (for `--save`) → forwarded
    `CliMemoryError`.
  - Save failure → `save failed: <reason>`.
  - Export failure → `export failed: <reason>`.

  **Tests added this iteration (`tests/test_cli.py::TestGenerateCommand`,
  12 cases):** basic generation prints the summary line +
  records the query on the stub; `--mode deep` forwarded to
  the builder override; `--json` emits the chain dict;
  `--save NAME` calls `memory.save_chain` with the right
  kwargs + prints `saved:`; save failure → exit 2 with
  `save-down` in stderr; `--output` writes the chain to a
  file + prints `exported:`; export failure (no-extension
  destination) → exit 2 with `export failed`; generation
  failure → exit 2 with `generation failed`; empty chain
  dict → exit 2 with "empty" + "nothing to" in stderr;
  MAGE-build failure surfaces; `main()` router routes
  `generate` correctly; `_result_chain_dict` falls back to
  `chain.to_dict()` when `chain_dict` is `None`.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care generate --help` renders
  the documented flag set.

  **`care run --execute` shipped 2026-05-20:** the residual gap
  in the §9 P2 CLI bullet closes — `care run <chain_id>
  --execute` now drives the chain end-to-end through CARL.
  Path:
  1. `_build_carl_executor()` (new) — lazy-imports
     `mmar_carl.{OpenAICompatibleClient, OpenAIClientConfig,
     ReasoningChain, ReasoningContext}`. Reads
     `CareConfig.mage.{api_key, model, base_url}` to build an
     `OpenAIClientConfig` (defaults to `openai/gpt-4o` on
     OpenRouter when the user's TOML doesn't pin a model).
     Constructs an `OpenAICompatibleClient` (CARL's
     `LLMClientBase`-compatible API). Returns an async closure
     `(chain_dict) -> ReasoningResult`.
  2. Per-call: `ReasoningChain.from_dict(chain_dict,
     use_typed_steps=True)` → typed chain.
     `ReasoningContext.from_chain_inputs(chain, api=client)` →
     a fresh execution context primed from the chain's
     `CareChainMetadata` (task_description + context_files,
     when present).
     `await chain.execute_async(ctx)` → real LLM-driven run.
  3. Result rendered via `_render_run_result(result,
