     stdout=, as_json=)` — duck-typed against
     `ReasoningResult.{success, step_results, final_answer}`,
     emits a one-line summary (`executed: status=ok, steps=N`
     + `final: <preview>`) or a JSON payload when `--json`
     is set.

  Failure semantics:
  - Carl-build failure (`mmar_carl` missing, missing
    `mage.api_key`, OpenAI client construction raised) →
    `CliCarlError` → stderr + exit 2.
  - `await executor(chain_dict)` raising → exit 2 with
    `execution failed: <reason>`.
  - Chain didn't parse during preflight → exit 1, executor is
    never asked to run (the runner refuses to invoke an
    unparseable chain).
  - Execution succeeded but `result.success is False` → exit 1.
  - Otherwise exit 0.

  Test-injection: `cli._BUILD_CARL_EXECUTOR_OVERRIDE` is a
  no-arg builder returning an async closure
  `(chain_dict) -> _StubReasoningResult`. Tests inject a stub
  with configurable `success` / `raise_on_run` so the entire
  `--execute` path is exercised without touching the real
  `mmar_carl` or an LLM API. Production callers leave the
  override at `None`.

  **Tests added this iteration (6 new cases in
  `TestRunCommand`, total 15):**
  - `--execute` succeeds with the stub executor — exit 0,
    summary line shows `executed: status=ok, steps=2`.
  - `--execute` with `success=False` → exit 1, summary shows
    `status=failed`.
  - CARL build failure surfaces with exit 2 + stderr message.
  - Executor raising mid-run surfaces with `execution failed`
    + `run-down` in stderr, exit 2.
  - Unparseable chain → executor never runs (exit 1 from
    preflight, no calls recorded on the test executor).
  - `--execute --json` emits the structured execution payload
    (`"executed": true`, `"success": true`).

  Replaces the prior `test_execute_flag_returns_two_with_message`
  test that asserted the deferred-wiring stderr — that
  message no longer fires because `--execute` actually runs
  now.

  **Smoke surface:** `uv run care run <chain_id> --execute`
  is wired end-to-end. Real usage needs an LLM API key
  (configured via `CARE_MAGE__API_KEY` or
  `care.toml [mage] api_key`); without one the command exits
  cleanly with a friendly stderr message pointing at the
  config path.

  **Every documented CLI subcommand is now shipped.**

  **`care run --execute` enriched 2026-05-20:** the executor
  closure now accepts two extra runtime knobs the user often
  needs:
  - `--task TEXT` — sets `ReasoningContext.from_chain_inputs`'s
    `outer_context` kwarg. Without this flag CARL primes the
    context from the chain's saved
    `CareChainMetadata.task_description`; with it the user
    overrides for one-off invocations (e.g. running a generic
    "summariser" chain against a fresh task).
  - `--input KEY=VALUE` (repeatable) — populates
    `context.memory['input']` via the `files=` kwarg on
    `from_chain_inputs`. Parsed with `partition("=")` so values
    can contain `=` characters (e.g.
    `--input expr=a=b=c` → `{"expr": "a=b=c"}`). Missing `=`
    or empty-key forms surface as exit 2 with a single-line
    stderr message before any LLM call.

  The production `_build_carl_executor()` closure now forwards
  these to CARL via:
  ```python
  ctx = ReasoningContext.from_chain_inputs(
      chain, api=api_client,
      outer_context=task,      # only when --task supplied
      files=inputs,            # only when --input supplied
  )
  ```
  Both kwargs are omitted from the call when the corresponding
  flag wasn't set, so chains with their own metadata-driven
  task / file priming aren't perturbed.

  `_parse_input_pairs(pairs)` helper validates the
  `KEY=VALUE` form and emits ValueError with a one-line
  user-facing message that the handler turns into exit 2.

  **5 new `TestRunCommand` tests** (total 20): `--task` forwarded
  to the executor closure verbatim; `--input KEY=VALUE` pairs
  parsed into a dict; `--input expr=a=b=c` preserves the value's
  `=` characters; `--input just-a-key` (no `=`) → exit 2 with
  `KEY=VALUE` in stderr; `--input =value` (empty key) → exit 2
  with `empty key`. The stub executor's signature now matches
  the production closure (`(chain_dict, *, task=None,
  inputs=None)`) so all 6 pre-existing `--execute` cases
  continue to pass.

  **`care run --save-result NAME` shipped 2026-05-20:**
  closes the §12 M1 milestone half — "runs persist as memory
  cards linked back to the agent". After a successful
  `--execute`, the handler delegates to the existing
  `care.runtime.record_run_completion(...)` helper so the
  saved card lands with the **canonical** tag scheme the
  InspectionScreen's Run-History tab already queries
  (`agent_run` + `agent:<entity_id>` + `status:<label>`) and
  the canonical `category=agent_run` body shape with
  `usage.{run_id, agent_entity_id, agent_name, finished_at,
  metrics}`. Side effect: the agent's `run_count` /
  `last_run_at` counters get bumped via
  `memory.client._record_run(...)` — same as a TUI run.

  Cross-piece wiring:
  - `--save-result NAME` lands on the card as a `label:<name>`
    tag (passed via `record_run_completion`'s `extra_tags`
    kwarg). Users can reuse the same `NAME` across runs
    without colliding on Memory's display name.
  - `_chain_display_name(chain_dict)` probes
    `metadata.care.display_name` and falls back to the
    chain_id for the `agent_name` kwarg, so the saved card
    carries the human-readable name when the chain was saved
    with CARE metadata.
  - `--task TEXT` lands on `card.task_description` (the
    canonical field `parse_run_history_entry` reads to
    populate the tab's task-description column).
  - `--input KEY=VALUE` pairs are still forwarded to the
    executor (driving `context.memory['input']`) — the card
    persists the resulting `ReasoningResult.metrics` which is
    where any input echo would surface.

  Net effect: `care run --execute --save-result NAME` makes
  the resulting card show up in the **TUI InspectionScreen's
  Run History tab** automatically, alongside runs persisted
  by the in-app worker. Same projection, same sort, same
  replay dispatch — no extra CARE wiring required.

  **`care memory history <chain_id>` shipped 2026-05-20:**
  closes the read-side loop for run-history persistence.
  Wraps `care.runtime.fetch_run_history` — the same data
  layer the InspectionScreen Run History tab uses — so any
  run persisted via `care run --execute --save-result` (or
  via the TUI itself) is browsable from the terminal.

  Flags:
  - `--limit N` (default 20)
  - `--channel CHANNEL` (default `latest`)
  - `--namespace NAMESPACE`
  - `--json` — emit a structured payload with the full
    `RunHistorySummary` aggregates + every documented
    `RunHistoryEntry` field

  Text output renders a summary header
  (`history: N run(s) (X ok, Y failed, success rate ZZ%, avg
  T.Ts)`) followed by one line per entry via
  `RunHistoryEntry.format_one_line()` (`✓ 2026-05-19 10:00:00
  · run run-001 · 2.5s · 100 tok`). Empty history emits
  `history: no runs recorded for <chain_id>`.

  JSON payload shape:
  ```json
  {
    "chain_id": "agent-1",
    "channel": "latest",
    "summary": {
      "total_runs": 2,
      "success_count": 1,
      "failure_count": 1,
      "total_tokens": 100,
      "total_duration_seconds": 4.0,
      "success_rate": 0.5,
      "avg_duration_seconds": 2.0,
      "last_success_at": "...",
      "last_failure_at": "..."
    },
    "entries": [
      {"card_id", "agent_entity_id", "run_id", "finished_at",
       "status", "duration_seconds", "step_count",
       "total_tokens", "error_message", "task_description",
       "description", "tags", "metrics"}
    ]
  }
  ```

  Failure modes: Memory build failure → `CliMemoryError` →
  exit 2; `RunHistoryError` (server unreachable, timeout,
  malformed response) → exit 2 with the canonical message;
  unexpected listing failure → exit 2 with
  `lookup failed: <reason>`.

  **Tests (`tests/test_cli.py::TestMemoryHistoryCommand`,
  8 cases):** populated history renders summary + entries;
  empty history emits the placeholder; `--json` payload
  carries the documented summary + entry fields;
  `--limit` / `--channel` / `--namespace` forwarded to the
  fetcher (which always pins `agent_run` + `agent:<id>`
  tags); Memory-build failure surfaces; client lookup
  failure surfaces with the underlying message; `main()`
  router routes `memory history`; parser surface check
  pins `_cmd_memory_history` as the routed handler.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care memory history --help`
  renders the documented flag set.

  Read/write parity now complete:
  - **Write:** `care run --execute --save-result NAME` →
    canonical `agent_run` card.
  - **Read:** `care memory history <chain_id>` → renders that
    same card via the canonical projection.

  No remaining gaps in the run-history loop from either
  the CLI or the TUI surfaces.

  **`care replay <source>` shipped 2026-05-20:** wraps the
  §6 `care.load_replay(source)` data layer + the
  `ReplaySession` cursor / `format_text()` rendering so a
  saved `ReasoningResult` / `RunRecord` JSON file can be
  stepped through from the terminal — same projection the
  TUI's `ReplayScreen` consumes.

  Flags:
  - `source` (positional) — path to a JSON file, or `-` to
    read from stdin (e.g. for piping `RunRecord.save(path)`
    output via shell).
  - `--step N` — render exactly one step's detail block.
    Seeks via `ReplaySession.seek(N)` which clamps out-of-
    bounds requests to the nearest endpoint (so
    `--step 99` on a 2-step run renders step 2 cleanly).
  - `--json` — emit a structured payload with chain
    metadata + every documented `ReplayStep` field per row
    (`step_number`, `step_title`, `step_type`, `success`,
    `skipped`, `execution_time_s`, `error_message`,
    `result_preview`, `result_truncated`, `model`).

  Default output walks every step in order — `session.seek(i)`
  then `session.format_text()` per cursor position — so the
  user gets a complete textual log without scrolling. Empty
  source (no `step_results` field) emits
  `replay: no steps in source`.

  Failure modes:
  - File read failed (missing path, permission) → exit 2 with
    `read failed: <reason>`.
  - Malformed JSON → `ReplayError` → exit 2 with the
    line/col location from `care.load_replay`.

  `_read_source_text(path, stdin=...)` handles the `-` →
  stdin convention.

  **Tests (`tests/test_cli.py::TestReplayCommand`, 10 cases):**
  default walk includes every step + correct cursor headers
  (`step 1/2`, `step 2/2`); `--step 1` renders only that
  step's block; `--json` payload carries chain metadata +
  every documented step field; empty session emits the
  placeholder; missing file → exit 2 with `read failed`;
  malformed JSON → exit 2 with `failed to parse`; stdin
  source (`-`) reads from the harness-injected
  `sys.stdin`; `--step 99` clamps to the last step;
  `main()` router routes `replay --json`; parser surface
  pins `_cmd_replay` + defaults.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care replay --help`
  renders the documented flag set.

  This completes the CLI's view of the run-history /
  replay loop: persist via `--save-result` (canonical
  `agent_run` card), browse via `memory history`, dump
  via `RunRecord.save(path)`, walk via `replay <path>` —
  every step shared with the TUI's data layer.

  **`care memory show <entity_id>` shipped 2026-05-20:**
  the single-entity drill-down complementing
  `care memory ls`'s listing surface. Wraps the new
  `CareMemory.get_entity(entity_id, *, entity_type, channel)`
  facade method (a thin wrapper over the SDK's private
  `_get_entity(...)`) so callers get the full
  `{entity_id, version_id, channel, etag, meta, content}`
  payload in one hop.

  Flags:
  - `--entity-type {chain,agent,agent_skill,memory_card,step}`
    (default `chain`).
  - `--channel CHANNEL` (default `latest`).
  - `--content-only` — emit just the `content` body as
    pretty-printed JSON. Handy for piping into
    `care validate <file>` (after redirecting to a file) or
    diffing two chains.
  - `--json` — emit the full SDK payload as JSON for `jq`
    consumption.

  Default text output renders a 5-line metadata header
  (`entity:` / `channel:` / `version:` / `name:` / `tags:`)
  followed by `content:` and the body pretty-printed. Best
  for one-off terminal inspection.

  Failure modes:
  - Memory build failure → exit 2 with stderr (same
    `CliMemoryError` path as the other `memory` subcommands).
  - Entity fetch failure (unknown id, network error) →
    exit 2 with
    `failed to fetch <entity_type> '<id>': <reason>`.
  - `CareMemory.get_entity` raises `ValueError` on an
    unknown `entity_type` (defended at the facade boundary
    so the CLI's choices argument doesn't drift from what
    the SDK actually supports).

  **`CareMemory.get_entity(entity_id, *, entity_type,
  channel)`** SDK helper: returns the SDK's
  `_get_entity` payload — the same shape callers get from
  the raw client. Accepts the five `_TYPE_PLURAL` entity
  types the SDK knows about. Unknown types raise
  `ValueError` (matches `list_entities`'s pattern).

  **Tests (10 new cases):**
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestMemoryShowCommand` (9 cases):
    default text output (header + pretty-printed body);
    `--json` round-trip; `--content-only` emits just the
    body; `--entity-type agent_skill` forwarded to the
    facade; `--channel stable` forwarded; Memory-build
    failure → exit 2 + stderr; entity fetch failure surfaces
    the underlying error message; `main()` router routes
    `memory show --json` correctly; parser surface check
    pins `_cmd_memory_show` + default `chain` entity-type.
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestMemoryGetEntityUnknownType` (1
    case): direct unit on `CareMemory.get_entity` confirms
    the `ValueError("unsupported entity_type ...")` contract
    the CLI surface relies on.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care memory show --help`
  renders the documented flag set.

  Memory surface area now complete from the CLI:
  - `care memory ls` — listing across entity types.
  - `care memory show` — single-entity drill-down.
  - `care memory history` — run-record listing for a chain.

  All three share the same `_build_memory()` builder + test-
  injection hook, so a stub installed once via
  `_BUILD_MEMORY_OVERRIDE` drives every memory subcommand
  uniformly.

  **`care lineage <chain_id>` shipped 2026-05-20:** walks the
  ancestry DAG for an evolved chain by wrapping the SDK's
  `get_chain_lineage` via a new
  `CareMemory.get_chain_lineage(entity_id, *, channel,
  version_id, max_depth)` facade method. Closes the read-side
  of §7's evolution loop from the terminal — the TUI's
  LineageModal consumes the same `LineageResponse` shape.

  Flags:
  - `--channel CHANNEL` (default `latest`) — start from this
    channel's head.
  - `--version-id ID` — walk from a specific historical
    version instead of the channel head.
  - `--max-depth N` (default 10, server clamp 1-100) — BFS
    cap. The `max-depth cap reached` footer note fires when
    the server hit the cap.
  - `--json` — emit the full `LineageResponse` payload
    (entity_id, root_version_id, max_depth_reached, versions[])
    as pretty-printed JSON.

  Default text output:
  ```
  lineage: <chain_id> · root <root_version_id> · N version(s) [· max-depth cap reached]
    v<N> (<version_id>) · depth <D> · <created> · root | parents=<id>, <id>...
    ...
  ```
  Versions sort by BFS depth ascending (so the most-recent
  evolution lands first), tie-broken by version number
  descending. Root versions render with the `root` badge;
  non-root versions list their parent version_ids.

  `_lineage_version_dict(v)` + `_format_lineage_version(v)`
  helpers project a typed `LineageVersion` (or a duck-typed
  dict-shaped equivalent) into the JSON payload / one-line
  text rendering. Resilient to either shape so the CLI works
  against the real SDK or a test stub.

  Failure modes (uniform with the other `memory`-adjacent
  subcommands):
  - Memory build failure → exit 2 with stderr.
  - Lineage fetch raised → exit 2 with
    `failed to fetch lineage for '<id>': <reason>`.
  - Empty `versions` list → exit 0 with
    `lineage: no versions returned for <id>`.

  **Tests (`tests/test_cli.py::TestLineageCommand`, 9 cases):**
  text output ordering by BFS depth (root last, latest first);
  `max_depth_reached` footer note; empty version list emits
  placeholder; JSON payload carries every documented field;
  `--channel` / `--version-id` / `--max-depth` forwarded to
  the facade; Memory-build failure → exit 2; fetch failure
  surfaces underlying error; `main()` router routes
  `lineage --json`; parser surface check pins `_cmd_lineage`
  + defaults.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care lineage --help` renders
  the documented flag set.

  Evolution-side parity now complete from the CLI:
  - `care evolve <chain_id>` — submit + stream + accept.
  - `care lineage <chain_id>` — walk the ancestry DAG of an
    accepted evolved chain.

  Both share the canonical `LineageResponse` /
  `EvolutionRef` types the TUI's EvolutionScreen +
  LineageModal already consume.

  **`care search <query>` shipped 2026-05-20:** wraps
  `CareMemory.search(...)` so the TUI LibraryScreen's search
  bar has a terminal twin. The same `SearchType` enum
  (`bm25` / `vector` / `hybrid`) drives both surfaces, and
  both project the SDK's `SearchHit` to a plain dict so the
  CLI doesn't pull the SDK's response model into stdout.

  Flags:
  - `query` (positional) — free-form search string.
  - `--entity-type {chain,agent,agent_skill,memory_card,step}`
    (default `chain`).
  - `--search-type {bm25,vector,hybrid}` (default `bm25`).
  - `--top-k N` (default 10).
  - `--json` — emit the full `{query, entity_type,
    search_type, hits[]}` payload as pretty-printed JSON.

  Text output renders a one-line header followed by one
  line per hit:
  ```
  search: N hit(s) for '<query>' (<entity_type>, <search_type>)
    <score>  <entity_id-prefix>  <display_name|name|(unnamed)>
    ...
  ```
  No-match emits the `no hits for <query> (...)` placeholder.
  Scores render to 3 decimals via `_format_search_hit`; non-
  numeric / missing scores fall back to `—`.

  Failure modes (uniform with the other Memory-adjacent
  subcommands):
  - Memory build failure → exit 2 with stderr.
  - Backend lookup failure (HTTP error, malformed response)
    → exit 2 with `lookup failed: <reason>`.

  **Tests (`tests/test_cli.py::TestSearchCommand`, 9 cases):**
  populated hit list renders header + per-hit lines + scores
  + entity-type / search-type echoes; empty hit list emits
  the placeholder; `--json` payload carries the full
  request + hit shape; every filter flag (entity-type /
  search-type / top-k) forwarded to the facade; Memory-
  build failure surfaces; backend lookup failure surfaces
  with `search-down` in stderr; missing-score hit falls
  back to `—`; `main()` router routes `search --json`;
  parser surface check pins `_cmd_search` + defaults.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care search --help`
  renders the documented flag set.

  Memory triad is now read-write-search-history-show
  complete from the CLI; the LibraryScreen's primary
  affordances (browse, search, drill-down, run-history,
  lineage) all have a terminal-mode twin sharing the same
  data layer.

  **`care diff <left> <right>` shipped 2026-05-20:** wraps
  `care.runtime.fetch_agent_diff` — the same data layer the
  TUI's DiffModal consumes — for terminal-mode chain
  comparison. Loads both chains via
  `memory.client.get_chain_dict(entity_id, channel)`
  concurrently (single `asyncio.gather` deadline shared
  across both fetches) and projects into a typed `AgentDiff`.

  Flags:
  - `left`, `right` (positional) — entity IDs of the two
    chains.
  - `--channel CHANNEL` (default `latest`) — Memory channel
    to read both sides from.
  - `--left-label`, `--right-label` — display labels for the
    header (default: entity_id).
  - `--json` — emit a structured payload carrying step-level
    rows + metadata-field deltas + summary counts.

  Default text output:
  - Header: `diff: <left-label> ↔ <right-label>  (<summary>)`
    where `<summary>` is `AgentDiff.format_summary()` (e.g.
    `+1 · ~1 of 3 steps`, or `no differences`).
  - Metadata-diff line when chain-level fields changed
    (`metadata: display_name: ... → ... · +tags: x, y`).
  - Per-step lines with kind-driven badges (`+ step N`,
    `- step N`, `~ step N`, `· step N`) followed by indented
    `<field>: <left> → <right>` rows for modified fields.
    `_truncate` keeps each value under 40 chars and escapes
    embedded newlines so the output stays one-line-per-row.

  JSON payload shape:
  ```
  {
    "left_entity_id", "right_entity_id",
    "left_label", "right_label",
    "summary": "<format_summary() string>",
    "counts": {"added", "removed", "modified", "unchanged", "total"},
    "metadata": {
      "fields": [{"field", "left", "right", "left_present", "right_present"}],
      "added_tags": [...], "removed_tags": [...]
    },
    "steps": [
      {"number", "kind", "label", "fields": [<field shape above>]}
    ]
  }
  ```

  `_format_step_diff_row`, `_format_field_diff_row`,
  `_format_metadata_diff`, `_diff_to_dict`, `_field_diff_dict`,
  `_truncate` — six private helpers handle rendering with no
  module-level state. `_DIFF_BADGES` constant pins the
  badge dictionary (`+` / `-` / `~` / `·`) shared with the
  TUI's DiffModal convention.

  Failure modes:
  - Memory build failure → exit 2 with stderr.
  - `AgentDiffError` (missing entity_id, missing SDK
    `get_chain_dict`, timeout, one chain returns None) →
    exit 2 with the canonical message.
  - Otherwise unexpected exception → exit 2 with
    `lookup failed: <reason>`.

  **Tests (`tests/test_cli.py::TestDiffCommand`, 10 cases):**
  text output renders header + step counts + per-step badges
  (added / modified / unchanged); `--left-label` / `--right-label`
  customise the header; `--json` payload carries every
  documented count + field; identical chains emit
  `no differences`; `--channel stable` forwarded to both
  `get_chain_dict` calls; Memory-build failure surfaces;
  missing chain (right side returns None) → exit 2 via
  `AgentDiffError`; mid-fetch exception propagates as
  `lookup failed`; `main()` router routes
  `diff --json`; parser surface check pins `_cmd_diff` +
  defaults.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care diff --help` renders
  the documented flag set.

  CLI surface area now totals **14 subcommands**. The
  LibraryScreen's complete primary-action set (browse /
  search / drill-down / run-history / lineage / **diff**)
  all share data layers with their terminal twins; nothing
  in the TUI's read-side library workflow is exclusive to
  the TUI anymore.

  **`care favourite <entity_id>` shipped 2026-05-20:** opens
  the write-side library surface from the CLI — first piece
  of mutation parity with the TUI's LibraryScreen. Wraps a
  new `CareMemory.mark_favourite(entity_id, *, entity_type,
  value)` facade method that dispatches to the SDK's
  private `_mark_favourite(entity_type, entity_id, value)`
  endpoint (which hits
  `POST /v1/{plural}/{id}/favourite`).

  Flags:
  - `entity_id` (positional).
  - `--entity-type {chain,agent,agent_skill,memory_card}`
    (default `chain`).
  - `--off` — unstar (`favourite=false`) instead of starring
    (`favourite=true`). Stars by default to match the TUI's
    `F` binding, which always toggles toward "starred"
    unless re-pressed.
  - `--json` — emit the updated entity payload as
    pretty-printed JSON.

  Text output: `★ starred: <entity_id> (<entity_type>) — <name>`
  or ` unstarred: ...` (when `--off`). The name probes
  `display_name` → `meta.name` → entity_id, matching the
  display-name fallback chain the other Memory subcommands
  use.

  Failure modes:
  - Memory build failure → exit 2 with stderr.
  - SDK mark call raised (404 on missing entity, HTTP error,
    timeout) → exit 2 with
    `failed to star <type> '<id>': <reason>` or
    `failed to unstar <type> '<id>': <reason>` matching the
    requested direction.

  **`CareMemory.mark_favourite(entity_id, *, entity_type,
  value=True)`** SDK helper: validates `entity_type` against
  `{"chain", "agent", "agent_skill", "memory_card"}` (raises
  `ValueError` for unknowns to defend the facade boundary,
  same pattern as `list_entities` / `get_entity`), forwards
  to `_mark_favourite`, and returns the updated entity as a
  dict (via `EntityResponse.model_dump(mode="json")`).

  **Tests (10 new cases):**
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestFavouriteCommand` (9): default
    stars; `--off` unstars; `--entity-type agent_skill`
    forwarded; `--json` payload round-trip; Memory-build
    failure surfaces; mark failure surfaces with star/unstar
    verb matching the request direction; `main()` router
    routes; parser surface check pins `_cmd_favourite` +
    defaults.
  - `tests/test_cli.py::TestMemoryMarkFavouriteUnknownType`
    (1): direct unit on the facade pins the
    `ValueError("unsupported entity_type ...")` contract.

  **Smoke-tested live:** `uv run care favourite --help`
  renders the documented flag set.

  CLI surface area now totals **15 subcommands**. The
  LibraryScreen's write-side mutation surface now has its
  first terminal twin (`favourite`); `run-recorded`,
  `metadata`, and `delete` remain open for future
  iterations.

  Behavior matrix:
  - `--save-result NAME` without `--execute` → exit 2 with
    `requires --execute` stderr (nothing to persist without an
    actual run).
  - Run failed (`result.success is False`) → card NOT saved
    (avoids polluting Memory with failed runs); exit code
    still 1 from the run.
  - `memory.save_memory_card` raised → exit 2 with
    `save-result failed: <reason>`.
  - Card body uses `result.to_dict()` (lossless) when
    available, else a duck-typed
    `{success, step_count, final_answer}` projection so the
    card still has the user-visible summary.

  `_persist_run_result(memory=, chain_id=, chain_dict=,
  result=, name=, task=, inputs=)` helper (12 lines, mostly
  a thin shim around the canonical `record_run_completion`
  helper) + `_chain_display_name(chain_dict)` agent-name
  resolver. Both private to the CLI; the canonical
  card-build + tag scheme + run-count bump all live in
  `care.runtime.run_recorder` and ship there already.

  **7 new `TestRunCommand` tests** (total 27): card lands
  with canonical tags (`agent_run` / `agent:<id>` /
  `status:success` / `label:<NAME>`) + canonical body
  (`category=agent_run`, `usage.metrics.duration_seconds`);
  `--task` lands on `card.task_description`; chain's
  `metadata.care.display_name` populates `usage.agent_name`
  when available; `--save-result` without `--execute` → exit
  2 + stderr; failed run skips the card save; card-save
  failure surfaces as exit 2; the run-count bump goes through
  to `memory.client._record_run` end-to-end.

- **[DONE]** Test suite: unit tests for `MagePoster`,
  `CarlStreamer`, `CareMemory`, every `SandboxBackend`. Smoke
  tests for each TUI screen using Textual's `Pilot`.

  **Shipped:**
  - **Unit-test coverage for every named target:**
    - `MagePoster` → `tests/test_mage_poster.py`
    - `CarlStreamer` → `tests/test_carl_streamer.py`
    - `CareMemory` → `tests/test_memory.py` (real `respx` HTTP
      mocks against the gigaevo-client SDK)
    - `CarePlatform` → `tests/test_platform.py`
    - Every `SandboxBackend`-side concern:
      `tests/test_sandbox_local.py` (real
      `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec`), `test_sandbox_audit.py`,
      `test_sandbox_resources.py`, `test_sandbox_trust.py`,
      `test_network_policy.py`, `test_output_mediation.py`
  - **Total: 727 tests passing**, +3 install-dependent skips,
    one Pydantic deprecation warning. Test count tripled over
    the project lifetime — every primitive shipped has its
    own dedicated file.
  - **Pilot smoke template** in
    `tests/test_screens_demo_pilot.py` — 6 cases exercising
    the only screen that exists today (`DemoScreen`). Three
    test classes: mount + structural checks (widgets present,
    title set, bindings registered), actions (`Ctrl+G` drives
    `PipelinePreview.show_pipeline`, `Ctrl+L` wipes the task
    input), message routing (the screen's
    `on_task_setup_generate_requested` handler runs without
    raising end-to-end through `pilot.press`).
  - **Template for future workflow screens.** Each future
    P0 workflow screen (`WelcomeScreen`, `LibraryScreen`,
    `QueryScreen`, `GenerationScreen`, `InspectionScreen`,
    `EditAgentScreen`, `ExecutionScreen`, `EvolutionScreen`)
    can copy the file's pattern: minimal `_DemoHarnessApp`
    host, `async with app.run_test() as pilot`, `await
pilot.pause()` between actions, `pilot.press("ctrl+x")`
    for bindings, widget-level assertions via
    `app.screen.query_one(...)`. Keeping the harness app
    trivial means a screen test exercises _the screen_, not
    app-level wiring — a `CareApp` regression won't false-fail
    these.
  - **Pytest-asyncio in `auto` mode** is already configured in
    `pyproject.toml` so `@pytest.mark.asyncio` works without
    fixture juggling — matches the convention already used by
    `test_carl_streamer.py` / `test_executor.py`.

  has shipped with its own dedicated Pilot-test file
  (`tests/test_screen_welcome.py`, `tests/test_screen_library.py`,
  `tests/test_screen_query.py`, `tests/test_screen_generation.py`,
  `tests/test_screen_inspection.py`, `tests/test_screen_edit_agent.py`,
  `tests/test_screen_execution.py`, `tests/test_screen_evolution.py`,
  `tests/test_screen_replay.py`, `tests/test_screen_help.py`,
  `tests/test_screen_conflict.py`, etc.). The Pilot harness +
  conventions documented in `tests/test_screens_demo_pilot.py`
  remain the reference template.

- **[DONE]** Telemetry opt-in: when enabled, write
  generation/run/evolution events to Langfuse so the user can
  replay sessions in a web dashboard.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/runtime/telemetry.py` with the full surface re-
    exported from `care.runtime`: `TelemetryEvent` value
    object, `TelemetrySink` Protocol, `NullTelemetrySink`
    no-op default, `build_telemetry_sink(config)` factory,
    `register_telemetry_backend` / `unregister_*` /
    `list_known_backends` registry. Mirrors the
    `care.runtime.llm_client` design — same lazy-import +
    factory-registry pattern users already know from the
    LLM provider surface.
  - **Zero-cost when disabled.** `TelemetryConfig.enabled`
    defaults to `False`; the factory short-circuits to a
    fresh `NullTelemetrySink` regardless of which backend is
    configured. Production users who don't opt in pay
    nothing — no imports, no I/O, no allocations beyond the
    sink itself. Even with `enabled=True, backend="langfuse"`
    on a sink-less build, the function still returns a Null
    sink (defensive — typo'd config can't fail open into
    silently broken telemetry).
  - **`TelemetryEvent` frozen dataclass** with `kind`,
    `attributes`, `trace_id` (auto-stamped `uuid4().hex`
    when omitted, so every event has a stable identity for
    cross-event correlation), `timestamp` (default factory
    yields `time.time()`). `kind` is a free-form `str` —
    no `Literal` constraint so adding event categories
    (`mage.stage_started`, `carl.step_completed`, …) doesn't
    require a schema bump.
  - **`TelemetrySink` Protocol** with three methods:
    `record(event)` (hot path), `flush()` (force buffered
    events to ship — TUI calls on task-transition events for
    live dashboard updates), `close()` (release backend
    resources on app shutdown). The Protocol contract
    explicitly says **none of these may raise** — telemetry
    failures must never break the surrounding chain run.
    `NullTelemetrySink` honours this with bare `return`s and
    a `dropped` counter for test introspection (production
    code shouldn't read it).
  - **`NullTelemetrySink`** as the default + the explicit
    debug option. Callers can unconditionally
    `sink.record(...)` without branching on
    `config.enabled` — the Null sink absorbs writes
    cheaply.
  - **Langfuse backend** lazy-imported only when
    `enabled=True, backend="langfuse"`. Internally wraps
    `Langfuse(public_key=..., secret_key=..., host=...)` and
    translates each `TelemetryEvent` into a `client.event(...)`
    call. Missing SDK → friendly `TelemetrySinkError`
    pointing at `pip install langfuse`. Missing credentials
    → clear "public_key + secret_key must be set" error
    rather than an SDK-layer auth crash later. The
    wrapper belt-and-braces catches inside `record` / `flush`
    / `close` so a Langfuse outage never propagates back to
    the chain code that fired the event.
  - **Custom backend registry** (`register_telemetry_backend`
    / `unregister_*` / `list_known_backends`). Mirrors
    `register_provider_factory` from the LLM client surface
    — case-insensitive dispatch, silent overwrites for
    test-harness convenience, generic factory exceptions
    wrapped in `TelemetrySinkError`, `TelemetrySinkError`
    raised by the factory propagates unchanged so callers
    handle one exception class.
  - **`TelemetryConfig`** Pydantic section on `CareConfig`:
    `enabled`, `backend` (`null` / `langfuse` / custom),
    `host` (defaults to `cloud.langfuse.com` — self-hosted
    deployments override), `public_key`, `secret_key`. All
    knobs surfaced via env vars + documented in
    `.env.example`.
  - **`.env.example` updated** with all 5 telemetry env vars
    (`CARE_TELEMETRY__ENABLED`, `__BACKEND`, `__HOST`,
    `__PUBLIC_KEY`, `__SECRET_KEY`). The §2 P1 schema test
    enforces parity, so adding a future telemetry field
    will fail CI until `.env.example` is updated.
  - **README quick-reference table** gains a `telemetry` row
    with one-line purpose.

  **Tests (`tests/test_telemetry.py`, 25 passed + 1 install-
  dependent skip):**
  - `TelemetryEvent`: independent default factories (mutating
    one event's `attributes` doesn't bleed to another;
    distinct `trace_id`s per default); frozen-dataclass
    assertion; explicit `trace_id` preserved; default
    `timestamp` is a sensible float.
  - `NullTelemetrySink`: `record` increments `dropped`;
    `flush` / `close` are no-ops.
  - `build_telemetry_sink` factory: defaults (`enabled=False`)
    return Null; explicit `enabled=True, backend="null"`
    returns Null; empty backend name returns Null;
    `disabled=True` with Langfuse-configured-but-not-enabled
    still returns Null (defensive against typo'd configs);
    unknown backend raises with the known-backend list in
    the error message; accepts both full `CareConfig` and
    bare `TelemetryConfig`.
  - Langfuse missing-dep: `pytest.mark.skipif` on
    `_langfuse_installed()` so the test exercises the real
    `ImportError → TelemetrySinkError` path in CARE's dev
    env where Langfuse isn't installed. Missing-keys error
    also tested when the SDK IS available.
  - Custom backend registry: register + dispatch; empty
    name raises; unregister returns bool; overwrites
    silently; generic factory exceptions wrapped;
    `TelemetrySinkError` from factory propagates unwrapped;
    case-insensitive dispatch (`CUSTOM-STUB` matches
    `custom-stub`).
  - `list_known_backends`: includes built-ins, includes
    registered customs, sorted.
  - Re-export check: `care.runtime` exports the public
    telemetry surface so consumers `from care.runtime
import TelemetrySink` without knowing the submodule
    path.
  - `.env.example` schema test now pins `telemetry`
    alongside the existing six sections — every
    `CARE_TELEMETRY__*` var lines up with a real Pydantic
    field, and every `TelemetryConfig` field appears in
    the example file.

- **[DONE]** Help screen + tutorial walkthrough for the welcome
  screen. Data layer + Textual screen + global `?` binding all
  shipped.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care/help.py` with the full surface re-exported from
    the `care` top-level:
    - `KeyBinding` frozen dataclass: `key`, `action`,
      `category` (Literal `"global" | "library" |
      "generation" | "execution" | "evolution"`),
      `screen`.
    - `TutorialStep` frozen dataclass: `title`, `body`,
      optional `hint_key`, optional `screen` for "jump
      to this screen" actions.
    - `HelpRegistry` mutable store with
      `add_step` / `add_binding` / `steps` /
      `step_titles` / `bindings` / `by_category(c)` /
      `by_screen(name)` lookups, `format_text` (CLI /
      footer rendering) + `format_markdown` (README /
      `care help --markdown` output).
    - `default_registry()` returns a fresh registry
      pre-loaded with the canonical-flow tutorial + every
      documented binding.
    - `build_registry()` = defaults + every plugin
      extension applied in registration order.
    - `register_help_extension(callable)` /
      `unregister_help_extension(callable)` — plugin hooks
      following the same convention
      `register_provider_factory` / `register_telemetry_backend`
      use. Buggy extensions can't break the registry — their
      exceptions are swallowed so a misbehaving plugin
      can't poison the help screen.
  - **Default tutorial: 7 canonical-flow steps** covering
    every screen the README documents — Welcome, Describe
    your task (QueryScreen), Watch the chain build
    (GenerationScreen + Esc to cancel), Save to your library
    (SaveAgentModal), Re-run from the library
    (LibraryScreen), Evolve when you're stuck
    (EvolutionScreen), Everything is configurable (config
    + env layered model).
  - **Default key bindings: 18 entries** spanning every
    documented surface:
    - 6 globals — `Ctrl+P` (palette), `Ctrl+Q` (quit),
      `Ctrl+S` (save), `Ctrl+R` (re-run), `Esc` (back /
      cancel), `?` (open help).
    - 7 library — `Enter` (open), `R` (run), `E` (edit),
      `F` (favourite), `Del` (delete), `Ctrl+F` (search),
      `/` (search alt).
    - 2 generation — `Ctrl+G` (generate), `Ctrl+L` (clear).
    - 1 execution — `Space` (pause/resume).
    - 1 evolution — `A` (accept current best).
  - **`format_text` rendering:** "# Tutorial" section with
    numbered steps + body + ⌨ hint, followed by
    "# Key bindings" grouped by category (`## global`,
    `## library`, …) with `(ScreenName)` suffixes where
    applicable. Empty registry returns an empty string so
    the future help screen can show "no content registered"
    without a special branch.
  - **`format_markdown` rendering:** README/CLI-friendly
    output with `**bold**` step titles, ``"`Ctrl+Q`"``
    backticks around keys, `> Try: \`Ctrl+G\`` blockquote
    hints, and `*(ScreenName)*` italic suffixes. Drives a
    future `care help --markdown` flag + a static
    "Quick reference" section for the README.

  **Tests (`tests/test_help.py`, 31 cases):**
  - Frozen dataclasses (4): both classes frozen + sensible
    defaults.
  - Registry mutation (5): empty state safe;
    insertion-order preserved for steps + bindings;
    `by_category` filters per category;
    `by_screen` filters per screen name.
  - Default content (6): default registry has ≥7 tutorial
    steps; first step is the Welcome banner; every
    documented canonical-flow screen has at least one
    step mention; all 6 documented globals present; the 5
    documented LibraryScreen keys present;
    `default_registry()` returns a fresh instance per call
    (mutating one doesn't bleed).
  - Extensions (4): `register_help_extension` appends
    steps + bindings via `build_registry`; buggy
    extension's exception swallowed but subsequent
    extensions still run; `unregister_help_extension`
    returns bool + is idempotent.
  - `format_text` (5): tutorial section present;
    bindings section grouped by category; per-screen
    `(ScreenName)` suffix; hint key surfaces under step;
    empty registry returns empty string.
  - `format_markdown` (5): markdown headings; backticks
    around keys; blockquote hints; italic per-screen
    suffix; empty registry yields trailing newline only.
  - `build_registry` (2): returns `HelpRegistry`
    instance; includes defaults.

  **UI shipped 2026-05-20:** `care/screens/help.py::HelpScreen`
  is a Textual `Screen` that reads `care.build_registry()` on
  mount and renders two panes:
  - **Walkthrough** (left, 3fr): each `TutorialStep` becomes a
    numbered title (`1. Welcome to CARE`), the body, an
    optional `⌨ <hint_key>` hint line, an optional
    `↳ <screen>` jump-target line, and a blank-row separator.
  - **Key bindings** (right, 2fr, left border): iterates the
    five categories (`global` / `library` / `generation` /
    `execution` / `evolution`) and emits a `# <category>`
    section header followed by `<key>  <action>  (<screen>)`
    rows.

  Empty registry shows `(no help content registered)` in a
  one-line strip under the body so a misbehaving plugin can't
  leave the screen visually blank. Constructor accepts an
  optional `HelpRegistry` override for tests / preview
  callers; defaults to `build_registry()` so the canonical
  tutorial + every registered plugin extension show up
  automatically.

  Keyboard: `Escape` / `q` → `action_back` pops the screen.
  Header breadcrumb is `("Help",)` and the footer renders in
  `scope="screen"` mode.

  **Global wiring:** `CareApp.BINDINGS` adds
  `Binding("question_mark", "open_help", "Help", show=False)`
  and a matching `action_open_help` that
  `push_screen(HelpScreen())`. The `?` chord works from every
  screen (the binding is on the App, not on individual
  screens). Matches the `Ctrl+B` task-list / `Ctrl+P` palette
  pattern.

  **Tests (`tests/test_screen_help.py`, 13 cases):**
  - **Compose (3):** both panes mount; tutorial pane carries
    the step titles + hint keys verbatim; bindings pane shows
    `# global` / `# library` section headers + every key the
    injected registry registered (including the `(LibraryScreen)`
    screen suffix).
  - **Defaults (3):** when no registry is supplied,
    `screen.step_count >= 7` (canonical-flow count) and
    `screen.binding_count >= 17` (every documented key);
    `"Welcome to CARE"` is in `_step_titles()`; the four
    globals `Ctrl+P` / `Ctrl+Q` / `Esc` / `?` are in
    `_binding_keys()`.
  - **Empty state (1):** registry with zero steps + zero
    bindings renders the `(no help content registered)`
    line.
  - **Navigation (3):** `action_back` pops the screen;
    `app.action_open_help()` lands HelpScreen on top of the
    stack (uses `mode="returning"` to bypass the
    WelcomeScreen splash race); `CareApp.BINDINGS` contains
    `open_help`.
  - **Pure helpers (2):** `_format_binding` renders global
    bindings without a screen suffix; scoped bindings get a
    `(<Screen>)` parenthetical.
  - **Re-exports (1):** `care.screens.HelpScreen` is the
    same class.

  **What this enables:** plugins extending CARE (custom
  screens, third-party tools) call
  `register_help_extension(my_ext)` in their entry points;
  their bindings + tutorial steps land in the same HelpScreen
  the next time it opens — no modal-screen modification
  required. The `care help` CLI subcommand (deferred behind
  the §9 P2 CLI list) can read the same `build_registry()`
  to render plain text via `format_text()` or markdown via
  `format_markdown()`.
- **[DONE]** Generated chain export: save as `.py` (using MAGE's
  `CodeGenerator`) or `.json`.

  **Shipped:**
  - `care.export_chain(chain, path, *, format=None, query="",
mage_config=None) -> ExportResult` in `care/chain_export.py`,
    re-exported from the `care` top-level namespace. Pure file-
    output module — the two destinations the TODO calls out
    (`.json` for round-trip-safe persistence + `.py` for a
    runnable ChainBuilder script).
  - **Three input shapes** accepted, mirroring the convention
    `care.validate_chain` already uses:
    - `dict` matching `ReasoningChain.to_dict()`,
    - JSON `str` (re-decoded to a dict before writing),
    - `bytes`/`bytearray` (UTF-8 decoded; bad bytes raise),
    - object exposing `.to_dict()` — duck-typed via `hasattr`
      so the function doesn't pull `mmar_carl` for an
      `isinstance` check. Lets `MAGEResult.chain` (a parsed
      `ReasoningChain`) feed straight in.
  - **Format resolution.** Explicit `format=` kwarg wins; falls
    back to the destination's extension (`.json` → JSON,
    `.py` → Python, case-insensitive). Neither decisive →
    `ChainExportError("cannot infer format")` rather than
    silently writing the wrong shape. Unknown explicit format
    string raises with the valid choices listed.
  - **JSON output** is always available — `json.dumps(chain,
indent=2, sort_keys=True)` so the file is diff-friendly
    and reproducible across runs. No upstream deps. Round-trips
    cleanly through `ReasoningChain.from_json`.
  - **Python output** lazy-imports
    `mmar_mage.code_generator.CodeGenerator` and calls
    `generate(chain_dict, query, MAGEConfig())`. `mage_config=`
    kwarg overrides the default-constructed config for callers
    who want non-default knobs (e.g. preserved from the
    original generation). Missing MAGE raises a friendly
    `ChainExportError` pointing at
    `pip install "care[mage]"` to enable `.py` export —
    matches the install-hint convention `LLMClientError` /
    `CapabilityPrimingError` use.
  - `ExportResult` frozen dataclass with `path` (resolved,
    tilde-expanded), `format` (literal of what was actually
    written), `bytes_written`. Narrow shape on purpose —
    anything richer leaks implementation detail callers
    shouldn't rely on.
  - `ChainExportError` covers every failure path (unknown
    format, malformed input, missing optional dep, MAGE
    CodeGenerator raising, disk write OSError) so callers
    handle one exception class instead of four.
  - Tilde expansion on the destination path. Parent dirs are
    NOT auto-created — exports usually land in a directory
    the user already chose; silent mkdir-p would mask typos.

  **Tests (`tests/test_chain_export.py`, 18 passed + 1
  install-conditional):**
  - Format resolution: extension-based inference for `.json`;
    `.py` extension with MAGE installed → Python; explicit
    `format=` overrides extension (writes JSON to a `.py`
    file when asked); unknown format string raises;
    no-extension + no kwarg raises; uppercase `.JSON` works
    (case-insensitive suffix lookup).
  - JSON output: dict input writes pretty-printed sorted-keys
    JSON; `bytes_written` matches actual file size; sort
    order is reproducible (regression guard); JSON-string
    input is parsed + re-emitted; bytes input is utf-8
    decoded; object with `.to_dict()` is unwrapped; invalid
    input type raises `expected dict / JSON str / object`;
    malformed JSON string surfaces line/col location;
    JSON not-a-dict raises; `.to_dict()` returning non-dict
    raises; invalid UTF-8 bytes raise; tilde expansion via
    `$HOME`.
  - Python output (split by install state via
    `pytestmark = pytest.mark.skipif`): - With MAGE installed → real `CodeGenerator` output;
    script starts with `'"""Auto-generated CARL chain
script."""'` header; query text lands in the
    `build_chain()` docstring; ChainBuilder import is
    referenced; empty query still renders. - Without MAGE installed → friendly install-hint error
    (skipped in the current dev env because MAGE is in;
    kept for builds without the `mage` extra).

---

## 10. Examples & docs (P2–P3)

- **[DONE]** End-to-end example: "weather report" — from `care`
  to a running chain that uses an MCP weather server +
  summariser LLM step. Bundled as `examples/weather/`.

  **Shipped:**
  - `examples/weather/chain.json` — a real, parseable CARL
    chain dict with the two steps the spec calls out:
    1. **`fetch_forecast`** (`step_type: mcp`) — references
       the `weather` MCP server with `tool_name:
       get_forecast`, demonstrating both the static-args mode
       (`arguments.city = "$city"`, `units = "metric"`) AND
       the runtime-binding mode (`argument_mapping.city =
       "$inputs.city"`) so the example doubles as a side-by-
       side walkthrough of MCP step's two argument flavours.
    2. **`summarise_forecast`** (`step_type: llm`,
       `dependencies: [1]`) — populated with `aim` /
       `reasoning_questions` / `stage_action` /
       `example_reasoning` so the LLM step shows the full
       MAGE-emitted shape (not just a stub).
    - Uses the typed-step `step_config` key (not the
      pre-coercion `config` field name) so the file
      round-trips through `ReasoningChain.from_dict(...,
      use_typed_steps=True)` cleanly on installed
      `mmar-carl 0.2.0`. Verified live via
      `uv run care validate`.
  - `examples/weather/mcp_servers.toml` — server registration
    using the `command` / `args` / `description` / `tags`
    shape `care.build_catalog(mcp_config_path=...)` reads.
    `weather` server name matches the chain's MCP-step
    reference, so the catalog discovery + chain reference
    line up exactly.
  - `examples/weather/README.md` — three-section walkthrough:
    1. What's in this directory (3-row file table).
    2. **Try it** — three shell commands using the shipped
       CLI surfaces (`care validate examples/weather/chain.json`,
       `care catalog --mcp-config ...`, `care import ...`).
       All three work offline against `mmar-carl 0.2.0` —
       no LLM key, no Docker, no running MCP server.
    3. **Chain shape** — ASCII flow diagram + an explanation
       of the two argument-binding modes side by side.
    Plus a "What CARE primitives this exercises" table
    mapping each CLI surface to its module + function, and
    a cross-link to `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` for the full
    reference.
  - **Smoke-tested live**: all three documented CLI
    invocations work end-to-end against the bundled files —
    `care validate` reports "chain parsed; preflight
    skipped"; `care catalog` lists the `weather` mcp_server;
    `care import` reports "0 imported, 1 validated, 0
    failed".

  **Tests (`tests/test_example_weather.py`, 13 cases):**
  - **Files present:** directory exists; chain.json,
    mcp_servers.toml, README.md all present.
  - **chain.json shape:** valid JSON; parses via
    `care.validate_chain` against real `mmar-carl`; step
    kinds pinned to `["mcp", "llm"]` (so future
    reorganisations don't silently change the example's
    canonical shape); MCP step references `server_name:
    "weather"`; LLM step depends on `[1]`.
  - **mcp_servers.toml schema:** `build_catalog` discovers
    exactly one `mcp_server` named `weather` with the
    described tags + summary.
  - **Cross-file consistency** — regression guard for the
    most painful drift: the MCP server name referenced by
    `chain.json`'s `mcp` step must exist in `mcp_servers.toml`.
    Catches typos that would silently break the example.
  - **Dry-run import** — `import_chains([chain.json],
    dry_run=True)` produces an `all_ok` report with 1
    `validated` entry.
  - **README integrity** — README mentions every bundled
    file by name + shows all three documented CLI commands
    (`care validate` / `care catalog` / `care import`). A
    future docs cleanup that drops one of the commands
    will fail until reconciled.

  **Why this is the right shape for the §10 example slot:**
  the example is built entirely from primitives CARE has
  already shipped + already tests. No additional runtime
  surface introduced, no MAGE generation required, no LLM
  keys needed for the walkthrough — anyone with a fresh
  `uv sync` can run the three commands and see the system
  working. Real execution (the "running chain" half of the
  TODO bullet) requires plugging in an actual MCP weather
  server + LLM provider, which the README walks through as
  an opt-in step rather than baking external deps into the
  example.
- **[DONE]** End-to-end example: "financier helper" — chain
  with PDF AgentSkill (anthropics/skills/pdf) + structured-output
  step + memory card persist.

  **Shipped:**
  - `examples/financier/chain.json` — a real, parseable CARL
    chain dict with the two steps the spec calls out:
    1. **`extract_pdf_text`** (`step_type: tool`) — a
       placeholder for the future `agent_skill` step type.
       The bundled SKILL.md represents the AgentSkill CARL
       upstream will reference once `AGENT_SKILL` lands in
       the installed wheel; the chain uses a `tool` step
       today so it parses cleanly on `mmar-carl 0.2.0`
       (which exposes only `conditional | llm | mcp |
       memory | structured_output | tool | transform`).
       `input_mapping.pdf_path = "$inputs.pdf_path"`
       routes the user's input into the tool call.
    2. **`normalise_financials`** (`step_type:
       structured_output`, `dependencies: [1]`) — a real
       JSON-Schema-constrained step extracting the
       `QuarterlyFinancials` shape with five required
       fields (`period`, `currency`, `revenue`,
       `net_income`, `total_expenses`) plus one optional
       array (`notable_alerts`). `strict_json=true` so the
       executor demands raw JSON output from the model.
       Uses the typed-step `step_config` key.
  - `examples/financier/skills/pdf-extractor/SKILL.md` —
    a real SKILL.md manifest CARE's `CapabilityCatalog`
    discovers. Frontmatter declares `name`, `description`,
    `tags: [pdf, finance, extraction]`, `allowed-tools:
    [Read, Bash]`. Body documents inputs/outputs +
    references PREPARE.md §5.1 for the future
    `agent_skill` migration path. Lives one level deeper
    than the weather example's flat layout so the same
    `--skills` dir can hold multiple skills.
  - `examples/financier/README.md` — three-section
    walkthrough mirroring the weather README's layout but
    showcasing primitives the weather example didn't:
    1. **AgentSkill discovery** via
       `care catalog --skills examples/financier/skills`.
    2. **`structured_output` step** with an inline
       `QuarterlyFinancials` JSON Schema.
    3. **`memory_card` persistence** — full Python example
       showing how to call `CareMemory.save_memory_card(...)`
       at the end of the run so future quarters become a
       searchable comparison.
    Plus a "What CARE primitives this exercises" table
    mapping each surface to its module + function, including
    the new `_scan_skill_dir` and `_parse_skill_md` paths.
  - **Smoke-tested live**: all three documented CLI
    invocations work end-to-end against the bundled files —
    `care validate` reports "chain parsed; preflight
    skipped"; `care catalog --skills` lists the
    `pdf-extractor` `agent_skill`; `care import` reports
    "0 imported, 1 validated, 0 failed".

  **Tests (`tests/test_example_financier.py`, 16 cases):**
  - **Files present:** directory exists; chain.json,
    README.md, skills/pdf-extractor/SKILL.md all present.
  - **chain.json shape:** valid JSON; parses via
    `care.validate_chain`; step kinds pinned to `["tool",
    "structured_output"]`; `tool_name == "pdf_extractor"`;
    structured_output schema has all five required fields
    pinned + `notable_alerts` correctly optional;
    structured_output depends on `[1]`.
  - **SKILL.md catalog discovery:** `build_catalog` finds
    exactly one `agent_skill` named `pdf-extractor` with
    the expected tags + `allowed_tools` metadata.
  - **Cross-file consistency:** the chain's `tool_name`
    appears in the README; the SKILL.md's `name`
    (`pdf-extractor`) appears in the README — both
    directions of the README ↔ artefact pairing pinned.
  - **Dry-run import** — produces an `all_ok` report with
    1 `validated` entry.
  - **README integrity:** mentions every CLI command;
    describes `memory_card` persistence (mentions
    `save_memory_card`); describes `structured_output` +
    `QuarterlyFinancials` (the unique aspects vs the
    weather example).

  **What this example exercises that weather didn't:**
  - `agent_skill` catalog discovery (the SKILL.md walk).
  - `structured_output` step with a real JSON Schema.
  - `memory_card` persistence flow (documented; the
    Python snippet shows the exact `CareMemory.save_memory_card`
    invocation).

  **Migration path note (in the README):** once CARL's
  `AGENT_SKILL` step type lands in the installed `mmar-carl`
  wheel, the chain can swap the placeholder `tool` step for
  an `agent_skill` step pinned to the SKILL.md's SHA-256.
  The schema + downstream `structured_output` step stay
  identical — only the extraction step's `step_type`
  changes.
- **[DONE]** `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` mirroring the diagram above
  with cross-links to MAGE/Memory/Platform docs.

  **Shipped:**
  - `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` — the contributor-facing entry-point
    doc that walks the four-module stack with concrete file +
    function pointers. Seven top-level sections:
    1. **The four-module stack** — reproduces the §0 ASCII
       diagram + a 5-row layer/module/role table.
    2. **Module boundaries inside `care/`** — full directory
       tree with one-line descriptions per file, including
       every `care/runtime/` adapter and every `care/sandbox/`
       backend. Plus rationale paragraphs on the two facades
       (`care.memory` / `care.platform`) and the
       Textual-`Message` translation contract in
       `care/runtime/`.
    3. **Layer-by-layer reference** — five subsections
       (Generation, Execution, Persistence, Evolution,
       Sandbox), each with a table mapping "what you need"
       → "where to find it" with concrete entry points
       (`MAGEGenerator.analyze_domain`, `ReasoningChain.preflight`,
       `client.find_capability_matches`, etc.).
    4. **The canonical user flow** — the §1.3 canonical flow
       (generate A → save → generate B/C → re-run A) with
       links to the shipped primitives that back each step.
    5. **Configuration & precedence** — the four-layer stack
       (defaults < user TOML < project TOML < env) cross-
       linked to §2 P2 and `.env.example`.
    6. **CLI vs TUI** — the `care` entry-point dispatch +
       the three shipped CLI subcommands.
    7. **Where to look next** — 8-row table cross-linking
       to PREPARE.md, TODO.md, README.md, .env.example,
       and every upstream module README/openapi.
  - **Cross-links to upstream modules** via relative paths
    (`../../carl-mage`, `../../carl-experiments`,
    `../../gigaevo-memory`, `../../gigaevo-platform`) so a
    reader inside CARE can jump to any sibling repo. Each
    layer section references the upstream `PREPARE.md` section
    that pins its prep status.
  - **README cross-link** — new "Architecture" section in
    `README.md` points readers at the doc from the repo
    landing page, so the doc is discoverable without prior
    knowledge.

  **Tests (`tests/test_architecture_doc.py`, 6 cases):**
  - File exists at `<repo-root>/docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`.
  - All 13 required headings are present (the seven top-level
    sections + the five §3 subsections + the document title).
    Drift catcher: removing a section to "clean up" the doc
    fails CI until the structure is reconciled.
  - Mirrors the TODO §0 diagram — five layer labels (`MAGE
async`, `CARL runner`, `GigaEvo`, `Platform`,
    `AgentSkill sandbox`) appear in the doc so the two stay
    in sync.
  - Internal links resolve: every relative-path link is
    checked against the on-disk file. Cross-module references
    (`../../carl-mage`) are allowed to be absent on stripped
    checkouts; CARE-internal references must exist.
  - Lists every `care/runtime/*.py` adapter by filename so a
    new adapter can't be added without updating the §2
    module-boundaries tree. Reverse-direction catch for the
    most common drift mode (new file, doc not updated).
  - README cross-link assertion — `README.md` mentions
    `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` so the doc remains discoverable.

- **[DONE — harness; recording is maintainer-gated]**
  Recording: asciicast demo for the README. The reproducible
  recording harness ships now — seed fixtures, recording
  script, wrapper, README link. The actual `.cast` file is a
  manual artefact (someone runs `scripts/record_demo.sh` in a
  TTY) and lands when a maintainer captures the session.

  **Explicitly NOT a `[P0-P3]` task for the automated loop**
  — recording in a real TTY can't run headless. Future audits
  should treat this as a maintainer-handoff item, not as
  unfinished automation work.

  **Shipped:**
  - `scripts/record_demo.sh` — Bash wrapper that drops the
    user into `asciinema rec` with the right options.
    - Validates prerequisites (`asciinema` + `uv` on PATH +
      seed dir present); each missing piece gets a friendly
      "install via …" hint instead of a cryptic failure.
    - Sets `CARE_MAGE__API_KEY=demo-key` (placeholder so
      first-run probes don't short-circuit during the
      recording) + `CARE_MAGE__PROVIDER=openai`.
    - Defaults output to `docs/asciicasts/care-tour.cast`
      (auto-creates the parent dir); custom paths accepted
      as `scripts/record_demo.sh path.cast`.
    - **Refuses to overwrite silently** — prompts before
      replacing an existing recording so a stray re-run
      doesn't nuke a freshly-uploaded version.
    - Records at 120×36 (readable on GitHub README embeds)
      with `--idle-time-limit 2` so long pauses collapse to
      preserve viewer attention.
    - `set -euo pipefail` + `chmod +x` so direct invocation
      works without `bash`.
  - `examples/asciicast/recording_script.md` — four-act
    keystroke list the recording follows:
    - **Act 1** (~20s): `care catalog` against the seed
      shows one entry per kind (`agent_skill` `pdf-helper`,
      `mcp_server` `weather`, `tool` `demo_tool`).
    - **Act 2** (~10s): `care validate` reports "chain
      parsed; preflight skipped" — pinned text.
    - **Act 3** (~10s): `care import` dry-run reports "0
      imported, 1 validated, 0 failed" — pinned text.
    - **Act 4** (~30s, optional): launch the TUI, hit
      `Ctrl+Q` to exit.
  - `examples/asciicast/seed/` — hermetic seed directory
    the wrapper points at:
    - `chain.json` — two-step CARL chain (mcp +
      llm) that `care validate` parses cleanly via the
      installed `mmar-carl 0.2.0`.
    - `mcp_servers.toml` — registers a `weather`
      MCP server so the catalog has something to render.
    - `skills/pdf-helper/SKILL.md` — placeholder
      AgentSkill manifest exercising the `--skills` flag.
    - `tools/demo_tool.py` — a no-deps Python file that
      lights up the tool listing.
  - **README "Demo" section** linking to the wrapper and
    the recording script so contributors can reproduce or
    re-record without spelunking through the repo.

  **Tests (`tests/test_asciicast_harness.py`, 23 cases):**
  - Harness files exist (5): asciicast dir, recording
    script, all four seed files, wrapper script
    executable bit.
  - Seed chain integrity (3): chain.json parses via
    `care.validate_chain`; step kinds match script's
    `["mcp", "llm"]` promise; MCP step references the
    `weather` server name.
  - Catalog discovery against the seed (4): builds a
    catalog from all three sources, verifies one entry
    per kind discovered; per-kind names pinned
    (`pdf-helper` / `weather` / `demo_tool`).
  - Expected CLI outputs (2): `validate_chain` produces
    the exact text the recording script promises in Act
    2; `import_chains` dry-run produces the exact text
    Act 3 promises. Failure means the recording script
    is out of date.
  - Recording-script content (3): every seed file path
    mentioned in the script (so a future contributor can
    grep); every CLI surface present (`care catalog` /
    `care validate` / `care import`); wrapper invocation
    mentioned.
  - Wrapper-script content (5): calls `asciinema rec`;
    default output to `docs/asciicasts/care-tour.cast`;
    sets `CARE_MAGE__API_KEY`; prompts on overwrite;
    validates prerequisites with friendly messages.
  - README link (1): mentions both `scripts/record_demo.sh`
    and `recording_script.md`.

  **What still needs a human:** running `scripts/record_demo.sh`
  in an actual TTY + uploading the resulting `.cast` (or
  embedding it in the README via the asciinema-player
  block). The harness makes that a one-command operation
  with the prerequisites validated up front + every line
  of expected output pinned by CI.

  **Out of scope for the automated cron loop** — recording
  in a real TTY can't run headless. Track this as a
  maintainer-handoff item rather than a `[P0-P3]` bullet
  the loop should swallow.

  **Status update (2026-05-20 — final):** every codeable
  P0/P1/P2/P3 bullet has shipped end-to-end, including the
  two `[P2]` follow-ups (Pareto-picker UI + Marketplace
  browser UI) that were split out of the
  `[DONE — data half]` parents. Those parents now read
  plain `[DONE]` (the data layer + UI both ship; the
  follow-up `[DONE]` bullets immediately below them carry
  the UI shipping notes).

  The only residual marker is the
  `[DONE — harness; recording is maintainer-gated]`
  asciicast item — explicitly NOT a `[P0-P3]` task for the
  loop. Test count: **2603 passed, 8 skipped**. CLI surface
  area: **16 subcommands**.

---

## 11. Cross-module dependency cheat-sheet

| CARE need                           | Blocks on (other module)                                                       |
| ----------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Save AgentSkill                     | gigaevo-memory: add `agent_skill` entity (P0)                                  |
| MAGE includes skills in planning    | carl-mage: extend `VALID_STEP_TYPES` (P0)                                      |
| Streaming MAGE progress             | (already supported via `MAGEProgressCallback`)                                 |
| Library: sort by run count          | gigaevo-memory: add `run_count`, `last_run_at`, `favourite` (P0, §1.4)         |
| Library: lineage view               | gigaevo-memory: `/v1/chains/{id}/lineage` (P2, §5)                             |
| Library: hot-reload across sessions | gigaevo-memory: `/v1/events` firehose (P1, §6)                                 |
| Saved task + context for re-run     | gigaevo-memory: add `task_description` + `context_files` to chain content (P0) |
| Submit chain population             | gigaevo-platform: `/api/v1/evolutions` (P1)                                    |
| SSE progress from evolution         | gigaevo-platform: SSE/WebSocket (P1)                                           |
| Sandbox-aware AgentSkill            | carl-experiments: wire `runtime` field (P0)                                    |
| One client for Memory + Platform    | gigaevo-memory: rename + repackage (P2)                                        |

---

## 12. Suggested milestones

- **M0 — Walking skeleton (2 weeks):** §1.1 P0 screens (Welcome → Library →
  Query → Generation → Inspection) + §1.3 P0 Library basics + §3 P0
  SaveAgentModal + draft auto-save + §4 P0 MAGE wiring. End-state: user
  can generate Agent A, save it with a name + favourite, generate B and C,
  return to A from the library. No execution yet.
- **M1 — Local execution & re-run (2 weeks):** §5 P1 execution + §1.3 P1
  re-run flow + run history + §6.1/6.2 P0 LocalSandbox + DockerSandbox.
  End-state: every saved agent in the library is runnable on demand with
  reused or new context; runs persist as memory cards linked back to the
  agent.
- **M2 — Editing & evolution (3 weeks):** §1.1 EditAgentScreen + §3 P1
  edit→new version + §7 P1 platform integration.
- **M3 — Capabilities & polish (2 weeks):** §8, §9, §10, §11.
